# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 2

169

B"H, Between Kisei and Asor, 5705

To the esteemed Avreichim HaTemimim, G-d-fearing, men of action, students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, may they live, Montreal.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your blessing for the coming year:

Whoever blesses others will be blessed by the Master of the World, in accordance with His promise (*Bereishis 12:3*), "And I will bless those who bless you."

— See *Berachos 55a*, and it is codified in *Shulchan Aruch* and *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken, Orach Chaim, sec. 201, clause 3*, that this applies to everyone from the seed of Avraham —

And it can be said that blessing one’s fellow is a matter of *gemilus chasadim*.

Now, our Sages of blessed memory have said (*Sotah 14a*), "The Torah begins with *gemilus chasadim* (clothing the naked, *Rashi*) and ends with *gemilus chasadim*... as it is written, 'And He buried him in the valley.'"

Torah means instruction (*hora'ah*), teaching us the knowledge: a) That one should never despair, for there is nothing that stands before *teshuvah*, as He is "abundant in kindness and ready to forgive." b) That even perfectly righteous individuals (*tzaddikim gemurim*) ask for nothing more than a free gift (*Sifrei* and *Devarim Rabbah*, beginning of *Va'eschanan*).

The proof is from the aforementioned: for they were at the ultimate depth—Adam and his wife were naked, and our Sages of blessed memory explain (*Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 19*) that "naked" means they were stripped even of the one *mitzvah* they possessed. Yet, the *Ribono shel Olam* clothes even such naked ones through *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above), in the manner of *gemilus chasadim*. For *gemilus chasadim* is greater than *tzedakah* (*Sukkah 49b*), as it is the extension of goodness (*Moreh Nevuchim, part 3, beginning of ch. 49*, cited in *Derech Emunah* by the Tzemach Tzedek on the verse "And He made garments of skin for Adam," sub-clause 1—this is page 67b—and see there).

And this is also true at the ultimate height, which may have been the case with Moshe Rabbeinu (*see Hilchos Teshuvah by the Rambam, ch. 7*). For fifty gates of understanding (*sha'arei binah*) were created in the world, and all of them were given to Moshe, lacking one. And *tzaddikim* are even greater in their passing, for in his death he attained the fiftieth gate, and regarding this it is said, "And no man knows his burial place" (*see at length in Likkutei Torah, beginning of the discourse "Me'at," with additional explanation on the concept of "And you shall count," and it is referenced in my letter to "HaChaver," Shavuos 5703*). Yet even this was *gemilus chasadim* and an *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is higher even than the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes from *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below) of the *Ribono shel Olam* (*see there in Likkutei Torah, "It is impossible for us to draw down... for this is drawn down afterward from above as a gift"*), in that He Himself occupied Himself with it, as it is written, "And He buried him." And the Mishnah concludes (*Sotah 9b*): "They said this not only regarding Moshe, but regarding all *tzaddikim*, as it is said, 'And your righteousness shall go before you, and the glory of Hashem shall gather you.'"

It can be said in a deeper sense that this specifically applies to *tzaddikim* who were in exile after exile, and according to the statement of our Sages of blessed memory (*Bereishis Rabbah, end of ch. 44*) that Avraham clarified the kingdoms, and the matter is understood.

Now, the aforementioned applies to the soul in general, and specifically to the year. The matter of "clothing the naked" occurred on *Rosh Hashanah*—the day of the creation of man—for every year is "poor" at its beginning (*see Rosh Hashanah 16b and Rashi there*), and we have nothing to do but plead: "Not by our deeds, etc., we remain naked, etc." And then we are promised that the *Ribono shel Olam* will make for us "garments of skin" from the "skin of the serpent" (*Targum Yonasan, Bereishis 3:21*), stripping the *kelipah* from the *guf* of the *tumah* and returning it to holiness. Then, from this, "garments of glory" are made (*Derech Emunah, ibid., sub-clause 12*), and they ascend from level to level until the *Chaf-Hei* (the twenty-five days of Elul), which is then the level of "desiring kindness" (*chafetz chesed*) that is higher even than *tzedakah* and mercy, for it applies even to the wealthy, as mentioned in *Maseches Sukkah* (*Likkutei Torah, end of Parshas Devarim*). And the ultimate height is on *Shemini Atzeres*, when we read, "And Moshe went up to Mount Nevo," to the fiftieth gate; the end is *gemilus chasadim*, for then it is "one bull... they shall be for you alone, and no strangers with you."

With blessings for a *chasimah v'gmar chatimah tovah*—immediately for *teshuvah*, immediately for *geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

170

B"H, Between the Throne and the Tenth [of Tishrei], 5705

To the distinguished *avreich*, man of valor, G-d-fearing, etc.,
The *Tamim*, Rabbi M.Z. [Gringlas], may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter—a letter of condolence.

Thank you. This can be understood based on what is known in many places: that the order is: *is'arusa d'le'eila* (which awakens and grants the strength for *is'arusa d'letata*), *is'arusa d'letata* (which must be fitting and a vessel to receive the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that follows it, in accordance with the *is'arusa d'letata*), an *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is higher than the *is'arusa d'letata* and the second *is'arusa d'le'eila* mentioned above (see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, the *maamar* beginning "Lehavin Inyan HaTa'am Lema SheHaIs'arusa," and elsewhere).

Specifically regarding the comfort of mourners (which the *Bahag* counts as a *mitzvah* from the Torah, and according to the Rambam it is at least a *mitzvah* from the Sages; see the Rambam’s *Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Shoresh* 1, and the commentaries there), the order is likewise in this manner:

1) *Is'arusa d'le'eila*: (Sotah 14a) "The Holy One, Blessed be He, comforted mourners..." (and it was related and revealed to us in this regard, for this gives you the strength, and since strength was granted for this, it follows that it is an obligation that) "you, too, comfort mourners."

2) *Is'arusa d'letata*: The act of comforting, and the formula is, "May the *Makom* (the Omnipresent) comfort you..." among the other mourners of Zion and Jerusalem (which also includes a preparation for the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that will come afterward), for just as He comforted mourners, so too [He acts] through his *is'arusa d'letata*.

3) *Is'arusa d'le'eila*: The Holy One, Blessed be He, will comfort the mourner and all the mourners of Zion and Jerusalem through the rebuilding of Zion and Jerusalem and the resurrection of the dead, and even more than this, so that there will be...

4) *Is'arusa d'le'eila* that is higher than the second *is'arusa d'le'eila* mentioned above—meaning that the comfort of the Holy One, Blessed be He, will be a double comfort (and not merely a return of the former state), as it is written, "Comfort, comfort [my people]," twice, for "the **glory** of this latter house shall be greater" than the former.

This refers to the house of the future, according to the interpretation of the *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 8, and it is also explained in the *Sefer Chassidim*, *Sha'ar Kiryat Arba*, section 52. This is the foundation for why I explained it this way in the *Bein HaMetzarim* booklet. One should not raise a difficulty from the literal meaning of the verse (and see also *Bava Basra* 3a, end of side a—that it refers to the Second Temple; this must be reconciled according to the Midrash—cited in Rashi, Yechezkel 43:11, brought in the opening of the *Tiferes Yisrael* to *Maseches Middos*, and see also *Berachos* 4a, end of side a—that the Third Temple was worthy to have been built at the time they ascended from Bavel, but the sin caused [the delay]).

It is worth noting *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning "Shos Asis," end of section 3, and the aforementioned *maamar* "Lehavin," sections 6 and 207, regarding the connection between double comforts and the third *is'arusa d'le'eila*.

With blessings for a *Chasimah* and *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*—immediately to *Teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

I enjoyed what you wrote in your letter regarding the resurrection of the dead from several perspectives, but in my opinion, the connection and *hishtalshelus* (chain of descent) from one concept to the next is missing, and a little "spice" should be added to correct this. It is as follows: The concept of death in general is—"He who falls from his level is called dead" (this is in *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning "Zos Chukas," end of section 2, and elsewhere; for the time being I have not found this exact phrasing, and time does not permit searching, but in *Zohar Chadash* 125b—cited in *Etz Chaim*, *Sha'ar Sheviras HaKeilim*, Chapter 2, and in *Mevo She'arim*, *Sha'ar* 2, Part 2, beginning of Chapter 3—it says, "He who descends from his former level upon which he stood, one calls him dead").

Now, in a person there are: 1) The *Nefesh Elokis*, 2) The *Nefesh HaSichlis* (intellectual soul), 3) The *Nefesh HaBahamis* (animal soul), 4) The body (it can be said that these are four levels, from below to above, *domem, tzomei'ach, chai, medaber*). 1) The *Nefesh Elokis*—its level is literally a part of G-d from above, and if it falls from this level, in that it is not in a state of *ratzo* (running) to cleave to G-dliness, it is called dead; the remedy for this is study, contemplation, and conduct according to the **teachings of Chassidus.** 2) The *Nefesh HaSichlis*—its purpose is to understand the *Nefesh HaBahamis* through intellect and *mochin* (mental faculties) as to how to conduct itself in its *midos*. Now, a child—both in years and in mind—has *midos* that are forceful and an intellect that is small; if the *Nefesh HaSichlis* is dragged after desires, even those that are permissible, like an animal, this is a fall from its level and is called dead. This is the concept of **education** (*chinuch*)—to establish him upon the correct path of conduct. 3) The *Nefesh HaBahamis*—it should be, by its own nature, at least like the beasts and animals that do not change their function. But if one commits a prohibition or a transgression, violating the will of its Creator, this is a fall from its level and is called dead; "The wicked in their lifetime are called dead," until, through rebuke and the fact that his fellow awakens him, he is aroused to *Teshuvah* and to strengthening the observance of *Torah* and *Mitzvos*, and returns to the **camp of Israel.** 4) The body—its purpose is as a vessel for the soul, and if the connection between them is severed, this is a fall from its level, death in the literal sense, and it is incumbent upon those who deal with it (**Chevra Kadisha**) to arrange everything so that it is prepared for the resurrection of the dead, speedily in our days.

May the Almighty merit us, speedily and in our days, to the fulfillment of the promise, "He will swallow up death forever... on the third day He will raise us up, and we shall live before Him," in body and soul together.

## 171

B"H, First Day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5705

To the honorable Rav, renowned for his praise, wise and learned, G-d-fearing, a man of vitality, a man of many accomplishments, engaged in communal needs with faith, etc., Moreinu Harav Eliyahu, may he live, known as Dr. Jung, New York.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter, along with the report regarding the printing expenses of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, was received in due time. Please accept my apologies for the delay in responding until now, caused by the pressure of work, especially at the beginning of the new term. Enclosed is the response from the editorial board of the Merkos.

I will take this opportunity to express my gratitude and the gratitude of the Merkos for your attention to our work, and I hope that you will use the power of your significant influence to expand the circle of those who study and read the books published by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

And to conclude with a matter concerning these days between Yom Kippur and Sukkos:

The Maharil writes: Immediately after Yom Kippur, every person should busy himself with building his Sukkah, because the days of teshuvah have concluded, and on the first day that one might enter into sin, G-d forbid, he should prioritize beginning a mitzvah. This content is cited in the Rema, Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, end of section 624.

A deep hint is alluded to here: When a person has done teshuvah for the past and fears that he might fall into sin in the future, there is a remedy for this—he should busy himself with the Sukkah.

This means: The most common reasons that lead an upright person to sin and transgression are that he errs in saying that Torah and mitzvos are only for a set time of the day, and afterwards he is free to do as he pleases; or he says that Torah and mitzvos belong only to a specific limb of the person: the head (the ethical teachings within the Torah are sufficient), the heart (the Merciful One desires the heart, and the actual performance of mitzvos is merely secondary and not essential), and the like.

But when he engages his intellect and contemplates the mitzvah of Sukkah—the first mitzvah after the atonement of sins—he will see that it must be "dwell as you live" (Sukkah 26a), for the mitzvah is the person's **dwelling**, and it encompasses the entire body of the person from the sole of his foot to the crown of his head, including his garments and his utensils as well.

With holiday greetings and a *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

172

B”H, Thursday, 28 Tishrei, 5705

To the distinguished Rabbi, the chossid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, etc.,
Rabbi M.A. Halevi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter reached me, and due to the rush, the response has been delayed until now, for which I ask your forgiveness.

I will address your points one by one:

1. You raise a point regarding what was brought in the third volume of the *Lubavitch* collection (p. 39), concerning the well-known difficulty with the statement in the *Zohar* (Vol. II, 183b) that on Shavuos, *chametz* is offered upon the *Mizbeach*. Yet, *shtei halechem* are not offered upon the *Mizbeach*. You write that the *sefer* *Lachmei Todah* resolves this by stating that it is also said in the Torah, "You shall offer the first fruits..." [as a *korban*], and even though they are eaten by the *kohanim*, this is because they merit them from the "Table of the Most High" (*shulchan gavoha*), which equates the eating of the *Mizbeach* with the eating of the *kohanim*, and it is as if they were burned upon the *Mizbeach*. You add that this is the superior answer, and you bring proof from *Menachos* (6a) and *Chullin* (120a), where the Sages say that *neveilah* is not considered "permitted from its general prohibition" because the *kohanim* eat the *chatas ha'of* that was *melikah*—because they merit it from the "Table of the Most High."

Now, I have not seen the *sefer* *Lachmei Todah*, and I have not been able to find it here among my acquaintances. Perhaps there is an additional explanation there beyond what you wrote. However, as it is transcribed in your letter, the entire argument is problematic, and since it is Torah, I must learn:

a) Regarding your proof from the verse (*Vayikra* 2:12), "You shall offer the first fruits..."—the verse concludes there explicitly, "But they shall **not** be offered upon the *Mizbeach*." If so, on the contrary, this verse strengthens the difficulty! If your intent is to bring proof that the Torah calls *shtei halechem* a *korban*, then the wagons of the *Nesi'im* (*Bamidbar* 7:3) and the gold vessels from the spoils of Midian (*ibid.* 31:50) are also called a *korban*, even though they were neither burned nor eaten.

b) Regarding the resolution that the *kohanim* merit from the "Table of the Most High"—this is highly questionable. Seemingly, it has no relevance to the difficulty at all. The principle of "meriting from the Table of the Most High" is a law regarding the **status of the *korban***, whereas the statement of the *Zohar* and the difficulty raised against it concern the *manner* of eating or burning the *korban*—which is a law regarding the **status of the *kohen*** or the **status of the *Mizbeach***. In *Menachos* and *Chullin* (ibid.), where it is resolved that they merit from the "Table of the Most High," the intent is also that the **meat** belongs to the Most High and not to a commoner, and therefore *neveilah*—in this meat—is permitted.

c) You resolve that the eating of the *kohanim* is equated to the eating of the *Mizbeach*—apparently referring to the Sages' teaching on the verse, "If it is eaten, it shall be eaten..."—that it is as if it were burned upon the *Mizbeach*. This is difficult, for the "eating of the *Mizbeach*" is not necessarily burning; the pouring of the *shirayim* (remnants) is also called "eating of the *Mizbeach*" (*Zevachim* 13b). Perhaps the language is not precise and you intended the discussion in *Kiddushin* (52b), "And this shall be yours from the Most Holy things, from the fire..."—just as fire [consumes], so too... However, aside from the fact that this is a subject of dispute there, it is a great stretch to interpret the *Zohar’s* language, "burned in the fire of the *Mizbeach*," as referring to the eating of the *kohanim* being equated to burning upon the *Mizbeach* (especially according to what is written in *Mikdash Melech*, "Upon the *Mizbeach* means through the power of the illumination of *Malchus*, which is called *Mizbeach*"—this does not apply to the eating of the *kohanim*. See the explanation of this in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Tzav*, *d.h. Ve'achaltem*, section 2; *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvah of Eating Kodshei Kodashim*, *d.h. Ki Hu Yevarech*—to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory—from the year 5700).

Furthermore, it is not understood according to the **two** reasons mentioned above, because the plain meaning of the *Zohar* implies that there is a novelty in the *korban* of Shavuos, that at that time *chametz* is burned upon the *Mizbeach*. According to your explanation, this is strange, for this exists throughout the entire year—the *chametz* in the *Todah* offering, which the *kohanim* eat, and they merit from the "Table of the Most High." Moreover, the Sages even say that the eating of the owners is from the "Table of the Most High" (*Beitzah* 21a, and elsewhere).

The conclusion from the above: I have not merited to understand the words of the *Lachmei Todah*, nor have I grasped your reasoning for why you wrote that the resolution of the *Lachmei Todah* is the superior one.

* * *

2. You also write: You discuss that since it is forbidden to plant a tree in the *Azarah* due to the prohibition, "You shall not plant for yourself any tree," how did the *kohanim* eat the remnants of the *minchos* during *Chag HaSukkos*? You resolve that since they merit from the "Table of the Most High," it is considered the eating of the Most High, which is exempt from *Sukkah*.

There are several notes on this matter, but for you, brevity will suffice: a) The prohibition of "You shall not plant" applies only under two conditions: a structure of wood and also a permanent one (*Rambam*, *Hilchos Avodas Kochavim*, end of Ch. 6; the sources are noted in the commentaries). According to the *Kesef Mishneh* (*Rambam*, *Beis HaBechirah*, Ch. 1, Halacha 7), there must be a third condition: fixed to the building.

If so, one could build a *Sukkah* without these conditions, and the *sechach* consists of straw and leaves, not wood (see *Shabbos* 66a, and the *Or Sameach* on the *Rambam* there).

b) Even though it is forbidden to add to the structures of the *Beis HaMikdash* in any way because it is written, "All this in writing, from the hand of Hashem, He instructed me"—in a place of a fence, and certainly for a *mitzvah*, it is permitted (*Sukkah* 51b). Especially since one could say that indeed, in "the writing from the hand of Hashem," there was also a *Sukkah*.

c) Based on the above, the verse (*Nechemiah* 8:16), "And they made for themselves *Sukkos*... in the courtyards of the House of G-d," can be interpreted according to its plain meaning, referring to the *Azarah*, and there is no need to force the interpretation that it refers to the Temple Mount.

Note the discussion in *Arachin* (3b) and *Tosafos* (*d.h. U'vnei*), and see *Tamid* (27a), that all twenty-four places were outside the *Azaras Yisrael*.

d) Even if we interpret the verse in *Nechemiah* as referring to the Temple Mount, one must conclude, as explained in notes a-b above, according to the *Sifri* (*Parshas Shoftim*)—cited in the *Kesef Mishneh*—that even one who builds on the Temple Mount violates a negative commandment.

e) What is written in *Yalkut Shimoni* (*Shoftim*), "You shall not plant for yourself a tree—even a house, even a *Sukkah*," according to the plain interpretation, does not refer at all to a *Sukkah* of *mitzvah*, but to a *Sukkah* in general. It says "even a *Sukkah*" in contrast to a house, similar to what is written (*Bereishis* 33:17), "And he built for himself a house, and for his cattle he made *Sukkos*," and so on.

f) In the *Sifri* (end of *Parshas Re'eh*): "The festival of *Sukkos* you shall make for yourself seven days—for a commoner. And from where do we know that it applies even to the Most High? The verse says..." In the *Sifra* (end of *Parshas Emor*): "Can it be that the *Chagigah* and the *Sukkah* are for the Most High? The verse says... How is this? The *Chagigah* is for the Most High, and the *Sukkah* is for the commoner." Even after the commentators resolve the contradiction between these two statements, it is still a matter of deep inquiry.

g) Regarding eating the remnants of the *minchos* in the *Azarah*, it is seemingly clear that it is exempt from *Sukkah*, for this is the rule for this *mitzvah*: "You shall dwell in the *Sukkah* as you conduct yourself in your home throughout the year" (*Sukkah* 27a). Just as throughout the year the *kohanim* would not eat the remnants except in the *Azarah* and not in their own homes, so too during *Chag HaSukkos* they would do the same.

And if you ask: If eating *Kodshei Kodashim* is exempt from *Sukkah*, what is the status of common food (*chullin*) there? (See at length in *Mishneh LaMelech*, *Hilchos Shechitah*, Ch. 2, Halacha 3, and sources cited there). If so, why did they make *Sukkos* in the courtyards of the House of G-d (if we interpret it as the *Azarah*)? This is not a difficulty at all, for the *mitzvah* of *Sukkah* is not only for eating and drinking,* but for all one's activities. And it is permitted to linger in the *Azaras Yisrael*, and even to enter there even not for the purpose of the *avodah*, as it is stated in *Keilim* (Ch. 1, Mishna 8): "The *Azaras Yisrael*... the *Azaras Kohanim* is more sanctified than it, for Yisrael do not enter there except at the time of their needs."

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah*—immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

\*) Rabbi A. Ziskind pointed out to me that we find an obligation of *Sukkah* in the *Azarah* even for eating, based on the above, regarding the eating of *Lachmei Todah* and the like, which are permitted throughout the city and are eaten even in the *Azarah* (*Shevuos* 15a).

## 173

173

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5705
Brooklyn

To my esteemed friend, the energetic activist and man of many accomplishments, etc.,
Mr. R. S. Palmer,
Chicago.

Peace and Blessing!

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, is, B"H, feeling better. May Hashem grant him a complete and speedy recovery immediately.

In response to your letter of Nov. 28:

Generally, it is difficult to obtain a large quantity of Chanukah lamps, and if one does obtain them, the cost for the cheapest ones is 27–35 cents per lamp.

If you are in agreement with this price, please inform us as soon as possible, and also whether you are prepared to take fewer than 200 in the event that it is not possible to obtain the full number of lamps.

We find a remarkable thing regarding the miracle of Chanukah. The Gemara (Shabbos 21b) relates that the cruse of pure oil that was found was "placed with the seal of the **Kohen Gadol**." To have proof that the cruse remained untouched, it would be enough to know that it remained sealed; why then does the Beraisa tell us that it was the seal of the Kohen Gadol?

From this, we can learn that if it is dark for the Jewish people, G-d forbid—both physically and spiritually—and there are those who wish to "make them forget Your Torah and force them to stray from the laws of Your will," how can one ensure that a cruse of pure oil remains, from which one will subsequently light an entire Menorah? This is achieved by guarding the cruse with the "seal of the Kohen Gadol"—a Jew who, in the words of the Rambam (Hilchos Kelei HaMikdash 5:7), "would sit in the Mikdash all day and would not leave except to his home at night, for an hour or two during the day."

We find another remarkable thing regarding the Kohen Gadol. The Gemara (Yoma 18a) states: "The Kohen Gadol is greater than his brothers... his brother Kohanim must make him great."

Seemingly, if it is necessary for the Kohen Gadol to have funds and even be wealthy, why specifically from his brother Kohanim?

But the explanation is as follows: The Torah does not need to instruct a simple Jew. If one were to approach a simple Jew and say to him, "Listen, the Kohen Gadol needs funds; do you want to take part in this, and do you want to see to it that all your acquaintances take part in this?" it would never occur to him to run to a Rav to ask what the Shulchan Aruch says about it. He would also be afraid that **he** would lose the opportunity for the merit of participating in something connected to the Kohen Gadol. For after all, "I have not seen a righteous man forsaken"; Hashem will certainly provide the Kohen Gadol with everything he needs, but it might not be through this Jew. He will therefore see to it that he does not let the merit slip away, doing everything he can—both with others and himself—so that the **"making him great"** should be through him specifically.

However, when one approaches a Kohen, it can happen that he begins to say: "a) Why are you coming to me? I am a holy person regardless. I know myself what I have to do. Go and provide merit to others. b) You want me to busy myself with the expenses of the Kohen Gadol and also busy myself so that others participate? Do you know that the avodah of the Beis HaMikdash rests upon me? Ask the Kohen Gadol himself; he will tell you what is more important. If I busy myself with the Kohen Gadol, might the avodah of the Beis HaMikdash be neglected? Are you telling me to do that? And what do the Poskim say about such a thing? You are destroying the Beis HaMikdash with your own words! I will not allow that under any circumstances."

Therefore, the Torah warns: "Make him great from his brother Kohanim" (and even that warning does not always help!).

And, incidentally, we learn from the story of Chanukah: The Greeks reached the Beis HaMikdash; they were able to destroy the Mizbei'ach and defile the Menorah. But the small cruse of oil that lay hidden, which the **Kohen Gadol** had guarded—that remained intact and ignited lights that have been shining for thousands of years.

Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 174

B”H, Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, 5705

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated, who conducts his business with integrity,
Rabbi Y. HaKohen Katz,
Chicago.

Greetings and Blessings!

Thank G-d, the condition of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is improving. May Hashem grant him a complete and speedy recovery, and may the verse (Tehillim 55:19) be fulfilled in him: “He has redeemed my soul in peace... for there were many with me.”

I received your letter in due time with the request to send a copy of the Sukkos sichos. Until now, I was unable to fulfill your request, as I only received the finalized copy yesterday. I am enclosing my copy herewith (for you to read or copy, as you wish) and ask that you return it to me as soon as possible.

I conclude with a blessing for Chag HaGeulah, and that we may merit the complete Geulah speedily in our days, and that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will lead us toward Mashiach Tzidkeinu; immediately for Teshuvah, immediately for Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 175

B"H, 3rd of Chanukah, 5705

My esteemed and distinguished friend, Mr. Dov Padber,

Shalom and blessings!

I have asked Mr. Zaborodka a few times about how you and your family are doing, and it was a pleasure to hear that you have settled in here and that you and your entire family are well.

I was pleased to receive your short letter, even though you do not mention anything about yourself in it.

Your letter stirred memories of our time in the cities of Vichy and Nice, where each of us lived under conditions to which we were not accustomed.

When a person is uprooted from an environment in which they have become settled, until they adapt to the new conditions and demands, aspects of their inner character are revealed—as it truly is, without the "makeup and paint" that society demands.

Often, these traits reveal the good hidden within a person—good that perhaps they themselves were unaware of because it was covered by a layer of "worldly etiquette." Happy is the person who does not allow these traits to be obscured again once they reach a state of tranquility.

A person finds themselves in such a state of mind—though to a much greater degree, both in quality and quantity—at a time of mesiras nefesh. At such a moment, hidden, essential powers are revealed within them, which is why they are subsequently capable of changing their life from one extreme to the other.

This is the connection and the principle of "measure for measure": because of mesiras nefesh—an act that defies a person’s nature—a miracle occurs for them, an act that defies the general nature of the world.

This is also true in a general sense, for the entire nation, just as it was "in those days, at this time": Israel, a small nation among the nations, rose up against the mighty Greek kingdom, and through this, the strong were delivered into the hands of the weak, the many into the hands of the few, and so on.

With Chanukah blessings and regards to your entire family, for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have arranged for some of our publications to be sent to you in a separate package, which I am sure will interest you.

166

166

B"H, Sunday, 8 Teves, 5705

To the Honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the man of many deeds, wise and understanding, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav A.E. HaKohen, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the third night [of Chanukah]:

As you requested, your letter has been copied here, and my notes are attached. It reads as follows:

Regarding the doubt in the law of Shabbos concerning a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah* (a patient whose life is in danger)—how the practical ruling stands: is it *dchuya* (deferred) or *hutra* (permitted)? You have surely already seen the disagreement among the *Rishonim* brought in the *Beis Yosef* in *Hilchos Shabbos*, *Tur Orach Chaim* 328. Indeed, from the plain wording of our great teacher, the Rambam, of blessed memory, in *Hilchos Shabbos* chapter 2, law 1, it appears seemingly that he holds it is *dchuya*, and this is how the holy *Mishnah Berurah* there understood his words. (a) However, after reflection, it seems to me that since the Rambam writes in his *Commentary on the Mishnah* for *Maseches Shabbos* chapter 18:

(a) That the opinion of the Rambam is that Shabbos is **dchuya** in the face of *pikuach nefesh*—and according to the plain meaning of his language at the beginning of chapter 2 of *Hilchos Shabbos*—this is stated **explicitly** by: the *Beis Yosef* (in *Beis Yosef* 328 and *Kesef Mishnah*), the *Bach*, the *Rema* (*Darkei Moshe* 330), *Korban Nesanel* (end of *Yoma*), Rabbeinu HaZaken (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 328:13), *Machatzis HaShekel*, *Minchas Chinuch* (end of Mitzvah 32), and others. (See also *Biurei HaGra* on *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah* at the end of 266). The author of the *Aruch HaShulchan* (*Yoreh Deah* 266) suggests that the Rambam was not precise in his language and that he holds Shabbos is *hutra*, but he himself retracted this (*Orach Chaim* 328:3) and wrote that "there is no necessity to take the words of the Rambam out of their plain meaning."

"That this desecration was only permitted to be done because of the great necessity," etc.—and our teacher did not neglect to bring this law of "because of the great necessity" in his *Halachos*—this implies that he retracted in his old age what he held in his youth. Our teacher’s intent here is deep and clear, and it is based on what he established in *Hilchos Shevuos* 5:11, where he writes that one who swears not to sleep for three days or not to eat anything for seven days, we lash him, and he may sleep and eat whenever he wishes. See the *Kesef Mishnah* there regarding the opinion of the *Ran* on this—meaning that he holds that what is permitted on account of danger effects a nullification of the essence of the matter (whereas the *Ran* would hold that the matter remains in its state of prohibition, only that the danger overrides the prohibition)—ponder this and understand. (b) Here, too, our teacher’s intent is that we should not say that in truth there is a law of Shabbos here, only that the danger overrides the prohibition alone—that is not the case; rather, the very body of Shabbos is deferred on account of the danger. This is what our teacher emphasizes by saying that Shabbos is *dchuya* in the face of *sakanah*. He did not touch here on the terminology of *dchuya* or *hutra* found in the *Gemara*, but rather to emphasize the law that the Shabbos itself has gone away for a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*, as if the essential law of keeping Shabbos did not exist regarding him, like the case of *Shevuos* mentioned above. Based on this, the reasoning of the *Mechilta* on *Parshas Ki Sisa*, *Masechta d'Shabsa*, on the verse "those who desecrate it"—*Rabbi Yehudah ben Beseira* says: "Since we have desecrated a part of it, shall we desecrate all of it? The verse says 'those who desecrate it shall be put to death,' even for a moment" (c)—will be clarified. The verse was needed to obligate one for Shabbos after the danger has passed, because since the body of

(b) It requires study whether the law of one who swears not to eat for seven days is relevant to our case at all. For there—the reason of the one who says he may eat immediately is (as written in the *Kesef Mishnah*) because it is a *shevuas shav* (vain oath), because he swore regarding a *mitzvah* or regarding something he cannot **fulfill**. And what difference does it make if he cannot fulfill it because it is *hutra* or because it is *dchuya* or because of nature (like not sleeping for three days)? And the reason of the *Yerushalmi* that the oath takes effect is, one could say, because his oath is not against nature, and it is also not against the *mitzvah* since the *mitzvah* does not take effect until he is in danger. There is more to say on this, as I wrote in *Teshuvos U'Biurim* Section 4 (*Kovetz Lubavitch*, issue 4).

(c) Seemingly, the intent of the *Mechilta* is clear: the inclusion of the verse is necessary so that we do not say that since this Shabbos is already desecrated and standing [as such] by these people, we should interpret "those who desecrate it" to mean one who has not yet desecrated it—thus excluding this Shabbos which has already been desecrated and is standing—similar to the way of our Sages in *Nazir* (42b). In truth, in *Nazir*, where there is no extra verse, the law is indeed so. With this, one can refute the proof from *Shabbos* to *Nazir* in the question of the *Minchas Chinuch* (Mitzvah 264) on the Rambam, *Hilchos Avel* end of chapter 2. One could also say: (If you will say—see on this *Tzafnas Paneach*, by the Gaon the Rogatchover, 2nd edition, Vol. 1, p. 26a-d) time is one continuum; consequently,

Shabbos is deferred—meaning as if it did not exist—therefore, a verse is indeed needed for a part of Shabbos, even for a moment, see there and understand, for it is a correct proof. In truth, the aforementioned doubt, whether it is *dchuya* or *hutra*, its source is in the *Yerushalmi*, *Maseches Eruvin* chapter 10, law 2, where one [Amora] posits it regarding a child in danger, and his colleagues (in the text it reads *chavraya*) challenge him: "If it is a child in danger, let them bring [the medicine] by hand," and he says to him, "He can bring it in a permitted way," see there in the commentators of the *Yerushalmi*. Thus, the opinion of the *chavraya* is that it is *hutra*. Apparently, this is the root of the disagreement (d). However, most *Rishonim* agree with the *Maharam of Rothenburg*, the teacher of the *Rosh*, that Shabbos regarding a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah* is like *Yom Tov*, where *ochel nefesh* (preparing food) is permitted. See the *Teshuvos* of the great *Tashbetz*, Vol. 3, section 37, s.v. *HaRamban z"l*. Similarly, the *Beis Yosef* assumes this (e) in the *Shulchan Aruch* there, sections 14 and 12. As he explains, regarding Shabbos, a [scriptural] inclusion is needed **that he is liable** even though he has already desecrated it, whereas in *Nazir*, where every single act of his is a separate matter in itself, on the contrary, a study is needed **that he is exempt** if it is already desecrated and standing. An example of the above (though not exactly similar): one who ate on *Yom Kippur*, is he obligated to fast the rest of the day? In the book *HaMoadim B'Halacha*, I saw it noted that this is discussed in *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Bnei Tzion* Vol. 1, *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Sho'el U'Meishiv* 1st edition Vol. 1, *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Sha'arei Deah* Vol. 2, *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Maharsham* Vol. 1, and these books are not with me. True, according to this interpretation of the *Mechilta*, the length of the language "and behold," etc., still requires study—for what difference does it make in what manner it was desecrated (unlike the interpretation in your letter)? And there is more to say.

(d) Seemingly, there is no disagreement here, only a question and answer.

In any case: see *Yoma* (6b) that even according to the one who says it is *hutra*, if there are pure [priests] available—the impure ones do not perform the service. So, too, the law must be here. (Also, according to the "some say" there that it is permitted for the impure ones, one could say that the Temple service is different, as it contains two aspects of a *mitzvah*: a) that the service be performed, b) the priest performing the service is doing a *mitzvah*, only that this does not override ritual impurity. But according to the one who says it is *hutra*, there is no prohibition here, so why would the impure priest be permitted for his *mitzvah*? Unlike the *Yerushalmi*, where there is no *mitzvah* in bringing [the medicine] specifically through a public domain). See also *Tosafos* s.v. *Shelo* (*Shabbos* 130b).

(e) From the language of the *Beis Yosef* (on the *Tur*), it is explicitly implied that he holds it is *dchuya*, and there is no foundation to say that he retracted this in the *Shulchan Aruch*. In the *Magen Avraham* (sub-section 9), he brings the reasons why we slaughter for a patient, etc., **both according to the one who says it is hutra and according to the one who says it is dchuya**, but he does not explain the conclusion of the *Shulchan Aruch*. See the *Pri Megadim*, who also writes that the *Shulchan Aruch* implies that he holds it is *dchuya*. Seemingly, a conclusive proof that it is *dchuya* is from the law in section 16, "they assessed him for two," etc. (as written in the *Biurei HaGra* mentioned above). Likewise, one can bring a proof from section 328, section 7, that we feed the patient little by little, etc.

Besides all this, since the Rambam (at least according to the *Beis Yosef*), the *Rashba*, and the *Ran* hold that it is *dchuya*—the *Rosh* is a lone opinion against them—only these opinions were brought in the *Beis Yosef*—and according to his methodology, he must rule in the *Shulchan Aruch* according to the majority opinion.

His opinion is that of the *Magen Avraham* (sub-section 9), and by his words we live. And from the words of *Tosafos* *Shabbos* 133, s.v. *Lo'es b'shinav*, there is no proof for those who say in the *Rema* there, section 12, that one should distinguish between *milah* (circumcision) and other *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah* cases, as the *Magen Avraham* distinguishes in the name of the *Maggid Mishnah* in section 330, sub-section 2, see there.

And see, I found in *Yeshuos Yaakov*, *Orach Chaim* section 328, sub-section 2, that he brings a clear and conclusive proof (f) for the opinion of the authorities who hold that Shabbos is *hutra* regarding a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*—from that which is in *Shabbos* 30a: "The first clause, with what are we dealing? If it is a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*, it is permitted, [so] it should have said [so]!" And if we say that it is only *dchuya*, we say in *Beitzah* 22a, "What is the law regarding extinguishing a lamp," etc., "if it is possible in another house, [if] he does not have another house, it is possible to make a partition," etc. If so, when he extinguishes for the sake of a patient, even though he is in danger, the term "exempt" is appropriate, but not the term "permitted," since it is possible with a partition or to bring the lamp into another house, for the standard case is so. Therefore, *ab initio*, he is obligated to do it via a partition or by inverting a vessel, and indeed he is exempt when he did it immediately via extinguishing, since it was done for the sake of a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*. Rather, certainly the standard of the *Shas* (g) is like the opinion of the *Rosh*, the *Tur*, and the *Beis Yosef* in the *Shulchan Aruch* that Shabbos is completely *hutra* regarding him. See in *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim* section 85, where he refutes the comparison from Shabbos to ritual impurity, from the *Shas* explicitly at the end of *Perek Teref B'Kalfi* to distinguish regarding the Temple service between Shabbos, which is *hutra*, and impurity, which is *dchuya*, see there.

From all these, it appears that the opinion of the majority of the authorities, *Rishonim* and *Acharonim*, is that Shabbos is a complete permission regarding a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*, and such is the opinion of our teacher the Rambam, as I wrote above, and the *Mechilta* supports him as mentioned.

(f) The book *Yeshuos Yaakov* is not at hand, but: see the *Commentary on the Mishnah* there, where he writes: "And this patient is a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah*, and on the condition that it is impossible to take him to another place or to hide the light from him." And like the language of the *Mishnah*, **because of the patient**, meaning that there is no other reason: that he does not want to exert himself, etc., and thus the proof of the *Yeshuos Yaakov* falls away.

(g) From *Menachos* (64a), "a patient whom they assessed," etc., from the *Mishnah* (*Shabbos* 133a) that he chews with his teeth (even though he is a *choleh sheyesh bo sakanah* as written there in *Tosafos*. And the distinction of the *Magen Avraham* section 330, sub-section 3, is plausible to say for the one who says **there is** a prohibition here but it is deferred, whereas for the one who says it is *hutra*, it is not, and see in *Shulchan Aruch HaRav* there), from the language of the *Ragil*: *pikuach nefesh* **overrides** [docheh], etc.—and does not say "permits"—it implies explicitly **that it is dchuya** (and since he says in *pikuach nefesh* **overrides**, he also says regarding the Temple service that it **overrides**, even though the service is *hutra*. Whereas if you say that in all of them it is **hutra**, he should have said in every place **permits**).

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 127

B"H, Monday, 9 Teves, 5705

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., Rabbi Menachem Mendel, may he live,
Shochet u’Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the questions in your letter:

1) You ask for an explanation of the phrase found in many places, **"one hundred and twenty combinations of the Name Elokim."** How is this calculated, and what is the concept behind these combinations?

**Answer:** The calculation of the combinations is based on what is explained in *Sefer Yetzirah* (Chapter 4, Mishnah 12; in some editions, 17): "Two stones build two houses... five stones build one hundred and twenty houses." The interpretation of this Mishnah is: "stones" refers to letters, and "houses" refers to words. "Two stones build two houses" means that from two letters, it is possible to form two words, each containing these two letters but in a different order. For example, the two letters Aleph and Beis build two words: *Av* (אב) and *Ba* (בא). Similarly, five letters (such as the letters Aleph, Lamed, Hei, Yud, Mem) can be combined in one hundred and twenty ways, each **different** from the other in the **order** of the letters, as is evident to the senses. Of these, 24 combinations begin with the letter Aleph, 24 with Lamed, 24 with Hei, 24 with Yud, and 24 with Mem. However, the primary combination is **Elokim**.

Now, every one of the 22 letters of the Torah is a unique light (and the form of the letter indicates the configuration of that light; see the end of *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe regarding this). The verse states, "In the beginning, Elokim created the heavens and the earth," meaning that the creation was through the Name Elokim (with the Name Havayah enclothed within it). The five letters of this Name indicate the five categories from which it is composed. It is therefore understood that when the combination (order) of the letters of this Name changes, the action produced by the Name also changes. The rule regarding this is known (*Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, ibid.): the letter that comes first in the combination is the dominant one and is the primary factor in the action resulting from that combination.

Elokim consists of the letters: *Eleh* (these) - *Yam* (sea). *Mi* (who). *Eleh* denotes revelation. *Yam* and *Mi* (which is unknown, and about which one asks) denote concealment and covering (see *Zohar Chadash* 2a and elsewhere; *Likutei Torah*, discourse *VeHayah Mispar Bnei Yisrael*, 62). Therefore, in the combinations of the Name Elokim that begin with the letters Aleph, Lamed, or Hei, the actions that follow from them manifest the Divine light and the flow from Above more openly and revealed. This is not the case with the actions from the combinations that begin with the letter Yud or Mem; since these letters are dominant in those combinations, as mentioned above, the Divine light within them is more concealed. Consequently, the *kelipos* and *sitra achra* derive their sustenance—after the descent and decline, etc.—only from these latter combinations, which number 48 (the 24 combinations beginning with Yud and the 24 beginning with Mem). This is the meaning of what is explained in *Chassidus* (*Hosafos LeTorah Or*, end of *Parshas Yisro*, and elsewhere), that the sustenance of the *kelipos* is from the 48 lower combinations of the Name Elokim, "the land of the sons of Cham."

In *Shaar HaKavanos* (*Inyan HaPesach*, Drush 1), it is also explained—at some length—regarding the 120 and 48 combinations of the Name Elokim. There, it is implied that specifically the *kelipah* of Mitzrayim derives its sustenance from these 48 combinations, but this is not the place to elaborate.

2) Regarding your question on the meaning of what is written in *Magen Avos* (discourse *Shuvah*, 202): "Ashrei is the opposite of the category of Havayah." The source of this is in *Yalkut Shimoni* (beginning of Tehillim), which states: "Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korcha said: The word **Ashrei** is written twenty times in the Book of Tehillim, corresponding to the twenty **Havayahs** in the Book of Yeshayahu." The explanation according to the literal meaning is that **Ashrei** denotes happiness and pleasure, while the word **Havayah** (in this context) denotes its opposite, namely, sorrow and grief.

The explanation according to *Chassidus* is found in the *Perush HaMishnayos* of the Tzemach Tzedek (printed under the title *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Part 2) on the verse "Ashrei yoshvei veisecha." It states that the word **Havayah** indicates that the *shefa* (flow) has withdrawn from *Yesod* (Yud) to *Tiferes* (Vav) and from there to *Binah* (Hei), and its opposite is **Ashrei** (*Asher*-Yud), because *Asher*, which denotes *Alma D'Atei* (the World to Come, *Binah*), shines upon *Ze'er Anpin* until it is drawn into *Yesod* (Yud). As for what is written in *Magen Avos* (in the discourses of *Machatzis HaShekel* and elsewhere) that *Yesod* is "orphaned" from *Binah*, that refers specifically to the time of *Golus*.

(In the *Siddur* of the Maharid on the verse "Ashrei yoshvei," it is explained that they have ascended to *Keter*. However, this is difficult to understand, as the word **Oi** denotes this, not **Havayah**, as is written in *Pardes*, *Shaar Archei HaKinuyim*, entry "Oi" and "Havayah," and it is noted in the *Perush HaMishnayos* there.)

3) The 288 *nitzotzin* (sparks) are explained in their specific levels in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar* 18. As for the reason for the number 288, the text there (Chapter 2) states: "The origin of the number 288 *nitzotzin* is the four categories of *Av* that descended from these four *Havayahs* (*Havayah* of *Av*, *Sag*, *Mah*, and *Ban*), and all of them together are 288 *nitzotzin*." See also *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Krias Shema*, Chapter 9, regarding this, and *Maseches HaNitzotzin*.

Regarding what is relevant to this: See *Torah Or*, *Vayeshev* (discourse *VeHineh Anachnu Me'almim*, 62), that the number 288 existed while they were still in *Atzilus*. But when they fell from *Atzilus* to the world of *Beriah*, and when they fell from *Beriah* to *Yetzirah*, and from *Yetzirah* to *Asiyah*, they were further divided and separated into thousands and myriads. With this, one can understand why the *Golus* has lasted so long; it is known that the entire purpose is to refine the 288 *nitzotzin*, and when the refinements are completed, Moshiach will come, immediately. (In the gloss of the Tzemach Tzedek—from *Mevo She'arim*, *Shaar* 2, Part 3, Chapter 9—he explains it in another way; see also *Emek HaMelech*, *Shaar Olam HaTohu*, 253). In *Torah Or*, *Bo*, discourse *BeEtzem HaYom HaZeh*, it says: "The 288 *nitzotzin* fell in *Sheviras HaKeilim*, and from this, 202 *nitzotzin* were refined during the *Golus* of Mitzrayim."

See also the discourses on *Vayeshev*—in *Torah Or* and *Torah Or HaHemshich*—and the discourse *Ish Al Diglo* (Parshas Bamidbar, 5700) for an explanation of the concept of *Sheviras HaKeilim* according to *Chassidus*.

With blessings for immediate *Teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 178

B"H, 23 Teves, 5705
Brooklyn

To the honorable management of Kolel Chabad, may they live and be well, and at their head:
The brilliant Rav,
The renowned Chossid, a man of understanding regarding a good matter,
A man of action, fear of Hashem,
Etc., my friend and colleague, Moreinu HaRav Sh. Y. L., shlita.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter, the letter of condolence, at its proper time. I had waited to reply, hoping I might be able to clarify the exact day of my father’s passing, may his memory be for a blessing, but as of now, I have not succeeded—the telegram was sent from there on the 12th of August, which is the 23rd of Menachem Av.

Many thanks for the arrangements regarding the fixed schedule of study and tefillah, etc., that you have established in memory of my father’s soul, may his memory be for a blessing. Likewise, for the tefillah for the health and peace of my mother, may she live, for long and good years.

"And a great act of kindness is greater, etc." (Sukkah 49b), for it is the extension of goodness (Moreh Nevuchim, Part 3, beginning of chapter 50, cited in Derech Emunah by the Tzemach Tzedek, on the verse "And He made garments of skin for man," see there).

Regarding the matter of comforting mourners according to Chassidic thought, it can be explained as follows:

It is known in many places and in many contexts that the order is: *is'arusa d'le'eila* (which awakens and gives the strength for there to be *is'arusa d'le'tata*), *is'arusa d'le'tata* (which must be fitting and a vessel to receive the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes after the *is'arusa d'le'tata* and in accordance with the *is'arusa d'le'tata*), and an *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is higher than the *is'arusa d'le'tata* and the second *is'arusa d'le'eila* mentioned above (see *Likutei Torah*, Shir HaShirim, the *maamar* beginning *Lehavin Inyan HaTa'am*, and elsewhere).

So too it is with comforting mourners (and the *Bahag* counts it as a positive commandment from the Torah, and even according to the Rambam, it is at least a positive commandment from the Sages; see the Rambam’s *Sefer HaMitzvos*, Principle 1, and the commentaries there): the order is likewise in this manner:

1) *Is'arusa d'le'eila*: (Sotah 14a) "The Holy One, Blessed be He, comforted mourners, etc." (And it has been told and revealed to us in this regard that this gives a person strength, and since strength has been given for this, it follows that it is an obligation that) "you too should comfort mourners."

2) *Is'arusa d'le'tata*: The act of comforting, and the formula is "HaMakom will comfort you, etc., among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim" (in which is also included a preparation for the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that will come after this), which is just as He comforted mourners, so too in His *is'arusa d'le'tata*.

3) *Is'arusa d'le'eila*: The Holy One, Blessed be He, will comfort the mourner and all the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim through the building of Tzion and Yerushalayim and the resurrection of the dead, and even more than this, so that there will be:

4) An *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is higher than the second *is'arusa d'le'eila* mentioned above—meaning that the comfort of the Holy One, Blessed be He, will be a double comfort (and not merely a return of what was lost), as it is written, "Comfort, comfort [My people]," twice, for "the glory of this latter House shall be **greater**" specifically.

This refers to the House of the future, according to the interpretation of the *Tikkunei Zohar*, Tikkun 8, and it is likewise explained in the book *Emek HaMelech*, Gate of Kiryat Arba, section 52. One should not raise a difficulty from the literal meaning of the verse (and see also *Bava Basra* 3a, beginning of the page—that it refers to the Second Temple, for they must be reconciled according to the Midrash—cited in Rashi on Yechezkel 43:11, and brought in the introduction of the *Tiferes Yisrael* to Maseches Middos; and see also *Berachos* 4a, beginning of the page—that the Third Temple was worthy to be built at the time they ascended from Bavel, but the sin caused [the delay]).

It is worth noting *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning *Sos Asis*, end of section 3, and the *maamar* beginning *Lehavin HaInyan* mentioned above, sections 6 and 207, regarding the connection between double comforts and the third *is'arusa d'le'eila*.

With the blessing of "immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

P.S. Please be so kind as to inform me regarding all the expenses involved in all of the above.

179

23 Teves, 5705
Brooklyn

To the honorable, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Ch. H. Havlin, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 13 Menachem Av, and in response to the questions in that letter and previous ones, which have not yet been answered:

a) The health condition of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, is steadily improving. Nevertheless, we continue to recite some chapters of Tehillim here every day after davening (in addition to the regular shiur, as divided for the days of the month). May Hashem send him a complete and speedy recovery, and may he stand among the many.

b) We are sending you immediately one hundred copies of everything we have printed here, without waiting for your order, except for those in English (or Yiddish), of which we only send a few. If there are buyers for the aforementioned in larger quantities, please be kind enough to inform us, and we will send them as you request.

c) We only have a few copies of Tanya, so we could not fulfill your request. "Hayom Yom" and the Kuntres "Etz HaChaim" have not yet been printed. Currently in print: the Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa, Mishnayos with additions I found in various booklets that have not yet been printed), Hemshech VeKacha Mayim Rabim and Hecherim, etc., of the Rebbe Maharash, a Siddur for Talmud Torah and school (all tefillos in order, large letters, etc.). However, due to current conditions, I do not know when it will be completed; my hope is within two to three months.

d) In accordance with the above: Perhaps you have some Responsa or chiddushim from the Tzemach Tzedek that have not yet been printed? Please be kind enough to inform me of the content in brief, and I will know if they are among the aforementioned additions or not. I also repeat my previous request: if you find, in your possession or among your acquaintances, any notes, etc., on the Tanya, please have them copied at our expense and send them here (naturally, if they have not already been sent by someone from your camp), or any stories—received by tradition—regarding the Tanya.

e) We have not printed volume 3 of our book, and in truth, it is not so necessary, as we proceed here in the order of study directly from part two to part four.

f) The largest discount from the price of "our book" is one-third (and the shipping costs are also at our expense, which amounts to a large sum). Several institutions here look for a donor who buys the books and gives them as a gift to the institution. "Our book" is spreading, and we have already printed another edition of part one, as well as Birchas Hamazon (with the English translation).

g) The lack of funds is a major hindrance to our work in general and to printing matters in particular. Therefore, please be kind enough to use all the money belonging to us (Machne Israel, Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, Kehot) that is in your possession to purchase Tefillin with the parshiyos and send them to us for the Tefillin and Tzitzis department of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. Naturally, the Tefillin must be kosher without any doubt, but since they are needed for people who are only beginning to put on Tefillin thanks to our outreach, and one must not be stringent with them at all—would that they would, etc.—they must be small. Surely there will be no difficulties in shipping, since you have been receiving books from us from time to time for some years now. An early response on this would be appreciated.

h) Regarding the books you requested for the Yeshiva—from the Shulsinger publishing house—we are sending you one copy of each for now (except for the Shas), and when we receive payment for them, as mentioned above, we will send more as you inform us then.

i) You surely received the "Lubavitch" collections on time, and you will surely participate in the various sections within them. Please be kind enough to alert those involved in this matter accordingly.

j) I have not answered your letters for some time, as well as other letters, because of the tragedy that befell me with the passing of my father, may his memory be a blessing.

I will say what I heard from my father, may his memory be a blessing (with additional references), regarding the Mishnah (Mikvaos, end of chapter 7): "A needle that is lying on the edge of the cave, he would move it back and forth in the water; once the wave has passed over it, it is tahor."

There are many designations for the neshamah, and it is called according to its actions. The essential purpose of its descent is to connect the lowest level with the highest level (which is why the creation of the human body was changed, etc., as explained in the Chassidic discourses, specifically the discourse starting with "Zeh"—in Torah Or and elsewhere). This is the function of a **needle** (machat), which sews and connects so that the revelation below will be as it is above (see Likutei Torah, discourse on "Vayikra Korach"). And how does one reach this level, which is higher than before it descended into this world? It is through immersion in "many waters," which are specifically the troubles of the time of galus (explained at length in the discourse "Mayim Rabim," Torah Or, Parshas Noach; in Likutei Torah, in the three sections there, and elsewhere). And even though it is a great descent—"in the deep pit" (b'yeira amikta), the "cave" (me'arah)—nevertheless, it is a necessity for the ascent, the "advantage" (ma'alah) of the cave. The manner of immersion is "moving it back and forth" (molich u'mevi), ratzo v'shov, and not by relying on one support, both in the service of Torah and mitzvos and in the affairs of this world. For then it is proof that one is not enslaved to the nature of his body (similar to what is explained in Torah Or, the explanation of "Mayim Rabim" in Parshas Toldos, chapter 4; see also Rambam, Hilchos Deos, chapter 1-2, and the commentaries there). Once **"the wave has passed over it"** (from the verse "All Your breakers and Your waves have passed over me," and see also Yevamos 121a), **"it is tahor"**—and as has been explained regarding the greatness of the level of taharah in Likutei Torah, discourse on "D'li B'Ozri," section 6, "And also because this level is relevant to the neshamah as well, etc."—see there.

And it can be said that this applies specifically to those who went into galus—gal (wave) after galus—"she has been punished double," and according to the Sages (Bereishis Rabbah, end of chapter 44), that Avraham chose kingdoms, etc., their reward is consolation in double measure (explained in Likutei Torah, discourse on "Sos Asis," end of section 3; discourse on "Nachamu," beginning of section 9, and elsewhere).

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, Thursday, 26 Teves, 5705

[It is also] Yitzchak (the fifth letter of the *Havayah* — *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, p. 404a). And regarding the general healing that will be in the future (see the *maamar* "Samchuni" in *Derech Emunah* by the Tzemach Tzedek) in the days of Moshiach, who will come speedily in our days: the days of the harp of eight strings, and then they will say to Yitzchak specifically, "For You are our father." And see (Sanhedrin 94a) that the Holy One, Blessed be He, sought to make Chizkiyahu the Moshiach, etc., "until when," etc., "until he comes with spoils and spoils of spoils" (which has already been fulfilled in our days), etc., Chizkiyahu, who has eight names, etc.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 181

B"H, Tuesday, 2 Shevat, 5705
Brooklyn

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Menachem Mendel, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

I received your second letter in due time. I did not answer your questions from the first letter immediately due to the many pressures that have surrounded me.

The two checks you enclosed with your first letter were handed over immediately to the secretary of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and not long ago he told me that receipts for them have already been sent, as he instructed in his letter.

Also in the future, if you have any questions, I am prepared to look into them as I see fit, but please do not press me for an immediate response, as the work here regarding "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," "Machne Israel," and "Kehot" is overwhelming (and it is surprising that your honor has not yet participated in these efforts).

I have ordered that the "Lubavitch" collection, which was just published, be sent to you. As it appears from your letter, several sections of this collection will surely interest you.

Regarding what you noted in the margin of your letter concerning haste: it is explained in Chassidus that there is—at times—a virtue in this, such as the haste of the Exodus from Egypt, "for the people fled" (see Tanya, Chapter 31; Shlah, Maseches Pesachim 3a). It is explained at length in the Maamar "V'Kacha" 5637 that this applies as long as the *birurim* (refinements) are not yet complete. Therefore, in the future, on the contrary, the virtue will be "you shall not go out in haste" (Yeshayahu 52:12). See also the Sicha of Simchas Torah 5703, section 2.

In a lighter vein, one could say that even now this should be the case—"not in haste"—regarding everything pertaining to Kabbalah and Chassidus, which is called the "Tree of Life," as it transcends the level of *birurim* (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26; the Introduction to Beurei HaZohar; the Kuntres Eitz HaChayim of the Rebbe Rashab, and elsewhere).

It requires further study why the Jewish people were praised at the Giving of the Torah as "a hasty people" (Shabbos 88a, where even Rava agreed with this), even though at that time they were free from the *yetzer hara*.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

You have surely seen in *Kovetz Lubavitch*, Vol. 4, the response to your previous question regarding the explanation of the concept of Mishnayos being learned by heart according to the revealed Torah; it is in the supplementary notes and additions to what I had written to you previously.

One may add an insight — according to Chassidus — regarding the concept of "smelling and judging" (*morach v'dain*) based on what is explained in *Likutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning *Le'va'er Inyan HaMasa'os* (see also the introduction to *Biurei HaZohar*). It is also explained there that "not by the sight of his eyes nor by the hearing of his ears" refers to Chochma and Binah. It is explained elsewhere that Chochma and Binah correspond to *achilah* (eating) and *shetiyah* (drinking), whereas *rei'ach* (smell) corresponds to *ruach* (spirit/wind) and *avir* (air).

I would also note — in passing — that in *Zohar* Vol. III, 78a, which is cited there in *Likutei Torah*, it states that Shlomo also judged without witnesses and formal warning (*hatra'ah*). This is also found in *Shir HaShirim Rabbah* at the beginning, whereas in the *Shas* (Rosh Hashanah 21b) and the Targum, it is implied that they do not hold this view.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 183

183

B"H, Sunday, 7 Shevat, 5705

To the honorable Rav, the G-d-fearing man, the accomplished scholar, etc.,
Rabbi A. A. HaKohen, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following my letter of 8 Teves, which I trust arrived on time:

Regarding the explanation of the Mechilta on Parshas Ki Sisa on the verse "those who profane it" — for a long time, the lengthiness of the language describing how "idolaters surrounded the Land of Israel, etc." was difficult for me. What is the practical difference regarding the manner of the profanation? And even if one were to say that it means they profaned the Shabbos specifically with permission (as I wrote in the previous letter), the standard example for this in our Sages' teachings is *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) and a sick person.

Recently, however, I saw in *Responsa Toras Chesed* (by R. Shneur Zalman of Lublin), *Even HaEzer* 6:2, where he writes regarding this Mechilta — in relation to a different matter — "Since the Mechilta specifies 'in such a case where idolaters surrounded the Land of Israel, etc.,' it is evident from this that even for that [case], it is only in such a circumstance, where it is permitted for **all** of Israel to profane the Shabbos with **all** the labors they might require, etc., and the Shabbos is profaned **completely for all** of Israel. But for an individual, where he is permitted to profane the Shabbos for *pikuach nefesh* regarding a specific matter, etc." — end quote.

From the above, it is explained simply, and it also resolves the distinction that must be made between a *nazir* and the affliction of Yom Kippur versus Shabbos (which I mentioned in the previous letter): there, it is a matter pertaining to one's own body, whereas Shabbos is different. And based on the above, it is understood.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B”H, Sunday, 7 Shevat, 5705

Regarding the other participants, it seems that since they were told the time for payment is 9 Adar, they are waiting for that day.

It is not advisable at all to let the matter grow stale, and who knows, etc. (The left line of the letter *hei*—which alludes to action—is separated from the two lines that allude to thought and speech, as explained in Torah Or, in the *maamar* beginning *Chayav Inish Livsumei*; see also Bava Basra 130b, and Rashi, s.v. *ad*).

In my opinion, when you come here for your brother’s wedding, may he live, you should collect in person from all those who pledged for this, provided that the date written on the checks is 9 Adar. For those you do not see at the time of the wedding, it would be best to prompt them immediately via letters and subsequently by telephone (naturally, at the expense of Kehot).

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, writes in a letter: The Tzemach Tzedek said: A word spoken in speech is for the many; in writing—it is before the world; in print—it is for generations upon generations.

Fortunate is the man who, through his efforts, establishes words of Torah in print—for this is for generations upon generations.

—Especially regarding the inner dimension of Torah, concerning which it is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of section 26, that in the days of Moshiach, the (primary) engagement with Torah will be in this, but, etc., and see the introduction to the commentary on the Zohar—

With the blessing of “immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,”

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Perhaps one could be precise regarding the expression “generations upon generations” (*dorei doros*), meaning at least four generations, generations of years, generations of years (as our Sages of blessed memory said in Sanhedrin 99a regarding the verse “generation of generations”), based on what is written in the commentary on Tehillim by the Tzemach Tzedek (p. 144), that “generation to generation” refers to the entire Seder Hishtalshelus, etc., for every world is called a “generation” (*dor*). If so, “four generations” refers to the four worlds of ABYA, and just as the four worlds of ABYA include many worlds, so too the expression “generations upon generations” includes many, many generations. See also Likutei Torah, in the *maamar* beginning *B’yom Inyan Motza’eihem*.
