## 186

186

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5705

To the honorable Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and wise, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham Mordechai, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a temporary receipt for the 25 shekel you sent to the World Tehillim Society. Surely, you will continue to participate in this lofty matter in the future and involve others as well, as you will in the other affairs of Machne Israel and Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch. "He who adds, is added to," and any explanation of the great value of this matter is superfluous.

To note briefly: The Sefer Tehillim is analogous to the Torah, as is hinted at in the Gemara (Kiddushin 30a): "The Sages taught... the verses of the Torah; Tehillim is superior to it, etc."

The distinction between them can be understood from the words of our Sages (Berachos 3b): "Rabbi Eliezer said: Until midnight he would occupy himself with Torah study; from then on, with songs and praises." (And even according to the one who disagrees with this statement, it is only regarding the conduct of Dovid, but there is no necessity to create a dispute and say that he also disagrees regarding the nature of Torah and Tehillim. In Zohar Vol. I, 206b, it is written in accordance with Rabbi Eliezer.)

Now, the plague of the firstborn, which brought about the redemption from Egypt—as the simple meaning of the verse indicates—began at midnight, and they were in agony from midnight until the morning (beginning of Maseches Semachos; this disagrees with what is written in Shemos Rabbah, ch. 16).

It is explained in the Zohar (Vol. II, 37b) that Moshe knew that the decree would only be executed in the latter half of the night.

The reason is explained there: "Because 'Koh' (thus) is awakened." And this is understood based on what is explained in Zohar Vol. I (90b): "From it, the judgments (dinim) are awakened." See also Likutei Torah by the Arizal on Parshas Bo, on the verse "And the dwelling of the Children of Israel." Therefore, Moshe prophesied this prophecy specifically with the word "Koh," even though he surpassed all the prophets in that he also prophesied with "Zeh" (Sifri, Matos).

Just as at midnight there was a plague for Egypt and healing for Israel (Zohar Vol. II, 36a), so too did they say regarding the attribute of "Koh" in general (Zohar Vol. I, ibid.): The Holy One, Blessed be He, said to [Avraham], "Go out from your astrology... 'Koh'—this is the gate for prayer; through it one finds blessing, through it one finds that a person's request is granted... for even though it is judgment, it is as if this 'Koh' is mercy."

In the introduction to Tikkunei Zohar (page 15a, Vilna 5727 edition), the superiority of "Shema Yisrael **Havayeh**..."—which has 25 letters—over "Baruch Shem..."—which has 24 letters—is explained. The connection to the aforementioned "Koh" is understood based on what is written in the seforim, that Pharaoh said, "I do not know **Havayeh**," specifically, unlike the name Elokim.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Regarding 24 and 25, see Sotah (36b); Tosafos, s.v. *d'mizdabna* (Bechoros 50a).

## 187

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5705

To our esteemed and distinguished friend, the brilliant Rabbi, G-d-fearing, etc., our teacher Rabbi Avraham Goldberg, Fort Bragg, N.C.

Peace and Blessing!

Many thanks for sending us the list of members of the Association of Chaplains in the military. It is a pleasure for us to see your positive interest in the spiritual state of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in the military, as this constitutes *zikkui harabbim* (meriting the many).

Regarding the upcoming holiday of Pesach:

The first Pesach of the generations (which serves as a directive **for the generations**, unlike the Pesach of Egypt, which differed in several respects—*Pesachim* 9:5—and was merely a temporary directive) took place in the second year after the Exodus. Our Sages of blessed memory (*Gittin* 60b) state that the introduction and preparation for it was the matter of the *Parah Adumah* (Red Heifer). Now, the *Parah Adumah* purifies the impure and renders the pure impure; that is, we say to the *Kohen* (and some say to the **High** *Kohen*—*Parah* 4:1), "Go and render yourself impure" (with a **minor** impurity), even though this will force you to leave the *Beis Hamikdash* and your service there for a time, so that through this, it will be possible for a Jewish person, even one who has become impure through contact with the dead, to become purified and enter the *Beis Hamikdash*. Furthermore, it is called *Chukas HaTorah* for this very reason (*Bamidbar Rabbah* 19:1)—meaning it is a general principle for the entire Torah (see *Likutei Torah*, beginning of *Parshas Chukas*). The moral lesson for each and every one of us is understood.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 188

188

B"H, 25th of Nissan, 5705

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, descendant of holy lineage, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Moreinu Harav Y. Leiner, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter, which was received with some delay, and subsequently, due to various reasons, the response was further delayed—please accept my sincerest apologies.

Due to the immense pressures surrounding the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, he handed me your letter to review and respond to, and I am writing here what appears to me. I would be pleased to hear your opinion on what I write below.

1) Regarding what you wrote: "I was very distressed by the glosses of the *Kadosh Yisrael* in the *Siddur Torah Or*, in note 14, on the Psalm *Tefillah L'Dovid*. It is a mitzvah to resolve this." The text of the gloss (by the Tzemach Tzedek) reads: "Make glad the soul of Your servant, for unto You, **Adonai**, I lift up my soul." Note: (In another version: *Havayah*).

**Response:** The source for this has already been pointed out in *Shaar HaKollel*—by Rabbi R. D. Lavut—printed in Volume 2 of the aforementioned Siddur, Chapter 11, Section 23, which states: "This is brought in the *Zohar*, *Balak* 195b. See there in *Mikdash Melech* that these are the four letters of *Havayah*."

However, if I may be so bold, I would say: The glosses of the Tzemach Tzedek were copied from his own personal Siddur.

As is evident from the language of *Shaar HaKollel*, the Tzemach Tzedek’s own words are only the two words "In another version: *Havayah*." The copyist erred in marking the gloss, for its correct place is in verse 8: "There is none like You among the gods, **Adonai**," where in another version the name **Havayah** appears here, as mentioned in *Minchas Shai*.

If this is the case: a) The source for the Tzemach Tzedek’s gloss is easily understood, as in the *Zohar* and *Mikdash Melech* there, there is no absolute necessity that the name *Havayah* is written in the verse itself. b) It explains why the Tzemach Tzedek did not gloss verse 8, which has two versions: *Adonai* or *Havayah*. Especially since in the *Siddur* of the Arizal (by Rabbi Shabsai of Rashkov), which was among the Tzemach Tzedek’s books (found in the library of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita), it is printed: "Make glad... unto You **Adonai**..."—just as it is in **all** the books—(and yet the Tzemach Tzedek noted that there is another version). "There is none like You among the gods, **Havayah**..."—which differs from the conclusion of *Minchas Shai* and what is written in many places as *Adonai*—and regarding this, he did not add a note.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of pointing out a source for the words of our Sages (as in the present case), that "this is *shimush chachamim*, for this is to explain and resolve their words, as Rashi writes in *Berachos* 47a"—

Seemingly, this is not precise. For according to Rashi, even if one knows the source, if he does not know the **reason** and the **logic**, it is still considered **not** having performed *shimush chachamim*. This is understood from Rashi’s language in *Sotah* (22a). According to Rashi, the essence of Talmud—which is what is called *shimush chachamim* in *Berachos* and *Sotah*, coming after one has read (Scripture) and studied (Mishnah)—is the knowledge of the reasons for the *halachos* that depend on **logic**. A strong proof for this view of Rashi is in *Berachos* there, where it says that even if one has studied *Sifra* and *Sifrei*, he is still considered as not having performed *shimush chachamim*; yet in *Sifra* and *Sifrei*, the laws—in the vast majority of cases—are brought together with the verse that serves as their source.

However, this is the view of the Rambam and the *Shulchan Aruch*—who disagree with Rashi on this—that knowledge of the source is also included in the category of *Talmud* (and the passage in *Berachos* there can be resolved, but this is not the place to elaborate). See *Kuntres Acharon* to *Hilchos Talmud Torah* (by the Alter Rebbe), beginning of Chapter 2.

3) Regarding your remark that there is a matter here of the mitzvah of honoring one's father—even though it is the fourth generation—this requires study. Especially if, as mentioned above, this is a gloss of the Alter Rebbe, and thus the daughter is in the middle of the generations. See *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah* 240:24: "Some say, etc.," and see the *Nosei Keilim* there and the *Biur HaGra*. Even according to the second opinion there, which writes, "and it does not seem so to me, etc.," it could be said that this applies specifically to one's grandfather, as it concludes with a proof from the *Midrash*. For the *Midrash Rabbah* is discussing one's grandfather, but we have no proof for anything beyond that—that the mitzvah of honoring one's parents applies there as well. See Rambam (*Hilchos Eidus* 13:5): "A father with his son's son is disqualified, but with his son's son's son... he is qualified." And in the *Nosei Keilim* of *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah* 245 regarding *Talmud Torah*—there is a distinction between a grandson and a great-grandson. See *Hilchos Talmud Torah* (by the Alter Rebbe), Chapter 1, sections 8 and 9.

And although there is no proof, a slight hint to the contrary can be brought, that even after several generations there is a place for honoring parents, from the words of our Sages (*Bava Basra* 91b) on the verse, "And he set a throne for the king's mother"—referring to Ruth. Of course, this is merely a hint.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*,

**M. Schneerson**

Since the content of section 1 above will surely interest the many, I am taking the liberty of printing it in *Kovetz Lubavitch* in the "Responsa and Explanations" section. The merit of the many, the readers who are interested in these matters, comes through you.

## 189

189

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5705

To the distinguished and honored, man of action, G-d-fearing, and scholarly, etc.,
Mr. Alexander Cohen, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

You surely know that our friend Mr. Stulman, may he live, has sent the check for Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. On this occasion, I would like to express to you once again my heartfelt thanks for your hishtadlus, exertion, and work in this matter, both in the past and the present, and also, as we all hope, in the future. The primary "yasher koach" you receive is from the things themselves that are being accomplished and can continue to be conducted through these donations.

Regarding the first utterance at the time of Matan Torah: "I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Egypt" — it is asked (for example: Ibn Ezra, Shemos 20:1) that it should have stated something greater: "Who created heaven and earth and who made you." Aside from the fact that "Who created heaven, etc." is a greater thing, it would also be a stronger reason for **all** generations, whereas at the time, "Who brought you out of the land of Egypt" was seen only by that generation, and its **primary** importance was also only for them.

Chassidus answers this:

Creation is the act of making *yesh* from *ayin*; upon this rests the illumination of Elokus that is relevant to the worlds. Yet, Yetzias Mitzrayim, which could only occur through signs and wonders (Devarim 4:34) — meaning, by extracting the *yesh* from the principles and boundaries of that *yesh* and of creation (this is also the hint in the word "Yetzias Mitzrayim" — exiting Mitzrayim/boundaries, as in Eichah 1:3) — this was a much higher revelation of Elokus. And therefore, Yetzias Mitzrayim is mentioned at Matan Torah, which is also higher than creation and boundaries.

L’havdil, among people it is the same: to teach oneself, or a friend, to walk on a good path from the very beginning is, **proportionally**, an easy thing. However, if one must remake principles and exit boundaries in which one has become accustomed to living — and which have even proven themselves, in certain matters, to be correct, but in a specific instance are hindering — this is a Yetzias Mitzrayim and [an exiting of] boundaries, which is much more difficult.

And in this, I hope, dear Mr. Cohen, that you will also help Mr. Stulman so that he may be able to exit his boundaries and principles and accept **in full measure** the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. And surely, as until now, you will have success in this as well.

With greetings and with blessings for the Chag,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

P.S.
Enclosed:
a) A copy of my letter to Mr. Stulman.
b) A supplementary statement from the accountant.
c) The publications "Shelah" and "Shavuos."

## 190

190

B.H., Monday, 20 Menachem Av, 5705

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished man,
The Tamim, the Gaon, Rabbi A. Hecht, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your question: The sefer *Maareches HaElokus* is authored by R. Peretz HaKohen, son of R. Yitzchak, one of the greatest Kabbalists of the time of the Ramban. The Tzemach Tzedek, in *Drush Gimmel Shitos* (printed at the end of *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Vol. 2), mentions him several times and endeavors to reconcile several of the discourses of our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) with his views.

His greatness is also understood from the fact that several generations later, the Kabbalist R. Yehuda Chayim—whom the Arizal praised, as mentioned in *Torah Or*, *d.h. Vayomer, etc., Hein HaAdam*—engaged in writing a commentary on the sefer *Maareches HaElokus*.

Regarding what you wrote in his name, "that the Ein Sof which we have mentioned is not alluded to in the Torah, etc.":

The explanation of the matter is understood in accordance with what is written in several discourses of Chassidus, including the beginning of *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah*, which states:

"The fact that the Kabbalists attributed Divine names to specific Sefiros—such as the name *E-l* to *Chesed*, etc.—is not intended to refer to the essence of the Sefirah itself, etc. For Scripture cannot be removed from its literal meaning, and when we call out **in the Torah a name from the names** by which He, may He be blessed, is called, our intention—**and this is the true meaning—is directed toward the Essence of the G-dhead**, may He be blessed, etc., whose existence is from His own Essence, etc. In truth, this is indeed our intention in this: to the Creator of the world as He shines and comes through in His attribute of *Chesed*, etc. Thus, even though there are ten names, etc., the *Ohr Ein Sof* that spreads within them is one, etc., **and to Him** we are directed in our calling, etc. But He, may He be blessed, **from the perspective of His very Essence**, has **no name** that can indicate Him, for He is not grasped by any letter or attribute, G-d forbid, as all the **Kabbalists** have stated." End quote.

See also the *Zohar*, Vol. 2 (42b), which states: "Before the Holy One, blessed be He, created, etc., it is forbidden to make for Him a form or image in the world, not with the letter *Hei*, nor with the letter *Yud*, and not even **with the Holy Name**, nor with any letter or point in the world. But after He created this image of the Chariot of the Supernal Man, He descended into it and is called by that image, ***Havayah***, so that they might know **Him**, etc. And when He withdraws from it, He has no attribute, no likeness, and no form, etc." See there at length.

And in the introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar* (in the *Maamar Eliyahu*): "And You have no known name, etc.," and in many other places.

This is also logically necessary **at first glance**, since every name is limiting; it provides some positive or negative depiction, in any event. But regarding the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, may He be blessed, no depiction is applicable to Him. See the *Shelah* at the beginning regarding this.

As for your question regarding an **allusion** in the revealed Torah: The matter is **explicit** in *Shemos Rabbah* (Chapter 3:6, cited in *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah* there): "The Holy One said to Moshe: You ask to know My name? **According to My actions I am called**, etc. And when I have mercy on My world, I am called ***Havayah***, etc." End quote.

See also the *Hemshech* 5666, *d.h. Kol HaShoneh Halachos*, regarding the name *Havayah* in the Essence, where there are no letters.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 191

By the Grace of G-d, 21 Menachem Av, the day after the Yahrtzeit of my father, 5705

To the honored, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Havlin

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters, and specifically your last letter dated 25 Tammuz:

1) I have received the blessing for the engagement of his daughter, may she live, to a *ben-torah*. May the wedding take place in a good and auspicious hour, and may the building be an everlasting edifice founded upon the foundations of Torah and Mitzvos, among a generation of the righteous who are blessed.

2) I received yesterday the *maamar* from R’ Sh.G. regarding the celebration of the *Chag HaGeulah* and the Jubilee (the photograph has not yet been received). Surely you will also send here the letters of blessing that were received from those who were invited to the celebration and responded in writing. I also suggest that you get in touch with the representative of the *Morgen Journal* **in your camp**, so that he may write about the celebration in the correspondence that he sends regularly **from there** to the *Morgen Journal*.

3) I have still not received a response regarding what you promised to clarify with the author of *Toras Chesed*, etc., which I mentioned in my letter of 23 Teves. Surely you will reply as soon as possible.

4) Please give on my behalf, in connection with the Yahrtzeit, from the *Melach* and *Machne* funds that are in your possession: one hundred dollars to *Kolel Chabad*, and eighteen dollars to *Yeshivas Toras Emes*. I have deposited the equivalent here. Also, twenty-five dollars to the *Chevra Tehillim HaOlamis*.

5) The price of the books published by Shulsinger is in a separate note. The price of *Likutei Torah* is now five dollars (both volumes together) for yeshivos. Regarding our other publications, the price is indicated on the books themselves. To this, one must add the shipping costs, which have become very high. I am compelled to repeat my words from before and emphasize them doubly: the lack of funds in *Kehot* prevents the execution of many, many matters. What you have received from various places, as well as what is due from them, has long since amounted to a very large sum. I suggest once again—as I wrote in section 7 of my letter of 23 Teves—that you send us *tefillin*, as detailed there. We received two pairs of *tefillin* from you, but their price is high—approximately the price of *tefillin* from Eretz Yisrael here—and it seems they were purchased one by one. Our suggestion is that you purchase a proper number of *tefillin* at once, and surely the price will be **much** cheaper. Please be kind enough to inform us in your reply regarding this.

6) Please send here, at our expense, the copy of the *beurim* of the Rashgam that were found with Rabbi Tiktz, as I wrote in my letter of 23 Iyar. Thank you in advance.

To conclude with words of Torah, continuing from what I wrote in my previous letter regarding what I heard from my father, of blessed memory, and the explanation of the Mishnah (*Mikvaos*, end of ch. 7), "A needle that is placed, etc." according to *Chassidus*:

It is possible to explain, in my humble opinion, the previous clause in *avodah* and according to the foundations of *Chassidus* (and one should note: a) "He descends and immerses" is redundant; b) Why does it need to teach us both "bundles of wood" and "bundles of reeds"? c) The repetition of "bundles and bundles" is redundant).

Briefly: The waters of a *mikveh* represent that which purifies, and in general, this is the matter of proper *hisbonenus* (contemplation). As the Rambam writes at the end of *Hilchos Mikvaos*, the immersion from impurities is one of the *chukim* (statutes), yet there is a hint in the matter... "He brings his soul into the waters of *Da’as*," etc. **Tevilah** (immersion) shares the same letters as *bitul* (nullification)—the *bitul* that comes as a result of the *hisbonenus* and its "therefore" (*habeichen*). See the *Siddur*, *Seder Ha-Dah* on the *kavanah* of the *mikveh*. It must be water in which his entire body is covered, and the same applies to a *ma’ayan* (spring). For if not—if a part of his body is not covered by them—this is proof that the *bitul* is not a true *bitul*.

Now, a **mikveh whose waters are shallow** means that while the waters have the required measure, nevertheless, his entire body is not covered by them. This is especially true if, when he immerses, his feet are covered but his head is exposed, or vice versa; or—if he immerses while lying down—his right side is covered while the left remains exposed, or vice versa.

For in a person, there are generally two types of *avodah*: *Talmud* (study) and *Maaseh* (deed). There is a person who understands with his intellect what is good before him, but cannot stand firm against his desire in actual practice; or vice versa—one who is "cold" by nature but "free" in his opinions. Similarly, there is one for whom the *avodah* of "do good" (the right side, which draws near) is easy, but he cannot stand the test of "turn from evil" (the left side, which pushes away), or vice versa—similar to the fact that at the Giving of the Torah, the children of Yishmael did not want to accept "do not commit adultery," and the children of Esau did not want to accept "do not murder." Since, in the *hisbonenus* itself, there is no deficiency—for the water has the required measure—yet his entire body is not covered, meaning he is not *batel*, it must be that he lacks the matter of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke). Therefore, **it is not only** (*lo mibeiya*) **by means of stones** (inanimate—"my heart did not become haughty," "I have calmed and quieted myself," *kabbalas ol*) that he can place into the water (mix into his *hisbonenus*) and be able to immerse and be purified; rather, he is purified even by placing **bundles of wood**—the vegetable level, the *middos*, the prioritization of the *avodah* of *ahavah* and *yirah* (love and fear) toward *Elokus*. However, it must be **bundles** specifically, because with **one** *middah* he will not overcome the *yetzer hara*, and it must be "and all the rest of the flocks were gathered" (as explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Vayeida*, at the beginning).

Furthermore, since the brain rules over the heart, and the *hisbonenus* in his brain did not help, he must specifically **press** (*kovesh*) **stones** upon them—upon the *ahavah* and *yirah*—to mix *kabbalas ol* into the *middos*. For if not, the intellect will also tilt them according to its own path.

- Based on this, the word **"kovesh"** (presses/conquers) in the Mishnah is understood, for the *kivush* (conquest/pressing) is also **essential**.

It is not that the *Tanna* is merely giving us good advice on how to behave so that the waters will be sufficient. *V'ka'l*.

There are two aspects to the *middos*:
1) Regarding their source: a) Through *hisbonenus* in *sovev kol almin*, according to the path of *da'as* of *tov*; b) Through *hisbonenus* in *memalei kol almin*, according to the path of *da'as* of *g'dullah*.
2) Regarding their essence: a) According to the *middos* of *Tohu*; b) According to the *middos* of *Tikkun*.

This is the difference between a reed (soft as a reed, hollow within, its primary growth is upon the water—see *Beurei HaZohar*, *Pekudei*, *d.h. V'lazmanin*) and wood in general.

Since each has what the other lacks, as explained in many places (see also *d.h. Le'olam Yehei Rach K'Kaneh*, 5705), the *Mishnah* mentions both: **bundles of wood or bundles of reeds**.

The test that this *avodah* has been effective—for a test is needed since he was previously "suspected," etc.—is that he **descends** (*yored*)—he "descends" (*b'tish*) and descends from his arrogance—and then the *Mishnah* promises him: "and he immerses" (*tovel*)—which shares the letters of *bitul*.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 192

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5705

To the honorable administration of Kolel Chabad, may they be blessed with peace, and at their head,
The brilliant Rabbi, the Chassid,
Renowned for his praise, who contemplates matters of goodness, G-d-fearing, etc., our relative,
Rabbi Sh. Y. L., shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of the 27th of Tammuz, and I thank you for having arranged all the matters of the first year and the day of the yahrtzeit as required.

Please accept one hundred dollars from Rabbi, the Chassid, etc., R’ Ch. H. Havlin, shlita, for the Kolel fund, from me, to cover the expenses involved in all of the above, along with my thanks.

It is worth noting the statement of our Sages (Shabbos 152b, and Zohar I 226a, 227b) that after twelve months—that is, on and from the day of the first yahrtzeit—the soul ascends and does not descend.

One may add a reason regarding Tzaddikim: Tzaddikim, on the day of their passing, are at an extremely lofty level—see the sources cited in Maavar Yabok, Part 1, Chapter 17, and see also Metzudas David, Part 2, Chapter 2, 10.

It is known that on the day of passing, "all the labor of a person that his soul labored during his lifetime, which was in a state of concealment and hiddenness, is revealed and shines in a state of revelation from above to below at the time of his passing" (the language of our Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 28). It is possible that this is the intention of our Sages (Avos, Chapter 6) that at the time of a person’s passing, none accompany him... except for Torah and good deeds—at the very **moment** [of passing].

If so, this is also the case at the turn of the year—that is, the day of the yahrtzeit—as it is known that all matters dependent on the seasons of the year return and are awakened every year on that date.

On the contrary, because Tzaddikim have no rest even in the World to Come and go from strength to strength, this is an ascent with even greater intensity than on the day of the passing (and note Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 14).

Now, regarding this aspect of "ascending and not descending," it is stated in Shaar HaMitzvos, end of Parshas Vayechi, that on the Shabbos before the completion of the twelve months, the soul ascends and does not descend again, and not specifically on the day of the yahrtzeit. This is unlike the aforementioned reason, and it still requires further study.

Please pray for the health and peace of my mother, my teacher, may she live, for long, good days and years.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 193

B"H, Friday, 8 Elul, 5705

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, faithful in his dealings, the generous and distinguished, etc.,
The Tamim, R' Shneur Zalman, may he live, Ganeles

Peace and blessing!

Through our friends, the Temimim, the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, a man of many accomplishments and great energy, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live, Kazarnovsky, and the distinguished and elevated individual who engages in communal needs faithfully, etc., R' Dovid Binyomin, may he live, Chaskin, we have received your contribution toward the printing (mimeographing) of the sichos of the Rebbe (Rashab), may his soul be bound in the bond of life.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the exalted value of this matter and the great satisfaction brought to the soul of the Tzaddik through this. For through your aforementioned contribution, the possibility is created that whenever someone studies this sicha, the lips of the Tzaddik murmur in the grave, and his soul is in the Yeshiva on High (see the language of Tosafos, s.v. *Agurah*, Yevamos 96b). And who is greater than Dovid Hamelech, peace be upon him, who yearned and requested of the Ribono shel Olam that it be His will that a teaching be cited in his name, thereby allowing him to dwell in two worlds—meaning that his lips would murmur, etc.

Now, when a teaching is cited in the name of its author, the Tzaddik’s desire that his lips murmur is fulfilled only at the moment of the citation. This is not the case for one who gives of his wealth for the writing and copying of the Tzaddik’s seforim; for at every hour, even in the furthest corners of the world, when a person studies this sefer, the Tzaddik awakens merit for the person through whom the sefer was publicized.

And this is a matter that applies to every person, and it is an extra merit for you, who have merited to be among his students. See the Zohar at the end of Parshas Bechukosai regarding the matter of honoring one's father, which is incumbent upon the son even after the father’s passing, *le-okir le-avui bi-trei alma* (to honor his father in two worlds). It is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding the verse "And you shall teach them to your children"—these are **the students**, for a person’s students are called children, as stated in the Sifrei and brought in the Rambam, Hilchos Talmud Torah, at the beginning.

And since every matter is *middah ke-neged middah* (measure for measure), it is reasonable to say that just as the Tzaddik dwells in **two** worlds through the citation of his teaching, so too is the reward of the one who facilitates this both spiritual and physical, in an abundance of physical and spiritual good.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

P.S. The request and insistence that a teaching be cited in their name is mentioned in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding Dovid Hamelech, Rabbi Yochanan (both in Yevamos, ibid.), and Rav Sheshes.

Therefore, it must be that the matter of "I will dwell in Your tent for worlds" concerns these three **more** than any other person. The reason for this may be: 
1) Dovid strove greatly that that sin be forgiven him, **and that all of Israel know** that it had been forgiven, as is stated in Shabbos (30a) and Sanhedrin (107a and there). Now, if a Rav is not like an angel, etc., one should not learn Torah from him, as our Sages said (Chagigah 15b; see Lechem Mishneh, Hilchos Talmud Torah, beginning of chapter 4). Therefore, Dovid specifically strove that a teaching be cited in his name, for through this it would also be known that that sin had been forgiven him.

2) Rabbi Yochanan, whose children died, as is stated in Berachos (8b; see Seder HaDoros regarding whether a son was born to him afterward). In order that the Holy One, blessed be He, not harbor anger toward him, he needed to leave behind students worthy of inheriting his legacy, as stated in Bava Basra (167a). Therefore, he specifically strove that a teaching be cited in his name.

3) Rav Sheshes. It is stated in Shaar HaGilgulim (end of Introduction 4) and in Sefer HaGilgulim (Chapter 10) regarding the explanation of why Rav Sheshes would say, "Rejoice, my soul! For you I have studied, for you I have learned, etc." Rav Sheshes knew that he had previously been in the body of Bava ben Buta, and he had perfected his soul, lacking only a small matter. For this, his soul was reincarnated a second time in Rav Sheshes. In this manner, the order is that the primary reward for the Torah and mitzvos that he performs in the second incarnation is only for the sake of his soul, not his second body. For at the time of the Resurrection, his soul will return to the first body, in which he performed the **majority** of the Torah and mitzvos required of him. Therefore, his body—that of Rav Sheshes—was sad, and he would say "Rejoice, my soul" specifically, and not the body.

It seems to me, in my humble opinion, that this is all regarding other Torah and mitzvos. But when a teaching is cited from the mouth of Rav Sheshes, which requires **lips** to murmur in the grave **in this world**, it is obvious that the lips of the body of **Rav Sheshes** will murmur. Therefore, he specifically strove that a teaching be cited in his name (and yet, he said "Rejoice, **my soul**," etc., because he was saying this regarding his own Torah study, as stated in Pesachim 68b. This is different from having a teaching cited, which is what he taught of Torah to his students; and the matter is clear).

## 194

B"H, 12 Elul, 5705

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Rabbi M. HaKohen,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, and all the checks you sent have been delivered according to your instructions. Surely, the receipts from each recipient have already arrived.

I am grateful for your wishes for success in our avodah of spreading the wellsprings of Chabad outward. May it be His will that your blessing be fulfilled, as it surely emanates from a pure heart. As a Kohen, you take a share in this avodah—and consequently, in the reward that comes through it as well. I write "our avodah" intentionally, because this avodah is primarily yours; in this avodah, you can be **certain** that it is yours and that it has fallen to your lot.

For generally, when a person chooses his path in life and his business affairs, he does not know with certainty whether he has chosen his true portion—as our Sages of blessed memory said (Pesachim 54b), "Seven things are hidden from man... and a person does not know in what he will earn his livelihood." This is not the case, however, with matters that do not depend on one’s own choice but are given from Above. These **certainly** belong to him, and **with them** he must serve his Creator. This is the purpose of man’s creation on earth, as our Sages said (Mishnah, end of Kiddushin), "I was created to serve my Creator." Specifically, these matters include everything given to a person from birth—for example, whether he is a Yisrael, a Levi, or a **Kohen**.

The distinction between these categories in general—even though each one is inclusive of them all—is written in the Tanach, explained by our Sages of blessed memory, and codified as halacha in the Yad of the Rambam:

1) Regarding the distinction between the Levi and the rest of Yisrael, he writes (end of Hilchos Shemitah v'Yovel): "The tribe of Levi... was set apart to serve Hashem and minister to Him" (referring to the service of the Beis HaMikdash, as stated in Hilchos Klei HaMikdash, beginning of Chapter 3), "and to teach His righteous ways and just judgments to the masses." (And because every category of Kohen and Levi is inclusive of all, he concludes there: "And not only the tribe of Levi, but every person... [see also Yoma 72a]").

2) Included in this are the Kohanim. The Kohen adds to the Levi, as (Hilchos Klei HaMikdash, beginning of Chapter 4) they were set apart from the rest of the Leviim for the service of the sacrifices. As it is written (Devarim 33:10), "They shall teach Your judgments"—which refers to the entire tribe, including the Kohanim—"and they shall place incense before You"—which refers only to the Kohanim.

Now, the fulfillment of the command to "teach Your judgments and Your Torah" can be achieved through teaching the masses **any** Torah study whatsoever. "They shall place incense and a whole offering"—which in our time is the tefillah that was instituted to correspond to the daily sacrifices (and Rabbi Yehuda HaNasi said that the Minchah offering was instituted to correspond to the incense; see Tosafos, Berachos 26b, and Lechem Mishneh on Hilchos Tefillah, Chapter 3, Halacha 2)—can be achieved by arousing one’s fellow to the avodah of tefillah and dveikus to the Creator in **any** manner.

However, both matters together—"teach Your Torah" and also "the whole offering," Torah and tefillah—which are **both** incumbent upon the Kohen as mentioned above, can be achieved specifically through the Torah of Chassidus Chabad. Chassidus Chabad includes both: Torah with yiras shamayim, and the avodah of tefillah through Chabad.

"Greater is the one who performs the act..." It would be appropriate for you to organize a committee in your locale that would take upon itself, bli neder, a fixed pledge—a set amount each month—dedicated to assisting in our avodah. This is **your** avodah as much as it is ours: the avodah of printing and distributing the seforim published according to the instructions of the Rebbe, may he live and be well.

With blessings for a good, inscribed year, and immediately for teshuvah—immediately for Geulah,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 195

12 Elul, 5705

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, descendant of holy lineage, etc.,
Rabbi Y. Leiner

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter, I will begin with your primary question, which is:

1) Our Alter Rebbe writes in his Siddur—after Hallel: On Rosh Chodesh... one says the *Shir Shel Yom* here... *Barchi Nafshi*... *Kaddish Yasom*... four men are called to the Torah, and afterwards one says *Ashrei* and *U’va L’Tzion*, and the Torah scroll is returned to the Ark, and then the Chazzan says the *Chatzi Kaddish*... and one removes the Tefillin on Rosh Chodesh **before** the Kaddish.

This requires deep study (*tzarich iyun gadol*), for it is written in *Pri Etz Chaim* (Shaar Rosh Chodesh, Chapter 9): "The Rav [the Arizal] would not remove his Tefillin until they had finished the entire Kaddish that follows the returning of the Torah scroll to the Ark, before Musaf, and only then would he remove the Tefillin and pray Musaf." This is also the ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Arizal. One cannot say that this was merely the personal practice of the Arizal and not a binding law for the masses, for it is written in *Machzik Bracha* (Masechet Rosh Chodesh, Chapter 3, Mishnah 2): "And after the Kaddish of *U’va L’Tzion*, one should remove the Tefillin." The same is stated in the Siddur of R. Shabtai of Rashkov. (In the book *Nagid U’Metzuvah* which you cited, I did not find this.)

Seemingly, the difficulty is even greater, because in addition to the above, it is explicitly stated in several other places that one removes the Tefillin **after** the Kaddish and not before it. Namely: in *Shaar HaKavanot* (Inyan Rosh Chodesh): "It is the custom to remove the Tefillin before the Musaf prayer, after the Kaddish that is said after returning the Torah scroll to the Ark." In *Kol Yaakov* by R. Yaakov Koppel: "After the Kaddish, before Musaf, one must remove the Tefillin." And others.

- In the book *Me’asef LeChol HaMachanot* (Orach Chaim, Siman 25, subsection 131), it cites *Responsa Radbaz* (Vol. 4, end of Siman 187), *Responsa Dvar Shmuel* (Siman 112), *Machzik Bracha* (item 15), *Kesher Gudal* (Siman 3, item 30), *Shilmei Tzibur* (page 41b), *Zachor L’Avraham* (Vol. 3, item 400), *Siddur Beit Oved* (item 1, after the Hallel order), *Chesed L’Alafim* (item 13), *Ben Ish Chai* (Vayikra, item 17), and *Kaf HaChaim* (item 94)—all of whom write that one removes the Tefillin before Musaf. It requires study whether they explicitly state "before or after the Kaddish," and these books are not before me.

To clarify the opinion of our great Rebbe—as this is the custom in all Chabad synagogues—it can be explained by first addressing the custom regarding the time for removing Tefillin, based on what is written in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* (Siman 25), that there are four customs regarding this. Two of them are: after *Aleinu* or after the *Kaddish Yasom* that follows *Aleinu*. This is not relevant to Rosh Chodesh, where one removes the Tefillin before Musaf. We need only discuss the remaining two: the custom of the world to remove Tefillin after the *Kedushah* of *U’va L’Tzion*, and the custom according to Kabbalah to remove them after having said three Kaddishes—(this is the version our great Rebbe upheld in his *Shulchan Aruch*, Siman 25, section 37, and according to this we are deliberating)—and therefore one should not remove them until after the Kaddish that follows *U’va L’Tzion*, at which point, together with the Kaddish after *Shemoneh Esrei* and the one before *Barechu*, these constitute three Kaddishes. (See further on this).

- And since they do not distinguish between whether it is a day of Torah reading—where there is also the *Chatzi Kaddish* after the reading, which completes the number of Kaddishes aside from the Kaddish after *U’va L’Tzion*—it must be that this Kaddish is not included in the count, as it pertains to the Torah reading and not to the prayer.

Now, all this applies to weekdays. But on Rosh Chodesh, since our Rebbe writes that after Hallel one should say *Shir Shel Yom* and the Kaddish after it, the number of three Kaddishes is completed **aside** from the Kaddish after *U’va L’Tzion*. Thus, immediately after the *Kedushah* of *U’va L’Tzion*, one already has three Kaddishes and four *Kedushahs*. And since there is no **necessity** for his Tefillin to be on him during the recitation of the Kaddish that precedes Musaf, it is, on the contrary, a **necessity** to remove them before that Kaddish, because this Kaddish pertains to the Musaf prayer (which one never begins without a Kaddish beforehand), and therefore one must connect them as much as possible, as is proven in the commentaries on *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* Siman 292.

See our Rebbe’s *Shulchan Aruch* there. Therefore, our Rebbe writes that one removes the Tefillin specifically before the Kaddish.

However, all this is according to our Rebbe’s order, where we say *Shir Shel Yom* and *Kaddish* before *U’va L’Tzion*. But according to the order in *Kol Yaakov*, which writes: "Avraham Zaken... and we take out the Torah... Kaddish after the reading... *Ashrei* and *U’va L’Tzion*... Kaddish"—and it is the same in all the aforementioned places—they did not mention saying *Shir Shel Yom* before *U’va L’Tzion*.

- (It requires clarification whether they did not say it at all, or if they said it after Musaf or after the prayer. In Siman 423 it says that the Sephardic custom is to say *Barchi Nafshi* **after** Musaf. See what I wrote in the name of *Shaarei Knesset HaGedolah* that on Rosh Chodesh they were accustomed to say *Barchi Nafshi* **in place of** *Shir Shel Yom*, though he challenged this. See further on this.)—Therefore, they would remove the Tefillin specifically after the Kaddish of *U’va L’Tzion*, so that there would be three Kaddishes.

Based on the above, the language of our Rebbe in his Siddur there also becomes clear: "One says **here** *Shir Shel Yom*." Seemingly, the word "here" is superfluous, but based on the above, it is understood that it comes to exclude the other aforementioned customs, and he emphasizes **this** specifically, because the time of removing the Tefillin depends on it: before the Kaddish or after it.

2) One should not raise the objection that if so, we have fallen from the frying pan into the fire; for we wanted to resolve that the words of the Alter Rebbe should agree with what is written in the writings of the Arizal regarding the removal of Tefillin on Rosh Chodesh, and by this resolution, our Rebbe would disagree with him regarding the recitation of *Shir Shel Yom*. That is absurd!

It can be explained that there are three opinions regarding the recitation of *Shir Shel Yom*: 1) It is not in the prayer order at all, and therefore either it is not said at all (it is not in the *Siddur Rav Saadia Gaon*, nor is it mentioned in the *Sefer HaMinhagim* of the Maharil Tirna; and in the prayer version of the Rambam, "some of the people were accustomed to read *Shir Shel Yom*"), or it is said **after the prayer** (the Ashkenazic custom), as it is done merely as a remembrance (see *Magen Avraham*, end of Siman 132 and its commentaries). 2) Some say: Once they have become accustomed to saying it, it should be said in its place; meaning, just as they said it in the Beis HaMikdash during the *Tamid* offering, so too now it should be said adjacent to the *Shemoneh Esrei* of Shacharis. 3) According to Kabbalah: Its place is after *U’va L’Tzion* and before *Ein Kelokeinu*, according to the order of the descent of the *shefa* (divine flow), as explained in the writings of the Arizal (in the aforementioned places; see also *Tefillah L’Moshe* by the Ramak).

All this applies to weekdays, but on Rosh Chodesh, when the order of the descent of the *shefa* is different—

- (See *Mikdash Melech* on *Zohar* Vol. 1, 75b, that on Rosh Chodesh the illumination is from *Beriah*, and in several Chassidic discourses it is written that it is from *Yetzirah*, and in *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek in the explanation of the discourse *Machar Chodesh*, page 22b, these opinions are explained at length)—

Perhaps it can be said that according to the **third reason**, there is no need to say it at all, and it is said only as a mere remembrance, **like the first reason**—(see what is written in *Shaarei Knesset HaGedolah*, cited in *Be’er Heitev* end of Siman 132, regarding the custom of **all places** in this regard). If so, its place is after the prayer, as mentioned above regarding the *Magen Avraham*. But our Rebbe holds like the second reason, which is why he rules that *Shir Shel Yom* is said adjacent to the Shacharis prayer even on Rosh Chodesh, as mentioned. Since the dispute between the first and second reasons is a dispute in the **revealed** Torah, there is no innovation in the fact that the Alter Rebbe ruled according to the second opinion, and not like that **custom** practiced in the place of the Arizal, and **consequently** the ruling follows that one removes them before the Kaddish.

This is unlike the removal of Tefillin before or after the Kaddish—if you say that it is a dispute **in its own right**, which is a matter of Kabbalah, as written in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* Siman 25, section 13, who would come after the Arizal to disagree with him on this?

See also *Magen Avraham* end of Siman 423, where it is evident from his language that the opinion that one removes them after the Kaddish is because of the number of Kaddishes.

Based on the above, the fact that the *Yaavetz* brings that one removes Tefillin after the Kaddish, and that according to the Ramah one should say *Shir Shel Yom* in Shacharis—he is "riding two horses," because the rulings contradict each other.

And one should not raise an objection to what our great Rebbe ruled from the Ramah, who instituted saying *Shir Shel Yom* in Shacharis—(**from the surface** of the Yaavetz’s language it seems the Ramah instituted two things: to say *Shir Shel Yom* and not *Barchi Nafshi*, and in Shacharis. This requires clarification in the *Responsa* of the Ramah, which are not before me)—and he was in the time of the Arizal, so why remove them after the Kaddish?

- The objection is invalid from the outset, for the Ramah holds that one removes the Tefillin before the Torah reading, as written in his *Responsa* cited by later authorities.

- The custom of the Sephardim in the time of the Arizal regarding saying *Shir Shel Yom* on Rosh Chodesh needs to be clarified; *Shaarei Knesset HaGedolah* is not with me to examine, and one cannot bring proof from the customs of the Sephardim now, as many customs have changed from then until now.

3) **Notes.** Based on the above, and according to our custom that we say *Shir Shel Yom* on weekdays before *Ein Kelokeinu* and *Aleinu*, seemingly, according to all opinions, one should remove the Tefillin **before** the *Kaddish Yasom* that follows *Aleinu*, for what the Rema wrote (Siman 25, section 13) that one should remove them after it, is according to his version that requires four Kaddishes while wearing Tefillin, and according to his custom that they said *Shir Shel Yom* after the prayer. This is not so for us.

- I have seen those who note that in the book *Artzot HaChaim* it is discussed, and he brings proof from the fact that he wrote that the Arizal would remove them after *Aleinu* and did not write after *Kaddish Yasom*. In the book *Ot Chaim* (Siman 25, subsection 12), he wonders that it escaped him that according to the Arizal’s custom there is no *Kaddish Yasom* after *Aleinu*. *Artzot HaChaim* is not before me to examine.

It requires study why one does not count in the number of three Kaddishes also the Kaddish before *Hodu* (or *Baruch She’amar*). In the book *Ot Chaim*, he writes the reason: because sometimes people are late in coming to the synagogue. This is forced.

\* \* \*

Regarding what you noted: why it was marked in the Siddur that there is a change in the tradition if it is the Name of Hashem and the like. It can be said that prayer is different, as the *kavanah* (intention) is more critical (especially regarding the Names). See the introduction of the Maharil Mianovitch—the brother of the Alter Rebbe—to the Rebbe’s Siddur, regarding how precise they were in this.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter about the honor of your father, may he live, and the generations after him—I have noted in my letter to the commentaries of the *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah* Siman 240, which discusses the aforementioned places. The books *Birkei Yosef* and *Shvus Yaakov* are not before me.

The collection was sent to you as you requested.

I will conclude with the blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for immediate *Teshuvah*, for immediate *Geulah*.

**M. Schneerson**
**Chairman of the Editorial Board**

196

19 Elul, 5705
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
The *Tamim*, Rabbi Y. Shochet, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter was received some time ago, and with it, my sincere apologies for the delay in my response, due to the pressure of many preoccupations. I am enclosing the response here. In my humble opinion, I have clarified some details that were not strictly necessary for you and those like you, but I did so to ensure it fits the style of the *kovetz*, which is intended also for those who have only a slight knowledge of *Chassidus*. Please be so kind as to acknowledge receipt of this letter. It is surprising that they are not participating in the *machlokes shalom achim* (the dispute for the sake of Heaven).

You will receive regards from everything happening here through our friend, the esteemed and distinguished Mr. Mendel, may he live.

***

**Question:** In *Torah Or* (by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe), *Parshas Shemos*, the *maamar* beginning "And he said to him, G-d, who placed a mouth" (page 50), it is written: "...Through the *bracha* of the *mitzvah*, the level of *makif* is drawn down [a], and through the *mitzvah* itself, the *ohr penimi* is drawn down... And therefore, regarding *tefillin* of the head, the Sephardim and Ashkenazim differ (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, sec. 28, sec. 6, and commentaries) as to whether one should recite a special *bracha* over it. Because the *makif* of *tefillin* of the head is very lofty, the Sephardic custom is not to recite a *bracha*, as they hold that it is impossible for us to draw down that *makif*, etc., while the Ashkenazim hold that we can draw it down," end quote.

*Tzarich iyun* (it requires further study): Based on this, how can we explain the law that if one spoke between the *tefillah* [of the hand] and the *tefillah* [of the head], one must recite a *bracha* over the *tefillin* of the head? If it is impossible to draw down the light, then even if one spoke, it should be impossible to recite a *bracha*.

**Rabbi Yitzchak Dubov, Shochet**
**Manchester, England**

***

**Answer:** The solution to the question can be found by first adding some clarification to the dispute between the Sephardim and the Ashkenazim.

Seemingly, one might interpret their positions as follows: The Ashkenazim hold that we recite a *bracha* over the *tefillin* of the head and thereby draw down the *makif*, while the Sephardim hold that it is not within our power to draw down the *makif*, and therefore one should not recite a *bracha* because the *makif* is not drawn down.

But the truth is not so. Even according to the Sephardim, the *makif* is drawn down; rather, they hold that it is not within the power of the actions of the lower beings to draw it down. Instead, it is drawn down of its own accord through an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above), because it is a light so lofty that an *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below) cannot reach it, and therefore they do not recite a *bracha*. The Ashkenazim hold that in the place of this *makif*, an *is'arusa d'letata* does reach, and therefore one must recite a *bracha*.

This is explicitly stated in *Shaar HaKavanos* (*Drushei Tefillas HaShachar*, *Drush* 2): "Through *tefillin* of the head, the world of *Atzilus* is rectified. However, regarding the *bracha* (of the *tefillin* of the head), there is a dispute. For one master holds that even in the world of *Atzilus*, one must create its *ohr makif* through our actions, therefore one must recite a *bracha* also over the *tefillin* of the head to create an *ohr makif* for it. And one master holds that the *ohr makif* of the world of *Atzilus*... is not created by us, but is created of its own accord, for we do not have the power to create it."

And with more detail in *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaTefillah*, Chapter 5: "Through *tefillin* of the head, the three lower [sefirot] of *Atzilus* are (rectified) [b] in the aspect of the *chitzoniyus* (externality), for the *penimiyus* (internality) requires no rectification at all, as even in the *penimiyus* of *Beriah*, the *kelipos* have no hold. And also the *ohr makif* of the *chitzoniyus* does not need to be rectified, and it is created of its own accord, and therefore one does not need to recite a *bracha* over them. But there are those among the *poskim* who disagree and say that one must also recite a *bracha* over them, over the *tefillin* of the head, to draw down an *ohr makif* through our own efforts, and it is in our power to draw it down," end quote.

It may be said that these three matters are dependent on one another, for such a light and influence that we have the power to draw down means that the action of the lower beings has significance there and occupies a place. And since a good deed occupies a place for the good, then a transgression or sin—an evil deed—draws the influence to the place of evil, meaning it causes nourishment for the *chitzonim*. And the absence of an action causes the absence of an *hemshech* (drawing down).

Now, there are two types of matters that come through an *is'arusa d'le'eila* on its own:
1) Matters that come through an *is'arusa d'le'eila* on its own and are drawn down in every place, whether it is prepared or not prepared.
An example of this: thoughts of *teshuvah* that fall upon a person without any contemplation or preparation on his part, and they fall even upon a wicked person.

2) Matters that come through an *is'arusa d'le'eila* on its own, but nevertheless are only drawn down in a place of perfection (*atar shalim*).
And the perfection does not force the matter to be drawn down—(just as in our case, the *bracha* over the *tefillin* of the hand forces, so to speak, the drawing down of the *ohr makif* of *Beriah*)—but rather, through the perfection, it is possible for the matter to settle there, and when it settles, it is by way of a gift and not by way of necessity [c]. An example of this: the matter of prophecy according to the Rambam, who wrote (*Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, ch. 7, laws 4-5): "All the prophets do not prophesy whenever they wish, but they direct their minds, etc., and isolate themselves, etc., and they seek prophecy, etc. And even though they direct their minds, it is possible that the *Shechinah* will rest upon them, and it is possible that it will not rest," end quote [d].

Now, the *ohr makif* of *Atzilus*, even though, as mentioned, it is drawn down of its own accord according to the Sephardim, nevertheless it is only drawn down through the fact that the Jewish person puts on *tefillin* of the head, which is proof that it is among the matters of the second type—meaning they are only drawn down in a place of perfection.

It is understood that this perfection, through which it is possible for this *ohr makif* to settle, must have some connection to it, since it is specifically what enables the *ohr makif* to settle (and just as in the matter of prophecy, they must direct their minds, isolate themselves, and seek prophecy).

And this is what is meant by the fact that one first recites a *bracha* over the *tefillin* of the hand, through which one draws down the *ohr makif* of the world of *Beriah* (as written in the writings of the Arizal there), which is adjacent to the world of *Atzilus* (similar to the "directing their minds and isolating themselves" mentioned above), and one intends in his *bracha* also for the *tefillin* of the head—meaning his intention is that the *ohr makif* of *Beriah* should be a preparation for the resting of the *ohr makif* of *Atzilus* (similar to "seeking prophecy"). All of this is akin to, and related to, the *ohr makif* of *Atzilus* that is drawn down of its own accord afterward.

And all this applies when one has not spoken between the *tefillah* of the hand and the *tefillah* of the head. But if one interrupted between the *tefillin* of the hand and the *tefillin* of the head, or when one only has the *tefillin* of the head, then the perfection is lacking. In that case, one must recite a *bracha* over the *tefillin* of the head. And the intention is not that through this one will force the *ohr makif* of *Atzilus* to descend, for according to the Sephardim, this is not in our power, but rather that through this *bracha*, the perfection comes, and the *ohr makif* can settle afterward.

Regards to all *Anash*, and I sign with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, 24 Elul, 5705

To the Honorable Chief Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, distinguished and exalted, known for his great accomplishments, a man of many deeds and noble character, etc., Rabbi J., known as Dr. Hertz,

Greetings and Blessings!

The Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, shlita, has addressed a message to Jewish soldiers for the upcoming Rosh Hashanah.

Given the great benefit to be gained from this message being read by Jews in the British Army as well—especially those stationed in countries occupied by British forces—so that they may be stirred to strive for the spiritual assistance of our Jewish brethren suffering there,

We have found it appropriate to send your honor a certain number of copies of this message, so that you may, if you find it appropriate, distribute them by air to the aforementioned soldiers.

We have also sent a certain number of copies of the letter from the Rebbe, shlita, to the Jews of Europe. Through the Religious Bureau under your leadership, these letters may reach various places in the liberated countries with which it is otherwise impossible to establish contact. We are channeling this merit through your honor and others who are worthy.

It goes without saying that if more copies of these two letters are needed, we will provide them immediately upon your instruction, to the address you provide us.

I will conclude with a blessing for the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, which falls on Shabbos: a blessing for a good and sweet year, one that will be entirely a day of complete Shabbos and rest.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

A blessing for the year and warm regards to your son-in-law, the Rabbi, of whom I have heard much regarding his great deeds in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit. May Hashem be with him and may he ascend.
