## 198

B"H, 28 Elul, 5705
Brooklyn

Highly esteemed Mr. Alexander Cohen,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In the name of Kehot and in my own name, I wish you and all your family a Shana Tova U’mesuka, and success in all your endeavors.

The precise meaning of **Rosh Hashanah** is the **head** of the year. Our Sages explain why it is not called *techilas*—the beginning—of the year, but rather **Rosh** **Hashanah**: just as the head directs the entire body, so too must the good resolutions and conduct that one takes upon oneself on Rosh Hashanah direct the entire year.

This year, Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos. The concept of Shabbos is that at that time, a person rises above their weekday life and worries, and becomes closer to the life of the neshamah.

And this is also our wish: that in the coming year, we should all move forward in our spiritual development, bring the body closer to the neshamah, and carry out all our good thoughts in our daily lives.

With a blessing of Kesiva V’chasima Tova,

**Menachem M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

199

[Before the beginning of 5706?]

Our Rebbe (Alter Rebbe) wrote (Iggeres HaTeshuvah, ch. 3), in the name of the *poskim*, that for every day of a *taanis* of *teshuvah* (a), one should give the value of 18 *peshitim*. You have requested to know what this amount is in our times.

**Answer.** **A.** The source for our Rebbe’s words is in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, siman 334, se'if 26, in the gloss of the Rema. The text relevant to our matter reads: "If one transgressed and desecrated [Shabbos], he must fast forty days, etc., and give in place of the *chatas* 18 *peshitim* (b) to *tzedakah*. If he wishes to redeem the fast, he should give 18 *peshitim* for every day to *tzedakah*."

The *Magen Avraham* writes regarding this, in the name of the *Levush*, that each *peshit* is equivalent to one and a half *gadol polnish* (c). According to this valuation, 12 *peshitim* are 18 *gadol polnish*, as our Rebbe wrote in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*.

Their value in the currency of our times is explained according to what our Rebbe wrote in his *Shulchan Aruch* at the end of siman 334: that 18 *peshitim* are the measure of a *sela* of Torah, and thus 18 *gadol polnish* are two-thirds of a *sela* of Torah. The measure of a *sela* is known in every country by the sum used to redeem a *bechor* in that country, which is worth five *selaim*. However, for *pidyon haben*, they are stringent with the measure because it is a *mitzvah asei* from the Torah, which is not the case in our current matter.

***

**B.** It still requires clarification whether these measures are equal in all times and in all places.

From the language of our Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch* and in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, it appears straightforward that these measures—both the measure in place of the *chatas* and the redemption of the fast—are equal in all times, except that a wealthy person should increase according to his wealth. It is necessary to clarify his opinion on this, as the *Magen Avraham* (siman 334, sub-paragraph 34)—followed by the *Machatzis HaShekel* and *Chayei Adam*—disagrees. This also appears to be the opinion of the *Chasam Sofer* (Responsa, *Yoreh Deah*, siman 155).

***

The *Magen Avraham* raised a difficulty regarding what is written in the Rema (in the name of the *Maharai*) that the measure in place of the *chatas* is 18 *peshitim*—which, according to the *Magen Avraham’s* calculation, is 27 *ma'ah* of silver—for in the case of a *chatas*, one fulfills his obligation even if he brings a *chatas* worth a *danka*, which is one *ma'ah*, as is found in *Zevachim* (48a). From this, he concludes that the amount of money one gives in place of the *chatas* depends on the price of a lamb at the time of the sinner.

In the time of the *Shas*, the price of a lamb was a *danka*, but in the time of the *Maharai*, they had become more expensive and rose to 27 *ma'ah*.

Thus, in our time, one must give an amount of money that is the price of a lamb in the country of the **sinner**.

—This is implied by the plain language of the *Magen Avraham*, and one does not calculate based on *Eretz Yisrael*. Even though in the time of the *Beis HaMikdash* they would bring lambs from Chevron (*Menachos* 87a), all lands were valid for this; it is just that those from Chevron were the choicest.—

Seemingly, since the measure of 12 *peshitim*—the redemption of the fast—is mentioned in the same breath as the aforementioned measure, one could say that according to the *Magen Avraham*, this measure also depends on time and place. That is to say, one estimates the person's intent in the time and place where he is found, so that the pain of losing this sum would be equivalent for him to the pain of the fast, similar to what is written in the *Magen Avraham*, siman 568, sub-paragraph 12.

However, according to this reasoning, it is difficult: if so, even though they did not set an upper limit and a wealthy person must add according to his wealth, there is also no lower limit to speak of. It is obvious that in every generation there are destitute poor people for whom the loss of even a small amount of money is harder than the pain of a fast.

Why has no *posek* mentioned that the measure of 12 *peshitim* in the time of the *Maharai* is a **medium** measure, and the poor person may reduce from it (d)? Therefore, it seems appropriate to say that even according to the *Magen Avraham*, the measure of 12 *peshitim* is the lower limit, meaning one may not reduce from it (e).

***

Our Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch* (end of siman 334) wrote the measure of 18 and 12 *peshitim*, and did not copy the opinion of the *Magen Avraham* that the measure of 18 *peshitim* changes according to the price of lambs. On the contrary, he concludes there regarding how to calculate this in **our** currency—from which it is clear that he holds that even in our time, the measure of 18 *peshitim* has not changed.

The aforementioned difficulty of the *Magen Avraham*, upon which he based his ruling that the measure depends on the price of lambs, is resolved by our Rebbe with the words he added: "And it (18 *peshitim*) is the measure of a *sela* of Torah." And it is no longer difficult why he is obligated to give 18 *peshitim* when a *chatas* of a *danka* suffices—for a *danka* suffices so that he is not called a transgressor, but a standard *chatas* is specifically a *sela*, as written in *Tosafos* (s.v. *miklal*, *Kerisos* 10b). In Rashi, *Menachos* (107b), it is implied that this is the law in the *Torah Shebe'al Peh* (see *Lechem Mishneh*, *Hilchos Ma'aseh HaKorbanos*, ch. 15, halacha 4) (f). Since the foundation has fallen, there is no longer proof for the *Magen Avraham’s* ruling that this measure of 18 *peshitim* changes.

Furthermore, according to the *Magen Avraham’s* ruling that the amount of money in place of the *chatas* depends on the price of lambs, it is difficult:

1) How did the *poskim* leave their words unexplained and not clarify this law?

2) If we say—as our Rebbe holds—that the sum in place of the *chatas* is fixed, it is understood why the *poskim* explained its measure in the currency of their country, yet the ruling applies to all countries. For in whatever place the sinner gives 18 *peshitim*, he fulfills his obligation, and it makes no difference in which country he lives. But according to the *Magen Avraham*, even in the time of the Rema, who provides this measure of 18 *peshitim*, the law only applies to those near him, for whom the price of a lamb in their place was 18 *peshitim*. Surely the price changes from city to city, and especially from country to country. How could he write the measure in a book of instruction for the masses?

3) The Rema, who is the one calculating 18 *peshitim*—as brought in the *Piskei Maharai*—is apparently the *Maharam of Rothenburg*, who wrote his responsa at the beginning of the sixth millennium in Ashkenaz.

The *Piskei Maharai* that brought this measure were written about two hundred years later in Austria.

The glosses of the Rema, who also copied the measure, were written more than a hundred years after the *Piskei Maharai* in Poland.

How is it possible that despite this long time and the change of countries, the price of a lamb was 18 *peshitim* just like in the time of the *Maharam*, no less and no more!

## R

[Summer 5705]

I have been asked to clarify: 
a) The details regarding the concept of the Resurrection of the Dead (*Techiyas HaMeisim*), which is a fundamental principle of the Jewish faith, yet its details are not sufficiently explained. 
b) The general concept of *Techiyas HaMeisim*: The survival and existence of the soul is understandable, as the soul is spiritual and a "part of G-d from above," and the "part" is similar to the "whole." But what necessitates that it must return to life specifically in a physical body, and what is the superiority in this?

**Mr. Elchanan HaKohen, Kohen**
**New York**

**Response:** We find that the great Sages of the Talmud (*Chazal*) discussed and investigated these questions, though the matters are scattered in various places. I will present here a portion of what *Chazal* have said on this, with additional explanation as required to answer these questions.

However, first we must address the objection of those who complain: Why discuss such matters at all? Is it not enough that we declare every day, "I believe with perfect faith that there will be a Resurrection of the Dead"? They base their argument on what the Rambam wrote (in his commentary to the Mishnah, *Sanhedrin* 10:1): "The World to Come... you will rarely find someone who thinks about what is the ultimate good... or distinguishes between the ultimate goal and the cause that leads to it. But what the entire public—the masses and the intellectuals alike—ask is: How will the dead rise, naked or clothed? ... Will the rich and the poor be there, etc.?"

But surely the Rambam is not complaining about the public's question, since in many places in the Talmud and Midrash, our great Sages discuss these very matters. His complaint is that people do not investigate the essence of the World to Come and *Techiyas HaMeisim*, and are content with asking only about the aforementioned details and the like. Based on what the Rambam writes at the beginning of his *Iggeres Techiyas HaMeisim*, it is implied that his intent in the aforementioned Mishnah commentary is that "people discuss only *Techiyas HaMeisim*—whether they will rise naked, etc.—while they have completely forgotten the World to Come (which, according to the Rambam, is for souls only and comes after *Techiyas HaMeisim*)." Therefore, I will answer these questions according to what appears to me, in order of their importance: first the second question, and then the first.

***

**A. What is the necessity for the Resurrection of the Dead to be for the soul specifically in a physical body, and what superiority is there in this?**

To understand this, we must first preface an explanation of the concept of *Techiyas HaMeisim*, through which it will be understood why the resurrection comes to the soul in a body.

*Techiyas HaMeisim* in the life of man has two aspects: 
a) A level of perfection for the human species. 
b) A level of receiving reward for his conduct in accordance with the will of his Creator.

***

In truth, both are one and the same. For man (and indeed all parts of creation) was created in such a way that he must ascend from rung to rung on the ladder of perfection, and he was commanded to strive in this (through Torah and *mitzvos*, as will be explained). When he approaches his perfection as much as he is able through his own *avodah*, he is then assisted from above even beyond his ability. This is alluded to in the words of *Chazal* (*Yoma* 39a): "If a person sanctifies himself a little, from below in this world, they sanctify him much, from above, in the World to Come."

- In the language of the Zohar, according to the explanation of Chabad Chassidus: An *is'arusa d'le'eila* (awakening from above) that awakens the *is'arusa d'letata* (awakening from below), and an *is'arusa d'letata* that brings about an *is'arusa d'le'eila* which follows the *is'arusa d'letata*.

Giving reward means providing the recipient with something that is good for him, from the giver or through him. Naturally, it is understood that the greatness and truth of the reward is measured by the good that comes from it.

An example: A laborer who receives bread to eat and a garment to wear as his reward. A student who serves his teacher, and the teacher, as his reward, teaches him wisdom. A student who serves his teacher, and the teacher shows him the purpose of his creation and the path he should walk so that he may reach his goal.

Since spiritual wealth is higher than physical wealth, and eternal happiness is higher than both, it is understood that the study of wisdom is a greater reward than bread to eat, and greater still is the instruction of the ways of life for eternal life.

There are many levels of good—both those that are graspable to us, as mentioned, and those that are not graspable to us. The common denominator is that the body or the soul derives pleasure from them or through them. Since the body and soul are created and limited, the pleasure is also limited, and therefore the reward is also limited.

Higher than all of them is when a person fulfills the *mitzvos* of his Creator and goes on to become refined and perfected; then, the fulfillment of this *mitzvah* connects him with the One who commands the *mitzvah*, his Creator, who is infinite and limitless. And the connection and companionship of the created man with his Creator—there is no good higher than that. Thus, the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* itself is the most exalted reward, as is known from the explanation of *Chazal*: "The reward of a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah*."

***

In the kindness of Hashem toward man, He taught him well the path he should ascend for his perfection. It is given and explained in the Torah—*hora'ah* (instruction)—which encompasses the entire life of man from the first moment of his days onward.

For it is understood that the perfection of any thing is according to the value and measure to which it strives and aligns with the purpose for which it was created.

The reason for creation in general, and the creation of man in particular, and their purpose, is because the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds specifically. That is, that the "lower ones" (in level and rank, for there is no "above" or "below" in place before Him, may He be blessed)—the *yesh* (existence) and the material—should be in a state of *bitul* (nullification), through which the light of Hashem, *Ein Sof*, is revealed and dwells within them. This *bitul* is the purpose and foundation of Torah and *mitzvos*, as it is written (*Devarim* 6:24): "And Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes **to fear** Hashem." This is why the Torah and *mitzvos* were given below, in physical things, and to the soul when it is clothed in a physical body specifically, so that they might transform the *yesh* into *ayin* (nothingness) and make it a vessel for *Elokus* (Divinity).

Just as in the actions of man, for which he was commanded, he was commanded in accordance with his powers and possibilities—slowly, from the easy to the difficult—so too is it with the levels through which he ascends from strength to strength; he climbs and ascends from level to level. And in the reward given to him, they give him the "power" to receive his reward—that is, they refine and accustom him little by little to receive spiritual light and the revelation of *Elokus*—which is the true reward—which goes on to grow more and more.

- Aside from exceptional cases of *hora'as sha'ah* (temporary rulings) where there was a revelation of light not according to value, such as at the time of the Exodus from Egypt, the Giving of the Torah, and the like.

For the **totality of creation in its essence** is being clarified and perfected—(though currently the lower levels of creation, the aspect of "feet and heels," are being clarified, and therefore *Chazal* said—*Shabbos* 112b—"If the first ones were angels, we are men")—even though there are parts of it that fall from their level for a time. Especially in a place where the hands of man, who has free choice, reach, and he can choose evil as well; then he falls, and his portion in the world, which belongs to him and depends on his *avodah*, falls from the level on which it stands. Until he does *teshuvah* and returns himself and all that depends on him to his previous level, and even higher than that. However, for now, all this is in concealment, and in the time to come, it will be revealed.

In general, there are three times for this: This World, the Days of Moshiach, and *Techiyas HaMeisim*. This World is the time of the war between the *yesh* and the spiritual, the good and the evil. "And one nation shall be stronger than the other"; sometimes the good wins, and sometimes, etc.

In the Days of Moshiach, when the Jewish people complete the war and clarify the good from the evil, and the evil is separated from the good, and they go out from exile, then **they** will reach the perfection of man as it was before the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, so that Israel will not be under the dominion of the "tree of good and evil." But there is still the *sitra achra* in the world, in the *erev rav*. And it is understood that consequently, there is also a lack in the perfection of the Jewish people. Therefore, all those who live in the Days of Moshiach will die before *Techiyas HaMeisim*, and only afterwards will they rise, as will be explained.

- It can be said that this is the perfection that man can reach through the power of his *avodah*, and through the reward given to him according to the value of his *avodah*. -

During the Days of Moshiach themselves, they will ascend through their *avodah* on the ladder of perfection, which is why the Days of Moshiach is the time of "today to perform them." And on the contrary, then is the main time of "today to perform them" and the purpose of his perfection.

Added to this is the World of Resurrection, which will remove the spirit of impurity completely from the earth, and there will be no sin or death in the world, for the **Holy One, Blessed be He**, will slaughter the *yetzer hara*, which is the Angel of Death. Then there will be the ultimate perfection of the human species, not only according to the value of his *avodah* and its reward, but what is given as a gift from above. Therefore, *mitzvos* are nullified in the time to come, in *Techiyas HaMeisim*; rather, the righteous sit with their crowns on their heads and derive pleasure from the radiance of the *Shechinah*. After man has reached his ultimate perfection, he receives a most exalted reward that we have no concept of, which is hinted at in the words "their crowns on their heads and derive pleasure from the radiance of the *Shechinah*." (In another place, the explanation of this hint was discussed, but it is not so relevant to our subject.) And this reward will be received below, by the soul in the body specifically, for then will be the purpose and perfection of the creation of this world. For this is why it was created from the beginning: to have a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, in the lower worlds.

***

Thus far is the explanation of the Days of Moshiach and *Techiyas HaMeisim* regarding the levels of perfection of the human species.

To explain their subject regarding the levels of the knowledge of Hashem, the revelation of the Divine light, its apprehension and feeling, one must understand as it is written (*Iyov* 19:26): "And from my flesh I shall see G-d," and according to *Chazal* (*Berachos* 10a): "Just as the Holy One, Blessed be He, fills the whole world, so too the soul fills the whole body."

The vitality of the soul that animates the body has two aspects: a) That which is divided according to the temperament of the vessels of the body's limbs and is clothed within them as an internal, limited light, according to the limb. This is from the power of the intellect in the head to the power of walking in the foot. b) The power of will, which exists within the entire body but is not divided according to the parts of the body's vessels to be clothed within them as a truly internal light; rather, it dwells within them as an encompassing light (*ohr makif*). Above these two is the soul itself, which is one simple, spiritual essence.

Man, because of the concealment of the physical body, cannot grasp the **essence** of spirituality, even the spirituality that is truly clothed within him—that is, the soul and its powers, even the internal ones—but through their actions, he feels their **existence**.

And like all these things, by way of analogy, it is with Hashem, *Ein Sof*, Blessed be He, who: a) Fills all worlds, as the radiance of the *Shechinah* is clothed within the interiors of the worlds and is divided according to their different levels. b) Surrounds all worlds, as the light is within them, but is not divided according to their levels; rather, it dwells within them as an encompassing light. And above these two is His essence and being, may He be blessed, which is not in the category of worlds at all.

- There are many, many levels in each of the aforementioned aspects, and I have written here only in a general way, and only as is necessary for our subject. -

And, as in the analogy, in this physical and material world we cannot grasp the **essence** of the Divine light, even the essence of the light that fills all worlds; rather, through its actions we know and feel its existence, as it is written (*Yeshayahu* 40:26): "Lift up your eyes on high and see who created these."

Added to this is the Garden of Eden, which is the world of souls, and there is no body there to conceal, so they grasp even the essence of the light that fills all worlds.

Added to this are the Days of Moshiach, when the material will be refined, and the image of G-d will shine in man, and as it was before the sin and even higher than that, there will be revelations from the light that surrounds all worlds.

Higher than all of them, after the dead rise, which is the ultimate perfection of this world, there will then be a revelation of the essence of *Ein Sof*, Blessed be He.

After the general subject of *Techiyas HaMeisim* has been explained, we will proceed to explain its details according to what is brought in the words of *Chazal*.

***

**B. Details regarding the concept of *Techiyas HaMeisim*.**

**Its Time.** We learned: The Holy Temple precedes the ingathering of the exiles, the ingathering of the exiles precedes *Techiyas HaMeisim*, etc. We learned: Forty years before the ingathering of the exiles to *Techiyas HaMeisim* (*Zohar* Vol. I, 139a; see also there 134a).

**Its Place.** Whether those buried in the Land of Israel or those buried abroad, their soul returns to their body in the Land of Israel.

From where do I know this? It is stated in *Kesuvos* (111a): "Rabbi Elazar said: The dead outside the Land do not live, as it is said: 'And I will give beauty in the land of the living'—the land whose beauty is in it, its dead live; that which has no beauty in it, its dead do not live, etc." And according to Rabbi Elazar, the righteous who are abroad do not live (immediately). Rabbi Ila'a said: Through *gilgul* (the bones roll until the Land of Israel and live there). He asks: *Gilgul* is a pain for the righteous! Abaye said: Tunnels are made for them in the ground (and they walk through them to the Land of Israel, and there they emerge).

Since even the righteous who are buried abroad live, it must be said that according to Rabbi Elazar, according to the conclusion, the meaning of the verse "And I will give beauty, etc." is that it does not speak of the place of death and burial, but of the place of resurrection, which will be specifically in the Land of Israel. And even those who came to the Land of Israel through tunnels are called the dead of the Land of Israel, since the soul is given into their body only after they emerge in the Land of Israel, as will be explained.

Since this is so, there is no necessity or proof that the place of burial matters for the subject of *Techiyas HaMeisim*. And if so, it can be said that even Rabbi Elazar holds that those buried abroad live. This is understood according to the simple meaning of what the *Shelah* writes (*Shaar HaOsios*, end of letter *Kuf*): "Rabbi Elazar said: The dead abroad do not live except through *gilgul*." And it is as mentioned above.

However, the righteous merit tunnels and do not have the pain of *gilgul* to the Land of Israel, unlike those who are not as righteous. But all of them come to the Land of Israel—and then they are called the dead of the Land of Israel—and there they live.

In this way, even according to Rabbi Elazar, the Mishnah (*Sanhedrin* 90a) that "all Israel have a portion in the World to Come" is understood according to its simple meaning. And the wonder of the *Tosafos* (*Sotah* 5a) is resolved.

Rabbi Abba bar Memel in *Kesuvos* (ibid.) disagrees with Rabbi Elazar and says that they will also rise in the Land abroad. But since several *Amoraim* in this passage hold like Rabbi Elazar or discuss the matter according to his view, it is understood that the *halachah* is according to him, as is known in the rules of the Talmud.

**Who rises in *Techiyas HaMeisim*.** "All Israel have a portion in the World to Come (*Techiyas HaMeisim*), etc. And these are the ones who have no portion in the World to Come: he who says there is no *Techiyas HaMeisim* from the Torah, etc." (*Sanhedrin* 90a). The Rambam elaborated on this in *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3.

See regarding this in the collection of responses and explanations in this volume, issues 6-7, and I will not repeat the words here.

**Old souls (that were already once in the world) and their bodies.** Rabbi Chizkiyah said: If you say that all the bodies of the world will rise and awaken from the dust, what will become of those bodies that were planted with one soul (which was first in one body and then came in a second body)? Rabbi Yosi said: Those bodies, etc. (*Zohar* Vol. I, 131a; *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 40). The *Arizal* explained his words (*Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 4): "If the first time... he did not merit to rectify the **entire** (soul) and died... therefore at the time of *Techiyas HaMeisim*, the first body has only that specific part (of the soul) which he rectified in life. And therefore, when this soul rolls into another body to complete its rectification... the aspects of the parts of the soul that were rectified in this second body... they belong to this second body at the time of the resurrection... and this is according to the aforementioned in the *Saba d'Mishpatim* (*Zohar* Vol. II, 100a) regarding *yibum*."

And one should not ask that if so, there will be several people who have only some specific parts of the soul and not a whole soul, for it is known that every part of the soul is included in all the parts. And every part by itself is a complete structure, even though from the perspective of being a part of a more general soul, it is only one aspect.

And greater than this we find, that the totality of all souls together is only one soul of Adam HaRishon, as hinted in the words of *Chazal* (*Shemos Rabbah* 40): "While Adam HaRishon was still a *golem*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, showed him every single righteous person who would arise from him; there is one who is dependent on the head of Adam, and there is one who is dependent on his hair, etc." See *Tanya*, Chapter 2 and Chapter 32, *Iggeres HaKodesh* 7, and more.

**Its Manner.** Just as a man goes, so he comes. He goes blind and comes blind, deaf and comes deaf, mute and comes mute. Just as he goes clothed, he comes clothed, etc. The Holy One, Blessed be He, said: "Let them stand as they went, and afterwards I will heal them" (*Bereishis Rabbah* 95; *Zohar* Vol. III, 91a; see there Vol. II, 199b).

Explanation of "goes clothed": It is taught in the name of Rabbi Nasan: The garment that goes down with a man to the grave comes with him (*Yerushalmi Kesuvos* 12:3; and so it is in *Niddah* 61b). And according to the version of the *Tosafos* (*Kesuvos* 111b), there is a dispute in the matter, and according to the Rabbi, they come in their garments that they were accustomed to in life.

And in the *Zohar* (Vol. I, 203b): "At the time that Israel will rise from the dust, many lame and many blind will be among them, and then the Holy One, Blessed be He, will illuminate them with that sun to be healed by it." And this is like the words of *Chazal* (*Nedarim* 8b): "The Holy One, Blessed be He, will take the sun out of its sheath, and the righteous will be healed by it."

**Its Order.** The dead of the Land of Israel live first, afterwards the dead of the Land abroad (*Yerushalmi Kilayim* 9:3 and *Kesuvos* ibid.), and afterwards the Generation of the Desert, and some say the Patriarchs (*Zohar* Vol. I, 113a). Rabbi Shimon says: The dead of the Land of Israel live first, afterwards the dead of the Land abroad, and afterwards those who sleep in Chevron. The reason is explained in the book *Avkas Rochel* (Book 2, Part 4): so that they may awaken and stir to joy upon seeing their children who have risen from their graves, and the land is filled with many righteous and pious people.

The righteous rise first and afterwards the rest of the people (*Zohar* ibid. 140a), the masters of Torah and afterwards the masters of *mitzvos* (ibid. 182a and in the explanations of the *Zohar*). And in the Midrash it is stated (brought in the book *Ohev Yisrael*, *Likkutim*, *Parshas Berachah*) that they will rise and be called by their names according to the order of the *aleph-beis*, but whoever has the trait of humility will rise first.

**The people who will be at the time of *Techiyas HaMeisim*.** Rav Saadia Gaon wrote (in the book *Emunos V'Deios*, end of Chapter 7) that because the verse did not speak of this and our Sages did not receive a tradition on this, they disagreed, etc.

But now that we have merited the revelation of the book of *Zohar*, it is found there (Vol. II, 108b): "Until now, death was from the *sitra achra*; from here on, 'I kill and I make alive.' From here, that at that time, all those who did not taste the taste of death, from Me (from the Holy One, Blessed be He) will be their death, and He will raise them immediately. Why? So that no impurity will remain in the world at all, and the world will be a new world through the works of the hands of the Holy One, Blessed be He."

**Details of the resurrection of the body.** That very body itself will rise to life, as it is written: "**Your dead will live**," and it does not say "will be created." For one bone remains from the body, and at the time of the resurrection, the Holy One, Blessed be He, softens it with the dew of resurrection, and the bone becomes like leaven for the dough, and from it the entire body is built (*Zohar* Vol. II, 28b; see there Vol. III, 169a).

**Whether there is a Day of Judgment after the dead rise.** There are three opinions on this matter: a) After *Techiyas HaMeisim* there will be the Great Day of Judgment in which all of humanity is judged according to their deeds (*Ramban* in the book *HaGemul* and others). b) Every person is judged immediately upon his death, and there is no room for an additional judgment after the resurrection. And what is found in many places as the expression "Day of Judgment" for the time after the resurrection—its meaning is a day of punishment and vengeance (*Mahari Abarbanel* in the book *Maayanei HaYeshuah*, Spring 8, Palm 7). c) The *Arizal*, and his words: "And if you say, since this soul has already passed through Yom Kippur and afflictions that cleanse, etc., and afterwards *gilgulim*, why must it return and be judged on the Great Day of Judgment? It can be said that the Great Day of Judgment is only for the nations of the world." (Brought in the book *Nishmas Chaim*, Essay 1, Chapter 17). And the author of this book adds: "And if you say, what will be of those who die close to the resurrection and have not yet received their punishment through *gilgulim* or afflictions, etc.? I will answer that justice dictates that under the long time of their judgment, they will receive such an immense and extreme punishment in a short time, so that the quality of the punishment will be under the quantity of time, so that they may merit the life of the World to Come. And these things are sealed and hidden, and blessed is the One who knows."

**Life after *Techiyas HaMeisim*.** The World to Come (after the dead rise) has no eating, no drinking, no procreation, no business, no jealousy, no hatred, and no competition; rather, the righteous sit with their crowns on their heads and derive pleasure from the radiance of the *Shechinah* (*Berachos* 17a), and they do not return to their dust (*Sanhedrin* 92a) and exist forever.

## 201

B"H, Tuesday, 23rd of the month of Menachem Av, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, G-d-fearing and observant, engaged in the work of Hashem, etc., Rabbi Y. [Pleyer] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the end of last week, enclosing the check for $41.41 for the subscriptions to the *sichos* and the *tacks* [tax/postage] in accordance with the list you sent: the booklets for the months of Tishrei and Mar-Cheshvan have been sent immediately to the aforementioned subscribers.

Regarding the *Chumashim*, it is possible to obtain the *Chumash Bereishis* with Rashi for a price of 41–45 cents per *Chumash*. If this is the type of *Chumash* you intended and you agree to the price, we are prepared to arrange the purchase and shipment.

To conclude with words of Torah: At the end of the *sedra* of this past Shabbos, [it is written,] "And his concubine, etc., and Maachah." It is customary to explain to students that Maachah was the daughter of the concubine. However, I have seen that this interpretation is a subject of dispute. For the intent of the verse in recounting "And his concubine, etc.," I have found three interpretations:

a) The verse is recounting **all** the good news that was brought to Avraham (Ramban).

b) The narrator is telling us that his concubine also bore Maachah, who was likewise worthy of his son [Yitzchak] had he not chosen Rivkah (Seforno).

c) It equates her families with the families of Avraham... eight sons of the wives and four sons of the concubines (Rashi, and this is in *Bereishis Rabbah*; the language of our Sages, "she equated," is in the singular, referring to Milkah alone. Perhaps it can be said that the sons of the concubines are considered as belonging to the wife—similar to what is written regarding Hagar, Bilhah, and Zilpah, although it is not entirely the same, as those were maidservants, and this still requires further study).

Now, according to the Seforno, Maachah is a woman’s name. But according to Rashi, the foremost of the commentators, and based on the *Midrash*, it must be that he was also a son; for if not, there would have to be another child in the house of Nachor to correspond to Dinah. As is understood, I subsequently found in *Seder HaDoros* explicitly that Maachah is a son of Nachor.

It seems the custom to interpret Maachah as a daughter—deviating from what is necessitated by Rashi—crept in because the matter is not **explicitly** stated in Rashi, and in the study of *Nach*, people are accustomed to Maachah being a woman’s name (the name of the wife of Dovid, and the name of the wife of Rechavam or his son Aviyah—Rashi, *Divrei Hayamim II* 13:2).

However, we also find Maachah as a man’s name (*Divrei Hayamim I* 11:43; 23:16—for it is forced to explain that they were named after their mother), because we have many names that are identical for both male and female (Ibn Ezra, end of *parshas Vayishlach*; and see there in the commentary of the Ramban).

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## Rav

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Mr. Tzadok Rivkin, may he live for long and good days,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is with joy that we inform you that, despite the great difficulties encountered recently in connection with the strike, the impossibility of obtaining paper, and so on, we have succeeded in printing the Siddurim for our brothers in Europe—an endeavor in which you participated by taking upon yourself the costs of the first edition.

We have sent you a few Siddurim in a separate package, and in these coming days, the first shipment of Siddurim is departing for the Jewish camps in Europe.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the great mitzvah you have performed by enabling the printing of Siddurim for our martyred brothers. Just imagine that several times a day—when davening, eating, reciting brachos, etc.—they will use this Siddur, and in doing so, they will think of the Jew, Tzadok Rivkin, in distant New York, who gave them the opportunity to daven and pray to the Ribono shel Olam just as they, their parents, and their grandparents were accustomed (not to mention that in many places, they are also learning in chadarim from these Siddurim with dozens of children).

The Gemara (Bava Kamma 92b) interprets the verse (Shemos 23:25), "And you shall serve Hashem your G-d," to mean serving Him through davening, through Krias Shema and tefillah.

We wish for you that the zechus of having given thousands of Jews the opportunity to serve the Ribono shel Olam should stand by you, so that the continuation of the aforementioned verse may be fulfilled in your life: "He will bless your bread and your water, and I will remove sickness from your midst... I will fulfill the number of your days"—may you be healthy and have a happy old age with arichus yamim v’shanim tovos.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

***

From the secretariat copy.

**Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel:** Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch.

## 203

B"H, Friday, 18 Kislev, 5706

To our dear friend, the distinguished and accomplished, wise and understanding, etc.,
The Tamim, R' Y.L. Halevi, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Since you are currently the only one in your city whom we recognize as acknowledging his responsibility for proper chinuch in your city in general, and for the existence of the chinuch institutions under the presidency of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, in particular, we are turning to you regarding the following matter.

You are surely aware that last year we agreed to the opening of a school for girls, Beis Rivkah or Beis Sarah, in Dorchester under the administration of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. In our decision, we relied upon our friends there to exert themselves in securing the financial means to operate the aforementioned school, so that it would be a self-sustaining institution. We agreed for a short period to provide the school—as a loan—a portion of their budget, in order to enable the timely payment of teachers' salaries.

However, sufficient time has already passed to stabilize the financial situation of the school, and to our distress, we are only informed of expenses, not of income, and we do not see the necessary interest in organizing this matter.

The expenses of the school are not that great, and when taking into account the income from student tuition, we see that it would not be difficult at all for you to obtain the necessary sum, with the help of a Ladies Auxiliary that you would establish for the school, or income from other sources.

In any event, you must know that the situation of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch does not allow for sending checks to teachers without receiving the necessary funds for this from you.

As you surely recognize, beyond the fact that the responsibility for the chinuch of girls is extremely great—as it is written, "The wisdom of women builds her house," and see Shemos Rabbah, parsha 28, that the existence of the giving of the Torah was dependent upon the women—the existence of all proper chinuch institutions and their success in educating their students depends very much upon the existence of a school for the chinuch of girls.

We strongly request that, despite your preoccupations, you please take **immediate action** regarding the means necessary to stabilize the situation of the girls' school. Since there are no others who will stand at the head of this enterprise, surely from Above they have cast this holy avodah upon you, and therefore you are also given the kochos to fulfill your shlichus.

We await your response as soon as possible, and we conclude with wishes for all the best for the upcoming Chag HaGeulah.

## 204

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The esteemed and elevated Mr. Dober Padowar, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

We hereby acknowledge receipt of your donation to Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch and enclose a receipt herewith.

I hope that you will continue to take an interest in the work of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch in the future, and that you will endeavor to assist in this not only with your own person and means, but also by utilizing your influence upon your circle of relatives and acquaintances to merit them as well, and to draw their hearts toward this work.

The verse states that "man is the tree of the field," and we see that any change, even a slight one, **in the seed**, changes the tree that grows from that seed from one extreme to the other. The same applies to the education of a child; therefore, even for the sake of a minor improvement in his education, it is worth exerting effort upon effort—and all the more so if the education requires correction in fundamental matters that are liable to affect the child throughout all the days of his life.

And it is a certainty that advocacy and action performed in truth do not return empty.

With blessing and respect,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 205

21 Kislev, 5706
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, etc.,
Rabbi M.D. [Rivkin], may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

Enclosed herewith is the return of the manuscript of Rabbi S. Sofer, a copy of the *maamarim* of the Rebbe Maharash, of blessed memory, which you requested to have photographed. Also enclosed is a copy of the books that have been printed in this manner.

It is unnecessary to elaborate, to him and to those like him, on the immense value of this matter and the great *nachas ruach* of the author, of blessed memory, when, through the request you made, these *maamarim* finally reach thousands of students and scholars. With every reading and study of them, "the lips of the righteous murmur in the grave, and his soul is in the Yeshivah of the Heavens" (*Yevamos* 96b, Tosafos s.v. *Agurah*; see also the language of Rashi in *Bechoros* 31b). And who is greater than David, King of Israel, who yearned and prayed that it be the will [of Hashem] that a teaching be stated in his name, thereby dwelling in two worlds—meaning that his lips would murmur, etc.

And since in every matter the conduct is *midah k’neged midah* (measure for measure), it is seemingly certain that just as the righteous one dwells in **two** worlds, so too the reward for all those who exert themselves in this is likewise both in spirituality and in physicality, with an abundance of physical and spiritual good.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

***

Since this matter has come before us, let us say a word about it: The request—and the **insistence**—that a teaching be stated **in their name** (in the introduction to *Divrei Nechemiah*, *Choshen Mishpat*, the author’s son elaborates on the reason why it must specifically be in their name; there is room to comment on his words, but this is not the place) is mentioned in the words of our Sages regarding David, Rabbi Yochanan (both in *Yevamos*, ibid.), Rabbi Sheshes (*Bechoros* 31b), and Rabbi Yitzchak (*Zohar* Vol. I, 217b).

In *Chassidus*, one can find a reason why the matter of "I will dwell in Your tent for all worlds" applies to these four individuals **more** than to ordinary people:

1) David exerted himself greatly that that sin be forgiven him, and furthermore, **that all of Israel know** that it had been forgiven him, as is found in *Shabbos* (30a) and *Sanhedrin* (107a). Now, if a Rabbi is not similar to an angel, etc., one does not learn Torah from his mouth, as our Sages said (*Chagigah* 15b; see *Chidushei Maharich* on *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, beginning of ch. 4). Therefore, David specifically exerted himself that a teaching be stated in his name, for thereby it would also be known that that sin had been forgiven him.

With this, one can also resolve the passage in the *Yerushalmi*, *Berachos* (ch. 2, end of halacha 4). After citing the passage in *Yevamos* that David requested that a teaching be stated in his name, it concludes: "David is not, etc. (And David said) 'May it come upon me that I rejoice in my heart' (regarding the building of the Beis Hamikdash)." Seemingly, this matter has no connection there. The *Sefer Chareidim* explicitly writes that we do not have this version there, but in all our books it is included. According to the above, it can be understood: David’s request was for a sign that his sin had been forgiven. Hashem told him that the sign would be specifically through the building of the Beis Hamikdash (*Shabbos*, ibid.). Thus, it was established through two things that the sin was forgiven: a) Through Israel stating a teaching in his name, as mentioned above. b) Through Hashem performing a sign. Therefore, after the *Yerushalmi* brings David’s efforts regarding the first matter, it concludes that David rejoiced in the building of the Beis Hamikdash, for that is a sign **from Above** that the sin was forgiven—and there is no need to corrupt the text of the books of the *Yerushalmi*.

2) Rabbi Yochanan’s sons died, as is found in *Berachos* (5b; see *Seder Hadoros* under his entry as to whether a son was born to him afterward). In order that Hashem not be filled with anger against him, he needed to leave behind students worthy of inheriting him, and he follows his own opinion in *Bava Basra* (116a). Therefore, he specifically exerted himself that a teaching be stated in his name.

3) Similar to the above regarding Rabbi Yochanan is the case of Rabbi Yitzchak. Although he had a son (*Zohar*, ibid.), our Sages said in *Bava Basra* (ibid.) at the conclusion of the passage that Hashem is filled with anger—that even if He is not filled with anger [at the father], if he left behind a son worthy of inheriting him (note *Sefer Maavar Yabok*, *Maamar* 45, ch. 28), nevertheless, death is spoken of regarding the father if the son is not **like him**. Regarding Rabbi Yitzchak’s son, it was said that "until now he had not merited in Torah" (*Zohar*, ibid., 218a). Therefore, Rabbi Yitzchak insisted that a teaching be stated in his name, for students are called children. With this, the **relevance** of the requests Rabbi Yitzchak made (*Zohar*, ibid.) is also sweetened: that they state a teaching in his name and that they teach his son Torah (his third request is explained in *Shaar Maamarei Rashbi*, end of *Parshas Vayechi*).

4) Regarding Rabbi Sheshes, it is found in *Shaar HaGilgulim* (end of Introduction 4) and in *Sefer HaGilgulim* (ch. 10), in explanation of our Sages' words (*Pesachim* 68b) that Rabbi Sheshes would say, "Rejoice, **my soul**, for you I have studied, for you I have learned, etc." Rabbi Sheshes knew that he was initially in the body of Bava ben Buta and had perfected his soul, lacking only a small matter. For this, his soul was reincarnated a second time in Rabbi Sheshes. In such a manner of reincarnation, the order is that the primary reward for the *mitzvos* he performs in the second incarnation is only for the sake of his soul and not his second body, for at the time of the Resurrection, his soul will return to the first body in which he engaged in Torah and *mitzvos* for the **majority** of what was required of him. Therefore, his body—that of Rabbi Sheshes—was sad, and he would say "Rejoice, **my soul**" specifically, and not the body.

It seems to me that all this applies to other *mitzvos*, but when they state a teaching from the mouth of Rabbi Sheshes, at which time the **lips** must murmur in the grave **in this world**, it is obvious that the lips of the body of Rabbi Sheshes, and not Bava ben Buta, will be murmuring. Therefore, he specifically exerted himself that a teaching be stated in his name. (And yet he said, "Rejoice, my soul, for you I have studied, etc.," because he was saying this regarding **his own** Torah study, as is found there in *Pesachim*; see also *Tanya*, end of ch. 37. Whereas stating a teaching, etc., is what he taught Torah to his students, and they would later repeat the teaching in his name. And this is clear.)

**Note:** Rabbi Yitzchak requested specifically of Rabbi Yehudah that he state a teaching in his name (the reason is understood according to what is written in *Shaar Maamarei Rashbi*, ibid.).

Now, in *Zohar Chadash* (39a), it is implied that Rabbi Yehudah interprets "murmuring the lips of those who sleep" as the speech of the mouth, but Rabbi Yitzchak **disagrees** with him (see there in *Biurei HaZohar*). And if you say that the event in *Zohar Chadash* (Vol. I) preceded the event in *Zohar Chadash* (Vol. III) (which was after the *Idra Rabba* in *Parshas Naso*, for it concludes there—39b—"Rabbi Yissa, our colleague, who has departed from among us," and he departed in the *Idra Rabba*, as written in *Zohar Chadash* 144a), it is possible that after Rabbi Yitzchak heard it from Rabbi Yehudah, he accepted it from him, or it is possible that there is only a difference in the interpretation of the verse "murmuring the lips of those who sleep," but both hold of the words of our Sages regarding "I will dwell in Your tent for all worlds."

In the *Yerushalmi*, *Shekalim* (end of ch. 2), the author of the statement "murmuring the lips, etc.—murmuring in the grave" is Rabbi Yitzchak. But it is possible to say as above, or that it is not the aforementioned Rabbi Yitzchak, for there are many Rabbi Yitzchaks in the *Shas*.

## 176

15 Teves, 5706

To the honorable Rav, Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc.,
Rabbi M.D. [Rivkin], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter.

1) You understood from my letter that I intend to explain that by reciting a *shmuah* (teaching) in this world, the *neshamah* of the author of that *shmuah* is, at that moment, studying in the *Yeshivah Shel Maalah*. You noted that the recitation of the *shmuah* is effective only regarding the concept that "his lips murmur in the grave," but that the fact of his *neshamah* being in the *Yeshivah Shel Maalah* is a separate matter, resulting from the fact that he studied Torah **in general** during his lifetime in this world, and is not related to the recitation of the *shmuah* from his lips. I did not find in your letter any reason that compels one to enter into this distinction. I stand by my opinion. Whether by *peshat* (simple meaning), *sevarah* (logical reasoning), or *ma'amar razal* (the statements of our Sages). *Peshat*: The simple meaning of the *sugya* is that by reciting the *shmuah* in his name, one accomplishes: a) "He dwells," b) he dwells in **two** worlds. For while it is possible to dwell in one world through other means (in this world, literally; and in the World to Come, through the performance of *mitzvos*), the recitation of the *shmuah* is effective for both worlds simultaneously. *Sevarah*: If the recitation of his *shmuah* in Torah is effective such that his lips **in the grave** will murmur, then *kal v'chomer* (all the more so) it should be effective that his *neshamah*—which is **the one who is primarily** studying the Torah (provided that the intention is "when the *yetzer hara* is between you"—*Shabbos* 89a)—will be murmuring at that time. *Ma'amar Razal*: Rashi in *Bechoros* (31b)—which I mentioned in my previous letter—implies that he interprets "in two worlds" as: in this world, meaning the lips of the one reciting the *shmuah*, and in the **World to Come**, meaning the lips of the one in whose name it is said. From this, we can infer for the other commentators who explain "I will dwell in two worlds" that it refers to this very *shmuah* itself. If you were to say that his dwelling **in the World to Come** is the case regardless, and does not depend on the recitation of the *shmuah* **now** from his lips, then the words of the *Tosafos* (in *Yevamos* 96b) regarding the *Yeshivah Shel Maalah* would be incomprehensible; they should have simply said "in the World to Come." We must therefore conclude that as a reward for having studied Torah previously, and because the repetition of his *shmuah* awakens this matter now, the reward of a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah* itself—that according to its essence, so is its reward: that they seat him **now** in the *Yeshivah Shel Maalah*. See also the statements of our Sages brought in *Chinuch L'Naar*, p. 22, that **at the moment** a good deed is performed that the deceased caused, he receives reward; from a son, we learn for a student.

2) Regarding your attempt to explain the difference between the two parables for "his lips murmur, etc." in the *Yerushalmi* (*Berachos* ch. 2, 5a, and elsewhere)—whether it is like "old wine" or "conditum" (spiced wine), which differ as to which *shmuah* causes the lips to murmur—that it refers to the inner dimensions of Torah versus the revealed and *pilpul* specifically—this is difficult to understand. For several reasons: a) From any perspective, it should have been clear to Rabbi Yochanan, etc., to specify that they are particular about **such** a *shmuah* specifically. b) In *Yevamos* and *Bechoros*, Rabbi Yochanan and Rabbi Shimon are dealing with the **revealed** Torah, and they were particular and placed under *cherem* over it; if the one who says "like old wine" were correct, all of this would be in vain. c) *Conditum* is wine with **honey** and peppers (*Pesikta d'Rav Kahana*, *Piska B'Chodesh HaShlishi*, cited in the *Aruch*), and when dividing the Torah as a whole, honey refers to the **hidden** [Torah], as it states in *Chagigah* (13a, 14b). d) In *Yerushalmi Shekalim* (end of ch. 2), it explains further, stating: "**What benefit is it to him?** One says like one who drinks *conditum*, another says like one who drinks old wine." According to your approach, this has no explanation.

In my humble opinion: In every *shmuah* that is said, whether in the revealed or the hidden, there is the essence of the *shmuah*, for which there is a measure and a limit, and the *pilpul* within the *shmuah*, which is something that has no end (explained at length in the *Kuntres Acharon* to *Hilchos Talmud Torah*—by the Alter Rebbe—beginning of ch. 9). The *Yerushalmi* is understood according to its simple meaning: It asks, what benefit is it to the author of the *shmuah* that he himself should repeat his **old** *shmuah* once again? To this it answers—and based on what is written in *Mesillas Yesharim* ch. 15, note 7: "The *Mishnah* is like wine and the *Shas* is like *conditum*"—one says like *conditum*, that as many times as he repeats the *shmuah* in the *Yeshivah Shel Maalah*, he will find in it new insights and **new** logic, as mentioned above regarding *pilpul*. And one says like old wine—the *Mishnah* is old—for even though he has already drunk it, he tastes it in his mouth, meaning that even after a long time, he feels and derives pleasure from the taste that is within it, even in the old logic.

See the *Korban HaEdah* on *Yerushalmi Shekalim* and the introduction to *Sefer Emek She'eilah* by the Maharammad of Arenstieple, who explain the difference between the two parables. This also requires further study, in my humble opinion, but this is not the place to elaborate.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 107

B"H, Wednesday, 15 Teves, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our dear friend, the distinguished and exalted Torah scholar, G-d-fearing, etc., the Temim, Rabbi Y. Zuber, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Now that the process of sending packages abroad has been eased to a certain extent, we find it appropriate to draw your attention to the publications of the "Kehot" publishing house, which was founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, some four years ago, and whose educational value has been acknowledged in all circles.

There is no doubt that even if not all of them are suitable for your country, as some are written in English, those written in Lashon HaKodesh and Yiddish will certainly find a readership. And surely there are many in Sweden who also know English.

At the end of the booklet "Moreh Shiur," you will find a list of all the aforementioned publications, as well as a list of Seforim of Chassidus and Sichos of the Rebbe, shlita, which will surely find those in your vicinity who understand these Seforim.

We are interested in knowing about the state of education in your country, both among those who have resided there for some time and among the children of the refugees.

We await your response.

Our Sages have said (Pesachim 119a) that **Yosef** concealed three treasures—he is called this after Yosef Li D’Ben **Acher**, who strives to transform even the "Acher" (the "Other") into a son (Or HaTorah, discourse *Ben Poras* at length)—and his intent is that the treasure **be revealed** and perform its function. This occurs in three ways: 1) He blesses, and a blessing is in "silver," in love, as is known from the Priestly Blessing, and as brought down in the Shulchan Aruch—in material influences of wealth and honor, which is the matter (there in the Gemara) of that which **was revealed to Korach** (Ohr HaTorah, end of Parshas Vayigash). 2) Those who are not observers of Torah and Mitzvos, he makes into Baalei Teshuvah, clarifying even from the *kelipos*, converts, which is the matter of that which was revealed to Antoninus. 3) In those who observe Torah and Mitzvos, he effects an elevation in their manner of Avodas Hashem, which is the matter of the treasure that is revealed to the **Tzaddikim**. It is understood that the first two ways are most relevant now, in this lowest of worlds, and the third way is the "World to Come in this world," and specifically the matter of bringing the Tzaddikim to Teshuvah. And this is what the Shas concludes there—that it will be revealed in the future.

It is obvious that every one of those who are Mekushar and connected to Yosef HaTzaddik must become a conduit, and at the very least assist and prepare his environment so that it becomes a vessel ready to receive the instructions and influences of Yosef, until the complete Redemption, immediately, which will be through the Holy One, Blessed be He, Himself, in the aspect that is called **Yosef**, as written in the Shach, cited in Ohr HaTorah, discourse *Vayiten Es Kolo*.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Redemption.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

**107**
From the secretariat copy.

**To... Zuber:** Another letter to him—see 117 below.

**Yosef HaTzaddik:** My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. See also the subsequent letter.

## 208

By the grace of Hashem, 5th of Shevat, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished *Tamim*, etc., R. Moshe Zev, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters:

1) We have been sending printing materials and *maamarim* to Shanghai from the *Yeshiva* for some time now, and we have sent the *seforim* from those categories that were not sent by *Tomchei Temimim*.

2) I, too, have heard that they have printed several *seforim* there. It is surprising that during all this time they have not sent even one sample copy, except for a *Kovetz Sichos* of the Rebbe, which was received—one copy for the Rebbe about two years ago, I believe.

3) The *hanacha* from 19 Kislev was taken by the Rebbe for himself, and he will return it with additions and changes in the near future—this is what he told me.

4) Regarding its printing, he instructed me that it is appropriate to print the *Reshimos Divrei* from 18 Elul and 19 Kislev **together** ("It is a pity that the listeners did not grasp the significance of the connection between 18 Elul and 19 Kislev, which has now been revealed to them, according to its importance"—these are the words of the Rebbe). However, for the time being, he has not yet provided all the *reshimos*, even though the vast majority are already completed.

5) Regarding the expenses for printing these *sichos*, I have not yet received anything from R. Menachem Mendel HaKohen, despite his assurances.

6) If you have notes on the *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*, why do you not write them to me?

7) Regarding your suggestion that *Anash*, the *Temimim*, etc., should record their memories of days gone by: the Rebbe has urged this many times. How many of those mentioned have responded to his request? And who is greater than us—for **three** years I have been speaking with the *Temimim* of Montreal about the *Reshimos Divrei* regarding the events of the year 5700, and apart from a few pages that you sent me (I believe this was **more than two years ago**), I have not had the merit to see even **one line** of these *reshimos*!!

8) *Tzemach Tzedek*, *Kuntres* 48, *Mayim Rabim*—these are not yet finished. When they are published, they will be sent to you as you requested.

9) The lack of letters is due to the multitude of preoccupations, especially regarding printing matters. You complain to me in vain. To give you an idea of the work involved: recently I have had to proofread (besides *Kuntres* 47, and primarily the additions within it, and the *Sichos* and *Talks*): a booklet on Purim, Pesach in French (similar to the one for Tishrei), a Purim *Kovetz* in English, Volume 1 of *Divrei Yemei Yisrael* in English, and the final proofreading of *Mayim Rabim*.

- In the middle of proofreading: The additions to the *Tzemach Tzedek* (which will include 125 *sheilos u’teshuvos* and over 100 pages of *chiddushim* on *Shas*, all this in addition to editing indices, etc.), the *Kuntres* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* and *Haskalah*, and a *Kovetz Sichos* of the Rebbe (which will contain over 300 pages, mimeographed).

- At the beginning of proofreading: *Sefer Maamarei Yilamdeinu Rabbeinu*, *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, a *Kuntres* regarding the Rebbe Maharash (a *Kovetz Sichos* and a list of his *maamarim*), *Sichos* of the Rebbe Shlita (5700—until Rosh Hashanah 5701; belonging to Dalfon), *Sefer Maamarei* of the Rebbe (5700—5702), a *Sefer Sheilos u’Teshuvos* between teacher and student on the religion of Israel and its customs in English, a *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch* for youth in English, and more.

If you consider that in addition to the above, there is work regarding the affairs of *Machne Israel* and *Kehot*—aside from the printing department—my hope is that several of your questions, if you have any, will resolve themselves.

Now, the above is what is happening here at the **center**. What is happening in the **circle**?

It is known that all exiles have their root in the exile of Egypt. If so, a parallel exists in all of them, and especially in the final exile (the purpose of which is that they shall be and shall plunder, etc., in a **general** sense in the Diaspora, what was done then only in Egypt). The difficulty of the exile is sweetened by the preparations and actions of Yosef HaTzaddik, who in truth is the only provider for the entire land. His general action is "And Yosef gathered all the money, etc., and he hid it" (*Pesachim* 119a). It is obvious that he did not intend for it to remain hidden as if it did not exist, but rather that everything goes toward one goal: the mission of Yosef, who is called Yosef because "Hashem has added (*yosef*) me another son," meaning that he will also turn an **"other"** into a son (*Ohr HaTorah*, *d.h. Ben Poras* at length). The action is through the three "hidden treasures" (*Pesachim* ibid.), which are three modes: 1) He blesses—and blessing is in money, in love, as is known from the Priestly Blessing and brought to *halacha* in the *Shulchan Aruch*—with material abundance, wealth, and honor, which is the matter (there in the *Gemara*) of what was **revealed to Korach** (*Ohr HaTorah*, end of *Parshas Vayigash*). 2) Those who do not observe *Torah u’Mitzvos*, he makes them *baalei teshuvah*, clarifying even from the *kelipas nogah*, converts—this is the matter of what was revealed to Antoninus. 3) Among those who observe *Torah u’Mitzvos*, he effects an elevation in their manner of *avodas Hashem*; this is the matter of the treasure revealed to the *tzaddikim*. It is understood that the first two modes are most relevant now, in this lowest of worlds, while the third mode is the "world to come" within this world—especially the matter of bringing *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*. This is what the *Shas* concludes there—that it will be revealed in the future.

It is obvious that every one of those who are *mekushar* and belong to Yosef HaTzaddik must become a channel, and at the very least assist and prepare his environment so that it becomes a vessel ready to receive the instructions and influences of Yosef, until the complete *Geulah*—which will be through the Holy One, Blessed be He Himself, in the aspect called Yosef, as stated in the *Shach* and brought in *Ohr HaTorah*, *d.h. Vayiten Es Kolo*.

With the blessing of immediate *teshuvah*, immediate *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

219

7 Shevat, 5706

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, etc., the Tamim, Rabbi A. Hecht,
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter:

**1) Regarding the World to Come: Does it involve eating and drinking?**

Regarding the designations and promises found in the Bible and the words of our Sages, there are three distinct time periods: the Messianic Era, Gan Eden, and the World after the Resurrection of the Dead. (Note: Both Gan Eden and the World of Resurrection are referred to as "the World to Come," which has caused several misunderstandings.)

1) **The Messianic Era:** There are two opinions in the Gemara (Berachos 34b) regarding how life will be conducted then: either it will be entirely miraculous, or there will be no difference between the current world and the Messianic Era except for the cessation of the subjugation to foreign kingdoms. Regarding the halachic ruling on this, see the *Kesef Mishneh* and *Lechem Mishneh* on *Hilchos Teshuvah* 8:6, and see *Zohar* Vol. I, 139a and Vol. III, 125a. While many details concerning the time of the Messianic Era were not explicitly defined in the "revealed" Torah, as the Rambam writes (*Hilchos Melachim* 12:2), it is clear that according to both aforementioned opinions, there will be eating and drinking, etc., in the Messianic Era. This is necessitated by several verses and statements of our Sages, and is explicitly stated by the Rambam (ibid.). See also the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26.

2) **Gan Eden:** This is a dwelling place for souls **without** bodies (see Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah* ch. 8 and the commentaries there; *Torah Or*, Parshas Yisro, *Maamar* "HaAvos Hem HaMerkavah," and elsewhere). It is obvious that there is no place there for eating and drinking, as those are only relevant to a body.

3) **The World of Resurrection:** This will specifically involve souls within bodies (see the sources cited in "Teshuvos U’Biurim" in the sixth *Kovetz Lubavitch*). Our Sages stated (Berachos 17a) that "the World to Come has no eating or drinking, etc." It is the opinion of the Rambam (*Hilchos Teshuvah*, ibid.) that this statement refers to the world that has no body, but that in the World of Resurrection, there will be eating and drinking (*Lechem Mishneh*, ibid., and explicitly in the Rambam’s *Iggeres Techiyas HaMeisim*). However, the Rambam holds to his own view that the ultimate purpose and primary reward will be in the world that has no body, because it is impossible for a soul to receive the fullness of the reward while clothed in a body. Therefore, he maintains that even those who rise in the Resurrection will eventually die and enter the World to Come, which is where the primary reward for the service performed in this world is found (*Iggeres Techiyas HaMeisim*; see also his Commentary on the Mishnah, beginning of *Perek Chelek*). Great Torah scholars have disagreed with him on these points, first and foremost the Ramban, who provided "clear proofs... that the Resurrection is the final purpose... and this is the truth according to Kabbalah" (*Derech Mitzvosecha*, Mitzvas Tzitzis; see also *Likutei Torah*, the first *Biur* on the *Maamar* "Shuvah Yisroel"). Consequently, it is certain that the statement of our Sages that "the World to Come has no eating or drinking" refers to the **ultimate** reward, which is the World of Resurrection.

**2) Regarding the Resurrection: Will people rise with a complete body, or will the disabled, G-d forbid, rise with their disability and then be healed?**

Our Sages stated (Sanhedrin 91b) that they rise with their blemishes (and afterwards) are healed. This is explained at greater length in *Bereishis Rabbah* (beginning of ch. 95): "Just as a person departs, so he arrives; he departs blind and arrives blind, etc.; just as he departs clothed, so he arrives clothed, etc., and afterwards I heal them." In *Zohar* (Vol. I, 203b), it is proven that this occurs through the "healing sun" mentioned by our Sages (Nedarim 8b). See more on this at length in the upcoming *Kovetz*.

**3) Regarding the Resurrection: For souls that have come in *gilgul* (reincarnation) multiple times, which body will rise?**

There are several details and distinctions here, but the general principle is: The reason a soul (and the intent here is the *Nefesh, Ruach,* and *Neshamah* in their entirety, or one of them—not merely the level called *Neshamah*) comes in *gilgul* is (in the vast majority of cases) to rectify what was not rectified during its first descent into a body. Since all of Israel are "filled with mitzvos like a pomegranate," with every descent and *gilgul*, various aspects of the soul are rectified. In the time of the Resurrection, each body will rise with the parts of the soul that it specifically rectified. *Shaar HaGilgulim* (Introduction 4) states: "If it [the body] did not merit to rectify it [the *Nefesh*] entirely and died... since this first body did not complete the rectification of all aspects of the *Nefesh*, therefore, at the time of the Resurrection, this first body will only have that specific part which it rectified during its lifetime. And therefore, when this *Nefesh* is reincarnated into another body to complete its rectification... the parts of the *Nefesh* that were rectified in this second body... belong to this second body at the time of the Resurrection."

Do not be troubled by the thought that there will thus be several bodies that possess only certain aspects of the *Nefesh* rather than a complete *Nefesh*. For it must be known that every aspect is inclusive of all aspects, and every aspect is a **complete configuration (*tziyur komah*) in actuality**, even if, from the perspective of being a part of a more general *Nefesh*, it is only one aspect. Just as the totality of all souls is but **one** *Neshamah*—the *Neshamah* of Adam HaRishon—as our Sages say (*Shemos Rabbah* 40): "While Adam HaRishon was still a formless mass, the Holy One, Blessed be He, showed him every righteous person destined to arise from him; some were hanging from his head, etc." See *Tanya*, chapters 2 and 32, and elsewhere.

**4) Regarding places where the day (and night) lasts longer than 24 hours**

(Note the *Zohar* (Vol. III, 10a): "There is a place where it is all day and night is not found there, except for one brief hour.")

How should one conduct the observance of Shabbos? Is the primary factor the count of hours, or the days as they are in other places, or the rising and setting of the sun?

I did not understand your question as to how it is possible to observe it according to the rising of the sun, when it may not rise for several days or even months, and then not set for a long time. Likewise, what is your intent in saying they should observe it according to the days in other places? Which place? For, as the *Zohar* says there, "When it shines for these, it is dark for those; for these it is day, and for those it is night."

It is simple that in these places one must count hours—that is, 24 hours to a day. The beginning of the holy Shabbos is the same for all places that share the same longitude, those located on the same horizon. (I believe this is discussed in the book *Sefer HaBris*, though I do not have it before me.)

However, what one must investigate in such a case is: a) Regarding matters that depend on day or night—such as the times for prayer—at what point do they begin to conduct themselves according to the clock rather than "proportional hours"? For example, in a place where the day is only one hour long, it is not logical to say that the fast of the 10th of Teves lasts only one hour, and so on. b) At the point of the North or South Pole, it is not applicable to speak of longitude; how should they conduct themselves there? This requires further study, and this is not the place to elaborate.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

210

B"H, 7th of Shevat, 5706
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and elevated one, who conducts his business with integrity,
Rabbi Y. HaKohen, may he live,

Shalom and blessings!

Your check for the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch was received in due time, and the receipts are enclosed herewith. Please excuse the delay, which was due to an overwhelming amount of work.

Based on what you discussed with me when you were here—that you desire to participate in the expenses of printing seforim—specifically the seforim of Chassidus D'A"H that we are publishing—I have included you, **if you agree to this**, in the printing of the *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus* in the amount of twenty-five dollars, and in the printing of the *Kuntres Etz Chaim* in the amount of thirty-five dollars. I am sending you the *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus* in a separate package; the *Kuntres Etz Chaim* has not yet finished printing, and it will be sent to you once it is completed.

There are other seforim of Chassidus currently in print, but several individuals have already volunteered to cover the printing costs, and therefore I cannot include you in those.

I will take this opportunity to ask you to return to me the "reid" [talks] from the holiday of Pesach that I lent you some time ago.

Regarding the laws of the holiday of Pesach, which are discussed in this week’s parsha, it concludes (*Parshas Bo* 13:8), "And you shall tell your son." This teaches us that just as at the time of the Exodus from Egypt, Hashem warned them about the effort to tell the son and help him understand the concept of Torah and mitzvos—and the Sages said, "According to the son's intelligence, his father instructs him" (*Pesachim* 10:4), meaning one must contemplate the mindset of the one being educated and seek ways to bring him closer—so too is it at every time and season. Since every day contains the concept of the Exodus from Egypt, a major principle is the effort to ensure that the other person, whoever he may be, is also brought closer to Torah and mitzvos, whether by speaking to him directly, or through written or printed materials that one has helped publish...

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you receive much nachas and pleasure from all your family members, and may you raise them to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee
