211

B”H, 1 Adar I, 5706

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and trustworthy R’ Y. HaKohen, Chicago

Shalom u’Bracha!

You surely received my letter of 7 Shevat. I hope that you will soon return the *reid* of Pesach that I borrowed from you.

As you recall, you once spoke with me regarding your desire to participate in one of our publications. An opportunity has just arisen, and that is why I am writing to you now:

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, has for some time given permission to publish in mimeograph form, in a limited quantity, a collection of *sichos* from his father, the Rebbe, n”e. The *sefer* should be finished by the end of the week; it will contain approximately 330 pages.

Regarding the expenses for publishing this *sefer*, which will amount to about $1,900, we had the following calculation: two partners at $500 each, and the remainder will be covered by sales. One of the two partners has already given his $500 toward this account, but the second found himself forced at the last moment to withdraw, because he cannot take the commitment upon himself.

On this occasion, I would like to propose that you become the second partner in helping to publish this *sefer*. It would not bother me if you paid the sum in installments of $100 a month over five months.

Regarding the importance of this matter, I consider it superfluous to elaborate to you. I would only ask you, since the *sefer* must be ready by the end of the week, to inform me of your decision immediately **in any case.**

To conclude with a word from this week’s *sedra*, *Parshas Eileh HaMishpatim*.

All the *dinim* following *Matan Torah* begin with the *din* of an *eved ivri*—"If you buy an *eved ivri*, he shall serve for six years, and in the seventh he shall go out free for nothing." It is very difficult to understand why it begins with such a *din*, especially since, according to the Gemara (*Kiddushin* 14b), this deals with a servant whom *Beis Din* sold because the Jew stole and did not have the means to pay. Firstly, if one were to begin with this *din*, it would have been **logical** to begin first with the *din* of theft—that a thief *shnayim yeshalem* (pays double), and then, if he does not have the means, *v’nimkar bigneivaso* (he is sold for his theft), and only then relate the *din* of an *eved ivri*. Secondly, it is generally difficult to understand why the *parsha* begins with *dinim* of a downfall: a) a Jew steals, b) he has no assets with which to pay, c) no one wants to help him until *Beis Din* is forced to sell him as a servant for six years.

However, this *din* is a reflection and a lesson regarding the entire subject of *mishpatim*, the purpose of which is to teach a person to subdue his negative inclinations and *taavos* and to rectify the bad he has done previously.

But how does a Jew, after *Matan Torah*, come to have negative desires and actions? It is as our Sages explain in *Berachos* (28b): because the Jew sometimes forgets that the *Baal HaBayis*—the *Ribono shel Olam*—sees what he is doing; consequently, he calculates that he can "sneak one in."

The advice for this is: the *ivri* becomes a servant to the *Ribono shel Olam*, and through the fact that *b’meshech* of "six years he shall serve"—*avodah* in Torah and *mitzvos*—then "in the seventh"—in the *elef ha’shevi’i*—*yetzei l’chofshi chinam*; then *mitzvos* will be in a different manner, as the Alter Rebbe explains this in *Torah Or* at the beginning of this week’s *sedra*.

With the blessing of *l’altar l’teshuvah l’altar l’geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad HaPoel

## 212

B"H, 12 Adar, 5706

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, the G-d-fearing, who walks in exile—after exile (having been stricken twofold), may you merit redemption after redemption (comforted twofold)—the Temimim and all those who join them, may they live.

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the beginning of the month of Shevat. Thank G-d, who has granted us life and sustained us all during the terrible times that have passed over the House of Israel.

(To note what is written in the Kuntres Sfas Emes, end of section 35—at the end of Emes L'Yaakov—that before the coming of Moshiach there must be a general "sawing" [separation], and this is the concept of the birth pangs of Moshiach, etc.)

And He who gives life will surely grant us sufficient strength, fortitude, and sustenance, both physically and spiritually, so that we may all fulfill the task incumbent upon each one individually, according to their situation and ability, and collectively, for all of Israel are responsible—and intertwined—with one another.

I have become aware of your activities in your current location throughout the years that have passed, for they are many, especially when considering the conditions of the place and the time. All the more so regarding what you are capable of bringing to fruition now, as the situation has improved, and it is a certainty that a shaliach—from Above—fulfills his mission.

...I will conclude with the subject of the opening, regarding the "sawing," whose purpose (as it is according to the simple meaning as well) is that there should be a return to "face-to-face"—which is on Erev Shabbos—and afterwards there will be a union of "face-to-face" on the day of Shabbos. May it be His will that the revelation of the light of Chassidus, the inner dimension of Torah, will assist in drawing down from the level of the inner essence of the Ohr Ein Sof, may He be blessed, to shine within the depths of our souls, that they may behold His countenance directly, as explained in Likutei Torah, in the discourse beginning "Ki Tishma B'kol," and see also the sicha of 19 Kislev, 5692.

With the blessing of "immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

## 213

213

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Tetzaveh, 5706

To the distinguished avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc., the chossid, the Tamim, Moreinu Harav M.Z. (may he live),

Greetings and blessings!

1) Thank you for sending me the *kuntres* that you received from the "Shomrei HaChomah," etc., in Yerushalayim. It would be worthwhile to warn them with all possible force, if you have the ability to do so, that they should not dare to use the name of the Rebbe (may he live and be well) — such as by reprinting his letters from the past — without **first** receiving permission from him for this. Naturally, this warning should not be in my name, etc., but in the name of the group of Chabad Chassidim. Please be so kind as to inform me if you do anything regarding this.

2) Thank you for sending the letter from Shanghai regarding the printing there. A similar letter was also received by R. A. Paris, and I have written to them regarding the Rebbe’s proposals for this, which involve a major plan in the field of printing. If they agree to our proposal, we can hope for the revelation of a great and good light. The letter is enclosed.

3) The Tamim Vitzky took his books some time ago, and surely you are aware of this.

4) I hope that in the coming week *Mayim Rabim*, *Tzemach Tzedek*, and *HaHaskalah* will be published, and perhaps also the *Sefer HaSichos* of the Rebbe (mimeographed). I have seen that his debt has grown once again. What is the logic in sending more books and adding debt upon debt, at a time when a lack of funds is hindering printing, education, etc.? And is it possible that in all these five years, it has not been possible to find even one or two donors in your entire country who would give two or three thousand? That would suffice for what is being sent to them over the course of two or three years. It is a pity to spend time discussing the debt and its collection.

5) I hope that in the coming week I will be able to send to the Beis Din the *Sichos* of Summer 5705 (beginning from 9 Adar) that belong to Mr. Dalfon. Because of the additions, I estimate that the printing costs will be approximately 400 dollars (80 pages in a binding, like *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*). For now, he has sent 175. Will he complete the remainder, and when? Please be so kind as to inform me as soon as possible, so that there will be no delay in the printing.

6) What are the comments you have regarding *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*?

And according to the saying: "One must live with the times" (*Kuntres Bikur Chicago*):

The commentators on the Torah have already addressed the reason why the matter of the Inner Altar is explained in a separate section in this week’s parsha — Tetzaveh — and not together with the other vessels of the Altar (see Ramban and Sforno).

The reason can be explained according to *Chassidus*: The Inner Altar represents the inwardness of the heart (*Likkutei Torah, "U'shaavtem" 1, ch. 1*), which is higher even than the *mochin* (*Likkutei Torah, "V'hayah bayom hahu yitaka," ch. 3*, and elsewhere), even though it is located in the body — the *heichal* of the *Mishkan* and the *Beis HaMikdash* — and not in the head — the *Kodesh HaKodashim* of the *Mishkan* and the *Beis HaMikdash*. The *avodah* of this is the *yechidah* in the soul, and it is distinct from the other matters of the *Mikdash*. This is especially so according to what is written in the *maamar* "Mizbach Adamah" — *Reshimot* on *Shemos*, apparently by the *Tzemach Tzedek* — and in the *maamar* "Zeh Yitnu" 5658, that the Altar of earth and stones refers to the externality of the heart, while the illumination of the inwardness of the heart, the Inner Altar, refers to the essence of the inwardness of the heart, not merely the illumination of the point — as their concepts are explained in *Likkutei Torah*, *maamar* "Ki Tetzei" 2, ch. 2-3.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

213

By the Grace of Hashem, Monday, 17 Adar I, 5706

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished scholar, R’ S. Glitzenstein,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I will begin by asking your forgiveness for not having acknowledged receipt of your gift — your book, "HaRav" (The Biography of the Alter Rebbe). Due to the heavy burden of printing the Tzemach Tzedek, in addition to other printing matters and the daily work at Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch and Machne Israel, I have not answered anything during this time except for the most urgent letters. In particular, regarding your book, I wished to go through it entirely and offer comments on points that, in my opinion, require revision. Therefore, I postponed the matter until I had free time and could clear the aforementioned burdens. I hope you will judge me favorably, both regarding the delay of this letter and regarding my comments.

I will begin by expressing my gratitude for the book with which you honored me.

I was happy to see it, as for a long time there has been a felt lack of a booklet that would describe the history of the Alter Rebbe in a readable style, and which, at the same time, would provide a non-superficial concept of his personality and awaken in the reader the desire to know more details about his Torah, his system, and his accomplishments. After asking your forgiveness, I must say that while your book meets the first requirement, I did not find in it anything that would be directed toward the second goal. To clarify my meaning: If there were a **special** chapter about the Alter Rebbe’s books with a description, in two or three lines, of the content of each book—when the reader reads the list of books and finds in them: the *Nusach* (down to every single word) of the *Siddur HaTefillah*; the *Luach Bircas HaNehenin* (in the laws of blessings, which are accessible to all and written in a style appropriate for this); the *Shulchan Aruch* (especially the laws of *Niddah* and the *Kuntrus Acharon*); the *Tanya* (which, in its first and third parts, could serve, in the eyes of the masters of *mussar*, as a model for *mussar* books; Part Two as an example of *chakirah*; Part Four as a guide for *Ahavas Yisrael*); *Torah Ohr* and *Likutei Torah* (his system in *Chabad*); the *Kuntrus Acharon* in *Tanya* and the language of the Rebbe himself in *Torah Ohr* (*Kabbalah*)—such a list, with a short explanation of the above, despite its "dryness," would proclaim and say: Here is a man of wonders.

Also missing from your book is a list of the sources upon which you relied, which, aside from other reasons, would also have been appropriate for the second goal mentioned above.

But what saddens me most are the errors contained within it.

I do not know if this is relevant for the future (for a second edition, or a correction in another way), but in any case, I am transcribing here my comments—most, though not all, of the details that I believe require correction—in the hope that you will not take offense. I will write them according to the page numbers:

Page 5: Schneur, etc., **"the sun and the moon."** This phrasing is not **at all** in the Chassidic style. If it is a tradition from a **reliable** source, we will accept it, but in any case, it is stated otherwise. See the letter of the Tzemach Tzedek printed in the introduction to *Sefer Derech Mitzvotecha*, and what is written in *Beis Rebbe* in the name of R’ Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl.

In general, regarding the birth of the Alter Rebbe, see *Kuntres Chicago*, *Sicha* 4.

8: "Mathematical riddle"—it is questionable what riddle is relevant here; it is merely a matter of calculation.

15: "The Baal Shem Tov had a *cheder*..." in the *Sefer HaKuzari*, etc. This is very puzzling and does not fit at all with the **spirit** of the Baal Shem Tov’s conduct and his system of gathering his students. I do not know of any source for this (for the **Alter Rebbe**, there was such a system; see the *Sicha* of 19 Kislev, 5703, section 22).

19: "That they offered the Alter Rebbe to fill the place of the Maggid"—this is refuted, considering the relationship of the Alter Rebbe and all the students to R’ Avraham HaMalach and R’ Menachem Mendel of Vitebsk, as is known from the letters and the *Pidyon Nefesh*. For the events of that time, see *HaTamim*, Vol. 2, p. 45.

20: "That the Baal Shem Tov sent his brother-in-law in his stead to the Holy Land"—this is questionable. In *Ginzei Nistaros*, it seems proven from the letters of the Baal Shem Tov and his brother-in-law that the latter was already in Eretz Yisrael when the Baal Shem Tov wanted to travel there.

34: "The wedding in Zalubin in the year **5547**, and then the first debate!" (The wedding of the daughter of the Mitteler Rebbe took place then, and the Mitteler Rebbe in 5547 was 13 years old!) See the letters of *Avos HaChassidus* (*HaTamim*, Vol. 4) and *Kuntres Chicago*, *Sicha* 3, regarding the great debate in **Minsk** in the year **5543**.

36: "Because of those who distort the face of the Torah, etc."—perhaps it is worth adding that according to the law, one turns the *nidui* (excommunication) back, etc. (and likewise on p. 23).

40: "That the Alter Rebbe traveled to meet with the Vilna Gaon in the year 5552-3, etc."—see the letter of the Alter Rebbe printed in *Beis Rebbe*, Chapter 12, which proves that he traveled to Vilna together with R’ Menachem Mendel and not afterward. If so, this was before the year 5538, and the Vilna Gaon did not want to meet with them, etc.

47: "Under the administration of R’ Menachem Mendel of Vitebsk"—he passed away about ten years before that.

50: "Close to the time of *Shkiah* (sunset)"—see the *Sicha* of 20 Kislev, 5703, sections 6-9, that it was several hours before *Shkiah*, and an explanation of the matter is brought there as well.

69: "When the Rebbe returned to his home, etc."—in *HaTamim*, Vol. 1, p. 37, it says that this was while he was still in P.B.

71: "Where is it written that one must say *V'Shamru*?"—it is written in many places, among them in the *Siddur* of the Arizal, etc. See what is written in the *Piskei HaSiddur* for *Siman* 266.

73: "On Motzaei Shabbos"—they traveled on Erev Shabbos, as written by the Mitteler Rebbe in his letter printed in *Beis Rebbe*, end of Vol. 1.

78: "They left Russia, etc. The time arrived, etc., at the beginning of the month of Teves, etc."—this requires correction based on the aforementioned letter of the Mitteler Rebbe.

I reiterate that I am writing all this in the hope that you will not take offense, relying on the saying of the wise—which the Tzemach Tzedek brought in a letter now printed in *Kuntres HaTzemach Tzedek VeHaHaskalah*, and most of which is also printed in *Beis Rebbe*: "Love the wise, and love the truth above all."

With blessings for an immediate *teshuvah* and an immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

According to the memoirs (Ch. 10), R’ Moshe, the grandfather of R’ Baruch, wandered from Posen and settled in Minsk. R’ Schneur Zalman (the father of R’ Baruch) settled in Vitebsk, and there R’ Baruch was born—approximately in the year 5483.

## 214

214

B"H, Shushan Purim, 5706

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Rabbi Y. [Elay], Shochet and Bodek,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear of your dedicated efforts in strengthening Torah and mitzvos in general, and specifically in distributing the publications issued according to the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita.

You are surely gaining strength from time to time in all of the above. This can be understood in light of what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh (Epistle 14) that every year, a new, supernal light is drawn down from a **higher** level, etc., which had not yet shone since the days of old. And man, who is called *adam* (akin to *adameh l'elyon*—"I will be like the Most High"), must also be in this state—meaning, he must create vessels to receive this light.

This is especially true regarding the dissemination of Chassidus, as those in your country who are able to engage in this are few.

Surely, if it is within your ability to find people in other towns in your country with whom you can establish a connection regarding our publications (in Lashon HaKodesh, Yiddish, and English), do not refrain from drawing them in and bringing them closer to this matter. Please inform us as well regarding this. For you and those like you, further elaboration is unnecessary.

I will conclude with matters of Purim: Purim is in the plural form (*Purim*), and according to the simple explanation, this is because he cast the *pur* (lot) for the days and the *pur* for the months.

Regarding the *pur* for the days, Rashi in Megillah explains that this refers to a specific day of the month. This requires study: if so, the verse should have delayed and said, "from month to month and from day to day," and not the reverse. However, in Esther Rabbah and Targum Sheni, it is explained that initially, he cast the *pur* for the days of the **week**, and afterwards for the months. (It could be said that just as according to the Midrash it is necessary to say that he subsequently cast the *pur* for the days of the month as well—for he did indeed determine the **day** of the month of Adar—so too, according to Rashi, he cast the *pur* for the days in a general sense, meaning the days of the week, and therefore they were mentioned first in the verse. But this is forced.)

Seemingly, it is not understood at all for what purpose he cast the *pur* for the days of the week. Since the essence is the determination of the month and the day of the month, even if you were to say he wanted to verify the matter by having all the lots align (similar to what we find regarding Nevuchadnetzar when he went to Jerusalem), he should have at least begun with the primary lot—the one for the months.

It can be explained that what Haman did by way of a lot specifically was because he wanted to draw down from above the level of conduct that is governed by intellect and logic—from the place where "darkness is as light," the externality of the *makif* (encompassing light), from which the nations of the world draw their sustenance. They count by the sun, which has no ascents and descents. This is not the case for Bnei Yisrael, who count by the moon, and whose drawing down is specifically through calculation (this is discussed at some length in *Kuntres U'Maayan*). Haman’s evil intent was that his influence would prevail. Now, **days** depend on the solar count, months on the lunar count, and the number of days in the month is a combination of both calculations.

This is why the **beginning** of the lot was cast specifically for the days of the week—because that is the source of his influence and power—and afterwards for the months.

Now, Bnei Yisrael, through their *mesiras nefesh*, reached the interior of the *makif*, where, on the contrary, there is no place for the nations of the world at all, and the sins of Bnei Yisrael do not take hold, for "He has not beheld iniquity in Yaakov, etc.," because the Divine Presence is with them (see *Likutei Torah*, *Levavtuni*, section 2, and the *Maamar* beginning *Velo Avah*). And although in the lower consciousness this was not drawn down until after their *mesiras nefesh*, in the level where everything is revealed and known, this was known even at the time the lot was cast.

With this, another difficulty is resolved: the Midrash relates that the lot for the days of the week did not "come up" for Haman at all, whereas with the lot for the months, there was room for error. Seemingly, based on the above regarding the solar count, etc., it should be the opposite.

But according to the above—that in the lot for the days of the week, which is a count that does not pertain to the actions of the lower beings at all (a *makif*), and in the **interior** of the *makif* which they reached at that time, everything is revealed—there is no room for error at all. This is not the case with the lot for the months and the days of the month, where there is the "grasp" of human hands. Just as even afterwards, there was a distinction in this regard between towns, with walled cities and villages preceding, etc.

It may be said that these are also the three matters present in Purim: **In oneself**, one must reach the state of *ad d’lo yada* (until one does not know), the *reisha d’lo ityada* (the head that is not known), and that which is enclothed within it (see *Likutei Torah*, end of the *Drushei Yom HaKippurim*, *Ke-Purim*), and below that is Achashverosh, whose end and beginning are one. **And for others**, the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (order of evolution), there are two matters: "Man to his fellow"—even if he is not a pauper and lacks nothing—the *sovev kol almin* (encompassing all worlds), *madi*. And "gifts to the poor"—the *memalei kol almin* (filling all worlds), *paras*, *perus l'ra'ev* (a portion for the hungry) (see the addition to *Torah Or*, *Maamar* beginning *Lehavin*, end of section 4).

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*," and with the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 215

B"H, Shushan Purim, 5706

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and faithful activist, Rabbi Y. HaKohen, Chicago.

Greetings and Blessings!

Under separate cover, I am sending you the *Sefer HaSichos* of the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which we were able to publish thanks to your participation in the expenses.

I will take this opportunity to express my thanks once again for this. Thank G-d, you have merited to be among those who bring merit to the many through the printing of a book of "the light of Torah, for it is good"—the light of the teachings of Chassidus.

Our Sages have said regarding the mitzvos of Purim: *Mishloach manos* (sending portions) to one’s fellow—two portions to one person; and *matanos la’evyonim* (gifts to the poor)—two gifts to two people (*Megillah* 7a).

The explanation according to Chassidus is as follows: It is known that the miracle of Purim involved the salvation of both the body and the soul together (unlike Chanukah, which was only a salvation from spiritual exile—see *Torah Or*, *Drush* on the concept of Chanukah; see also the *Levush* cited in *Taz*, *Orach Chaim* 470:3). The Jewish people merited this through *mesiras nefesh* for the sanctification of Hashem’s name, by which they cleaved to Him, may He be blessed, in a state of simple *ratzon* (will) that transcends intellect and comprehension. For if they had wished to convert, Haman would have done nothing to them, as his decree was only against the Jews—all of which is explained at length in the literature of Chassidus in the *drushim* for Purim.

The purpose of *mesiras nefesh* is that it should influence one’s daily life—meaning that only the *nefesh elokis* should rule over one’s body and *nefesh habehamis*. The intermediary between them is the *nefesh hasichlis* (the intellectual soul), as explained in the *maamar* "Raba Chazya" (from the year 5730, when the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was in the United States for the first time) and in many other places.

Now, there is no "poor" person except in knowledge, and no "rich" person except in knowledge. Therefore, the *nefesh hasichlis* (and certainly the *nefesh elokis*) cannot truly be called "poor," unlike the body and the *nefesh habehamis*.

This is why, after the *mesiras nefesh* of that time, the Jewish people were commanded to perform mitzvos that hint that the *nefesh elokis* must extend the *mesiras nefesh* into the *nefesh habehamis* and the body: *matanos la’evyonim*—specifically to two "poor" ones. And *mishloach manos* to one’s fellow—the *nefesh hasichlis*, which is called a "fellow" (*rea*) to the *nefesh elokis*, and can therefore serve as an intermediary, as explained in the aforementioned *maamar* (specifically **two** portions, because intellect is not true intellect unless it arrives at a conclusion after first debating the logic and its opposite—*chesed* and *din*, question and answer. This is the nature of intellect, as explained in many places).

The type of Torah literature that includes within it content for the *nefesh hasichlis*, the *nefesh habehamis*, and the body alike, is the *Sichos* of the Rebbes, which include: 1) Deep intellectual concepts; 2) Guidance in good character traits and emotional refinement; 3) Stories and practical conduct.

Happy is the person who has merited to fulfill the mitzvos of *mishloach manos* and *matanos* as described above for the many.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

P.S. I received your letter in due time. The *kuntres Toras HaChassidus* was sent to you some time ago, and it surely arrived on time. The *Sefer HaSichos* was published on the eve of Shabbos *Parshas Zachor*, and therefore it was only sent now. The *kuntres Eitz Chaim* is in print, and I hope it will appear by the 2nd of Nissan, G-d willing. Please be so kind as to confirm receipt of the aforementioned.

## 116

B"H, Shushan Purim, 5706

To the honorable and distinguished, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Moshe Zalman Feiglin, Shepparton, Victoria, Australia

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of February 19th was received with thanks. We were pleased to hear about the financial contribution, for, naturally, the need here is very great. Beyond the fact that we support 25 girls' schools (*Beis Sarah* and *Beis Rivkah*), the expense for our publications is also very high, as they are not printed for the sake of profit, and large shipments are sent to Europe, and so on (the *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch*, *Machne Israel*, and *Kehot* work hand-in-hand). Therefore, it goes without saying that any assistance is a *davar b'ito* (a timely matter).

Our Sages of blessed memory said regarding the mitzvos of Purim: "And *mishloach manos* man to his fellow" — two portions to one person; "and *matanos la'evyonim*" — two gifts to two people (*Megillah 7a*).

According to Chassidus, one can explain this as follows: As is known, the miracle of Purim was that the Jewish people were saved both physically and spiritually (unlike Chanukah, where it was only a spiritual salvation — *Torah Or*, *Drushei HaRan*, the concept of Chanukah. See also *Levush*, cited in *Taz*, *Orach Chaim*, section 470, subsection 3). The Jewish people merited this through their *mesiras nefesh* for *Kiddush Hashem*, because they attached themselves to the Ribono shel Olam in a manner of *ratzon pashut* (simple will), which stands higher than *sechel* and intellect. For if they had only wanted to renounce their faith, Haman would not have done anything to them, as the decree was only against the Jews, as is explained at length in Chassidic discourses on Purim.

Now, the purpose of *mesiras nefesh* is that it should influence the daily life of a Jew; that is, that only his *nefesh elokis* should rule over his body and his *nefesh habahamis*. The intermediary between them is the *nefesh hasichlis*, as is explained in the *maamar* "Rabbah Chazya" (from the year 5690, by the Rebbe, when he was in the United States for the first time), and in many other places.

We know that "there is no poor person except in *da'as*, and there is no rich person except in *da'as*." Therefore, one cannot call the *nefesh hasichlis* (and certainly not the *nefesh elokis*) truly destitute (*evyon*), but one can certainly call the body and the *nefesh habahamis* by that name.

This is the meaning of the mitzvos of Purim. After their *mesiras nefesh* at that time, they received such mitzvos that hint at the fact that the *nefesh elokis* must extend that *mesiras nefesh* to the *nefesh habahamis* and the body as well — these are the *matanos la'evyonim* (and specifically to **two** *evyonim*). *Mishloach manos ish l're'ehu* — the *nefesh hasichlis* is called *re'a* (friend) to the *nefesh elokis*, which is why it can be the intermediary, as explained in the aforementioned *maamar* (**two** portions specifically, because the intellect is only a true intellect when it reaches a conclusion after weighing the argument and its opposite, *chesed* and *din*, question and answer, which is the essence of *sechel*, as is explained in many places).

Now, just as there are all these aforementioned distinctions within the person himself, there are similar distinctions between people: there are those who occupy themselves with nothing more than physical matters; there are those who also have a natural feeling for others, or at least for their own; there are those who also occupy themselves with contemplating their actions and seeing, according to their intellect, how they should conduct themselves, but all according to human intellect. Of Torah and Divine intellect, they, for the time being, do not wish to know.

And it is here that the holy obligation falls upon everyone, according to their capabilities, to see to it that all these aforementioned types are brought to the truth of Torah and mitzvos: a *mishloach manos* and *matanos la'evyonim* — to the many, as mentioned above.

And this is the great merit that you have: that in a desolate land, where there are **for the time being**, according to your letter, so few who observe Torah and mitzvos, you should be the one who disseminates and strives to strengthen Torah and Yiddishkeit through your own example and words, and also by bringing to them the light of Torah through various *sefarim*, writings, pamphlets, and *maamarim*.

*V'zechus harabim talui bo* (and the merit of the many depends upon him).

Being certain that in the future as well you will continue your aforementioned work, with even strengthened energy and with the help of your family members, may they live, I sign with the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach holiday,

*Le'alter l'teshuvah, le'alter l'geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 219

[Winter 5706]

Since this booklet is intended for the time beginning with 19 Kislev—the festival of the liberation of the Alter Rebbe—I am including in this maamar some of the questions that have been asked of me regarding the Sefer Likutei Amarim (Tanya).

**Question.**

In the beginning of Chapter 30 of Tanya, the Alter Rebbe quotes the saying of our Sages: "And be lowly of spirit before all *ha-adam* (the man)," and its source is in Pirkei Avos, Chapter 4, Mishnah 10. However, the version there is: "before all *adam* (man)," without the letter *hei*. Is this a printing error in Tanya?

**Answer.**

In all the editions of Tanya that I have seen, it is written this way: *ha-adam* with a *hei*. Therefore, this is not a printing error.

In our Mishnah in Avos (ibid.), there are those who have the version *adam* without a *hei*, and there are those who have the version *ha-adam* with a *hei*.

In Tanya here, the Alter Rebbe adopted the second version. I emphasize "in Tanya here," because in several places the Alter Rebbe cites the version *adam* without a *hei*, as noted below. This is also the case in the Pirkei Avos found in his Siddur.

Now, every single word in Tanya is precise in its *chaser* and *yaseir* (defective or plene spelling). And even though, on the face of it, in our case this is a minor change—and what difference does it make if it is written with a *hei* or without a *hei*?—upon a little reflection, it becomes clear that the explanation of the entire concept depends on this change. The Alter Rebbe was precise in bringing *ha-adam* with a *hei* here, while in other places he specifically wrote *adam* without a *hei*.

The explanation of the matter is as follows: There are two ways to arrive at lowliness of spirit before everyone:

1) According to the words of our Sages, "Do not judge your fellow until you reach his place," for his "place" causes him to sin; by nature he is heated, and his *yetzer* is in a great and mighty battle against him. Each person must weigh and examine himself to see if he is serving Hashem in the context and level of such a mighty battle—as is elaborated upon in Tanya, Chapter 30.

2) Each person is perfected by his fellow, specifically through his fellow. This is like the analogy of a person: although the feet are the lowest level and the head is the highest, nevertheless, the feet have an advantage and a virtue, for one must walk with them, and they support the body and the head. Furthermore, when there is heaviness in the head, one draws blood from the feet, and it is healed and receives its vitality from them—as is elaborated upon in Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Nitzavim.

These two paths differ in their effect in two ways:

The first path leads to lowliness, sadness, and bitterness. Nevertheless, this is the required *middah*, as per the words of our Sages, "A person should always **arouse** his good inclination against his evil inclination," provided that he conquers it and becomes one who "turns from evil and does good," as explained in Tanya, Chapter 31. Furthermore, this contemplation produces lowliness not only before fellow Jews, but even before non-Jews, such as the contemplation regarding the honor of a father by Dama ben Nesina (Kiddushin 31a) and the like.

The second path leads to lowliness, but not to sadness, and it applies specifically before one's fellow Jew, for all Jews are one complete stature, and every limb is connected to and in need of the other. However, this does not apply before a non-Jew.

Now, our Sages have said, "You are called *adam* (man), but the non-Jews are not called *adam*," yet the name *ha-adam* includes non-Jews as well (Yevamos 61a, Tosafos s.v. *v'ein*).

Therefore, when a person cannot fight the *yetzer* because of the heaviness in his heart, and he needs to *l'achpaya* (force) the *yetzer hara*, to crush, humble, and prove to himself that he is worse, etc., than the impure animals, etc.—he is forced to follow the first path mentioned above. Consequently, he arrives at lowliness even before a non-Jew, etc. Therefore, the Alter Rebbe is precise in quoting the version: "before all *ha-adam*"—with a *hei*.

But when he speaks about the love of one's fellow Jew, this contemplation is not relevant here. Rather, the focus is on the fact that all **Israel** are one complete stature and each one is perfected by his fellow, etc. Therefore, the Rebbe quotes the version: "before all *adam*"—without a *hei*. See Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Epistle 22; Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Nitzavim; Siddur, Shaar HaElul, s.v. *Atem Nitzavim*.

Similarly, when he speaks about the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*, and in general about a lofty manner of *avodah*—and not about "turning from evil," etc.—there is no place here for the contemplation of how he is worse and repulsive, etc. Rather, the contemplation is how his fellow is more elevated than he, and he should strive for that, etc. Consequently, the version *adam*—without a *hei*—is specifically applicable here. See Torah Or, Toldos, s.v. *Vayachperu*; ibid., Mikeitz, s.v. *Vayehi Mikeitz* (the first); Likutei Torah, beginning of the maamar *B'yom HaShemini Atzeres* (the first).

Based on the above, it is also understood why the primary version in the Mishnah is *adam* without a *hei*, and this is what the Alter Rebbe established in his Siddur, as mentioned above.

For the Mishnah, in its primary, literal sense, speaks about the study of Torah—that one should be lowly of spirit before every *adam* and learn from him, or that even though he is engaged in Torah, he should still be lowly of spirit before everyone—and this, of course, only applies to fellow Jews.

***

And if we learn all of the above from the surplus of a single letter in Tanya, how much more is there to learn from a single word, a single phrase, a single paragraph, and all the more so from a single chapter in Tanya!

## 220

**220**

Regarding the request to explain what is written in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, Chapter 7: "And *Va'ad* (ו-ע-ד) is *Echad* (א-ח-ד) through the substitution of letters."

**Response.**

This statement is found in the *Zohar*, Vol. II (134a). In the *Mikdash Melech*—which is transcribed in the *Nitzutzei Oros* on the margin of the *Zohar*—it is explained: "The *Aleph* is interchangeable with the *Vav* according to the *Ahui* (א-ה-ו-י) group of letters; the *Ches* is interchangeable with the *Ayin* according to the *Acha'a* (א-ח-ע-ה) group of letters."

This means that the *Ahui* letters are related to one another, as they are all "letters of continuation" (they are drawn out—in pronunciation—following the letters that precede them), "letters of rest" (at times they are quiescent and not audible in pronunciation), and "letters of breath" (only through them does any letter come to expression in speech)—as all of this is discussed in the books of grammar. See also the commentary of the *Ibn Ezra* (Shemos 3:15) and his *Chidah* (printed in the introduction to his commentary on the Torah), and *Likutei Torah*, discourse *Es Shabbosai*, end of Chapter 1.

Similarly, the *Acha'a* letters are related to one another, as they all originate from the throat.

* * *

This is the explanation of the substitution in a general sense.

To understand why specifically these letters are substituted, one must first preface with what is written in *Tanya* (loc. cit., prior to this)—which is found in *Zohar Chadash*, Bereishis 18b—that *Shema Yisrael* is *Yichuda Ila'ah* (Higher Unity), and *Baruch Shem* is *Yichuda Tata'ah* (Lower Unity). It is regarding this that the explanation is given that *Va'ad* is *Echad* through the substitution of letters.

The matter **in brief:** *Yichuda Ila'ah* is like the nullification of the radiance of the sun within the sun itself—the nullification of the world of *Atzilus*, a nullification in essence, a nullification that occurs automatically, for it does not feel itself to be an "entity" at all.

*Yichuda Tata'ah* is the nullification of the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah*—the nullification of the "something." This means that the world **feels** that it exists, but understands through its intellect that it is nullified, since it is located within the source of its being, like the radiance of the sun within the sun (but all of this is in its understanding, not in its feeling).

Now, the nullification of *Yichuda Ila'ah* occurs **when one feels** the source. And when does one feel the source? When the source, even though it is extended to bring into being and give life—for it emanates the world of *Atzilus*—nevertheless does not come in garments that conceal.

All of this is hinted at in the letter *Aleph*—the *Alufo shel Olam* (Master of the World). It is extended through the *Ches*—*Chochma Ila'ah* (Higher Wisdom), the beginning of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—until it emanates a world through the *Dalet*—speech. However, this speech is **connected** to its source in thought.

And even higher: the speech **is in its source**, meaning speech within thought; therefore, the *Dalet* is a *Dalet Rabbati* (a large *Dalet*).

However, the nullification of *Yichuda Tata'ah*, which comes about because one **understands** that one is located within the source but does not **feel** it—this comes about because the source is extended, but in its extension, it is clothed in a garment that conceals. Therefore, the created being arrives as separate in its feeling.

This is hinted at: the extension of the source (*Aleph*) downward—is the letter *Vav*. A line extended from above to below (meaning the *Aleph* is substituted with a *Vav*).

Afterward, it is clothed in *Chochma* (*Ches*), but the primary clothing is in the *Midos* of *Chochma*, in the externality of *Chochma Ila'ah*, which is hinted at by the letter *Ayin* (meaning the *Ches* is substituted with an *Ayin*).

Afterward, it is extended to bring into being the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah* through the letters of speech. And since it is extended through the **externality** of *Chochma Ila'ah*, the speech is also extended from its source and its internality (*Dalet Rabbati*), and the letters of speech are formed in reality—a *Dalet* of standard size (meaning the *Dalet Rabbati* is changed into a standard *Dalet*).

* * *

See *Imrei Binah* (beginning of *Shaar* 1-7 and *Shaar HaKrias Shema* 70-78), the *Tzemach Tzedek’s* *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah* (19, 22, 38), and the discourse *Kol HaMa'arich BeEchad* of the year 5678—see there for all of this in greater detail.

#### 220

See the note to the previous section.

## 221

I saw it written in the maamar *Teshuvos U’Biurim* (Kovetz Chovret Sheini, p. 22) that everything written in the sichos of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has a source in the words of our Sages. And certainly, all the more so, there is a source for what is stated in the maamarim and seforim of Chassidus.

I asked whether there is also a source in **Nigleh** for what is written in Tanya, *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 7: that a multitude of minor transgressions can cause a blemish similar to that of a prohibition involving *kares* or *misah*.

* * *

**Response.**

An example of the above in **Nigleh**—and not only that, but also in **practical halacha**: It is stated in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim (siman 328, se'if 14): If there is a patient who is dangerously ill, one must slaughter meat for him, and we do not say that we should feed him *neveilah*. Even though if he eats *neveilah* less than a *kezayis*, it is merely a standard prohibition, whereas slaughtering on Shabbos is a prohibition punishable by *sekilah*, we nevertheless slaughter. One of the reasons is that in such a case, he transgresses the prohibition of *sekilah* only once, whereas by eating *neveilah*, he would transgress with every single act of eating, even though each is only a standard prohibition (Ran and Magen Avraham, cited in our Rebbe’s Shulchan Aruch there, se'if 16). And some say (Bach, Taz) that this is the law even regarding a Rabbinic prohibition, and even if the prohibition is very minor.

See also the sefer *Lekach Tov* by R. Y. Engel, Klal 15 (regarding whether a multitude of quantity outweighs quality), where he notes several places in Shas regarding this. Among them are Rashi in Yevamos (32b) and Tosafos, s.v. *Kasbari*, in Sanhedrin (50a) [9].

***

221
See the note to siman 219 above. This letter has since been found in its original, and it is to R. M. M. Margolies, dated Monday, 20 Menachem Av, 5705. Additional letters to him—above 177, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**In the maamar Teshuvos U’Biurim:** Above, Vol. 1, letter 154.

**Only once... and eating:** See also regarding this below, letter 256.

9) In letter 20 there, he raises a difficulty regarding this principle: if so, one should be obligated to "let yourself be killed rather than transgress" (*yehareg v'al ya'avor*) even regarding other transgressions if he is forced to transgress multiple times, just as one is obligated to do so regarding the three cardinal sins even when forced only once. But this is not difficult, for our Rebbe has already explained in Tanya, Chapter 24, that the law of *yehareg v'al ya'avor* (or *ya'avor v'al yehareg*) is not based on the lightness or severity of the transgressions.

## 222

222

In Iggeres HaKodesh (Letter 28): "Tikun" and "Notzer" are the letters of "Ratzon." I asked: 
a) "Notzer" is missing the *vav*. 
b) In Shemos (34:7) it is written "Notzer Chesed" without the additional *vav*.

**Response.**

a) Two points can be made: 1. We also find "Ratzon" written without a *vav* in the text. For example, in Bereishis (46:6). According to the Masorah in Daniel (8:4), it is found in Tanach without a *vav* eight times. Conversely, "Notzer" is found with a *vav* (Mishlei 28:7; II Melachim 17:9; ibid. 18:8). Therefore, it is obvious that one can say the letters of this word are equivalent to the letters of that word, whether we assume they are written *chaser* (defective) or *malei* (plene). Furthermore, from what is written in many places that "Notzer" and "Ratzon" have the same gematria as "Moshe"—including the *kolel*—(Pri Etz Chaim, Shaar HaSelichos, Ch. 8; Shaar HaKavanos and references there), and in Meorei Ohr (entry "Moshe")—it is proven that they understood "Notzer" and "Ratzon" as being written *malei* with a *vav*.

2. The dispute is well known regarding whether we follow the *mikra* (the written text) or the *masorah* (the tradition), or both together (Kiddushin 18b and references there). However, in a place where they do not contradict, we interpret both (Tosafos, s.v. *v'Rabbi*, Sukkah 6b, and elsewhere). This is the case here as well, as it is clear that we follow the *mikra*.

* * *

b) Regarding the difficulty that in the verse it is written "Notzer" without the additional *vav* at the beginning: It is true that in Iggeres HaKodesh, Letter 25, and in many places in Chassidus, it appears as "v'Notzer." However, I have seen the first printings of Iggeres HaKodesh, and in all of them, it is written "Notzer" without the additional *vav*. In my humble opinion, this should be corrected in the Tanya as well, from the 1900 edition onwards.

Regardless, the language in that letter of Iggeres HaKodesh requires study and correction. For example, in the text: "The eighth, etc., is Tikun and Notzer, the letters of Ratzon, and it is also an *eis ratzon*." This requires clarification: 1. The word "etc." is not understood. 2. In the instance where it mentions "Notzer" later, it also adds the word "Chesed." In the first instance, it writes "v'Notzer" alone. The reverse would be more logical. 3. The word "also" is not understood.

In the earlier printings, it is correct, and it reads: "The eighth is Tikun, Notzer Chesed, Notzer, the letters of Ratzon, and it is an *eis ratzon*... because the *mazal* of Notzer Chesed is from the *mem-mem-samech* of Arich Anpin." And this is well-explained.

It seems that in later printings, they omitted the text from "Notzer" to "Notzer."

Perhaps it can be said that out of force of habit—since the lower *mazal* is "V'Nakeh" with a *vav*—they also wrote "v'Notzer" with a *vav* for the higher *mazal*.

#### ***222***

See the note to Letter 219 above.

10) In Torah Or (discourse *Marehem u'Maasehem*), in Likkutei Torah (explanation of the discourse *Vayedaber... Rashei HaMatos*, Ch. 3), and elsewhere, it is brought that "Notzer" are the letters of "Tzinor" and the letters of "Ratzon," without citing a source. For the time being, I have found in the writings of the Arizal in Likkutei Torah (Parshas Toldos and Parshas Tisa, and in the parallel places in Sefer HaLikkutim) and in Pri Etz Chaim (Shaar HaSelichos, Ch. 8, and in the parallel places in Shaar HaKavanos and the writings of the Arizal) that "Notzer" are the letters of "Ratzon." And in Mikdash Melech to Zohar III 190a, and in Zohar HaRakiya to Zohar I [50a] (which is brought in Likkutei Torah, discourse *Es Korboni Lachmi*—the second—end of Ch. 2), it is stated that "Tzinor" are the letters of "Ratzon."

11) It is worth noting a similar matter to the one at hand, which is that our Sages (Bamidbar Rabbah, Ch. 18:21; Tanchuma there; brought in Rashi at the end of Parshas Shelach) state: "Tzitzis" equals 600. Yet "Tzitzis" is **everywhere** missing the final *yud*. As they questioned in Tosafos (s.v. *Lo*, Menachos 39a) and in Ramban on the Torah. They answered (Mizrachi, brought in Minchas Shai there) that we follow the *mikra*. See also the answer of the Gilyon Zohar Chadash 227a, that the *chirik* vowel point fills the place of the *yud*, and the answer of the Tosafos there. The various opinions on this are brought in Minchas Shai there.

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5706

To the esteemed avreich, the learned and G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi M.Z. [Gringlas] may he live,

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letters of the 7th and 22nd of Adar Sheni:

I do not have copies of the Sefer Midos Rashbi.

Is the sum sent by Karakowski on account of what he pledged for the printing of the Divrei Yemei Admur Maharash, or is it an independent donation? This also affects the wording of the receipt.

The sichos from Chai Elul to 19 Kislev of this year are still with my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita.

The Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa and Chiddushim) and Mayim Rabim have not yet been finished at the bindery.

Regarding your debt, which has already exceeded five hundred [dollars] (aside from the Yeshiva and Beis Rivkah), I do not know if you are correct in saying that you are already doing everything in your power regarding this. But you should certainly believe that the printer is not at all concerned with this back-and-forth. For the books that he has already printed, he must be paid in full. The only choice we have **from here on in** is not to print any more.

I have been trying for quite some time now to explain, double and triple over, to people like him, that when they refrain from paying a debt they owe, it is not merely a failure to fulfill the mitzvah of paying a debt; rather, it has caused and continues to cause a deficiency and a failure to fulfill the work plan outlined by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, in general, and the printing department in particular.

At a time when they should be striving to increase the possibilities for printing as much as permission is granted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita (and this itself would also increase the permission, as it is known that the desire of the recipient increases the influence), not only by paying debts but by adding sums beyond that—instead, everyone comes with their own argument in hand, hoping that I will surely acknowledge their justification. And how many maamarim of Chassidus would be printed through this?

My hope is that the above will bear fruit. And if it is true that you have already done everything within the power of your revealed faculties, then awaken your hidden and essential faculties (see the maamar of 2 Nissan of this year) and add strength to the above.

This can be understood according to what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh (Epistle 14), that every year a new, higher light is drawn down from a level that is **higher still**, etc., which had not yet shone since the days of old. And man, who is "like the One Above," must also be in this manner—meaning, he must create vessels to receive this light.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate geulah, and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 224

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5706

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, energetic activist, and man of many accomplishments, R. Sh. Palmer, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

The printing of the booklet for youth regarding the festival of Pesach, published by Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, was completed today, and we are sending you one copy. In a separate package, we are sending you a specific number of copies, which you will surely want to distribute via your activists to the students of the Talmud Torah, etc. Please be so kind as to inform us how many more copies we should send you.

Our distinguished and honored friend, the G-d-fearing R. D. B. Haskind, informed us of the content of his telephone conversation with you regarding the burden of the printing costs for this booklet. In accordance with his words and instructions, and in view of the limited time remaining until Pesach—which leaves no time for negotiation—we have attributed the printing of the first edition of this booklet to your merit. Based on the ruling of our Sages that the Torah also writes and publicizes the one who performs a mitzvah (Responsa of the Rashba, cited in Magen Avraham, Orach Chaim 54:22), we have recorded this as a memorial in the booklet itself.

In the order of the "Seder," one of the first matters is the recitation of *Ha Lachma Anya*—"all who are hungry, let them come and eat"—the concept of *Maos Chittim*. But prior to this, we perform *Urchatz* and *Karpas*, which is done so that the children will wonder and ask about the laws and customs of Israel. Immediately after this, we remove the *ke'arah* (the Seder plate), which is also done so that the child will wonder and ask.

And if one were to say, "It is sufficient if I give of my wealth, my strength, and my time for the 'wise son' who is engaged and interested in the religion of Israel, or at most for the benefit of the 'simple son'—who, although not wise, at least feels that 'the Jewish people shall dwell alone' and asks 'what is this,' but does not intend to rebel"—the answer comes immediately: "The Torah speaks against four sons: the wise, the wicked, the simple, and the one who does not know how to ask."

Moreover, while the wise son is discussed in the Book of Devarim, and the simple son in Shemos 13, the **beginning** of the discourse (Shemos 12) is to save, bring close, and rectify the one who does not know how to ask and the wicked one.

(And the answer to the wicked one is the verse for the one who does not know how to ask, because in truth, **all** of Israel are believers, the children of believers. The one who acts wickedly does so only because, for the moment, he does not know of this, and he does not even know how to ask about it, for a spirit of folly has entered him.)

This is what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live, outlined in the program of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch: to take an interest in bringing close even those who know neither Lashon Kodesh, nor Yiddish, nor even the most well-known customs of the Jewish people. And according to the effort is the reward and the *nachas ruach*.

The greatness of the merit of those who participate in this work cannot be fully explained. For you and those like you, surely any elaboration on this is superfluous. Therefore, we are confident that our intention in the above aligns with your desire, and "one may act to the benefit of another in his absence."

With blessings for all the best, for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

For the sources of what is written here regarding the Seder, see the Kehot Haggadah with *Likutei Minhagim*.

To the distinguished Avreich, the brilliant Torah scholar and G-d-fearing Chassid, the Tamim,
R' Chaim M. Bukiet, may he live:

You wrote well that there is a distinction between *goral* (lot) and *yerushah* (inheritance), and this is explained in the *maamar* "Ashreinu" (2 Nissan 5700), that the parts of *goral* and *yerushah* are: the service of the heart, the mind, and the feeling of Elokus in every matter, which is present in *yerushah*. The service of the *nefesh, ruach, neshamah*, of *ratzon* (*maamar* "Ashreinu" 5700) and *taanug*, the point of Yiddishkeit, individual vitality, general vitality, and living in essence. The specific service of the *nefesh habehamis* by the *nefesh elokis*, general service, and the service of the *nefesh elokis* from its own essence (*seder maamarim* "B'Chodesh HaShevi'i" 5692).

However, your suggestion that *yerushah* is more similar to *goral* than other forms of acquisition—both in *nigleh* and in *nistar*—is, in my humble opinion, not the case. On the contrary: in *nigleh*, *yerushah* **adds** to other forms of acquisition, as it is an acquisition by necessity, whereas *goral* is **less** than other forms of acquisition, to the point that some say it is not an acquisition at all (see the commentaries in the Shas, *Bava Basra* 106b; *Tur Shulchan Aruch Choshen Mishpat* 273 and sources cited there). This also corresponds to *nistar*, for the feeling of Elokus, the point of Yiddishkeit, etc., exists in everyone, and even at the time of sin, it was "in trust" with him (*Tanya*, *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, ch. 24).

After this comes the specific service of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, which everyone is obligated to perform. Above this is general service, etc. (or the preference and extra caution, which is also one of the distinctions between *chelek* and *goral*. See *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of ch. 67).

(It seems that what caused some confusion is that in *nistar*, the **revelation** mentioned above, which comes through *yerushah*, comes about through the prior service of *chelek* and *goral*. It may be said that an analogy for this is the division of the Land, where the *yerushah* was theirs from their forefathers—*Bava Basra* 119b—but it was only revealed in practice after they conquered it—a **specific** war: "The King of Jericho, one," etc.—and divided it by **goral**. See *Tosafos* s.v. "V'lo," *Rosh Hashanah* 13a; *Yerushalmi Challah*, beginning of ch. 2; *Parshas Derachim*, *Drush* 9, and elsewhere. I will not elaborate further.)

229

229

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5706

To the honorable Rav, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi A. A. Axelrod, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter regarding what I wrote in the Haggadah concerning the reason we say **"with love"** (*be'ahavah*) for *mikra kodesh* on Shabbos—namely, that they accepted the *mikra kodesh* of Shabbos with love—I noted there the source, that this is the opinion of the Levush, etc.

Regarding your observation that if so, the meaning of the words **"mikra kodesh"** would change between weekdays and Shabbos: there is no change here, but rather an **addition.** When it falls on Shabbos, **"mikra kodesh"** refers both to "this holiday" and to "this day of Shabbos," which is not the case on a weekday. However, the word **"with love"** is stated for specific instances, and it refers only to Shabbos. There is no difficulty here, as this is also the case later on, where it says: **"with love and with will"** (*be'ahavah u'b'ratzon*), which refers only to Shabbos and not to Yom Tov, and afterwards: **"with joy and with gladness"** (*b'simcha u'v'sason*), which refers to Yom Tov and not to Shabbos.

Regarding your question that Shabbos is called *kodesh* and not *mikra kodesh*, as written in *Likutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning "To understand what is written in the Haggadah": it is an explicit *mikra* that Shabbos is also called *mikra kodesh*, as it is written (*Vayikra* 23:3), "And on the seventh day is a Shabbos of Shabbos, a **mikra kodesh.**" As our Alter Rebbe writes in his *Shulchan Aruch* (Orach Chayim, beginning of 242), Shabbos is included in the *mikra'ei kodesh*.

Admittedly, in *Netinah LaGer*, he cites the *Chiddushei Aggados* of the Maharsha and the Gra, who interpret "and on the seventh day" in that verse as referring to Yom Kippur (and the six days preceding it as referring to other Yomim Tovim and Rosh Hashanah). However, aside from the fact that this contradicts the literal meaning of the verse and the interpretation of the Alter Rebbe as mentioned above, it is proven from several places in *Chazal* that the verse is speaking about the day of Shabbos (see *Toras Kohanim* in its place—cited in *Aderes Eliyahu* on the Torah by the Gra; *Kiddushin* 37a, *Tosafos* s.v. *v'harei*; *Chullin* 101b).

Now, so that the aforementioned *Likutei Torah* does not contradict this verse, one could perhaps explain that its intent there is primarily that Yom Tov is not called *kodesh*, whereas regarding Shabbos, if it is called *kodesh*, it is certainly included in *mikra kodesh*. However, in the *Zohar Chadash* (95a, cited in *Siddur Shaar HaMoadim*), one cannot say this, for it writes: "Because of this, Shabbos, etc., is called *kodesh* **and not** *mikra kodesh*."

Perhaps it can be said that *mikra kodesh* has several meanings: a gathering for the offering of *korbanos musaf*, the prohibition of performing *melachah*, clean clothing, and eating and drinking, which is *zamin kodesh*. When the *Zohar* says "and not *mikra kodesh*," it does not mean that it is not called *mikra kodesh* in the verse, but rather it explains that in terms of *zamin kodesh*, Shabbos is not called *mikra kodesh*. This is similar to what is found in the *Magen Avraham* in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe there regarding *Chol HaMoed*. But this still requires further study.

Regarding what I wrote that we refrain from eating the *zeroa*: I mentioned this, as with other customs, as the custom of the House of the Rebbe—that is, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, may he live. He also explained to me the reason: so that there should be no resemblance to the *Korban Pesach* (and we require a distancing, as it is in memory of it).

One can sweeten the understanding of why this instruction—not to resemble the *Korban Pesach*—is specifically through the **abstention from eating**: because the *Pesach* differs from all other *korbanos* in that the eating is its essence, not just a detail among other details as in other *korbanos*. As *Chazal* say (*Pesachim* 76b): "It was not created from the outset except for eating." And Rashi explains there: "When the essence of the *Pesach* was commanded, it was commanded for eating." Therefore, when one is careful not to eat it, one is negating the essential aspect of the *Korban Pesach* (which is not the case with an instruction to eat it after its time, as you wrote in your letter).

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 230

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5706

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Ch. [Havlin], may he live,

Shalom and blessings!

Please forgive me for not having replied to your letters, including your own, for various reasons.

1) I will begin by expressing my gratitude for your efforts regarding the certificate for my mother, may she live and be well.

While there is currently no ability to influence the Russian representatives here, it has been said here that since the matter concerns a woman of seventy, it is possible they will grant her an exit permit. Given the situation there, when one requests an exit permit and already possesses an entry permit for another country, the prospects for a positive outcome are much greater than otherwise (not to mention that in such a case, they do not look unfavorably upon the applicant, and to the wise, a word is sufficient). Therefore, I hope that by keeping this in mind—and noting that the Chief Rabbi has also promised his assistance in this matter (and perhaps there is also an advantage in the fact that she already had a certificate)—with your appropriate efforts, you will succeed in obtaining a certificate for her.

2) I have become aware that some years ago, a teacher at the Chayei Olam Talmud Torah named Yitzchak Isaac Eisen had a collection of letters from Rabbi Avraham of Kalisk and his contemporaries (and perhaps also from the Alter Rebbe).

You would be doing a great service if you could locate this man and his collection, and endeavor to have the collection sent to the Rebbe, may he live and be well.

3) For some time now, I have been collecting the letters and sichos of the Rebbe [Rashab], and the first volume of these was published not long ago.

If you know of anyone who possesses any of the aforementioned materials that were not included in this volume, please inform me, and I will contact them.

I will conclude with the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
