## 231

B"H, Erev Shavuos, 5706

To the esteemed Temimim, the Rabbis R. A. Tz. Cohen, R. M. Cohen, and R. B. Y. Mintzberg, and R. Ch. M. Rosenberg, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 15th of Iyar, I spoke with the Rebbe [Rayatz] shlita, and these are his instructions in addition to what was written in his previous letter:

1. In accordance with the directive of the Rebbe shlita, all publishing of books, collections of maamarim, and the like, on behalf of the institutions under the administration of the Rebbe shlita, is to be centralized under the publishing house "Kehot," except in exceptional cases.

2. A specific, individual license from the Rebbe shlita is required each time any of his letters, sichos, or maamarim are printed.

3. Special attention is required regarding material printed alongside the teachings of the Rebbe shlita.

In accordance with all the above, if you decide to continue publishing the Torah journal, it must be done according to the following order:

1. All material must be sent here to Kehot before printing (it is advisable to keep a copy yourselves so that there will be no need to send the proofs back from here), and only material approved from here should be included in the journal.

2. Every journal must bear the "Kehot" seal as it appears in our publications, with the addition of the words below the seal and within the seal itself: "Jerusalem Branch, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days."

3. Naturally, the budget must be secured, meaning that you have the funds in hand for its printing.

And to conclude with a matter relevant to the festival of Shavuos:

The question is well-known (in Likutei Torah, *Vesafarta Lachem* for Shavuos, sec. 67; *Hachodesh Hazeh* 5700, and elsewhere) regarding the verse "I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim," and it does not say "who created you." The explanation for this is that the exodus from Mitzrayim and limitations—even those of holiness—is a higher matter, accomplished through the revelation of "I am who I am." In terms of avodah, this is a mode of conduct that transcends intellect and emotion, a total *bitul* of one's will (Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Bamidbar).

Now, since one finds himself in a "Mitzrayim of holiness" and has no connection to the *sitra achra* at all, seemingly, how can he know the action he is required to perform if not through intellect and emotion, and how can he test himself?

However, we learn this too from Matan Torah. Just as then, the intermediary was Moshe, and Hashem said to Moshe, "Behold, I come to you... and they will also believe in you forever," so too must it be afterwards: every person must be connected, devoted, and in a state of *bitul* of will—even if it seems to him that he is in a "Mitzrayim of holiness"—to the head of his generation, who is the *hitpashtuta* (extension) of Moshe in that generation.

And perhaps it can be said that this is the allusion in the fact that the Hillula of Dovid Hamelech, who is the man who "established the world," is on Shavuos (Yerushalmi, Beitzah, ch. 2, halacha 4). Similarly, it is the Hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, the founder of the teachings of Chassidus, where the connection between teacher and student is dependent on intellect, whereas the connection between a Chossid and a Rebbe is not.

With the blessing of receiving the Torah with joy, immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 232

B”H, 17 Sivan, 5706

To the distinguished Avreichim, the venerable Rabbonim and Chassidim, the G-d-fearing, the Temimim, may they live, Shanghai.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the details provided to me by R’ Garfinkel, may he live:

1) I have already written, by instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, that one must not print **anything** published by any of his institutions without requesting permission from him in advance, and it makes no difference in which language it is. Yet, they have again printed the "Taks," "Shelah," etc.

We do not understand the meaning of this conduct here. You will surely inform us, so that I may know what to tell my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, or you may write to him directly.

2) The two hundred have already been delivered to R’ G., and the remainder—pertaining to the Siddur—will be delivered to him within four weeks, as you instructed. Regarding the Siddur, please send only two copies here to Kehot for the time being. The rest should remain with you (you may sell them in your location for a price no less than two and a half U.S. dollars) until we notify you where to send them.

3) *Derech Mitzvosecha* and *Shaar HaKollel* should be sent here. If they have not yet been bound, then send them unbound, and we will print another title page here; perhaps there will also be some additions. Likewise, regarding anything printed from now on, if for any reason there is no time to wait to send the text of the title page and the additions, then send them here unbound.

4) *Toras Chayim* and the *Peirush HaMishnayos* of the Mitteler Rebbe have been sent to you, and you are surely printing them.

I will repeat my request to inform me which books (and from which printing) from the list in my first letter you have in good condition, so that we do not need to search for them here. This is especially relevant for *Torah Or* (from the Zhitomir 1862 printing).

5) Regarding the printing materials for *HaYehudi HaTza'ir*, they have been sent to you as you requested. Also, what will be published in the near future in English has been sent (it would be good if all the students of the Talmud Torah would become subscribers to the *Shmuessen* and the *Taks*), and you should credit their price to the printing account there.

6) If there are members of our people, especially from the younger generation, who understand only the local language (Chinese), then it is worthwhile to translate—naturally, in a way that the translation is good and accurate—those of our publications that are most necessary according to their spiritual state (Shabbos, Tefillin, *Torah V'Yisrael*, books for the holidays, the sayings in the English *Yalkut Yomi*, and the like). Perhaps also a portion of the *Sichos* and the biography of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. Please inform me of your opinion on this immediately.

Regarding the weekly Parsha, concerning the verse "And Aaron did so," our Sages of blessed memory state—as cited in Rashi—that this is to tell the praise of Aaron, that he did not deviate. The *Likkutei Torah* of the Arizal explains why Scripture specifically informs us here that he did not deviate: because, on the face of it, there is a change here. For Moshe was commanded: "Towards the face of the Menorah shall the seven lamps **give light**," meaning, immediately at the beginning of the lighting; whereas regarding Aaron it is written: "Towards the face of the Menorah he **kindled** its lamps," meaning after the flame had already risen. Therefore, it explains that he did not deviate, and immediately from the beginning of the lighting, it was "towards the face of the Menorah."

However, it adds that even after the flame had risen, it was also thus. And this addition is a praise. This is the essence of his words.

One may explain this according to Chassidus: At the beginning of the *avodah* ("There is no service like the service of love"—the Kohen being the man of *Chesed* and love), it is still easy to intend that it be "towards the face of the Menorah," the true intention of the *mitzvah*. This is not the case when the flame rises, in the intensity of *ratzo*, where one finds many rationalizations and ways to express that *ratzo*; ultimately, one could miss the intention and imagine that this is the will of the *mitzvah*, rather than one's own reasoning.

Therefore, extra caution and *kabbalas ol* are required. And this is the praise of Aaron, who draws down **great** love into the souls of Israel, and in such a way **that he does not deviate**.

With blessings for an immediate Teshuvah and an immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

233

B”H, Friday, 22 Sivan, 5706
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and wise, etc.,
Moreinu Harav D. Shapira, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter:

I have received your book—*Responsa Bnei Tzion*, Part One—and I thank you for honoring me with your work. I was pleased to see the analysis of matters pertaining to astronomy (*techunah*) as found in the words of Chazal regarding the calculation of years, etc. Very few engage in this field of our Torah, and those who possess knowledge of it are fewer still, despite the statement of Chazal (*Shabbos* 75a) that it is a mitzvah for a **person** (and it does not say **Beis Din**; see *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol*, Positive Mitzvah 47; *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Rambam, Root 2*) to calculate the *tekufos* and constellations, and one who knows how to calculate and does not do so is forbidden to be spoken with, and of him it is said, "They do not look at the work of Hashem," etc.

Your aforementioned book, which you sent to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, was received in due time. The list of participants in the writing of the Sefer Torah also arrived in its time, and your name and your family’s names are included therein. Regarding the letter you wrote two years ago to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, I will clarify the matter after such a long time has passed.

I would like to offer a few remarks on two or three places in your book, based on a cursory reading. Following the dictum of Chazal (*Bava Metzia* 84a), "Argue with me... and the study will naturally expand, and you will say a *beraisa* that supports you"—this applies only where, in my humble opinion, there is room for further study. I have chosen the most surprising topic in the book, which is the *Kuntres Ohr Z’ HaYamim* by your father, shlita:

1) **Page 26, column 4:** You compare the three opinions regarding the light of the sun in the time to come (7, 49, 343). Based on the words of Chazal in *Bereishis Rabbah* (10:4) that before Adam HaRishon sinned, the sun traveled on a short path, it is possible to say that the solar sphere was seven times closer to the earth. In that case, the apparent width of the sun would be seven times larger, its apparent surface area would be 49 times larger, and the influences from the entire solar sphere would be 343 times greater.

Now, although you are correct regarding the 7 and the 49, what you wrote regarding the 343 is not understood. Since the size of the sun **in actuality** did not change, and only the distance between the sun and the moon was shortened by a factor of seven, all the influences spreading across the surface of the receiving earth are strengthened by a factor of 49, not 343.

An example of this: The force of gravity depends on the **mass** of the attractor and the attracted. Even so, if they were to approach each other by a factor of seven (but their mass remained unchanged), the force of gravity would increase by a factor of 49, not 343, as is known, and as you yourself wrote in your book on page 28, column 3.

If we wish to reconcile the three opinions in the aforementioned manner, it is possible only if we say that the sun itself changed **in actuality**, in such a way that its diameter grew sevenfold. Then its surface area would increase by 49 times, and its mass—and all influences dependent on the mass of the sun—would increase by 343 times.

—Although, seemingly, the intensity of light depends only on the surface area of the luminous object and not on its thickness or mass, we find otherwise regarding other lights, such as a metal coal that glows because it is heated; the heat depends on the mass, not the surface area, as is understood. Especially since, regarding the nature of sunlight, we do not currently know the manner of its illumination (see *Shabbos* 39a, *Yerushalmi Rosh Hashanah* ch. 2, halacha 4, Rambam *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah* ch. 2, halacha 3, and elsewhere).

2) **28, 3:** Regarding the interpretation of Chazal’s words **"briefly and quickly"**: According to the astronomers—**upon whom you base your words in this section**—if the distance of the sun were shortened by a factor of seven, the orbital period would be shortened by eighteen and a half times (approximately, and not 49 times as you wrote in the text, because the orbital period depends on more than just the force of gravity), because the ratio of the square of the orbital period to the cube of the distance does not change—(I have not seen the *Sefer Mahalach HaKochavim* and the like that you cite in your book, but surely it also mentions this). It is obvious that the *Midrash Rabbah* needed to inform us of this, because not everyone knows this (note the Rambam, *Hilchos Shevuos*, end of ch. 5), especially since this law was only discovered about three hundred years ago.

Note on this section: The beginning of your words and the proofs you bring imply that you mean the speed increased by 343 times, **and in addition to this**, the path was shortened sevenfold, and the premise of the entire *kuntres* is that the **total** orbital time was shortened by 343 times.

3) **31, 4:** Section 26, you resolve according to your system what is written in the *Beraisa d’Shmuel*, beginning of chapter 6, which states: "The sun was created in Aries at 15 degrees, the moon in Cancer at 15 degrees," etc. You interpret that the *Beraisa* holds that the *molad* was on Wednesday at 204 [chalakim], and the movement of the luminaries began on Wednesday at 15 [hours]. During the intervening time, the luminaries traveled the distance they travel **now** in approximately 70 days—from which there were 7 days of rebuke and standing, leaving 70 days. This works out well: if the sun was at the time of Wednesday 204 in Libra at 23 degrees, then at the time of Wednesday 15, its position was in Aries at 15 degrees. What is not understood is: a) The rebuke was after the complaint of the moon, which occurred at the moment of Wednesday 204, according to the *Targum Yonasan ben Uziel*, meaning after they had already traveled the distance of 70 days. b) If at the time of Wednesday 15 the sun was at 15 Aries and the moon at 15 Cancer, then when each of them traveled the distance they travel now in 70 days, according to the movement of the sun and moon explained in the *Beraisa* there (end of chapter 5), the sun would be approximately 103 degrees away from the moon, and there is no room for a *molad*. There are several other comments on this *kuntres*, but this is not the place to elaborate.

* * *

Regarding what can be said simply to resolve the statement of Akilas to Hadrian (*Shemos Rabbah* 30:12) concerning the greatness of Israel—that the smallest among them knows how much time has passed since the creation of the world—even though there are differences of opinion regarding the count of years from the creation, as you questioned in your book: The answer is that among the nations of the world, they know nothing at all about this, or they only have conjectures, and even in their conjectures, they are divided from one extreme to the other (and so it remains to this day). This is not the case with the Children of Israel, where even the smallest has knowledge—not merely a conjecture—of this, and a doubt of two or three years in what is counted is nothing compared to the complete lack of knowledge of the nations of the world.

Alternatively, it can be said that there are four "anchors" for the calculation of the *molados* and the years—as you also wrote in your book, and according to what I will write below, there is perhaps a fifth—and they are in order: Wednesday 204, *Beharad* (Monday 5:204), *Veyad* (Friday 14:0), *Gakav Tatu* (Tuesday 20:676). It is possible to say regarding the words of the *Rishonim* (and we are not responsible for reconciling all the words of the *Acharonim* into one opinion) that the reason for their disagreement regarding the time of the "anchor" is that it is possible to begin the calculation in four ways: from Rosh Hashanah when Adam HaRishon was created; the year before that, because that is when the world was created; the year after the creation of man, because it was a full year in its count (unlike the year of his creation, which was missing several hours in its count; see also the commentary of the Rambam, *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* ch. 6, halacha 8). And in accordance with the dispute as to whether the constellations functioned in the year of the Flood (*Bereishis Rabbah* 25:2), there will be a difference of one year in the aforementioned. This is discussed in several *Sifrei HaIbbur*; see also the *Acharonim*, *Choshen Mishpat* 67, the end of the commentary to the *Beraisa d’Shmuel* by Maharal Lipkin, and others.

According to this, all this dispute concerns the calculation of the years, the *molados*, and the like, but regarding the number of moments of time that have passed since the moment of the creation of the world, everyone’s opinion is the same. And this is what Akilas meant: that the smallest among them knows how much has passed since the creation of the world.

Regarding what I wrote above that there might be a fifth anchor: it is to interpret the words of the *Beraisa d’Shmuel*, and according to what is written in *Tosafos* (s.v. *LiTekufos*, *Rosh Hashanah* 8a) that the anchor *Veyad* is based on the words of Chazal (*Sanhedrin* 38b) that "on the ninth he was commanded, and on the tenth he sinned." Now, some say that he sinned at midday (see *Seder HaDoros* at the beginning, based on *Bereishis Rabbah*, end of ch. 18). If so, he was commanded at the beginning of the sixth hour, and thus the anchor is Friday, 11 hours.

According to this, it is simply understood what is written in the *Beraisa d’Shmuel* (beginning of ch. 6) mentioned above, that the sun was at the time of creation at 15 Aries and the moon at 15 Cancer, and it concludes there: "It is found that the new moon of the beginning of the creation of the luminaries was 2 days and a quarter, and the movement of the sun was 2 degrees and a quarter." This means that until the *molad* it must be 2 days and 11 hours. The *Beraisa* holds that the movement began at the beginning of the night of Wednesday, and if so, the *molad* was Friday 11:00. This aligns with the aforementioned words of Chazal. It is also understood simply what it concludes in the *Beraisa*, "It is found that the new moon," etc., which is the first *molad* in actuality. This is unlike what you wrote in the *kuntres*, where it is difficult to understand what it informs us by saying "It is found that the new moon," etc., since the *molad* that is taken as the anchor is not this *molad* but rather two or three *molados* after it, and the actual rotation was also not 2 days, etc., but 343 times faster.

—In *Pirkei D’Rabbi Eliezer* (ch. 11), the version is "on the eighth he was commanded," and if so, according to the above, there would be a sixth anchor: *Veyg* (Friday 13:0), but I have not found this anchor anywhere as of yet. Conversely, the *Veyad* anchor fits the simple interpretation of the *Beraisa d’Shmuel*. If you say according to the interpretation of the *Yaaros Devash* (Part 1, 4a) that what is written in the *Beraisa* "on the 15th of Av the luminaries were created" refers to their location, which is in the constellation of the 15th of Av, meaning 15 Aries, and it comes to explain the beginning of its words in the *Beraisa*, "The sun was created in Aries at 15 degrees," as you wrote in your *kuntres*.

(Indeed, it is difficult for me: for what purpose is this interpretation? On the contrary, with this interpretation one might err that it refers, as it literally sounds, to the time, whereas at the beginning of the statement, the wording clearly refers to the "place" of the creation of the luminaries.)

Surely it has not escaped you that the *Yaaros Devash* there wrote that the *molad* was on Friday 21 hours, and I have not found a source for this. (And in *Drush* 15, he holds by the *Veyad* anchor).

* * *

4) **38, 3:** You wish to resolve the words of the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch* (*Hilchos Shemiras Guf V’Nefesh*, end of ch. 7) regarding mixed drinks, that his intention is "mixed for drinking" and not the usual interpretation of "mixed with water." Aside from the fact that then the reason "and needless to say water itself" is difficult, and also what is the precision of the word "themselves"—the Alter Rebbe clarified his opinion explicitly, for his words there are: "One should not drink mixed drinks that have passed the night 'after being mixed with water,' and this is our custom," etc.

Incidentally, the words "and needless to say water itself," etc., are enclosed in parentheses, and it is known that any doubt he placed in parentheses, and his intention was to return and revise this chapter to see if "his words were correct" (*She’eris Yehuda* to *Orach Chaim*, siman 363, cited in *Shaar HaKollel* ch. 1, sec. 2).

I trust you will not be offended by my remarks; "the end of the matter is the main thing."

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

The matter of "the light of the moon shall be as the light of the sun" and "the light of the sun," etc., according to Chassidic teaching, has two interpretations: a) That then the light of the moon will be like the light of the sun (in the time to come). b) That then there will only be the light of the sun sevenfold, etc. (as in *Limudei HaMashiach* and the interpretation of the *Shas*). Also, the two interpretations of the "seven days"—whether it speaks of the days of now or the seven days of creation—are explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Tzav*, *d’h Vehayah Ohr HaLevanah*, and in the *drush d’h Im Bechukosai* which is in the continuation of the *Yom Tov* of Rosh Hashanah 5666.

Perhaps according to this, one can also reconcile the three opinions regarding the "sevenfold" (7, 49, 343).

I saw at the end of your introduction that you mention and relate to the Honorable Rabbi and Chassid, etc., R. Boruch Mordechai of Bobruisk. I found regarding his surname that some say "Etinga" and some say "Etinger." Do you have clarification on this? Surely you have seen in the *Kuntres Bikur Chicago* (from the *sichos* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita), *sicha* 2, from his biography. Perhaps there is additional information in his family regarding this, such as his date of birth, passing, etc.

Also, perhaps you have in your possession the writings of the Rav HaM., his *chiddushim*, and the like?

***

**233**
Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 8, p. 183, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Approximately 103 degrees:** Because the difference in the speed of the sun’s movement from the moon is 11'27" per day.
After 70 days—33.5'. Since at the time of creation there were 3030 between them, then after 70 days there are 103030.5' between them.

**2 days and a quarter:** Because the movement of the moon is 35', so it traverses 3030 in 2 days and a quarter (plus 39 minutes).
During this time, the sun moved 2 degrees and a quarter, because its movement per day is 59'8".

**2 days and 11 hours:** Since according to the above calculation the difference in speed per day is 11'27", then 3030 = 2.4646, which is two days, 11 hours, and two and a half minutes.

**Regarding mixed drinks:** See also the letter following this.

**Chairman of the Executive Committee:** Kehot.

## 234

B"H, Wednesday, 27 Sivan 5706
Brooklyn

To the honorable Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, etc.,
Rabbi Menachem Mendel Shapirov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Nissan:

1) You raise a point regarding what I wrote in *Kovetz Lubavitch* (Issue 3), explaining the difference between the level of *merkavah* (chariot) of every person and the fact that the Patriarchs were the *merkavah* in the plural sense (which, as is understood, is one): a) that their *avodah* as a *merkavah* was for **all** their days, and b) with **all** their limbs — unlike every other person.

You wish to add another distinction: that the Patriarchs felt the Rider (and surely you mean that they felt the wonder of the Rider and the distance of His value from their comprehension; though this requires further study from *Likutei Torah*, *seder d'h L'susti* [the first and second discourses]), unlike other people. You bring support from what is stated in *Tanya*, Chapter 34: "One should bring to his heart that since his intellect and the root of his soul are too small to be a *merkavah* and a dwelling for His unity, blessed be He, in truth, etc." — implying that the level of *merkavah* in truth depends on intellect.

Now, if we were to accept your interpretation—that the feeling of the wonder of the Rider is a trait and part of the *avodah* of *merkavah* in truth—there are several difficulties: a) In the parable, this is not the case at all. b) In *Tanya*, Chapter 20, Chapter 39, *Iggeres HaKodesh* 25, and many other discourses where the *avodah* of the Patriarchs' *merkavah* is discussed, this is not mentioned at all, even though other details are explained. c) In Chapter 34 and Chapter 46, this is brought in a different context (pertaining to the level of the Patriarchs), but not when discussing the level of the Patriarchs' *avodah* in that very chapter.

Therefore, it seems to me that one must distinguish here between the cause and the effect. Generally speaking, the *avodah* of *merkavah* is *bitul* (nullification) toward the Rider, even though in truth it possesses a superiority relative to the Rider (which is why it brings the Rider to a place He could not reach by His own power). This *bitul* is total, to the point where the *merkavah* has no will of its own at all (and all that it has is nullified to the Rider; this is stated in *d'h Atah Hu* of the year 5700 regarding the *merkavah* of the Patriarchs, though the surface reading of the language implies this is true for every level of *merkavah*, and this is also implied in *Biurei HaZohar*, beginning of *Parshas Beshalach*), even though it is an entity in its own right. Thus, it is only a *bitul hayesh* (nullification of existence) of the *merkavah tachtah* (lower chariot) of the *serafim, chayot,* and *ofanim*, or *bitul b'metzius* (nullification of essence) of the *merkavah ila'ah* (higher chariot) of the Patriarchs—the souls of *Atzilus*—and likewise the physical limbs that fulfill the *mitzvah* (unlike the *mitzvah* itself, which is in the category of *yichud* [unification]. And this is like the superiority of the *keilim* [vessels] of the *Sefiros* of *Atzilus* over the souls of *Atzilus*, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 20. As is explicitly stated in *d'h Lehavin Mah Shekasuv* in *Likutei Torah*, Chapter 23, said on 24 Teves 5613).

Now, how does one arrive at this *avodah*? The **cause and the path** to it is the root of his soul, the greatness of his intellect, his comprehension, etc.

Based on this, it is not difficult that the parable contains no such element, because the parable is about the essence of the *avodah* of *merkavah*, not the path to arrive at it (and in the parable, there is no need for special causes to arrive at this *bitul*, because it exists by nature, unlike in a person, as is written in *Likutei Torah*, *Emor*, *d'h V'henif HaKohen Otam*).

It is also understood why, in every place where the **avodah** of the level of *merkavah* is explained, this is not mentioned; it is merely a cause and a path to the *avodah*, except in Chapter 34, where he wants to explain that a person should not despair even if he does not attain the *bitul* of Chapter 31 and the *avodah* of *merkavah*, and what he should do then—he explains the cause for not attaining the *avodah*, which is that he lacks the conditions preceding this *avodah*, for his intellect and the root of his soul are small, etc. Just as after the Giving of the Torah, when they could not bear it, they made a *Mishkan*, so too he must set times for Torah study. And similarly in Chapter 46, where he needs to explain how one can say "your G-d" like "the G-d of Avraham," etc., for everyone, even for an unlearned person.

2) Regarding the discussion on what the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Hilchos Shemiras Guf V'Nefesh*, end of Section 7, which states: "One should not drink mixed beverages that have spent the night after being mixed with water... and this is ours in metal vessels or earthenware vessels (and it goes without saying, water itself that has spent the night in metal vessels)." To resolve: a) The fact that in the Holy Land it is impossible to be careful about this, because the water in the courtyards is kept in metal vessels. b) The fact that this is questioned from several places in the *Gemara*.

I have not heard anything about this from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*.

In response to your suggestion, I will provide my own thoughts on this:

a) You wished to resolve the custom of the Holy Land through a new interpretation of the Alter Rebbe's words: that he does not intend to forbid drinking water that has spent the night in metal vessels, but rather that it follows the previous law regarding mixed beverages. Our Rebbe adds that if the water spent the night in metal vessels and then beverages were mixed into it, and then it spent the night, it is certainly forbidden.

The points that require study in this interpretation, in my opinion, are: a) The main point is missing in our Rebbe's words, especially since in this section he **details** his words, which is why he added several words to the language of the *Gemara*. b) He should have said: "And it goes without saying if the water itself spent the night, etc.," for his language implies that it is a law regarding the water itself. c) Where does our Rebbe derive such a novel law? In the *Gemara*, water is not mentioned at all. One must perforce say that it is because he holds that water is more susceptible to *ruach ra'ah* (evil spirit) than other beverages, and proof for this is from the laws brought there in Section 4, which apply only to water. Therefore, specifically **mixed** beverages are forbidden because of the water within them. If so, this "it goes without saying" should apply to the main law—that one should not drink water that has spent the night in metal vessels. Now, in the *Responsa Bnei Tzion*, Section 10, subsection 11 (by Rabbi D. Shapiro of Jerusalem), he wishes to interpret the words of the Alter Rebbe such that "mixed beverages" means beverages (and water is included) that were mixed **for drinking** specifically, and he is not speaking about mixing with water at all; see there.

Aside from the fact that one can raise points against this interpretation in its own right, the Alter Rebbe **clarified** his view as he wrote: "after they were mixed with water, etc., and it goes without saying water, etc." This proves that he interprets "mixed" as "mixed with water," and that the prohibition of water itself is learned only from the "it goes without saying," not that it is explicit in the *Gemara*.

- It is possible that this is also why the law of "it goes without saying water itself" is surrounded by parentheses, as this marking indicates that there is doubt regarding this law, as written in *She'eris Yehuda* on *Orach Chaim*, Section 363, cited in *Shaar HaKollel* at the beginning. The doubt is whether one can derive a *kal v'chomer* (a fortiori argument) in such matters.

For my own part, I wanted to resolve the custom of Jerusalem: that the prohibition of beverages applies only when they spent the night in a vessel, meaning a detached vessel, like a standard vessel found everywhere, unlike if the vessel is attached to the building or the ground, which in many respects loses the status of a "vessel." Regarding matters of *ruach ra'ah*, one should not add to it, and we have only what is explicitly written.

In truth, I do not know if we need all these resolutions. It is clear that since "the masses have trampled upon it" (i.e., it has become common practice), "Hashem protects the simple" (as the Sages say in *Shabbos* 129b, and in the places cited in *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Even HaEzer*, end of Section 11). Moreover, in a place of natural danger, such as in *Shabbos*, *Yevamos* (72a), *Avodah Zarah* (30b), and the like, one must say that "Hashem protects the simple" requires protection nonetheless, for one cannot say the danger is nullified. But in our case, since it is a *segulah* (mystical/spiritual) matter, one can say that because the masses have trampled upon it, the matter is nullified entirely. If so, it is obvious that even a Torah scholar may rely on this, even if you were to say (see the opinions in *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek* there) that in a place where "Hashem protects the simple" is said, one should not rely on it.

- A hint that it is possible to nullify such a matter, and not just to be careful so it does not cause harm, can be found in the *Yerushalmi*, end of *Peah*, which brings the verse "Do not move a boundary" regarding this, and moving a boundary means that they are pushing it away. Another proof is from *Pesachim* (111b), and it is ruled in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe there, Section 9, that bread is susceptible to poverty, but not meat and fish, since that is their way. But this proof can be refuted, for there the cause is not hanging in the air, but rather that he is demeaning the bread by doing so, and hanging is considered demeaning, as in *Berachos* (24a). Since meat and fish are usually treated that way, there is no demeaning, and thus it does not apply to our case. Although the Sages said (*Avodah Zarah* 30a) "a solution for the danger," I have not come with the above except to resolve the custom already in practice.

* * *

b) Regarding what was questioned in the name of the book *Over Orach* (I have not seen this book itself) against our Rebbe the Elder from *Chullin* (55b) regarding *mishkelei shumi*—you, sir, have well-resolved that who says he does not pour out the water afterward, especially since the lung was soaked in them for a full day and night.

But what he wished to resolve a second time—that since there is something in the water, the *ruach ra'ah* does not rest upon it—I do not accept, for if so, he should have said this explicitly, as is written in such a case in *Bava Metzia* (29b), and cited in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe there, end of Section 4. And even there, it only permits something that is usually put into these beverages.

He also questioned from *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 455, which permits, *b'dieved* (after the fact), taking water that spent the night in a copper vessel.

Now, it can be said that we do not find anywhere that it permits it even if it spent the whole night in this copper vessel, only that *l'chatchilah* (initially) it is forbidden to **draw** (take) in a copper vessel, and *b'dieved* they permitted it, but it does not speak of the law of spending the night. And what is written in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe (there, end of Section 19) that it is permitted even if the water remained in it for many days—it can be said that this means without nights, and he did not explain this explicitly since it does not pertain to the law of water that spent the night, but to the laws of *Shemiras HaGuf*, just as he did not explain in the laws of *Pesach* that *l'chatchilah* one should not let them spend the night in any metal vessel—and this is somewhat forced.

Perhaps it can be said that the language of the *Gemara* is "the one who **drinks** mixed beverages, etc.," and since it is a *segulah* matter, and not natural like uncovered beverages, we have only its innovation that it is forbidden to drink them, but when one mixes them into dough and they do not come to the state of drinking, we have no issue with it.

And one should not compare one thing to another in this, just as we do not find a prohibition against using them for any other use, similar to what they said regarding water for *netilas yadayim* in the morning (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 4). And through this distinction—that they only forbade drinking in the case of mixed beverages—it also resolves what was questioned from *Sukkah* (48b), that they would let the water for the *nisuch* (libation) spend the night in a golden pitcher, even though in the *Yerushalmi* there (unlike the *Bavli* according to Rashi and Tosafos) it says that we require it to be from the beverage of Israel.

Regarding the resolution of the *Reshim* of Brezhan that *ruach ra'ah* does not rest in the *Beis HaMikdash*, see the *Responsa Bnei Tzion* which discusses this.

With the blessing of immediate *teshuvah*, immediate *geulah*,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Editorial Committee

B"H, Friday, 29 Sivan, 5706
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished *tamim*, etc., R' Moshe Zev [Greenglass], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters: 
a) I am surprised that you did not respond affirmatively to the requests of Rabbi Quint that he wrote to you on my behalf. I am overwhelmed with tasks, and I do not have the time to answer everyone exactly when they wish. I have said that one should be willing to accept that a response to his letters and the like may be delayed, provided that the publication of materials currently in print or being prepared for print moves forward, as this is for the benefit of the many.

b) I do not have Mr. Arlin’s address, so I am enclosing the letter to him. Please ensure it reaches him together with the *kuntres* being sent, and consult among yourselves as to who should deliver it to him: you, or R' L. Kramer, may he live. I hope Mr. Arlin will understand everything written in my letter, and if necessary, you will surely explain to him what requires further clarification. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to hold a small *farbrengen* in honor of the occasion, and see to it that those gathered will be inspired by Arlin and do likewise, etc. I rely on your judgment.

c) You should certainly endeavor to collect everything due from Arlin and send it as soon as possible, as the printer is pressing. Likewise, send everything received from Delfon, what was received on account of the debt from R' L. Kramer, on account of his own debt, etc. What is the news regarding those pledging for the printing in general?

d) They have already printed *Derech Mitzvotecha*, *Shaar HaKollel*, and *Siddur Torah Or* in Eretz Yisrael. I wanted to add notes and supplements to all of the above, but I do not know if, should they send them here, they are bound according to my instructions; if they are, they will print the supplements here and bind them together.

e) Currently, the following are at the printer here: *Kovetz Lubavitch* 9; the *sichos* pertaining to Mr. Delfon (though their conclusion is not yet arranged, so the time of their appearance is unclear); the book of *maamarei* *Da"Ch* in Yiddish (from *Kuntres* 33 and those printed in *HaKovei'a HaKadosh*); the first two parts of *Divrei HaYamim* in English; and a collection of stories in English.

f) What has been done regarding the students’ signatures on the *shmuessen*?

g) The *sichos* from 19 Kislev of this year are still with the Rebbe, *shlita*, and therefore I cannot fulfill your request regarding them.

h) The two stories from the *hanachos* of the Rebbe, *shlita*, that were not transcribed in *Toras Shalom* are on a separate note, as R' A.P. [Priz], may he live, will transcribe them, together with two other stories, for select individuals. I have not yet found the letter regarding [...] in the *beis medrash*. Regarding the original manuscripts, etc.—in the near future, I will send them as I promised.

i) Thank you for the list of *sefarim* of *Da"Ch* printed in Eretz Yisrael that you sent me.

j) I hope that perhaps I will soon have some free time to occupy myself with preparing for print the *Hilchos Netilas Yadayim* and *Birchos HaNehenin* of the Alter Rebbe with *marei mekomos*, etc., as the Rebbe, *shlita*, desires. Perhaps there are some of R' A.D. Lavut’s notes in your camp that pertain to this, or perhaps he has some *sefarim* that could be of assistance in the above. Please be kind enough to inform me as soon as possible.

I will conclude with what I wrote to someone last week...

Regarding the *parsha* of the week, on the verse "And Aaron did so," our Sages of blessed memory state—and it is brought in Rashi—that this is to tell the praise of Aaron, that he did not deviate. The *Likkutei Torah* of the AriZal explains why the verse specifically informs us here that he did not deviate: because, on the face of it, there is a deviation here. For Moshe was commanded: "Towards the face of the Menorah shall the seven lamps **give light**," meaning immediately at the beginning of the lighting. And regarding Aaron, it is written: "Aaron **lit** the lamps," meaning after the flame had already ascended. Therefore, it explains that he did not deviate, and from the very beginning of the lighting it was "towards the face of the Menorah," but he added that even after the flame ascended, it was also so. And this addition is a praise. This is the essence of his words.

And one can explain this according to *Chassidus*: At the beginning of the *avodah* ("There is no service like the service of love," for the *Kohen* is the man of *chesed* and love), it is still easy to intend for it to be "towards the face of the Menorah"—the true intention of the *mitzvah*. This is not the case when the flame ascends, the intensity of the *ratzo* (the soul's yearning to ascend), where one finds many rationalizations and ways to express that *ratzo*. Ultimately, one can miss the intention* and imagine that this is the will of the *mitzvah* and not his own reasoning. Therefore, one requires extra caution and *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke). This is the praise of Aaron, who draws down *ahavah rabbah* (great love) into the souls of the Jewish people, in such a way that he does **not** deviate.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

The order of writing names in a dedication (parents first)—I learned this from a hint from the Rebbe, *shlita*.

Regarding your questions: Concerning questions of practical conduct, it is a great rule to first clarify if there is an accepted tradition regarding it. One must inquire in Eretz Yisrael among the elders of Chabad regarding the *tefillin* and their size. When I am free from preparing the *maamarei* *Da"Ch* for publication, perhaps I will be able to clarify it in the *sefarim*.

Regarding your second question—enclosed is what I have already answered regarding this, **on the condition that it be returned.**

The customs printed in *Hayom Yom* and the *Haggadah* are instructions for the many according to the Rebbe, *shlita*, except for those where it is explicitly written: "Custom of the Rebbe" or "The Rebbe’s household." In those cases, each person must clarify how he should conduct himself.

Everything that was newly added in *Siddur Torah Or* printed here is by the instruction of the Rebbe, *shlita*. Regarding what was not changed, I did not ask, except in a few places where I had a doubt.

237

B”H, 29 Sivan, 5706

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and faithful businessman,
The distinguished Mr. Yeruchem Fishel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

It is with great satisfaction that I wish to inform you that the sefer **Etz Chaim**, for which you and your wife, may they live, took it upon yourselves to cover the printing costs, has been completed these past few days. A copy is enclosed.

Please write to us and let us know how many copies to send you.

Regarding the magnitude of the zechus of providing thousands upon thousands of Yidden the opportunity to study this sefer, which contains the Torah of our Rebbes along with the introductory letters from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Admur shlita — I am certain that it is unnecessary to explain this to you at length here.

I only wish to point out one hint and example from this week’s parsha:

The parsha recounts for us the story of the Meraglim, and how, through their lashon hara, they brought misfortune upon themselves and upon generations after generations, down to our own generation.

The remedy for this, the Gemara tells us (Arachin 15b), is Torah, as it is written: "A healing tongue is an **Etz Chaim**," where "Etz Chaim" refers to Torah.

The severity of the punishment for speaking lashon hara—which is heard only by the people who are in **that** time and in **that** place—gives us an idea of the great zechus and reward one receives for **speaking** Torah in a specific place and time. From this, one can imagine how great the zechus and reward are for **printing** Torah, for then the sefer, and the Torah within it, can reach all lands, and the sefer remains and is studied even decades and centuries after it was printed.

I conclude with the wish that this great zechus should stand by you in all that you need, and that you should continue to take part in similar endeavors, which encompass Torah, mitzvos, and maasim tovim.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 238

B”H, 5th of Tammuz, 5706

Greetings and blessings!

... **Question:** In *Nagid U’Metzaveh* (regarding the Shacharis prayer), it is stated that "the night is not a suitable time for tzedakah." Seemingly, the opposite should be true: since the night is a time of *gevuros*, it would be appropriate to increase tzedakah in order to sweeten them.

**Answer:** One must add another question to your inquiry: What is the rationale for the variations regarding this matter in the writings of the Arizal, concerning the reason why one should not give tzedakah before Maariv, as cited below?

To understand all this, we must first premise that there are two ways in which mitzvos and the times of their performance relate: 1) The essence of the mitzvah and the essence of the time of its performance are in harmony. Examples include Torah study at midnight, when the Ribono shel Olam comes to delight with the *tzaddikim* in Gan Eden (Zohar I, 72a, and further in the *maamarim* cited in the Siddur regarding *Tikkun Chatzos*); or the prohibition against kindling a fire on Shabbos, because at that time "all the fires of the harsh fire are hidden" (Zohar II, 203b, and explained in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvas Lo Teva'aru Esh), and others. 2) The essence of the mitzvah is the opposite of the essence of the time of its performance, and it comes to rectify it. Examples include the blowing of the shofar on Rosh Hashanah; as stated in the Zohar (III, 99a), Yisrael requires the shofar on the day of judgment, not the *keren* (horn), because... "I do not want the judgment to be attached."

Regarding our subject: According to the first approach, in the morning, *chesed* is aroused (*Pri Etz Chaim*, Shaar HaTefillah, Ch. 2, and elsewhere). Therefore, "one must give tzedakah every morning, in the secret of 'I shall behold Your face in righteousness' (*b'tzedek*), before praying the Amidah" (*Shaar HaKavanos*, Shacharis, p. 4), and "at the time of Mincha, it is a time of *dinim*, so it is not as essential" (ibid., Mincha, end of p. 4). However, "there is no need to give before the Maariv prayer as one does in Shacharis, because now is a time of harsh *dinim*" (ibid., Maariv, p. 4).

According to the second approach, the Mincha prayer is "in the secret of *Gevurah*, and one must sweeten the *dinim*. The primary means of sweetening is through tzedakah, as is known. Therefore, one must give tzedakah three times before the Mincha prayer" (*Sefer Kol Yaakov*, Mincha). However, "at Maariv, one should not give tzedakah, because that is the time of the dominion of absolute *dinim*, and it is written, 'Do not muzzle an ox while it is threshing'—now is the time of their dominion, and it is not the time for their eradication" (ibid., Maariv).

This can be understood based on what the Ramaz writes on the *Ra'aya Mehemna* (Zohar II, 40b), which is explained in the *maamar* beginning *Zeh HaYom* 5735: The *kelipos* and the *sitra achra* were also created, and if so, it is inevitable that some vitality must be drawn to them. The matter is that there are two types of vitality for the *kelipah*: the first is what is allotted to it by Divine decree, and the second is what the sinners add.

— It is worth noting the words of our Sages (*Shekalim* 5:4): "Rav Huna bar Pappa would distribute tzedakah at night. One time, the 'Master of the Spirits' encountered him and said to him, 'Did your Rabbi not teach you: "Do not move your neighbor’s boundary"?'" Based on the above, this is understood simply, and there is no need for the *Korban HaEdah*’s explanation that the objection was because he went out [to seek the poor]. —

In the *Sefer HaShem* of Rashkov, it is added to the opinion of the Maharik that "one should not give tzedakah at Maariv, because it is then night, the *dinim* are powerful, and there is fear of the hold of the *chitzonim*."

***

A general question that may be raised regarding this entire matter is: Tzedakah is a positive commandment that is not time-bound (*she'ein hazman gerama*), so how can it be said that it is not for the night?

Seemingly, one could answer that the aforementioned writings of the Arizal speak of the obligation of giving tzedakah *before* prayer, and it is specifically regarding this that it is said one should not give before Maariv. But this is not the case—for the reason provided, that the night is a time of *dinim*, etc., is a reason that remains in full force throughout the entire night.

Perhaps it can be said that there are two modes of the mitzvah of tzedakah: 1) One who sees a poor person asking, regarding whom it is said, "Do not harden your heart," and one must give immediately, as is written in the *Shulchan Aruch* (Yoreh Deah, beginning of Ch. 247) regarding the story of Nachum Ish Gam Zu. 2) A person should not withhold himself from the mitzvah of tzedakah even if no poor person has come to ask of him (*Bava Basra* 9a, and ruled in the *Shulchan Aruch* there). Now, the writings of the Arizal are speaking of the latter mode (and see *Shaar HaKavanos* there, that he would give it to the *gabbai tzedakah*, **and not to a poor person**). This is unlike the first mode, where there is no difference between night and day, as mentioned: "Do not harden your heart," etc.

One should not raise the objection that, after all, because of the reason that the night is a time of *dinim*, etc., as mentioned above, and "do not move your neighbor’s boundary," what is the difference between the first and second modes? The difference is significant: since **from Heaven** a poor person was brought to him, and he did not go out to seek him, this is an indication that this does not interfere with what was allotted to them by **Divine** decree. And this is well understood.

***

There is still room for further study based on what our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) writes in the introduction to the *Shulchan Aruch* and in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 8, explaining the matter of giving a coin to a poor person before praying, which is to ensure that the drawing down [of holiness] also occurs in the physical realm. If so, this should also be the case for the Maariv prayer. Perhaps it can be said that the Maariv prayer is different, as all the drawing down that depends on us has already been accomplished in Shacharis and Mincha, as is known regarding the fact that Maariv is optional. Or, it may be said that specifically in Shacharis and Mincha, when the *Malchus* ascends to Him, special effort is needed to draw down [holiness] into the physical as well, whereas in Maariv, the *Malchus* is in the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*. Especially since the night is the time when "she gives food to her household." This still requires further study, and this is not the place to elaborate.

With the blessing of "immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

In the *Haggadah B'Chafazon* for Pesach (Section 70, Law 1), it is brought from the book *Maaseh Tzedakah* that every **night** after the counting [of the Omer], one should give a coin to tzedakah to rectify what one has damaged in the realm of the supernal *chasadim*.

I do not know who the author of *Maaseh Tzedakah* is (apparently one of the Sephardic Kabbalists), but if he is an authority and is following the Kabbalah of the Arizal, then seemingly it requires study, given what was said about giving tzedakah **at night**. However, based on what was written above, this is also resolved, because he is speaking about the rectification of what **one has damaged**, and if so, it does not interfere with what was allotted by Divine decree.

## 239

## 240

240

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5706

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, wise, and understanding [scholar],
The *Tamim*, Rabbi A. [Hecht], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby express my special thanks to you and to all those who joined you for your important assistance in the fundraising campaign for **Keren HaMitzvos** under the auspices of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which was conducted in the Sephardic community in your city.

The work of **Keren HaMitzvos** is great, providing spiritual aid to our refugee brethren, may they live. After all their suffering and toil, thank G-d, the wicked have not crushed their spirit, and their souls thirst to cleave to their Father in Heaven through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. At a time when many, thank G-d, are concerned with their material needs, we must not forget or neglect their spiritual needs, without which their lives are not lives. We are confident that you, may you live, will continue to participate in this lofty endeavor, as well as in the other areas of work of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

Regarding the assistance with *mitzvos* and the like for those who do not yet acknowledge this, one must not only provide the *mitzvos* themselves, but also prove to them—with gentle words—the necessity of fulfilling the *mitzvah*.

Some may ask: "What do we have to do with this trouble? Is it not better if we occupy ourselves with our own self-improvement, and with ascending in goodness itself from level to level? Why should we descend below to argue—or at least to speak—with those who are 'called dead while they are alive,' and in the meantime, we will neglect our own Torah study, engagement in *mitzvos*, etc.?"

To these, and to those like them, one should reply based on what is explained in the *Midrash Rabbah* (Chapter 19:4) regarding the previous *Shabbos* portion: "For every single thing that the Holy One, Blessed be He, told Moses, He told him its impurity and its purity. When he reached the portion of *Emor El HaKohanim*, Moses said, 'Master of the Universe, if a person becomes impure, how is he purified?' He did not answer him. At that moment, Moses’ face turned pale. When he reached the portion of the Red Heifer (*Parah Adumah*), He told him..." Seemingly, it is not understood why He did not answer him immediately, as He did with everything else. It is even more difficult to understand, as Rabbi Levi—who is a master of *shmita* in *Midrash Rabbah*—states in *Gittin* (60a) that the portion of *Emor* and the portion of the Red Heifer were said on the same day. If so, why were they not placed next to each other?

Briefly, we can explain this by first clarifying the difference between the impurity of a corpse (*tumas meis*) and all other forms of impurity: The Jewish people are called "living," based on the verse, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today" (*Avos D'Rabbi Nosson*, end of Chapter 14). Therefore, before the sin—when this matter of *dveikus* existed throughout the entire world, for Adam HaRishon said to all created beings, "Come, let us bow down and prostrate ourselves" (*Zohar Vol. I, 221b*; see also *Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer*, Chapter 11)—the concept of death did not exist at all.

As long as this *dveikus* was not severed, even if the "rope" of connection was weakened by sins and transgressions, it could easily—proportionately—be strengthened again in its *dveikus*. This is not the case with the sin of death, where one is cut off from his root in the "Living G-d" (*Sefer Shel Beinonim*, end of Chapter 24). When the Jewish people are at their level, this spiritual death also causes physical death (*Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapters 4-6; see also *Kuntres Uma'ayon*, *Maamar* 7), and gives place to all the laws of *tumas meis*.

Therefore, regarding all other forms of impurity, He could answer him immediately regarding their purification, because the connection to the source of purity was not completely severed, and there was no interruption in the process of *hishtalshelus* from level to level. This is not the case with death and its impurity (spiritually and physically), where the order of *hishtalshelus* is interrupted and requires an *hemshech* from above that level. Because there is a break and a leap between the impurity and its purification, there was also a break in the telling of their laws in the Torah. As is known, the articulation of a matter in the Torah is its very existence, as per the interpretation of the Sages' expression: "The Sages spoke of that which is *hoveh* (present/actual)" (*Likutei Torah*, *Seder HaMaamarim*, *B'Yom HaShemini*, etc.).

With this, we can also clarify the Mishnah (*Keilim* 1:4): "The most severe of all is the corpse, which imparts impurity **in a tent**" (the commentators have already addressed why this does not contradict the case of the *metzora*). There are three levels of vitality through which the soul enlivens the body: specific vitality (internal, *memalei kol almin*), general vitality (encompassing, *sovev kol almin*), and that which is above both of them (the distant encompassing light, above *memalei* and *sovev*). Corresponding to these in human needs are: food, clothing, and shelter (*Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* *Mizmor Shir Chanukas*). Therefore, a corpse, which has touched even the distant encompassing light, imparts impurity even in a tent.

Yet, despite all this, after the interruption, He did answer Moses regarding the purification of the corpse, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, told him that to him He would reveal the reason, while to others it would be a **"chok"** (statute), and that his *parah* (heifer) would exist forever (*Midrash Rabbah*, ibid.).

It is known that *mitzvos* that have ceased to exist physically are nevertheless present spiritually, as is known regarding the matter of *tefillah* and *korbanos*.

So too is it regarding the matter of the purification of the corpse. Even if it appears to our eyes as a *chok*, and we ask, "What business do we have dealing with the impurity of such-and-such a person, which is the impurity of a corpse, for he is cut off, G-d forbid, from his root, and how can he be purified?"—and furthermore, and especially, because it temporarily imparts impurity to those who deal with it—nevertheless, the Moses of every generation, who are our Sages, their *parah* exists. All Jews are commanded, and especially those who draw near, "And they shall take to you—specifically—a *parah*," and then, ultimately, it purifies the impure and brings him to eternal life.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*,"

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 241

[20 Tammuz 5706]

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Y. A. Orenstein, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the wedding of your son, may he live, in a good and auspicious hour, I wish to express my *mazel tov* wishes. May they build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*.

It can be said that regarding the descent of the *neshamah* into this world—which is likened to a wedding celebration—there are two aspects: 1) The refinement of the body, the *nefesh ha-chiyunis*, and one’s portion in the world (as discussed in *Tanya*, Chapter 32). 2) An ascent in the *neshamah* itself, through this descent and the *avodah* within the body.

When one has already reached the stage in his *avodah* of refining his portion in the world, regarding this our Sages said (*Yevamos* 63a), "A man brings wheat... and he is in need of his 'help-mate'—this is his wife."

This is also the order, applicable to all, that was established in the *Mishnah* (*Avos*, end of Chapter 5): "Five years for *Mikra*... ten for *Mishnah*... thirteen for *mitzvos*... fifteen for *Gemara*... eighteen for the *chuppah*." Only then, when he has reached the stage of being occupied (which is the "great preoccupation" mentioned in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the *Alter Rebbe* below) with the refinement of this world—which occurs when he is twenty—

For then he has already fulfilled "adorn yourself first," as he is in a state of ultimate perfection, as is understood from what is written in *Likkutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning "Ben Esrim Li-Mchor."

- He will have already completed the study of *Gemara*, which spans five years, as stated in the *Alter Rebbe’s* *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 2, Section 9.

- As for what is written there, "two or three years," it can be said that this presents alternative options, depending on the two interpretations regarding the age of eighteen: whether it is a full eighteen (*Tosafos*, *Kesubos* 50a) or at the beginning of eighteen (*Rambam*, *Hilchos Ishus*, Chapter 15, Law 2; see also *Shulchan Aruch Even HaEzer* 1:3 and *Nosei Keilim*).

Regarding the fact that even before this, our Sages said "thirteen for *mitzvos*," it can be said that this is the beginning of the *avodah*, which relates only to his body and *nefesh ha-chiyunis*, without connection to his portion in the world, for "little by little I will drive them out."

However, since this is not the primary aspect of the *mitzvos*, it is not called a *mitzvah min ha-muvchar* (a *mitzvah* in the most preferred manner). With this, we can clarify the precise wording of the *Shulchan Aruch* there: "And one who marries early at thirteen is a *mitzvah min ha-muvchar*." According to Rashi, this applies even a year earlier, for even then he is a "minor who is close to adulthood" (*mufla samuch l'ish*), and his vows are valid by Torah law.

Through this *avodah*, an ascent is also achieved in the *neshamah*, and this ascent is incomparable—from *Memalei Kol Almin* (the Divine light that fills all worlds) to *Sovev Kol Almin* (the Divine light that encompasses all worlds). The introduction and preparation for this was related to us by Yeshayahu—as it is known that everything related in *Tanach* and by our Sages provides a lesson in the *avodah* of Hashem—in the description of the *Merkavah*: "And I saw the L-rd... *seraphim* standing **above** Him." The *Alter Rebbe* explains (*Likkutei Torah*, *maamar* "Ve-Nikdashti," Section 6) that because their primary desire is to attain the level of *Sovev Kol Almin*, which is above the name *Adonai* (the Master of all, who fills all worlds), it is as if they are standing there.

This desire and *avodah* must not be in the category of love alone or fear alone, etc., but rather in the integration and connection of all the *midos* together, the "weaving of three... of four" (*Torah Or*, *Parshas Toldos*, *maamar* "Mayim Rabim," Section 6). Through this *avodah* specifically in this world, the Jewish people ascend in actuality to the *Sovev Kol Almin*, even higher than the *seraphim*, as our Sages said (*Chullin* 91b), to the world of *Ein Sof*. This is why **this** world is specifically likened to a wedding celebration: just as through marriage the power of procreation is revealed—which exists in *neshamos* and not in angels—which is a reflection of the power of the *Ein Sof* (see *Likkutei Torah*, end of the explanation of "Sheshim Heimah Malchos").

With *mazel tov* blessings, for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

## 242

B"H, 22nd of Tammuz, 5706

To the esteemed avreich, the G-d-fearing, who engages in the needs of the community, R' Y. shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your invitation to the Pidyon HaBen of your son, Shalom DovBer shlita:

May it be the will of Hashem that it takes place in a good and auspicious hour, and may you and your wife tichyeh raise him to Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim, with abundance in both physical and spiritual matters.

The concept of Pidyon HaBen begins with the fact that it is in exchange for Hashem having redeemed the firstborn of Yisrael on the day He struck down every firstborn in the land of Mitzrayim. Our Sages of blessed memory have said (Shabbos 133b): "Be like Him; just as He is gracious and merciful, so too must you be gracious and merciful." In our context, this is the avodah of every individual—whoever has the ability—to save the children of Bnei Yisrael, of whom it is said, "Yisrael is My **firstborn** son," so that they do not become assimilated among the nations, Heaven forbid. Rather, one must bind them to the G-d of life through the Torah of life, through which the verse "you are all alive today" will be fulfilled in them as well.

You have merited that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, has entrusted you with a portion of this holy avodah, and you will surely strive, as much as depends on you, to be a worthy vessel for this merit and to bring it from potential into actuality.

May it be His will that speedily in our days we will all merit to see the redemption with which our Father in Heaven will redeem His firstborn son, Yisrael, from this final galus, and may the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, lead us to greet Mashiach Tzidkeinu, truly soon. Amen, may it be His will.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Regarding Kohanim and Leviim, there is no concept of Pidyon HaBen, for "our G-d is a Kohen" (Sanhedrin 39a). See *Likutei Shoshanim* by the Maharash of Ostropol regarding when one is at the level of a Kohen Gadol and when one is at the level of a common Kohen. However, this does not contradict the above; for the fact that there is no concept of Pidyon HaBen with five selaim for a Kohen or Levi is, on the contrary, because five selaim are insufficient to redeem them in exchange for those whom Hashem redeemed in Mitzrayim; rather, their very bodies are sanctified through this, as stated in the verse (Bamidbar 8), and this is well understood.

From the Secretariat copy.

**R' Y.:** Hecht.
**Chairman of the Executive Committee:** Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch.

243

B"H, Thursday, 4 Menachem Av, 5706

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi A. A. Axelrod, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from last week:

1) Regarding the vocalization of the word *lirzot* ("*rach lirzot*" in the *Anenu* prayer and *HaOchez B'Yad*): There are variations in the printed Siddurim and Machzorim, and it is impossible to determine who the one responsible for the change was—whether it was the typesetter or the person after whom the Siddur is named. For example, in the Siddur *Shaar HaShamayim* by the Shelah (Amsterdam, 5477) — in *Pirkei Avos*, Chapter 5, Mishnah 11 — *lirzot* is written with a *patach* under the *resh*. In the Warsaw edition (5642), it is written with a *kamatz* under the *resh* and a *tzere* under the *lamed*.

However, I found that the Yaavetz, in his commentary *Lechem Nikudim* on *Avos*, writes: "*Lirzot* — the *lamed* with a *chirik*, the *resh* with a *shva*, and the *dalet* with a *patach* from the *kaved* (heavy/guttural) — is incorrect."

Similarly, in the Siddur *Avodas Yisrael*, which was edited according to several manuscripts and Siddurim, it is written that this is the version in the oldest manuscript Siddur he found (on parchment from the year 5106), and that this is the primary version.

Also, in the Siddur printed in Rostov (in *Pirkei Avos*), it is as mentioned above, and it is said that it was edited according to the Rebbe [Rashab]. (However, in the Siddur *Torah Or* and the Warsaw 5642 Siddur — in *Pirkei Avos* — the vocalization is: the *lamed* with a *tzere* and the *resh* with a *kamatz*.)

In the Rostov Siddur, in the *Tefillas Tal* at its beginning, the *lamed* has a *shva* and the *resh* has a *patach* (and so wrote Rabbi A. Ch. Naeh, may he live, in his *Kuntres HaSiddur* based on his own reasoning), because there it is a transitive verb regarding the earth, as is understood.

While on the subject, it should be noted that they changed the prayer to say "**rach** lirzot," even though the language of the Mishnah is "**noach** lirzot." It is possible that they wanted to arrange it according to the alphabet, but that is somewhat forced.

2) Regarding the text of *Avinu Malkeinu* on a public fast day: Until I received your letter, there was no doubt in my mind that it should be: "*Zochreinu l'chaim tovim*" (Remember us for good life), and the like, omitting the word "*b'sefer*" (in the book), just as it is written: "Remember us for life, etc., and write us in the book of life, etc." What connection is there between "remembering" and "in the book"? (Also, it is a matter of inquiry, at first glance, whether there is a "writing in these books" throughout the entire year, other than the Ten Days of Repentance).

I searched now in the Siddurim and found in the Siddur *Beis Yaakov*, known as the Siddur of the Yaavetz (Lemberg, 5664), "*Zochreinu l'chaim*" with the omission of "*b'sefer*." This is also the case in the Siddur *Otzar HaTefillos*, which is precise according to its value. In the Siddur of the Shelah (5477) and the Siddur *Beis Kel* which the Yaavetz himself printed, there is no *Avinu Malkeinu* for a public fast day separately. However, in the Siddur *Shaar HaShamayim* (Warsaw, 5642), I found "*Zochreinu b'sefer chaim tovim*," and this is also somewhat the opinion of Rabbi Ch. A. Yehuda in the Siddur he printed. (And see, I found a new thing in the Siddur *Tefillah L'Moshe*, which states after the *Shacharis* prayer: "There are those who have the custom to say *Avinu Malkeinu* on a public fast day, and one must be careful to skip the *Avinu Malkeinu* of 'Chadash' [New Year], etc., and the five *Avinu Malkeinu* in which it is written 'write us,' etc." In the aforementioned *Beis Yaakov* Siddur, he brings two opinions: to skip the *Avinu Malkeinu* of "write us," and others say to say "remember us." He does not mention the *Avinu Malkeinu* of "Chadash" at all, nor does he mention whether to say "in the book." In the Siddur *Beis Kel*, none of this is mentioned at all.)

With the blessing of "immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 244

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5706

To the esteemed and distinguished Dr. A. Hillman, shluchim,

Greetings and blessings!

In the archives of the *HaKriah VeHaKedushah* editorial office, which have come into my possession—the publication of the *Kodesh* has been suspended for some months—I found your letter regarding a "commentary on a passage in the Tanya."

In response:

1) In the Tanya, end of Chapter 32, the words "and David, peace be upon him, did not say—see Chapter 16 of Shabbos" appear in parentheses, even in the first printing of the Tanya (found in the library of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shluchim).

2) The content of this chapter is that one who makes his soul the primary focus and his body secondary thereby attains a love for all Jews, since they are all called brothers in the literal sense, due to the root of their souls in the One Hashem. Regarding this, he raises a difficulty in the parenthetical remark: If so, how is it possible to hate a fellow Jew with **total** hatred, when he possesses a soul that is literally a "part of Elokus from above"? He explains that this applies only to *minim* (heretics) and *epikorsim* (skeptics) who incite jealousy, etc., and there is no room for the aforementioned love because they have no portion in the Elokus of Yisrael; that is, they have been cut off, Heaven forbid, from their root, and therefore they cannot be called brothers (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Section 7; Tanya, end of Chapter 24; Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 5).

For those who are not his peers in the observance of Torah and mitzvos—and consequently there is no commandment to hate them due to the evil within them, for what concern is it of his?—two conditions must be met: a) A reason why there is no room for love: they have no portion in the Elokus of Yisrael; b) A reason for the hatred: "Do I not hate those who hate You, Hashem," etc.

Based on the above, several nuances can be understood: a) Why our Rebbe added "also *epikorsim*," even though the Gemara in Shabbos speaks only of *minim* (for the distinction between them, see Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, and Tur Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, Section 158, and Choshen Mishpat, Section 425). This is because there is also a commandment to hate *epikorsim*, which is why we "lower them" (Avodah Zarah 26b; there, informers are also listed, but the reason for them is not because of hatred, but due to the law of a *rodef*—pursuer—and it is not regarding them that it is said "total hatred," etc.). b) Why our Rebbe did not list those liable for *kares* (excision) and death penalties, even though they too are cut off from their root and thus cannot be called brothers. c) Why our Rebbe added the words "that they have no portion in the Elokus of Yisrael."

In any case, our Rebbe is not speaking in the end of Chapter 32 only about *meshumadim* (apostates), nor even about **all** *meshumadim* (note also the response of the Rambam in his *Kovetz Teshuvos*, Section 163), but rather about *minim* and *epikorsim*, whose nature is explained in the Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, there.

3) The intent of this chapter is to explain an additional level that comes as a result of the contemplation in the previous chapter, which is the mitzvah of *ahavas Yisrael*. However, for the **completeness** of the matter, he also explains the situation where there is no room for this love at all, and therefore it is only included in a parenthetical remark. See similar instances in Chapter 1: "And if afterwards," etc.; end of Chapter 32: "And the sinners and rebels," etc.; end of Chapter 5, and elsewhere.

* * *

By the way: There is an unusual expression in this chapter: "**And even if not** he has not lost." Seemingly, it should have been "**And even if** he has not lost." This is highly noticeable, given the simplicity of the language and the absence of flowery rhetoric or fragmented verses in the *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, and *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*.

It is possible to explain the difference between the two expressions: "Af" (even) denotes a matter of addition and something **secondary** to what preceded it. "Hen" (if/whether) is intended to emphasize the equality between two things. In our context, our Rebbe wanted to emphasize that the love must be equal in both scenarios: *whether* he brings them closer to Torah, etc., *or* not. Therefore, he used the expression "hen." See also the words of our Sages (Bamidbar, Chapter 15:14) regarding the verse (Daniel 3:18) "And if not (v'hen lo), etc."—they said to him: whether He saves or whether He does not save, etc. Note also the Mishnah at the end of Chapter 5 of Sotah: "Even if He kills me, etc."—this teaches that he did it out of love—that in both cases it must be with equality.

With wishes for all the best and with regards,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

The matters in Chapter 32 of Tanya are also explained in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael.

*Tomer Devorah*, Chapter 2: One should accustom himself to instill love for people in his heart, even for the wicked, as if they were his brothers, and even more than that.

*Shevet Mussar*, beginning of Chapter 2 (in the name of our Sages): "There is no peace, says Hashem, for the wicked"—from here we see that the Holy One, blessed be He, loves the wicked.

*Sichos Kayitz* 5700: That one must love a completely wicked person just as one loves a completely righteous person.

## 245

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5706

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and faithful businessman, the distinguished Mr. Aryeh Leib Brailowsky, Shanghai

Peace and Blessing!

It was with great joy and pleasure that I received the news from our dear bochurim who arrived from Shanghai, that you have accepted the proposal to dedicate yourself to securing the means for the printing of the sefarim of our holy Rebbes, the Torah of the living G-d, in Shanghai.

I have, naturally, informed my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, about this. He was extremely pleased to hear it and hopes to receive good news from you in the near future.

Regarding the magnitude of the merit in providing thousands of Yidden with the opportunity to study sefarim that contain the Torah of our Rebbes, I am certain that it is unnecessary for me to explain it to you at length. I would only like to point out one example, which is related by Chazal:

Chazal relate that the entire matter of the galus began because the spies spoke lashon hara, and through this, brought misfortune upon themselves and upon generations after generations, down to our own generation.

The remedy for this—as the Gemara states (Arachin 15b)—is Torah, as it is written, "A healing for the tongue is a tree of life" (*Eitz Chaim*), where *Eitz Chaim* refers to the Torah.

The severity of the punishment for speaking lashon hara—which is heard only by the people present at that time and in that place—gives us an idea of the great merit and reward one receives for speaking Torah in a specific place and time. From this, one can imagine how great is the merit and reward for printing Torah, for then the sefer, and the Torah it contains, can reach all lands, and the sefer remains and is studied even decades and centuries after it was printed.

I conclude with the wish that this great merit should stand by you in all that you need, and that you should continue to take part in similar endeavors that encompass Torah, mitzvos, and maasim tovim.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel
