## 246

B"H, Friday, 6 Elul, 5706

To the honorable, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Havlin, may he live

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the Bar Mitzvah of your son, Eliezer, may he live:

I offer my blessings that you may raise him (see Kiddushin 30a: "Your hand is upon your neck, your son is upon your neck," etc., until twenty-two, and some say until twenty-four; seemingly, there is room for study regarding the opinion of the Alter Rebbe—Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 1, end of subsection 6—who adopts both stringencies, but this is not the place to elaborate) to Torah, the chuppah, and ma'asim tovim, with abundance in both spirituality and physicality.

Regarding a thirteen-year-old becoming obligated in mitzvos, we learn this from Shimon and Levi (Rashi, Nazir 29b; see also the notes on the Mishnah, end of Chapter 5 of Avos). It can be said that the matter of fulfilling mitzvos at the time of Bar Mitzvah, at least initially, consists of: 1) A path of war with the body and the nefesh habehamis, for "the earlier one anticipates, the more one is burdened." 2) The intention to draw down the Ohr Ein Sof into them and into the physical object with which the mitzvah is performed. 3) The ability to win this war exists because the Ribono shel Olam assists him, for were He not to assist him, etc.

And this is: 1) Shimon—his avodah is in the category of *shemiah* (hearing) rather than *re'iyah* (seeing) (see Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Va'eschanan, end of Kunteres HaAvodah, and elsewhere). 2) Levi—the intention that he should "accompany" (yilveh) the Ohr Ein Sof below (see Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Vayechi). 3) Eliezer—he is victorious even if the yetzer overcomes, because his G-d is his helper, continuing to grow until he becomes "very great."

* * *

In response to your letters:

a) Thank you for your efforts in fulfilling my requests for the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

b) The Sefer HaSichos of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, was printed via mimeograph in a limited quantity, and therefore it does not fall under the general terms of our publications. Its price is as stated: 10, and for yeshiva students, 8.

c) What you saw there regarding our publications is certainly from those who purchased a proper number of copies here for cash and sent them there at their own responsibility; in such a case, naturally, the terms are most favorable. We have entrusted the primary sale of the Tzemach Tzedek books for the duration of a year to a bookseller here, on the condition that he also send them to Eretz Yisrael.

d) I have been instructed to clarify with you where the deed and documents for the house and property in Chevron are, which are registered in the name of the Rebbe, may he live and be well. (What was received here is only the bill of sale in the name of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.) Please be so kind as to make photocopies of them to keep there, and send the original documents to the Rebbe, may he live and be well. The earliest possible attention to this would be appreciated, and thank you in advance.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah," and with a good inscription and signature in both spirituality and physicality,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## Hint

B"H, 7 Elul, 5706

To the honorable Rabbi, the man of many accomplishments and great energy,
[Titles omitted]
Rabbi Sh. Z. Hecht, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter.

... I called him and requested, per the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live, that he come to New York for a day or two. Since this was done through me, I must arrange the matter of the expenses; if they have not yet reimbursed him, please be so kind as to inform me.

Certainly, you will now continue your efforts regarding the donations for the distribution of the *Shelah* pamphlets among those with whom you have spoken about this, and "he who adds, is added to."

And although it is explained—in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Tetzei*, on the verse "And she shall shave her head," and at length in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, in the mitzvah of the shaving of the *metzora* when he becomes purified—that excessive effort is superfluous and even detrimental, this refers to matters of livelihood, as explained there, because one's sustenance is predetermined. This is not the case, however, regarding matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, as is understood.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah*, immediate *geulah*.

**Menachem M. Schneerson**

## 248

B"H, Sunday, 12 Elul, 5706

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and trustworthy R’ Y. HaKohen, may he live,

Shalom and blessings!

You surely remember our conversation regarding the printing of one of the seforim of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, at your expense and without partners. I have not mentioned this throughout the intervening time, as I was not certain when such a sefer could be expected to be finished in print, given the current difficulties with paper, labor, and so forth.

I now have the following proposal: According to the printer’s firm promise, the first *Sefer HaMaamarim* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, will come off the press in a week or two. It will contain the Chassidic maamarim in Yiddish that were printed in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah* (55 maamarim, approximately 220 pages, in the same format and binding as *Toras HaChassidus*; printing costs are $1200–$1400).

I await your reply: a) whether this proposal is suitable for you and you accept it, and b) if so, whether we may use the same phrasing regarding your donation as in *Toras Shalom*, or if you would like it done differently.

Since the printer is rushing the work, and I am certainly rushing, I am writing via airmail and hope for your reply in the same manner. Thank you in advance.

To conclude with a matter of the day: Rashi explains (in this week’s parsha, 26:4, and it is in the Sifrei) that the Kohen places his hand under the hand of the owner and waves it.

What is the moral lesson to be derived from the fact that both the hand of the Kohen and the hand of the owner are required? It is that every Jew consists of: a) A Kohen—for "Kohanim are the messengers of the Merciful One" (Kiddushin 23b)—representing the *at-erusa d’leila* (arousal from above) that is granted to him from Above, his *nefesh elokis* which, even at the time of sin, "remained faithful to Him" (Tanya, end of Chapter 24). b) An owner—for "the earth He has given to the children of man"—representing the *at-erusa d’letata* (arousal from below) that one must toil for himself, the *nefesh habehamis* which is in the world and possesses free choice as to where to turn.

The ultimate purpose of refining the matters of the world is that the best and most delightful of them should be "and you shall place it before Hashem your G-d" and (the Kohen) eats it—not to be burned—in accordance with the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse "When you see the donkey of your enemy..." (*Hayom Yom*, p. 23), that both things, eating and "before Hashem your G-d," must be present. And this can only be achieved—not in a deceptive manner (see *Toras Shalom* 50, 62, 122, etc.)—specifically if both the Kohen and the owner, which are within every Jew, take part in it, as is understood.

I sign with the blessing of *Kesivah VeChasimah Tovah*.

## 249

B"H, 27 Elul, 5706

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, wise in good matters, etc.,
R' Elchanan HaKohen, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

On the threshold of the New Year, I wish you, in the name of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch and in my own name, a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* in both material and spiritual matters.

On this occasion, a word regarding the day.

One can learn many things from every matter, especially from matters connected to Torah.

The Torah did **not** set aside the day of the creation of the world from the other days of the year; however, it did establish Rosh Hashanah on the sixth day of the *Maaseh Bereishis*, the day of the creation of man!

The content of this, in short, is as follows: The creation of this material *Olam Hazeh* is not a cause for joy or a *Yom Tov*. For **on the contrary**, it is yet another descent in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*; the *Ohr Eloki* clothes itself in yet another *levush*, a *levush* that conceals and hides. It is a darkness doubled and redoubled, to the point where it provides a place not only for the false opinion of *shtei rashuyos* (two powers), but even for the claim of "I and there is none else."

However, when the day of the creation of man arrives—the one to whom was given the power to illuminate **this** world through his *avodah* according to the instructions of the Torah, and furthermore, through his *avodah* in **this** world to elevate **all** the worlds in the entire creation—that is when we establish a day of remembrance for *Maaseh Bereishis*. Man takes upon himself the *Malchus* of the *Ribono shel Olam* to crown Him over all of creation, just as Adam HaRishon did on the day of his creation (*Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer*, ch. 11; *Zohar* I, 221a), and the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* grants man a good and sweet year in both material and spiritual matters.

Wishing you and all your family once again a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of my letter to our friend Mr. Stulman, may he live.

## 251

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5707

To our esteemed friend, the G-d-fearing man, lover of Torah and pursuer of tzedakah, the renowned activist and philanthropist, etc., R' Gershon, may he live, Axelrad,
Valdosta, GA.

Shalom u’vracha!

In the name of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch and in my own name, I wish you and all your family a Shana Tova U’mesuka, and success in all your endeavors.

The precise meaning of **Rosh Hashanah** is the **head** of the year. Our Sages explain that it is not called *techilas* (the beginning) of the year, but *Rosh* (head) of the year, because just as the head directs the entire body, so too must the good resolutions and conduct that one takes upon oneself on Rosh Hashanah direct the entire year.

And this is also our wish: that in the new year, we should all move forward in our spiritual development, in the fulfillment of our duties, and in the practical implementation of all our good thoughts and plans.

We hope this letter finds you in the best of health; we are surprised that we have not heard from you for such a long time.

With blessings for a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 254

B"H, Monday, 26 Tishrei, 5707
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and wise, etc.,
Rabbi A. M. [shlita],

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter with New Year’s greetings, which was received with some delay:

I return my thanks and blessings, and "whoever blesses is blessed" by the Master of Blessings, as it is written, "And I will bless those who bless you." Thus, when Reuven blesses Shimon, Reuven’s portion is actually greater, for Shimon receives a blessing from a flesh-and-blood person, while Reuven receives the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He.

Perhaps it was to equalize their portions that they instituted (and, according to some, obligated—see Rashi, Makkos 23b) that one must greet his fellow specifically by name.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, where you mention the "Book of Redemption and Salvation" (Sefer Geulah v’Yeshuah): If, before the Geulah, one is still in need of *yeshuah* (salvation), then seemingly the phrasing should be "Yeshuah and Geulah." Furthermore, if we interpret *Geulah* in its literal sense—redemption from exile—then the place for a request to be inscribed in this book would be after the other books (though, for the time being, I have not found a reason for the order of the entire *Avinu Malkeinu*, but these five books seem to be a single unit).

Therefore, it seems to me that we should interpret *Geulah* as redemption from the troubles that constantly come upon us, and *Yeshuah* as something that follows—similar to the Amidah prayer, where we say "Redeemer of Israel" and afterwards "Save us and we shall be saved" (see Rashi, Megillah 17b, and the commentary *Iyun Tefillah* on the Amidah in the *Otzar HaTefillos* siddur). Initially, the request is general—for a good life—and then it proceeds to specify: 1) In material matters: *Geulah* and *Yeshuah* (the removal of harm), followed by sustenance and livelihood. 2) In spiritual matters: merits, that the merits should tip the scale (and in this context, one may request that He should "bear and conquer iniquity"), and then forgiveness and pardon, that the sins should be completely erased.

Further points to note regarding this matter:
a) These books are mentioned in the *Yehi Ratzon* recited on Hoshana Rabbah after the books of Tehillim. However, after the "Book of Judgment and Testimony" (Sefer Din v’Heid), we say "Book of the Upright and Perfect" and "Book of the Righteous," and after the "Book of Redemption" (Sefer Geulah), we say "Book of Sustenance and Good Livelihood." In the *Tikkun Tefillah* commentary in the aforementioned siddur, these versions are cited from the Tunis Machzor, etc.

If so, since these changes were not adopted in our siddur, the *Yehi Ratzon* mentioned above should also be adjusted accordingly.

b) Regarding what is written in *Etz Yosef*—that the "Book of Forgiveness and Pardon" corresponds to the Book of Vayikra—aside from the fact that he does not explain why it comes at the end, it is also refuted by the aforementioned *Yehi Ratzon*, which states that after the "Book of Redemption" (which is in Tehillim and corresponds to the Book of Vayikra), we say "Sustenance and Good Livelihood."

With wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 55

B"H, Sunday, 9 Cheshvan, 5707
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Rabbi Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Elul, 5706, I was happy to hear that you arrived safely in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days. I was delighted to learn that you have found a community of anash, may they live, where you will be able to quench your thirst to study Torah and learn the way of Hashem.

Surely, there too, you will endeavor to influence others as well, to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos and to strengthen them in their observance.

It is known from our Sages (Bereishis Rabbah, end of ch. 5) why it is called Eretz (Land)—because it desired (ratzah) to do the will of its Creator. And Yisrael (Israel) is so named because "you have striven (sarisa) with G-d and with men and have prevailed." If so, dwelling in Eretz Yisrael means that one does the will of his Creator, even though this requires struggling against people and also against the forces of nature (for the constellations and angels are the agents that govern it, and therefore the numerical value of "nature" [hateva] is equal to "Elokim," as written in the Shelah, Maseches Pesachim, Drush 3). This is because the atmosphere of Eretz Yisrael imparts wisdom and assists one so that a "spirit of folly" does not enter him (for a person only commits a transgression if a spirit of folly has entered him).

We look forward to hearing good news about you and about your activities in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit.

With best wishes,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

**Chairman of the Executive Committee:** Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch.

## 256

256

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5707
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the *avreich*, the learned, G-d-fearing, etc., the *tamim*
R' M.Y., may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your questions:

1) Regarding the matter of *bitachon* (trust): Is one required to create a *keli* (vessel/means), or is prayer and *bitachon* alone sufficient? I have heard some say that *tzaddikim* do not require a *keli*. If so, it is difficult to understand why Avraham needed the advice of "Say, I pray, that you are my sister."

Answer: It is simple that, in general, one must create a *keli* in addition to *bitachon*. The entire Tanach and the *Midrashim* of our Sages are full of this. The *hishtadlus* (effort) to create a natural *keli* does not contradict the concept of *bitachon* in Hashem, since it was said to him by Hashem his G-d, in Whom he trusts, that He will bless him "in all that he does" specifically—not that he should sit idle (*Sifrei Devarim* 15:18).

From this, two points are understood: a) The *keli* and the cause must be created only because one was commanded to do so. However, if one considers them to be something that is beneficial or harmful in and of itself, this blemishes the quality of *bitachon*. b) Since a person is only commanded regarding what is within his power—for the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not act tyrannically with His creatures—if it is not in his power to create a *keli*, this itself is proof that the *Rachmana* (the Merciful One) has exempted him from it, and this does not weaken the *bitachon* that his request will be fulfilled.

There are still two questions on this matter: a) Why were we commanded to create a *keli*, given that the *keli* itself, on the face of it, neither adds nor detracts? b) What happens if one does not create a *keli*?

Regarding the first question, the reason is explained in *D'rach Chassidecha* (*Mitzvas Tgilchas Metzora K'sheyitaher*, p. 61): Because of a deep intent, the *shefa* (bounty) from above into the world of *Asiyah* is granted specifically through the "garment" of nature. Therefore, man, who is in the image of the Above, must also create a "garment" and engage in a livelihood (*Kuntres U'Maayan*, *Maamar* 25 at length; see *Chovos HaLevavos*, *Shaar HaBitachon*, Ch. 3—cited in *D.H. V'Lo Zachar Sar HaMashkim* 5671—in a different manner, and they can be reconciled. But this is not the place).

b) If one does not create a *keli*, even though it is in his power to do so, regarding this our Sages said (*Shabbos* 32a): "A person should never... say that a miracle will be performed for him; perhaps a miracle will not be performed for him." In that case, not only will his *bitachon* not be fulfilled, but in addition, he will be punished for this, as he is "robbing his own soul" (*D'rach Chassidecha* ibid., and *Chovos HaLevavos* ibid., Ch. 4). And if a miracle *is* performed for him, they deduct from his merits (*Shabbos* ibid.) and he is a burden upon his Creator (*Ramban*, *Shaar HaGemul*, cited in the aforementioned *D.H. V'Lo Zachar*).

Now, regarding *tzaddikim*—even those who are *neshamos* of *Atzilus*, meaning that the *neshamah* clothed in their body is truly of the level of *Atzilus* (*Likkutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, further explanation on the verse *Yonasi* at the end of the chapter)—if the affairs of the world of *Asiyah* and its burdens still distract them, and in the world of *Asiyah*, as mentioned, the *hashpa'ah* (influence) is through a "garment," then they, too, engage in creating a *keli*, for the reason mentioned above. This is not the case for *tzaddikim* whose worldly burdens do not distract them at all from their *dveikus* (cleaving to G-d). Because even when they are engaged in worldly affairs with great intensity, they are in their true *dveikus* just as they are above, literally. Since the world occupies no space for them at all even while they are engaged in it, they do not need to create a *keli*. This is explained at length in *Toras Chaim*, *D.H. Ben Poras Yosef*, and in *D.H. V'Yaasor Yosef* 5656, that the Patriarchs were on the first level, and therefore they were shepherds and lived in seclusion from worldly affairs. Avraham, as mentioned, and Yaakov, because of Esav, utilized various strategies. This is unlike Yosef, who was on the second level, and therefore did not need to create a *keli*; on the contrary, he was punished for it.

Seemingly, one could raise a difficulty regarding the above: In *Toras Chaim* (ibid., Ch. 13) and in *D.H. V'Lo Zachar* 5671, it is asked why Yosef was punished for utilizing strategies to be released, while Yaakov utilized many strategies and was not punished for it. It answers that it is because Yosef was from the level of *Seder Hishtalshelus* and *Tohu* and *Tikkun*, etc. They did not explain the reason as mentioned in this letter. However, there is no room for the difficulty at all, because there it also answers why Yosef did not fear that he might cause a sin, etc., as Yaakov feared. Therefore, it **added** to what was explained there in the previous chapters—that for Yosef, worldly burdens were not distracting—that Yosef is above all the "opposing forces," etc.

—It is worth noting that in *D.H. U'B'Voah Lifnei HaMelech* 5654, it is written: "I saw in the name of one of the greats: One who has a great trouble, G-d forbid, must trust in Hashem. This means he should not pray for it and should not do anything, such as going to the *mikveh* or the like, but only trust in Hashem, etc." This is the concept of silence, which is a great *bitul* (a "strong setting aside")—and it is a wonder.

Also worth noting: There is a livelihood that comes by way of "bread from the earth," and there is a livelihood that comes by way of "bread from the heavens." However, this matter is only partially relevant to the aforementioned topic (see *R' D.H. V'Hayah Ki Tavo* 5666; and what is written in *R' D.H. Ani L'Dodi*—the second one—in *Sefer HaMaamarim*, it can be understood easily).

***

2) In the *Midrash* on the verse "Say, I pray, that you are my sister," it states: "From here we learn that one may slaughter [an animal] for a sick person on *Shabbos*." The *sefarim* explain simply that from the fact that Avraham utilized strategies and did not rely on his *bitachon* in Hashem alone, we learn that even for a sick person, one does not rely on a miracle. You ask for further explanation on this.

You did not cite the location of the *Midrash* or the commentaries, for "the words of the wise make one wise," as the aforementioned explanation is not understood. If so, the *Midrash* should have said: "From here we learn that one does not rely on a miracle." See *Zohar Chadash*, Part 2a, that on the contrary, Avraham *did* rely on a miracle, and that is why he went down to Egypt. In *Zohar Chadash* 52a, it explains that he saw an angel walking before Sarah and not before him; he said, "She is protected, but I am not protected, and therefore I said, 'Say, I pray, that you are my sister,' etc."*

Seemingly, one could explain the *Midrash* by saying that from the fact that Avraham said that **Sarah** should say "you are my sister" for the sake of **Avraham's** rescue, we learn that it is permitted to commit a **prohibition** for the sake of saving **one's fellow.**

However, even according to this, it is not resolved, for it should have said: "From here we learn that one may desecrate the *Shabbos* for a sick person." Why did it specifically choose "slaughtering"? To resolve this: The well-known difficulty is, to sharpen the point**, how did Avraham know that the Egyptians would kill him and transgress the prohibition of bloodshed in order not to transgress the prohibition of forbidden relations with a married woman, which is why he said "Say, I pray," etc.? One of the answers is that when they kill him, they will only commit the transgression once, whereas if they take Sarah while Avraham is still alive, then with every act of intimacy, they transgress the prohibition of *gilui arayos*. The *Midrash* learns from this that in such a case for a sick person, one may slaughter for a sick person on *Shabbos*, and we do not say "we will feed him *neveilah* (non-kosher meat)." The reason is along the lines of the above: with *neveilah*, one transgresses for every *kezayis* (olive-sized portion), whereas with slaughtering, one only commits one prohibition (*Ran*, cited in *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, Laws of *Shabbos*, Ch. 328, Sec. 16).

One might ask: How does the *Midrash* know that one may slaughter for a sick person—which is a capital prohibition—once, and we do not feed him *neveilah*—which is a prohibition of a negative commandment—many times? In the incident of Avraham—from which we want to learn—both *gilui arayos* and bloodshed carry the same penalty of death.

The proof can be explained: Even regarding Avraham—how did he know they would kill him and transgress bloodshed, a capital prohibition, once, in order to avoid the **capital** prohibition of *gilui arayos*? He could have had relations with her in an unnatural way, which is also pleasurable (see *Rashi* on *Sanhedrin* 66b), and for that one is not executed (*Sanhedrin* 58b). One must conclude that since even in an unnatural way it is a repulsive act (see *Tosafos* on *Sanhedrin* 57b), and it is not done even among the nations of the world, for they restrained themselves from forbidden relations due to the Flood (*Bereishis Rabbah*, end of Ch. 6; and the difficulty of the *Ramban* in *Bereishis* 34:7, see the commentary of *Maharzu* there), they certainly would have killed him. For it is better to transgress a severe prohibition once than to transgress a light prohibition many times. Therefore, he said "Say, I pray," etc., and we correctly learn that one may slaughter for a sick person, etc.

Alternatively: If the Egyptians had taken her by force and he could not prevent them, this falls under the category of *ya'ush* (despair) and the law of robbers (*Bava Kamma* 114a). It could be said that through this she becomes divorced, for among the sons of Noach, they do not have divorce by document, but rather by separating from one another (*Rambam*, *Melachim*, Ch. 9, Law 8). If so, she is no longer a married woman, except that the act is repulsive, etc., as mentioned above.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

I have just seen in *Torah Shleimah*, *Parshas Lech Lecha*, Item 145, that it cites the aforementioned *Midrash* in the name of *Midrash Peliah* and explains it as above, based on the reasoning of the *Ran*. However, it did not address the difficulty that in Avraham's case the prohibitions are equal, unlike the case of *neveilah* and slaughtering.

***

\*) It discusses this in the name of *Shem Mishmuel*, *Parshas Vayeira* (by the Holy Rebbe of Sochatchov).

\*\*) According to the simple meaning of the verse: "And they will say, 'She is his wife,' and they will kill me," because they would not expect that I would agree to give you to them, as explained by the *Sforno*.

257

B"H, 1st Day of Chanukah, 5707

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, wise and understanding, etc.,
Rabbi R. A. A. HaKohen, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter dated Sunday, Parshas Vayeishev, in due time. Although I did not know what to advise regarding it, I have nevertheless fulfilled your request.

And to conclude with a matter of Chanukah:

The Greeks championed the name of "intellect," as is well known in history. Through this, they sought to "make them forget Your Torah"—that the Torah is Yours, for had the Torah not been given, we would have learned modesty, etc. (Eruvin 100b)—and "to force them to stray from the statutes of Your will"—specifically *chukim* (statutes). This is also why they specifically defiled all the oils, for *tumah* (ritual impurity) is a decree of the King, not something based on human logic (Rambam, end of Hilchos Mikvaos).

The reason they were able to defile all the oils (the intellect of holiness, the intellect of Bnei Yisrael) is because when one conducts oneself based on intellect alone—even the intellect of the *nefesh ha'elokis*—there is room for error (and consequently, for sin thereafter). Furthermore, it can even mislead a person into thinking that by doing so, he is fulfilling what he was commanded, and is even fulfilling *chukim* and decrees that are beyond intellect. As is known, this was the sin of Shaul, who spared the best of the [spoils] to sacrifice to Hashem, and said, "I have fulfilled the word of Hashem" (Shmuel I, 15).

This is why we are commanded to judge a true judgment **to its truth**. Tosafos (Megillah 15b) notes the precision here, even though the witnesses are testifying. This can be explained based on the above: even though testimony is a decree of the King (Bava Basra 159a) and seemingly there is no room for suspicion—especially if we say that testimony is a *din* (a legal status) rather than a *birur* (a clarification of fact), and therefore the matter does not "touch" the judge because the Torah is the one decreeing—nevertheless, one must investigate, because the hand of his own intellect is also involved. It may be that this is the connection to the matters in the Megillah (ibid.) regarding being a "crown" (a *makif* that is above comprehension; see Hilchos Teshuvah 8:2 regarding the precision of the language) for one who "judges his inclination," who judges a true judgment to its truth, who overcomes his inclination, and afterwards—when they debate the "war of Torah."

Therefore, the war against the Greeks was also above intellect (for they were weak against the mighty, etc.), possible only through *mesiras nefesh* and the strength of the will that is above intellect. This is why for the seven days—the seven days of construction, the seven days of Creation—there was no oil, because they had defiled it. But for the first day, the power of the will and *mesiras nefesh* that is above the division of levels, there was oil (similar to what is explained regarding why *Chag HaShavuos* is one day, while *Chag HaMatzos* and *Chag HaSukkos* are seven days—in the *hosafos* to *Torah Or*, end of Parshas Yisro).

With best wishes and the blessing of Chanukah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 258

258

B"H, Thursday, 26 Kislev, 5707.

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, distinguished and elevated, who conducts his business with faith,
Rabbi Y. Katz, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

According to your letter, the Sifrei HaMaamarim were sent to you in a separate package, as well as the Sicha of 10 Kislev and the Chanukah story. I am sure you have received everything in time.

Knowing your desire to study the Sichos of Sukkos that you attended, I am enclosing my copy. As you will see, it is unedited; not knowing when the editing will take place, I do not wish to delay until then. I am sure you will send it back to me **as soon as possible.**

I wish to be in order regarding the commandment "Do not be to him as a creditor," especially since you write that you are currently tied up. However, I hope and **wish to be certain** that, taking into account the difficult situation of the post-war period (and especially since more than two months have passed since the printer delivered the Sefer HaMaamarim), you will do everything you can at the first opportunity to handle this as soon as possible.

To conclude with a matter of Chanukah:

Regarding Chanukah, it is related in the Midrash (Yalkut Shimoni, Melachim 1, Remez 184) that the Mishkan (in the desert) was completed on **25 Kislev**, but the Almighty commanded that they wait to erect it until the month of Nissan. The "payment" for that day came 1,200 years later—with the celebration of Chanukah. Despite all this, the Jews are praised for having given their donations for the Mishkan over two days: 11-12 **Tishrei**. In truth, what was the benefit of this, given that afterwards there was no rush at all to erect the Mishkan? Rather, we learn from this: a) how precious alacrity is, and b) that every effort of a Jew in a matter of a mitzvah bears its fruits, even if it is not apparent for the time being.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

## 259

259

B”H, 3rd of Parshas Vayechi Yaakov B’Eretz Mitzrayim, 5707

To the honorable, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R’ Y. Goldstein,

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter of 11 Kislev, bearing the good news that you have established regular, public study groups, has been received. As you requested, we have sent several of our publications to your name in a separate package. Please confirm receipt. You should arrange for them to be used by many people, whether by placing them in a location where many gather (a shul, a reading room, or the like), or by lending them out with the condition that they be returned so they may be lent to another. Whoever enables the many to merit, the merit of the many depends upon him.

We do not have copies of the Tanya, as they are out of stock and have been sold. You should contact Tel Aviv directly, as I believe they may still have a number of copies.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote in his letter of 14 Sivan 5741 (which I copied in *Hayom Yom*, p. 12) that when the Tzemach Tzedek was a child and was learning the verse, "And Yaakov lived in the land of Egypt seventeen years," his teacher translated it for him—based on the commentary of the *Baal HaTurim*—as, "Yaakov Avinu lived his seventeen best years in Egypt." When he came home from *cheder*, he asked his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe: "How can it be that for Yaakov Avinu, the choicest of the Patriarchs, the choicest years of his life were the seventeen years he lived in the land of Egypt, the 'nakedness of the land'?"

The Alter Rebbe answered him: "It is written, 'And he sent Yehudah before him to Yosef, to direct him to Goshen.' The Midrash states—as cited by Rashi—that Rabbi Nechemiah said: 'To establish a house of study for him, so that Torah would be there and the tribes would be occupied with Torah.' When one learns Torah, one becomes closer to the Almighty, B”H, and thus, even in Egypt, it was *Vayechi*—he lived."

One may add a nuance here: why was it specifically Yehudah who was sent? It may be explained as follows: The Alter Rebbe’s interpretation—based on the *Baal HaTurim*—that "Goshen" means "closer to the Almighty, B”H," achieved through the study of Torah, is still not fully understood. It is obvious that even while in Eretz Yisrael, Yaakov was an elder sitting in the *yeshivah*, just like the other Patriarchs (though the verse informs us that **even** in Egypt this was the case; see *Yoma* 28b). Why, then, are his years in Egypt specifically considered the **choicest** of his years? If it is because of the abundance of sparks that were specifically in Egypt (see *Torah Or*, *Va’era*, the *maamar* beginning *Vayomer... Vayivla Mateh*; and see the *maamar* in Parshas *Bo* beginning *Be’etzem*), those were not clarified until much later, after that entire generation had passed. Furthermore, the Alter Rebbe’s language implies that it depends on the study of Torah, not on the clarification of the sparks. And if one were to say that this is the way of Torah—that one must live a life of hardship and then "happy are you and it is good for you"—that refers to physical pleasures (as it says, "a morsel of bread with salt," etc.), yet in this regard, they actually ate the "fat of the land" in Egypt, which we do not find they did while in the land of Canaan.

However, were it not for this, Egypt is the "nakedness of the land," whereas Eretz Yisrael—from which they had departed—has an atmosphere that makes one wise in the study of Torah (*Bava Basra* 158b; it is somewhat forced to say that the atmosphere only makes one wise once the Jewish people entered the land, similar to the Sages' statement in *Megillah* 14a).

Therefore, he sent Yehudah specifically: the acceptance of the yoke of a simple servant, who possesses *taanug* even in his service of *kabbalas ol*, because the *taanug* of the Master is his own *taanug* (see *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, ch. 19; the *maamar* beginning *Acharei D’a Tielchu* 5666, and elsewhere). The Master’s *taanug* in this is most profound specifically through the study of Torah in Egypt. For in the matter of the work of *birurim* (clarification), there is a place **in the intellect** for why the descent to Egypt was necessary, as mentioned above. This is not the case with the study of Torah, which seemingly contradicts the intellect—even the intellect of the *neshamah*—but is rather a profound counsel of the Master to reveal the *Atzmus* (the Essence; *Ohr Torah*, the *maamar* beginning *Yadoa Teda*). Through the attribute of Yehudah, even the servant experiences a profound and essential *taanug* in this. Therefore, through the study of Torah specifically in Egypt, these became the choicest of his years.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

It is a great wonder that you do not mention her well-being or health, nor whether the anash located there are assisting her as much as they can with all that she requires (and it goes without saying that I must cover the expenses), etc. I am certain you will provide details in your next letter.

As you requested, several of our publications have been sent to you in a separate package. Please be kind enough to confirm receipt. You should arrange for them to be used by many people, whether by placing them in a location where many gather (a shul, a reading room, or the like) or by lending them out with the condition that they be returned so they can be lent to someone else. Whoever brings merit to the public, the merit of the public depends upon him.

I have heard that in your current location there are Chabad seforim that were printed in Hungary, Czechoslovakia, etc., during the war or shortly thereafter (perhaps by Rabbi Rapaport?). Please be kind enough to inform me and send a copy of each of these seforim here, addressed to the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch or Kehot. (I believe your father was involved in this when he was in P.B.) This, too, is being sent to you, and please follow the aforementioned instructions regarding its use. Please be kind enough to confirm receipt of all the packages.

I await your letter bringing good news regarding my mother, may she live and be well, as soon as possible. See the Targum Yonasan on the verse "Naftali is a hind let loose" (Bereishis 49:21). The Midrash, as cited in the sefer Tzeror HaMor, explains that "Naftali is a hind let loose" refers to Naftali, who was a man of peace, and his father and brothers made him a messenger to bring tidings of peace. There is a connection between Naftali, speed, and good tidings, based on what is explained in Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek: that Naftali is related to the term for prayer and connection from above to below, and when one proceeds with speed, it is only good and kindness, as is known regarding the almonds of Aharon (Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Korach).

With best wishes for all that is good.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 264

264

By the grace of Hashem, Thursday, 23 Shevat, 5707

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., the *tamim*... may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your inquiry, the content of which is:

1) I have found a dispute regarding the matter of *zivugim* (matrimonial pairings). According to the philosophers, there is free choice in this, while according to the *mekubalim*, it is a matter of divine decree. I ask how the teaching of Chassidus resolves this.

2) It is implied in many places in *Chassidus* that this matter is a decree. If so, what is the function of *hishtadlus* (effort) in this? Is it merely creating a vessel and clothing it in nature?

You did not specify in your letter the sources where you found the above, nor did you mention the distinctions that exist within each of these two schools of thought themselves. Furthermore, your first question touches upon *halacha l'maaseh* (practical law), and the ruling has already been established by the *poskim*.

I will present the various approaches to this matter, and through this, the above will be clarified.

***

Regarding the matter of *zivugim*—whether there is complete free choice, partial choice, or none at all—we find several distinctions and approaches. In general, they are founded upon and dependent on how one interprets the words of our Sages in *Moed Katan* (18b), *Sotah* (2a), *Sanhedrin* (22a), *Bava Basra* (12b), *Bereishis Rabbah* (beginning of ch. 68), *Zohar Chadash* (91b, 207b, 229a), *Zohar Chadash* (170b), *Zohar Chadash* (283b), and others (some cite *Midrash Tehillim*, but it is not at hand for me to examine).

***

The approaches to this are:

1) *Bas Kol* (a heavenly voice) decrees "the daughter of so-and-so to so-and-so," and the prayers of another are of no avail, except that the other may marry her for a short time, but he will not consummate the marriage, and afterwards he divorces her or dies, and she marries the one for whom she was decreed (*Sefer Chassidim*, sec. 383). Although *Sefer Chassidim* does not specify which *zivug* he is speaking of, in order to avoid increasing the contradiction between the *sugya* in *Moed Katan* and *Sotah*, one can say he refers specifically to the first *zivug*.

2) The prayer of another is effective so that he may marry and consummate the marriage, but in the end, she is divorced or her husband dies, and she marries her true partner (*ibid.*, according to the first interpretation of Azulai*, and the *Ran* in *Moed Katan*).

3) *Bas Kol* decrees, but prayer can annul the decree entirely (*Rashi* on the *Rif* in *Moed Katan*, since he does not explain that it is only for a time; *Tosafos* in *Sanhedrin* 22a, since he compares it to the changing of a fetus from male to female, which is a total change. This is also the opinion of the *Tzemach Tzedek* in his *Chiddushim* on *Shas Moed Katan*).

4) There is free choice to marry or not, but if one chooses to marry, it is decreed by *Bas Kol* that it will be the daughter of so-and-so. Another, through prayers, can preempt him, but their union will not endure, as in the second approach (*Tashbetz*, Vol. 2, sec. 1).

5) The *Bas Kol* going forth is not a matter of decree, but merely an inclination of nature. By the nature of his creation, it is close and easy for him to choose the daughter of so-and-so due to her nature, but the choice remains free (*this is the opinion of the Rambam at the beginning of ch. 8 of his Eight Chapters; see also his Responsa, sec. 159*).

According to this interpretation, that "the daughter of so-and-so to so-and-so" is because of their natural affinity, this must apply to both the first and second *zivug*. Why, then, did our Sages say that the second *zivug* is according to his deeds? One can say that by nature, there should be a *Bas Kol* for the second *zivug* as well, but because of the matter of reward and punishment, nature is overridden, and they are paired only according to his deeds (this can be read into the language of the *Rambam* in his responsum cited in the *Tashbetz*). However, initially, even for the second *zivug*, one must decide **by his own choice** if he desires to marry, for in this there is no compulsion from Above, as it is a matter of *mitzvah*—both for the first *zivug* and even if he has already fulfilled the *mitzvah* of *pru u'rvu* (procreation), for "it is not good for man to be alone" (*Yevamos* 61b).

6) **All** *zivugim* are according to a person's deeds. When our Sages say that a *Bas Kol* goes forth for the first *zivug*, they refer to the joining of matter and form, the body and the soul (*Akeidah*, Gate 8 and 102).

7) According to what is explained in the writings of the *AriZal* (partially brought in *Yaavetz* to *Sotah* 2a), the **first** time the soul comes into the world, a *Bas Kol* goes forth saying, "The daughter of so-and-so to so-and-so." When the time for taking her arrives—[and until then, she may be the wife of another, as with Uriah and Bas-Sheva (*Zohar Chadash* 73b)]—she is provided to him in an instant without toil or trouble. However, sometimes he does not merit this, and then he does not take his true partner—[and another who has no partner can preempt him through prayer (*Zohar Chadash* 91b, 229a, cited in *Midrash Talpiyos*, entry *Zivug*)]. However, a woman is provided to him according to his deeds. Sometimes his soul is exchanged (from bad to good or vice versa), and he loses his partner and takes another, because he is no longer the same person. Sometimes he is reincarnated in order to take his partner, or he is reincarnated for other reasons, and he has many merits that cause his partner to be reincarnated with him. But since he sinned and needed to be reincarnated, he has accusers who prevent him from that *zivug*, and it is as difficult to pair them as the splitting of the Red Sea (*Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 8, 20; *Sefer HaGilgulim*, ch. 13, 57; *Sefer HaLikutim*, *Tehillim* 48). If his partner was not reincarnated, they pair him with a reincarnated soul who also has no partner; therefore, it is difficult to pair them because they are different in nature (*Sefer HaLikutim*, *Parshas Vayeitzei*). However, she must be close to him in terms of their root (*Sefer HaGilgulim*, *ibid.*). Some say that if the aforementioned are not reincarnated, he takes a wife according to his *hishtadlus*, in the secret of "and you shall snatch for yourselves from the vineyards, each man his wife" (*Bnei Aharon* on *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 8, in the name of the elders who heard it in the name of the *AriZal*).

***

What is derived from **all** the above approaches is that in **all** *zivugim*, another can preempt him. The *halacha* is decided **practically** that in any case, one may betroth women during *Chol HaMoed* for this reason, and consequently, there is room for *hishtadlus*.

***

In the end of *Ohr HaTorah* by the *Tzemach Tzedek*, he explains the words of our Sages in *Bereishis Rabbah* (beginning of ch. 68) that a man's *zivug* is from Hashem in two ways. The first way, one can say—though the language is not clear to me—is that there is choice as to whether to marry, but who the partner is, is determined from Above, similar to what is written in the *Tashbetz* mentioned above. He explains the second way as being like the children, life, and sustenance, which depend on *mazal* (fortune) and not on *zchus* (merit/deeds). If so, here too there is room for *hishtadlus*, just as with children, life, and sustenance; for if his *mazal* is not as it should be, G-d forbid, then through great merit, the *mazal* is changed (*Tosafos* s.v. *Ein*, *Shabbos* 156a). Even with good *mazal*, action is required (see *Responsa Chasam Sofer*, *Yoreh Deah*, sec. 52) and merit, as explained in *Biurei HaZohar*, end of *Parshas Vayeira*. It is worth noting additional explanations on this in *Chassidus* in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, *Mitzvas Tgilachas Metzora*, *Mayim Rabim*, p. 104 and onwards, end of *Chanoch L'naar* (there is a typo there, "v'kacha" should be "mayim rabim"), and elsewhere.

***

Regarding *avodah*, the matter of the first *zivug* and second *zivug* and their distinction is explained in the *maamar* "Anchi" of 5672, *Ais'ar*. The general explanation is that the first *zivug* from Above is the concept of *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from Above) that precedes *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below)—the first redemption. The second *zivug* according to his deeds is *is'arusa d'leila* that comes after *is'arusa d'letata*—the final redemption.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate redemption,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

***

*From the secretariat's copy.

*) However, in the *Sefer Chassidim* manuscript, Parma edition, *Mekitzei Nirdamim*, sec. 868, it is proven like the second interpretation of Azulai, which is the first approach mentioned above.

## 265

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5707

To the honorable, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Ch. Havlin, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters:

1) Many thanks for your efforts regarding the certificate for my mother, may she live. I have conveyed the content of your response to the Rebbe, may he live. In the meantime, a doubt has arisen for me regarding her age, etc., due to various discrepancies, and so forth. I am awaiting clarification, after which I will proceed with this and, naturally, inform you.

2) Regarding the deed of sale for the house and property in Chevron: among the documents you sent, there is only a deed in the name of the Rebbe, the Rebbe Rayatz’s predecessor. Since a deed was surely drawn up later in the name of the Rebbe, may he live, I have been instructed to ask you to search for it, keep an official photograph of it for yourself, and send the original document to the Rebbe, may he live.

3) Some time ago, I instructed that you be sent—as a contributor and participant in our work, the work of the Melach and Kehot—the following: *Bad Kodesh*, the *Sefarim* of the Tzemach Tzedek, the supplement to *Derech Mitzvotecha* by the Tzemach Tzedek, and the *Maamar* for 13 Shevat. Please acknowledge receipt.

4) The sale of the Tzemach Tzedek’s *Sefarim* here was entrusted to Mr. Goldman, and he has also sent them to Eretz Yisrael; therefore, we do not send them to buyers there. Nevertheless, since you have repeated your request regarding sending the Tzemach Tzedek to Rabbi Y. Orinstein, I have, as an exception, ordered one set to be purchased here at the lowest price (15 shekel) and sent to him. Surely you will confirm receipt.

5) Regarding *Yalkut Shimoni* and *Keren Orah*, the publisher says he is already in direct contact with you.

6) Copies of the letters of Rabbi Avraham of Kalisk have been received thus far only once, and addressed to the Rebbe, may he live.

7) In the newspaper *HaMeishar* of 20 Adar Rishon 5706, there was an article regarding the father of the Alter Rebbe. Is it possible to obtain this article? What is the nature of the author of the article?

8) I saw in the library of the Rebbe, may he live, a book titled *Toldos Mishpachat HaRav MiLiadi* by Mr. M. S. Slonim. It contains several typographical errors and missing details. Who is the author of this book, and what is his nature?

9) It has been a long time since I wrote to the students of Toras Emes (Cohen, Weber, etc.), to Rabbi M. R. A. L. Shapiro, and to Rabbi D. Shapiro (author of the book *Bnei Tzion*), and I have not received confirmation of the receipt of these letters.

10) To conclude with a matter of Torah:

As I am currently preparing for print the *Maamarim* of the Rebbe, may he live, with the addition of references and citations, I came across the standard *Maamar* in *Chassidus* regarding "the *pnimiyus* of Abba is the *pnimiyus* of Atik."* The source for this is noted in *Likutei Torah*, *Vayikra*, in the *dih* "Shos Asis," Chapter 3, where he writes that this is necessitated by *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Krias Shema*, Chapter 15. Seemingly, this requires further study, for there—as well as in *Shaar HaKavanos*, *Krias Shema*, Discourse 2—it is explicitly written that it is the *chitzoniyus* of Atik.

Perhaps it can be explained based on what is written there, and also in *Remez* to *Zohar* Vol. 3 (104b), which is cited in *Likutei Torah* there: that the *pnimiyus* of Abba is considered like the light of Atik that is **within Arich**. Now, in Arich Anpin, only the *zayin tachtonot* (lower seven) are enclothed, while the *gimel rishonot* (upper three) remain revealed (*Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Arich Anpin*, Chapter 1, and elsewhere). The *Chabad* of Arich Anpin clothe the *Chagat* of Atik, and the *zayin tachtonot*—which later clothe in *Chochma* and *Binah* (for from the *Binah* of Arich Anpin, *ketarim* are made for *Abba* and *Imma*)—clothe the *Nehi* of Atik. Now, *Chagat* in relation to *Nehi* is called *pnimiyus*, and in relation to the *gimel rishonot* it is *chitzoniyus*. In the *Krias Shema* of the morning, which is the subject of *Pri Etz Chaim* there, we draw from the *Nehi* of Atik through the *chitzoniyus* of *Abba* and *Imma*. The *pnimiyus* of *Abba* and *Imma* is the *Chagat* of Atik, and even though *Pri Etz Chaim* calls this the *chitzoniyus* of Atik, it is called (in the glosses of the RNS, etc., cited in *Likutei Torah* there and in the *Maamarim* of *Chassidus*) the *pnimiyus* of Atik in relation to the *Nehi* of Atik. Note also the *Ipeh Shleimah* on *Otzrot Chaim*, *Atik*, Chapter 4, subsection 7. All of this aligns with what is written in the *Hemshech* of 5666, sections 12-13, in the explanation of the concept that the *pnimiyus* of Abba is the *pnimiyus* of Atik—that all of this is *taanug hamurkav* (compound pleasure), but *taanug hapashut* (simple pleasure) that is not felt is not the *pnimiyus* of Abba. See this concept also in *Shaar HaYichud*, Chapter 23 and onwards.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

266

B"H, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5707

To the Committee of the "Beis Rivkah" School for Girls
Paris

Greetings and blessings!

By order of the Rebbe, *shlita*, we have registered the Beis Rivkah school in Paris into the network of schools under our administration.

We are sending you, in a separate package, the standard curriculum for Beis Rivkah schools. If you find it necessary to implement any changes to the curriculum for the Beis Rivkah school in Paris in accordance with local conditions, please inform us of your proposal regarding this.

The pronunciation used in studies at Beis Rivkah schools is Ashkenazic.

We are enclosing a questionnaire; please complete it and send it back to us.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, stated (*Taanis 29a*): "When Adar enters, we increase in joy," which is on account of the days of Purim. Now, the essential theme of Purim, and especially according to what is explained in *Chassidus*, is that "they fulfilled what they had already accepted" (*Shabbos 88a*) at the Giving of the Torah. Therefore, just as the Giving of the Torah was dependent on the fact that the women were the first to agree to accept it, as our Sages, of blessed memory, stated (*Shemos Rabbah 28:2*), so too, the essential miracle of Purim was also through women, as the Rashbam writes (*Tosafos, s.v. "She-af," Megillah 4a*; and see the *Rashash* there for a resolution of the difficulties).

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem M. Schneerson**

From the secretariat copy.

267

1 Adar, 5707

To the esteemed and distinguished Dr. A. Hillman, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Cheshvan:

I have read it once and twice, but I cannot agree with the classification of types that you propose, as it does not align with the perspective of religion and Halacha in general, and with the words of Tanya, Chapter 32, in particular.

In Halacha, the **primary** "touchstone" is the **motive** and manner in which the transgression is committed—whether it is done out of appetite and as a temporary lapse, or out of spite and as a permanent state—rather than the essence of the transgression itself.

An example from our own time: One who speaks the truth that there is one single G-d (and consequently, the speaker **fulfills** the Torah and mitzvos), but says that He is not the sole First Cause, for there is a primordial, eternal matter from which He created the world—this person is a *min*, equivalent to an idolater (though this is a difficult point, as the *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part II, Chapter 26, implies that this is not dualism). Yet, in common parlance, he is not called a *meshumad*. A lesser offender, though one who is called a *meshumad*, is one who registered himself as a non-Jew, G-d forbid, **out of appetite**, and subsequently lived a life of **licentiousness out of appetite**, because there is no one to rebuke him and correct his ways. For the sources on this, see Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3, the commentaries there, and elsewhere, as I mentioned in my first letter.

Another example: One who abandons the permitted and eats the forbidden may be lent money at interest. One who was taken captive as an infant among the non-Jews and knows **nothing** of the Torah of Israel may not be lent money at interest (*Yoreh Deah*, sec. 159). (Those who disagree do so for secondary reasons.)

Regarding what you wrote about the Tanya: If one must use the concepts in your letter and divide them into exactly three types, the division would be:
a) Those whom it is a mitzvah to love, and there is no hatred there at all (those who fulfill Torah and mitzvos, and secular Jews who do not fall into category 'c' and are not at all close to him, to the point that there is no room for the mitzvah of "you shall surely rebuke").
b) Those for whom there must be both hatred and love (those who are close to him, whom he has rebuked, and who do not repent).
c) Hatred only (minim and apikorsim, as their nature is explained in the Rambam there and elsewhere).

The general distinction between the secular Jews in category 'a' and category 'c' is: out of appetite versus out of spite. That is to say, all who fall into category 'c' are those who act "out of spite" (see the *Bach*, *Yoreh Deah*, end of the aforementioned section; *Radak*, *Beis Cheder*; *Responsa Maharash Halevi*, *Yoreh Deah*, sec. 29).

(Regarding what is written in Rambam there, Halacha 7, "A *mumar* to the entire Torah... at a time when they decree persecution..."—the *Or Sameach* has already pointed to *Rashi*, *Avodah Zarah* 54a, and *Rashi* there concludes: "After he sees that the hand of Israel is low, **his heart** inclines toward idolatry." This is a difficult point in light of what is written in the *Lechem Mishneh* there. Similarly, what is written in *Yoreh Deah*, end of section 158, in the *Hagah*: "Mumarim..."—this refers to *mumarim* **in general**, and their status still requires clarification; see *Tosafos*, s.v. "Ani," *Avodah Zarah* 26b).

I will now turn to the proofs you brought in your letter.

a) Regarding category 'c', the Tanya says they have no portion in the G-d of Israel. Based on the above, it is understood that not everyone called a *meshumad* **in common parlance** is included in this category, and not everyone included in this category is currently called a *meshumad*. See Rambam there: "The *minim*... one who says He is not the sole First Cause... *apikorsim*... one who denies the prophecy of Moses our teacher... those who deny the Torah, saying the Torah is not from Hashem, even one verse." All of these would not be called *meshumadim* today.

b) The Tanya cites the beginning of Chapter 16 in *Shabbos*, which speaks of "those who alienate themselves." Rabbi Tarfon and Rabbi Ishmael are speaking there of the Christians of their time—that is, the early Christians (see *Aruch HaShalem*, entry *On*; *Bei Avidan*, where what was omitted by the censor is brought, and it is proven as above). This sect at that time did not wish to separate from the people of Israel; on the contrary, they spoke in their praise (and until Saul of Tarsus came, they did not even want to speak with the non-Jews). They considered themselves part of the Jewish people in all matters, followed their customs, including the study of Torah and the observance of the vast majority of mitzvos, and they disparaged the faith of the idolaters—that is, the ruling religion of that time, as is known. See in *Shabbos* at the end of the passage there: "I have not come to subtract from the Torah of Moses..." It is just that they had an element of idolatry (which is a matter for further study) and they mocked the unity of our Sages (see the omissions of the Shas, also brought in *Otzar Yisrael*, entry *Yeshu*). That is to say, they were not *meshumadim* as we define that word **now**, but rather secular Jews, transgressors, *minim*.

c) The *minim* in Shas *Shabbos* there refer to the Christians—this is true, as stated above. But: 1) The Christians of that time do not fit the concept of *meshumadim* of our time, as stated above. 2) If our Rebbe had interpreted "minim" in Shas (*Shabbos* there) as "*meshumadim*," he would have written "meshumadim" or "mumarim" or "those who converted to the religion of the Ishmaelites" or similar terms common in such cases due to the censorship, and he would not have used a word that is defined in many places in halachic literature in a way that is **not** suited to that meaning. 3) Our Rebbe in Tanya also adds *apikorsim*, so it must be that he is speaking, at the very least, of **two** categories.

d) In *Choshen Mishpat* 575:20: "*Apikorsim* from Israel, and they are **meshumadim**—and not idolaters." I do not know what proof this is, and what difference it makes **for our purposes**, since it continues there: "or one who performs transgressions out of spite, even if he ate *neveilah* or wore *shaatnez* out of spite." It is also simple that in Shas and the *Rishonim*, a *meshumad* in the specific sense is one who worships idols, even if in **all** other matters he is not separated from the Jewish people at all. (However, when they began to force and decree—not regarding idolatry per se, but regarding joining the ruling religion and becoming one of the "people of the land"—the content of the word "*meshumad*" changed little by little, until the most prominent part remained: that he separates from the Jewish people, lives only in the environment of the "people of the land," does not feel or suffer the troubles of Israel, etc.). Even regarding this, there are those who are doubtful; see *Aruch HaShalem*, entry *Mad* 3 and entry *Meshumad*.

*Be'er HaGolah* in *Choshen Mishpat* 575, letter *Pei*, states: "The language of the Rambam there, Chapter 4, Halacha 5, is from the *Baraisa*, Chapter 2 of *Avodah Zarah* 26b, and the passage of the Gemara there. There are other versions in the *Beis Yosef*, and I have copied it in *Yoreh Deah*, sec. 159, and see there," end of quote.

e) In the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Hilchos Metzi'ah U'Pikadon*, section 37: "The **apikorsim** are those who deny the Torah," and in *Hilchos Nizkei Guf V'Nefesh*, section 10: "The **minim** from Israel are those who deny the Torah." It seems your intent is that if so, there is proof that there is no distinction between a *min* and an *apikorus*. Yet, it is simple that in *Hilchos Nizkei Guf V'Nefesh* there is a printing error, and it should say: "The *apikorsim*," just as it is written in *Hilchos Metzi'ah U'Pikadon* and in all the places cited as sources for the law in *Hilchos Nizkei Guf V'Nefesh*. This is also necessitated by the style of the paragraph itself: "And he ate the forbidden out of spite, this is a **min**, and the **minim** from Israel are..."—the repetition of the word is not understood. But it is simple that if it should read as above, "this is a *min*, and the *apikorsim* from Israel," it is also necessitated by the *Kuntres Acharon* in that paragraph, which writes that this is not similar to the **apikorus** mentioned here.

f) Regarding the "meshumad" in Shas and the corruptions of the censor in this regard, see *Aruch HaShalem*, entry *Meshumad*, as stated above.

g) Regarding the book (in English) on Bereishis: It is a mixture of good and errors. It contains several explanations and ideas that are **surprising** in their novelty, but also matters that are not true. The author did not agree to the changes. Since the good outweighs the bad, and the main point—that in the current situation here, in the field of missionary propaganda (a plague of the state here), it can serve as a good tool against them—it was decided to publish it. Over the years that have passed since then, the book has influenced various circles to bring them closer to a love of Torah and Judaism and to awaken in them a desire to deepen their study of Torah. The book is available for sale from its author, and its price is seven dollars. If you wish to purchase it, let me know and I will instruct that it be sent to you.

With wishes for all that is good, and with regards to your family, may they live,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 260

4 Tammuz, 5707

To the esteemed Anash, G-d-fearing and G-d-loving, etc., in the city of Paris,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

Thank G-d, we arrived here safely. In due time, I sent a telegram regarding the address on Rue Yves Kermes, and it is strange that the telegram was returned with the claim that there is no such street in their camp!

1) Naturally, I delivered the *pidyon nefesh* to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, as well as what pertains to the *maamad*. However, it has been a week or more that we have been waiting to receive the list, as well as your letter informing us about the committee and its good works, and as of now—nothing! If this is how it is at the beginning of the matter, "what will be" when the matter grows old? My confidence is strong that you will not delay your letter any further and will inform us as soon as possible regarding your activities thus far, regarding the expansion of the committee’s involvement beyond the four cubits of the Lubavitcher group as discussed before I left (which is a primary matter, both physically and spiritually), and the plan of work for the future.

Enclosed here is a letter pertaining to the *maamad*.

2) Enclosed here is the form of the questionnaire for writing the letters in the Sefer Torah for the *Kabbalas Pnei Moshiach*. All those who wish to participate, they and their households, should prepare a general list answering all the questions and indicating the amount of participation (and I have already announced that this is only so that each person has a share in the expenses; anyone who wishes to add more, in my opinion, should add it to the *maamad* fund), and you will inform them afterward which letters fell to their lot.

3) Enclosed is a form for participation in the *Mishnayos* society by heart, along with some letters pertaining to this. If you prepare a list of those who wish to participate in this, you should also hold a lottery for them and inform them of their portions.

Rabbi Friedman from the synagogue at 25 requested that you also include congregants from the synagogue in this society, and you should certainly ask him about this now and encourage the expansion of the matter.

4) Enclosed here is a form for establishing or expanding *Tehillim* societies. Those who wish to join should provide their names, etc., according to what is explained in the form.

In the collection of letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita* (the second volume), there are several of his letters regarding sections 3 and 4. They are being sent to you now separately.

5) A package of what we have printed has been sent to you. Please be kind enough to send to the attention of the *Melach* a list of what I delivered to you before I left, so we will know what to send as soon as possible.

Regarding the above, you can write either to each of the aforementioned institutions separately, or to me. The main thing is that the matters should be brought from potential into action, as the Alter Rebbe explained (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 21) regarding the necessity of alacrity in this.

Regarding the fact that he emphasizes twice in *Iggeres HaKodesh* (ibid.) to say "in this world," it may be said that he is hinting at the action and virtue of *tzedakah* specifically, to draw down the light and the *shefa* into this physical world, as is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 60, and elsewhere. And according to the above, the conclusion "for man is judged on every day" will also be understood, as this too pertains specifically to the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, and according to what is explained in *Etz Chaim* (Rosh Hashanah), *Chanoch L'Naar* (at the end), and the *Kuntres U'Maayan* from page 17 onwards, that the judgment on every day pertains to the drawing down into this world specifically.

The letter was delayed until Monday, and just now a letter was received, along with the list for the *maamad*.

Waiting for a letter conveying good news.

## 271

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5707

Mr. Alexander Cohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to meet with you recently and to have the opportunity to speak with you in general, and in particular regarding the situation of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

Knowing your deep interest in the work of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, I am certain that without waiting for the return of our good friend Mr. Stulman, may he live, you will do everything to assist the Merkos in the current critical situation, which threatens, G-d forbid, to paralyze this vital work.

The Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya, states in Iggeres HaKodesh (Chapter 16) that although tzedakah does indeed have a prescribed measure according to the laws of Shulchan Aruch, and it is proper to conduct oneself in all respects strictly according to the laws of Shulchan Aruch, nevertheless, just as we Jews pray to Hashem that He should conduct Himself toward us with kindness and mercy, we too must conduct ourselves in this manner regarding tzedakah, and not limit ourselves strictly to the "legal measure."

I appreciate your help and dedication to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch with deep gratitude, and you certainly do what you can. But in the current critical situation of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, I hope that you will do much more than the "measure" and will make a special effort to provide timely assistance—a rescue effort—for Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

With regards and respect,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## Erev

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5707

To the esteemed, learned, and G-d-fearing [name], etc., Moreinu Harav B.Z. [Shemtov], may he live,

Shalom u'Bracha!

Your letter dated 9 Tammuz was received on the Chag HaGeulah, 12 Tammuz. On that very day, I brought to the attention of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live and be well, those who are imprisoned in every place—specifically Goldin, Serebryanski, and all the bochurim and anash in our country.

Based on the teaching of Chazal, "The wine belongs to the master, but the thanks go to the waiter" (see *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Mitzvas Milah, Chapter 3), I mentioned that this was brought about through the awakening of Harav B.Z.

You have surely seen the telegram from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the Chag HaGeulah. Regarding a specific response to my mention of you, the Rebbe said that it is not necessary.

The *Sefer HaToldos Maharash*, which was published for the Chag HaGeulah, has been sent to you, and you will surely confirm its receipt.

It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter whether you have already brought your family, may they live, to Paris, and what has been done regarding your papers and your visa to come here.

Please convey my regards to all those who seek our welfare. I sign with wishes for all that is good,

**Menachem Schneerson**

My mother, my teacher, the Rabbanit, shlita, is, thank G-d, well.

*Erev*

From the secretariat copy.

**Moreinu Harav B.Z.:** Shemtov. Additional letters to him—see below, 299, 310.

**Those who are imprisoned:** See also below, letters 299, 324.

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5707

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, and distinguished Rabbi Shmuel, may he live,
Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

It is with joy that I inform you that the book *Toldos Admur Maharash*—the book for which you took upon yourself the expenses of printing—has already come from the bindery.

We bring merit to a meritorious day: the book was delivered on 12 Tammuz, the festival of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, on the day marking twenty years since his liberation. On that very day, I presented it to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita.

It is brought in the aforementioned book (p. 71) that the Alter Rebbe said that "Shmuel" means "Shmo-Kel" (His name is G-d; see *Shelah*, beginning of *Parshas Toldos*, and the glosses of the Chida to *Zohar* Vol. III, 145b, printed in the Vilna Zohar in a slightly different manner).

Perhaps one can explain this based on what the bearer of this name himself, Admur Maharash, n.e., said (in *Hemshech VeKacha 5637*, ch. 10) regarding our Sages' statement that Hashem called Yaakov "E-l." This refers to the fact that He gave him a taste of the World to Come, for in the time to come He will bequeath 310 worlds, and a "tithe of this" is "E-l." (It could be said that this is why Admur Maharash, n.e., was wealthy even in material terms, even though generally, when tzaddikim seek to dwell in tranquility **in this world**, the Satan prosecutes, arguing that [their reward] is prepared for them in the **World to Come** (*Bereishis Rabbah*, beginning of *Parshas Vayishlach*). This is also the simple explanation of "He gave them a taste of the World to Come" (*Bava Basra*, end of the first chapter)).

The magnitude of the merit in publishing the aforementioned book surely requires no explanation to you or those like you. I will only emphasize what occurred—through Divine Providence—that it was completed on the day of the redemption and birthday (when one’s *mazal* is dominant; *Yerushalmi, Rosh Hashanah*, ch. 3, halacha 8) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita.

May it be His will that the blessings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, which you received from him while in his presence or in writing, be fulfilled for you.

Signing with wishes for all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is one copy, and in a separate package, another five. Please be so kind as to inform me how many more to send and to which address.
