From the secretariat's copy.

**Rabbi Shmuel:** Karakowaski.

## 210

1 Menachem Av, 5707

To the honorable, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing, distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Ch. Havlin, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 12 Nissan—my letter is delayed due to my visit to Europe.

1) Thank you for your blessing regarding the arrival of my mother, the Rabbanit, may she live and be well. May whoever blesses be blessed with abundant increase, etc. Thank G-d, the journey went well and she is in good health.

2) The deed of sale for the house and property in Chevron, which is in the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live and be well, was not among the papers you sent here some time ago. Furthermore, the copy of this deed, which you promised to send in your aforementioned letter, has not yet been received. It is my hope that this deed will now be sent immediately to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, without any further delays.

3) The book dealer says that he sent them the *Yalkut Shimoni* and *Keren Orah*.

4) Copies of the letters of Rabbi Avraham of Kalisk addressed to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, have been received only once during this entire period; none have been received addressed to me.

5) The maamar printed in *Mishor* has not arrived as of yet.

6) I have already replied to Rabbi M. L. Shapiro and Rabbi D. Shapiro (author of the book *Bnei Tzion*) regarding their letters some time ago. It is surprising that they did not confirm receipt of my letters.

7) Two packages of the *Kuntres* "Ha" and a package of the *Yoman* printed in Eretz Yisrael were received.

8) The *Sefer HaToldot Admur Maharash*, may his soul be in Eden, has just been published and has been sent to you via a traveler.

9) Regarding the missing page in your *Tzemach Tzedek*, you will surely be able to obtain a complete copy in your area and copy it from there.

10) For the Yahrtzeit of my father, may his soul be in Eden, on the 20th of Menachem Av, please give on my behalf, from our funds, ten shekel to Tiferes Bachurim, ten shekel to the Kollel, and five to the World Tehillim Society.

I said at the farbrengen of Shabbos Mevarchim Menachem Av that the name of the month is Av, and that is how it is written in a *get* (see *Kav V'Naki*, *Seder Nisuin*, subsection 4). However, in a *kesubah* and in *Birchas HaChodesh*, we say "Menachem Av." This can be explained according to what is elucidated in Chassidus: that one must perceive the greatness of a father's love even when he strikes his son. This is during the time of Galus, when Yisrael is like a woman who has been divorced (*Yoma* 82a); therefore, in a *get*, we write "Av" (an expression of *av*—father; see *Maamarim* 5668, "Nachamu"). But our request is that the love be revealed specifically; therefore, in *Birchas HaChodesh* (and likewise in a *kesubah*, which is intended so that it should not be easy [to divorce], the opposite of a *get*), we specifically say "Menachem."

A blessing for immediate Geulah and double consolation.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 275

7 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing individuals, those who volunteer for the dissemination of Chassidus, the doers and the facilitators, and foremost among them, the brilliant Rabbi Meir, may he live, and the learned Rabbi Chaim, may he live, a shochet and bodek.

Peace and blessing!

It is with joy that we have learned that the work of Hashem has succeeded in your hands, and you have collected a portion of the funds necessary for the printing of the works of the Mitteler Rebbe. These books have been published, and surely they have already been sent here as discussed.

Undoubtedly, you are continuing to exert yourselves as much as possible to increase the amount collected, in order to cover at least a further portion of the remaining expenses.

The magnitude of the merit of this matter in general surely requires no explanation, and certainly not at length, for people like yourselves. I have written this only to emphasize that the reward is great, to protect and to illuminate **in the World to Come and in this world, in both soul and body.**

This is understood based on the words of our Sages (Sanhedrin 90a), that all of the measures of the Holy One, Blessed be He, are measure for measure. **In the World to Come and in this world**—for it is known that there is no reward for a mitzvah in this world (Kiddushin 39b). The reason is that the reward for a mitzvah, which was commanded by the Ohr Ein Sof—the Infinite and Unbounded—is likewise Ohr Ein Sof and unbounded.

Therefore, it is impossible for it to be clothed in this physical and bounded world (see Iggeres HaKodesh, section 3). This applies to mitzvos in general; however, there are certain mitzvos through which the one who performs the mitzvah also effects something in this world. If so, in addition to the aforementioned infinite level, there is also, in the performance of this mitzvah, the aspect of action within this world (see Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah, Peah 1:1). Therefore, its reward also contains both elements: the primary aspect remains for the World to Come, and the secondary aspect—for this world.

Now, how greatly the giants of Israel yearned (Yevamos 96b, Bechoros 31b, Zohar Vol. I, 217b) that their teachings be quoted in this world while their souls are in the Heavenly Academy, for through this they would dwell in two worlds—the World to Come and this world. Therefore, the reward for those who cause this to happen by assisting in the dissemination of their Torah is, measure for measure, also **in the World to Come and in this world, in soul and body.** Although Torah and mitzvos were given to the soul within the body specifically (Shabbos 88b), their primary relevance and effect is upon the soul, which is spiritual, and not upon the material body. When one does work upon the body, it is **to break it** so that it acts against its nature. The Baal Shem Tov came and paved the way for the service of Hashem **with the body and with joy**, not through breaking and self-affliction, as is known from the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "If you see the donkey of your enemy..." (a sicha of the Rebbe Rayatz, brought in *Hayom Yom*, p. 23), and as explained in many places in the teachings of Chassidus. Therefore, when the dissemination of Torah—as in the present case—is in the form of Chassidus, which effects in the person who studies it a connection to the "Tree of Life," not through self-affliction but through joy, then the reward is measure for measure: a spiritual reward, and also a physical one, in an abundance of physical and spiritual goodness.

Signing with honor and abundant blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 257

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed and exalted Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished,
The Tamim, Moreinu HaRav R' M. Ashkenazi, shlita,

I was in Europe for several months, which is why my response to your letter was delayed; please accept my apologies.

It has now become clear that those who were initially considered for this cannot travel. Following his instruction, the Vaad HaPletim has written to Europe regarding this, and when there is news, they will inform you.

We are also sending five additional copies of each for sale through those who do His will, or for free distribution if you find it necessary. Please be kind enough to inform us if we should continue to do so in the future and how many to send. How many should we send of the English books for "The Young Jew"?

Signing with the wish that these days will very soon be transformed into joy and gladness,

## 179

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5707

To our esteemed and distinguished friend, the G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished
Rabbi D. Browman, may he live

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of the 15th of Tammuz has reached me, and I was already wondering and concerned about your silence until now.

1) Immediately upon receiving your letter, I conveyed its contents to my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, who was pleased that the printing project is progressing. You will surely ensure that it is done with the greatest possible beauty.

2) In the introduction that I am signing (for the Tanya, Ateres Rosh, and Shaarei Orah), the date must be changed.

It should read: 20 Menachem Av, 5707.

3) I have informed Rabbi B. G. that if you request it, he should provide you with up to 500 shekels for the printing, on my responsibility. Therefore, when the need arises, you may turn directly to him, and he will certainly fulfill your request immediately. Without a doubt, you will minimize expenses as much as possible (provided it does not detract from the beauty of the books), for they are acting in good faith.

4) In the Shulchan Aruch, there is no need to print the additions of the Tzemach Tzedek that appear at the end (as they do not pertain to the Shulchan Aruch, contain many errors, and have been printed in a corrected and expanded form in the new edition of the Tzemach Tzedek). I will send the title page and introduction soon, and you may begin printing the Shulchan Aruch. You should print only 1,000 copies.

5) According to the plan for now, in addition to the Tanya, Ateres Rosh, Shaarei Orah, and Shulchan Aruch, you should print our books: Part I, Part II, and Part IV, as well as Shaar HaEmunah and Shaar HaYichud by the Mitteler Rebbe—1,000 copies each—and the complete Siddur Tehillas Hashem (correcting it according to the list of corrections sent to you, as much as possible)—2,000 copies. Once the first copies are received here and we see the quality of the printing and binding, we will decide on the future.

6) Please return the explanations on the Zohar to Shalom DovBer Schneerson.

7) I will await your notification regarding the other prices, as you promised in the aforementioned letter. Most importantly, keep me informed about the progress of the printing. Send one sample booklet (to show here) for every twenty or thirty pages printed.

8) You will surely make every effort to ensure that the Tanya can arrive here before Rosh Hashanah (there will certainly be travelers coming from there to here), and it would be even better before the celebration of the 18th of Elul (if you notify us in time, they will print the booklet pertaining to the Tanya here in time). Ateres Rosh and Shaarei Orah should also arrive by that time, and at the latest, by the month of Cheshvan.

9) If the books are sent here via travelers, then three-quarters of everything printed should be sent.

10) I do not know which route will be faster, so I am writing directly to you and also through our friend * in Paris. Please inform me of the procedure for this in the future.

To conclude with the words of the Rebbe:

My father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, writes in one of his letters: "The Tzemach Tzedek said—a word spoken in speech is for the many; in writing, it is before the world; in print, it is for generations of generations."

- Perhaps one could explain the precise wording "generations of generations" as referring to at least four generations: *dorei shanim doros shanim* (similar to what our Sages said in Sanhedrin 99a regarding the verse *dor dorim*).

According to what the Tzemach Tzedek wrote in his commentary to Tehillim (145:4), " 'Generation to generation' refers to the entire order of *hishtalshelus*, for the entire world is called a 'generation.' " If so, the four generations are the four worlds of *Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*. Just as the four worlds of *Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah* include all the worlds, so too, the expression "generations of generations" includes all generations. See also *Likutei Torah*, discourse *Be'ur Inyan Motza'eihem*.

Awaiting good news from you.

**M. Schneerson**

## 280

B”H, 12 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and honest merchant, R’ Y. HaKohen,
Shalom U’vracha!

You surely know that I spent several months in Europe, and I have now returned with my mother, shlita.

Upon arriving, I found on my desk the transcriptions of the sichos of the Rebbe, shlita, from Tishrei 5707, which were likely submitted by you—thank you very much.

Actually, I would have liked to end my letter here, but the situation at Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch compels me to write the following as well:

The financial state of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch is very strained. Added to this are the expenses connected with our growing work in Europe (chinuch and printing), even though we are very calculated in our expenditures. This forces the Merkos to turn to all its friends, requesting that they immediately pay all their past pledges and donations, and to contribute anew for the future, as much as they can—and even beyond their means.

Counting you among the closest friends of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch, this appeal is directed to you. I am certain that it will find the proper resonance with you, both in acting immediately as mentioned above, and in ensuring that all those upon whom you can exert an influence should also act immediately in the same way.

I know that you have various arguments for delaying this for the time being, so I would like to conclude with a statement of our Sages connected to the days from which we have just emerged:

Our Sages say (Bava Metzia 30b) that Jerusalem was destroyed only because they based their judgments strictly on the letter of the law. When one acts *lifnim mishuras hadin* (that is, even if it appears to **oneself** that according to the strict letter of the law one is currently exempt), this brings closer the Geulah and the rebuilding of Jerusalem.

In the hope of hearing good news from you,

And with blessings for immediate Teshuvah, immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

In a separate package, I have sent the newest publication of Otzar HaChassidim: *Sefer HaToldos*.

## 281

281

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5707

To the brothers, the G-d-fearing, etc., Mr. Yitzchak,
Meir Moshe,
Yaakov Yosef, may they live:

Shalom u’vrachah!

I have been in Europe for several months, and this is the reason why my correspondence has been delayed until now. Furthermore, some time ago, the *Sefer HaSichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, was published—the book for which you took upon yourselves the costs of printing, *le’ilui nishmas* your brother, R’ Shlomo, a”h.

Regarding the *zechus* you attained by providing the means to publish the *Sefer HaSichos*, and regarding the great *aliyah* for the *neshamah* of the departed, I believe it is unnecessary for me to elaborate.

However, I would like to note here one advantage that this has in comparison to many other *mitzvos*.

Our Sages state that the reward for most *mitzvos* is not in this world. The explanation for this, based on what the Alter Rebbe writes (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, ch. 3), is that the reward is too great for this world to contain.

This applies to most *mitzvos*. However, there are *mitzvos* that consist of doing good for other people here in this world. This means that these *mitzvos* possess both advantages: *tov la’Shamayim* (good for Heaven) and *tov la’brios* (good for the creations). In such a case, in addition to the reward for the first category of *mitzvos*, one also receives reward, *midah ke’neged midah*, in this world as well.

You, by enabling the printing of the *Sefer HaSichos*, have made accessible to thousands of people a book that contains Torah and *midos tovos*, and which will, for a certain number of them, be instrumental in finding the right path and the answer to their problems in this world.

And therefore, this is a matter that brings with it, in addition to the *keren* (principal) for the World to Come, also its *peiros* (fruits) in this world, in an abundance of material and spiritual good.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Understand the explanation in this letter through a parable: A great king, who ruled over the entire world, once went out of his palace and encountered a child named Yisrael. He said to him: "I ask of you to find the appropriate diamonds for my crown, so that for my jubilee coronation, the crown will be truly magnificent and beautiful." Yisrael did so; he cast aside his toys, found the gemstones, and brought them. Experts polished them and set them into the crown, and at the coronation, the king wore the crown, and everyone marveled at its beauty.

The reward for the child was decreed: when he grew up, the king would make him the highest minister, above all other ministers.

The next day, Yisrael did not find his food at the usual time, so he began to cry: "I provided the precious stones for the king, and he does not ensure that my food is not delayed today!" But when he grew up, he understood that the true reward was that he had been made a viceroy to the king. The *nimshal* (the lesson) is clear.

In continuation of the above—a parable for the second category of *mitzvos*: The king asked Yisrael to do him a personal favor: to feed the king’s children. Yisrael cast aside all his own interests and fulfilled the king’s request.

Therefore, the reward, **in addition** to the reward for fulfilling a request of the King of Kings, is also that Yisrael does not stand on the side hungry while others receive their food through his—Yisrael’s—efforts; rather, he sits at the table as well.

The *nimshal* is, once again, clear.

## 283

14 Menachem Av, 5707

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished *tammim*,
Rabbi A. [Hecht], may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your inquiry regarding what you heard—that the *tzaddik* of Zidichov disagreed with the Chabad approach concerning the concept of time—and your request to be directed to the book where this dispute is found and its content:

The matter is found in his book *V’aseh Tov*, near the beginning. It states there: "There is someone I have seen (and this is also written in the *Siddur Shaar HaKriat Shema*, in the *Drush* for understanding the first chapter of *Kriat Shema*, though I do not know if he is referring to that *Siddur*) who wrote in the name of the Rabbi, the Maggid of Mezritch, may his soul rest in Eden, a resolution to this difficulty (why the world was not created earlier): that time was also created, and in the beginning, there was no time. But in truth, I do not believe that this came from the holy one... and what will the Rabbi do with the *Midrash Bereishis Rabbah* (it is chapter 9), which says 'this teaches that there was an order of times beforehand,' and the Gemara says 'two thousand years before the world, the Torah preceded it,' etc., and he hints to the *Sefer Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 2, Chapter 30."

See *Shomer Emunim*, the second debate, from page 17 to 20.

Now, beyond the opinion of the Rambam (there) that time was created, many of the great Torah scholars and *geonim* have stated this explicitly: the Rav Saadia Gaon (*Emunot V’Deot*, Maamar 3, the fourth proof), the Rashba (*Responsa*, 114), the Ramah of Pano (*Asarah Maamarot*, Part 1, Chapter 17), the Sforno at the beginning of his commentary on the Torah, and others.

And with greater depth, it can be said: There are two aspects to time: 1) Time that is measured and calculated (by some form of motion), and 2) the essence of the duration of time (this is what the Jewish philosophers in *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 2, Chapter 13, call "measured time," "a likeness of time," or in the language of *Sefer HaIkkarim*, Part 2, Chapter 18, "unmeasured time"). Even the essence of the duration of time is created (contrary to the opinion of the *Ikkarim* there). See the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvas Emunas Elokus*, section 11, and in many places in the book *Asarah Maamarot* (there).

Regarding the statement of our Sages in the aforementioned *Bereishis Rabbah*—so that it does not lean toward the opinion of the eternity of the world—they have already resolved it in various ways; see the *Ikkarim* there, the *Rabbeinu Bachya* at the beginning of *Parshas Bereishis*, and others.

According to *Chassidus*, there is a distinction between "time" and the "order of times" mentioned in the aforementioned *Bereishis Rabbah*. The "order of times" is more subtle than the concept of "time" (the opposite of the explanation of the author of the *Ikkarim*), and it is the root of time (as is also mentioned in *Pardes*, *Shaar Eirech HaZman*, regarding "order of times," and in *Sefer Avodas HaKodesh*, Part 4, Chapter 5), as explained at length in *Sefer HaMitzvos* (there) and in many other places.

With the blessing of "immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

*By the way, many people confuse these two aspects of time, and through this, they arrive at many confusions and errors. For example, in recent times, those who occupied themselves with Einstein’s Theory of Relativity—this only touches upon the first aspect of time, and they erred as mentioned above, and consequently arrived at very strange conclusions, but this is not the place to elaborate.*

*Beyond the aforementioned dispute, the tzaddik of Zidichov disagreed in general with the approach of those who occupy themselves with the study of the knowledge of Elokus, such as the study of the concept of Yichud, the Seder Hishtalshelus, and the like. According to his opinion, faith is sufficient, as brought in the aforementioned book.*

*If the Rebbe of Komarno, whom you mention in your letter, is the one who spoke with me once regarding the two shin-nun [letters] in "Tishrei," etc., please convey my regards to him, and you may also show him this letter.*

*And lastly, the most important thing (according to our Sages) is not the study, but the deed. Last year, when you were in "Ne'ot Deshe," you occupied yourself with obtaining means for the "Keren HaMitzvos," and surely you will do so now as well, with even greater effort, for the necessity is constantly growing, and the help from the Ribono shel Olam is also growing, as the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh, section 13. The main thing is that here below, we should not evade [our responsibility] with excuses, and we should become worthy vessels.*

## 286

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5707

To the members of Anash, the G-d-fearing, etc.,
And at their head, the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, R' Sh. Sasanka, and R' B. Wilshansky,

Peace and Blessing!

1) Your two letters, along with the list of seforim and the list of participants in the Sefer Torah, have duly arrived.

2) You will receive additional seforim via the post, from R' Sh.Z. Butman and R' A.Sh. Kahanov.

Please confirm their receipt and notify me of the titles of the seforim.

3) These days, the letters will be inscribed in the Sefer Torah, and you will be notified.

4) Regarding what you wrote—that I am **demanding** speed: Heaven forbid, I have not come to **demand**, but to awaken, and the matter itself demands it. The proof of this is the very fact that so many obstacles and delays arise, the greatest of which is that it seems as though even within the intellect of kedushah, there are reasons for a lack of speed.

5) Regarding what you wrote concerning the subject at hand, about the superiority of man over the angels in that they do not perform two missions: seemingly, this is not relevant here. For regarding angels, the precision is specifically if the missions are different, whereas if they are in the same matter (as in the subject at hand, of connecting to the *ilana d'chaya*, etc.), it is different. This is as written in Tosafos, *dihah* "Hahu" (Bava Metzia 86b; it is evident there that the entire statement of Tosafos is a single resolution), and it is also evident from the reason explained in Chassidus.

With this, one can resolve what has puzzled me for a long time: that in many places in Chassidus, the words of the Rambam in his introduction to the Mishnah are brought as proof for the above. Now, the Rambam writes "a single action" or "**two actions.**" Seemingly, it is not understood how it is possible to say "two actions." And although one could say that this is because in the *Olam HaTohu*, their consciousness is *Tohu* within *Tikkun*, if so, this reason should also apply to angels—so why do they not perform two missions? According to the above—that they do not perform two *different* matters specifically—it works out. See the beginning of the *Biur* on "V'heinif" (*Likutei Torah*, Parshas Emor), which emphasizes the example that there is no mercy in the cruel raven, and no cruelty in the merciful eagle.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 287

25 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, etc., R’ Chaim Havlin,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letters from 29 Tammuz and 13 Menachem Av were received, as was the newspaper *Kol Yisrael* in which your sons are mentioned. May it be Hashem’s will that you raise them to Torah, chuppah, and good deeds, in prosperity.

Regarding your letters:

1) Concerning the printing of your son’s *chiddushei Torah*: A collection of *chiddushei Torah* from students of *Tomchei Temimim* and the like is not currently being published here.

2) *Yalkut Shimoni* and *Keren Orah* were requested from the publisher and have been sent to you by our secretary. *Sefer HaToldos* was sent to you by the lawyer of *Machne Israel*, Mr. Shtral—a G-d-fearing man of fine character, etc. Also sent to you were *Kuntres Nun* and *Sefer HaSichos* via post, as a contribution to our work.

3) The minimum price for the *Tzemach Tzedek* is fifteen shekel. Per your request, a second copy of *Bad Kodesh* and the *maamar* for 13 Shevat have been sent to you.

4) Since R’ M.Z. Rivkin sent the *“Atah Hareisa”* without further specification, we are currently clarifying with him whether there was a specific intent behind it; we will inform you after we clarify.

5) There is no need to copy the letters of R’ Avraham of Kalisk, only those that were not received even by the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita (the pages were received; the last letter begins with “Shalom ve’Emes me’Eretz Chaim,” etc., from R’ Avraham of Kalisk).

6) You will surely expedite the sending of a copy of the deed of acquisition in the name of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita...

7) Many thanks for your efforts in distributing my donations for the *yahrtzeit*.

* * *

In your first letter, you discuss *Chassidus*. **Based on your proposal**, I will offer a few comments:

1) You analyze what is written in the *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”* (5666): “And as is written in *Etz Chaim* that *Me’od* is the level of *Atik Kaddisha* etc., and it is higher even than the level of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* now, which is the level of *Chochmah Stima’ah* and *Atik Yomin*.”

Actually, you happened upon an erroneous copy; it should read “*Me’od* is *Adam Kadmon*,” with an *Aleph*. This is how it appears in the Rebbe’s own handwriting, and this is how it appears in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Seder HaAtzilus*, Chapter 2. This is also necessitated by the proof provided: “for *Me’od* is the letters of *Adam*” (see also *Biurei HaZohar* on *Vayeshev* and the *maamar* beginning *“Im BeChukosai”* in the aforementioned *hemshech*).

2) You are uncertain about what is meant in the aforementioned *maamar* by “the level of *Chochmah Stima’ah* and *Atik Yomin*”—to which level does it refer by *Atik Yomin*?

This can be explained by first noting that, on the face of it, it is difficult to understand why *Atik Yomin* is mentioned at all, as the text only spoke of *Chochmah Stima’ah*. However, it corresponds (in Kabbalistic terminology) to what was stated previously (in Chassidic terminology): that there are two types of “taste” for the composite will: an intellectual taste and a pleasurable taste. Regarding this, it states that the essence of the simple will is higher than both tastes, or in Kabbalistic terms: *Adam Kadmon* (corresponding to the simple will; whereas *Atik Kaddisha* corresponds to pleasure) is higher than *Chochmah Stima’ah* (intellectual taste) and *Atik Yomin* (pleasurable taste).

It is understood from all this that it is speaking of *Atik Yomin* as a pleasurable taste for the will—namely, the levels within *Atik* that are enclothed in *Arich*, which are the *Zayin Tachtonos* of *Atik*. According to what is explained in the *maamar* beginning *“Kavod Malchus”* (5660) that both types of taste have their place in *Chochmah*, one could say that the intent here is primarily the level of *Atik Yomin* that is enclothed in *Chochmah Stima’ah*, namely the *Gevurah* of *Atik Yomin*. This still requires further study; see below, section 6.

3) Which level is called *Atik Kaddisha*? The primary name for this is *Ein Sof* (*Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Arich Anpin*, Chapter 2; *Mevo Shearim*, *Shaar 3*, Part 1, Chapter 1; *Zohar* Vol. 3, p. 10; *Shaar Maamarei Rashbi*, *Parshas Haazinu*). Seemingly, it is proven (see *Etz Chaim* there and *Shaar Seder Atzilus*, Chapter 1; and see the *Tzemach Tzedek’s* gloss in *Mevo Shearim* there) that the intent is *Adam Kadmon* from the *Tabur* downwards, only that it is called *Ein Sof* relative to them. However, in the *maamar* beginning *“Naso”* (5672), he cites what is written in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Sheviras HaKeilim*, Chapter 7, that above the *Gulgolta* of *Adam Kadmon* there is a likeness of the level of *Atik* of *Atzilus*, and he writes that in the *Zohar* and *Idra* it appears that *Atik* is truly His essence and being; see there. It is also called by this name in several levels below the aforementioned, to the point that even *Arich Anpin* is called this, as written in the aforementioned places.

See the various levels of *Atik* in *Likkutei Torah*, end of the *drushim* for *Yom Kippur*, and in the aforementioned *maamar* beginning *“Im BeChukosai.”* Regarding the *Sefer HaKabbalah*—refer to the book *Emes LeYaakov*, *Maareches HaAyin*, which cites *Etz Chaim*, *Mevo Shearim*, etc.

In short, *Atik Kaddisha* or *Atik Yomin* is explained in every place according to its context, and one should not equate two places without clarification.

4) You brought what is written in *Hagahos U’Biurim* (on *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Arich Anpin*, Chapter 2), subsection 2. But I do not understand his interpretation. To me, the language is difficult. The intent of the *Ohr Zarua* is that *Atik Yomin* in general (meaning, in a place where it does not come to specify a level within *Atik* itself) is *Reisha D’Lo Yitya*, and *Atik* in general is *Arich Anpin*, even though at times they are called *Atik Kaddisha* or *Atik Yomin*.

With this, the *Ohr Zarua* resolves why in *Shaar Arich Anpin* it calls *Reisha D’Lo Yitya* “*Atik Yomin*”—because there it only distinguishes between it and *Arich Anpin*—and in *Shaar HaMelachim* it calls the *Zayin Tachtonos* “*Atik Yomin*,” because there it explains the details of the levels within *Atik* itself. Perhaps there is a typographical error in the glosses, and I do not have the *Sefer Shem MiShmuel* or *Ohr Zarua* with me to verify the source.

5) You bring what is written in the *maamar* beginning *“VaYechulu”* (the *hemshech* of 5666) that the will of the *mitzvos* belongs to the *Chasadim* of *Atik Yomin* (and not to the *Gevuros* of *Atik Yomin*). You wish to explain that this refers to: a) the hidden taste of the will of the *mitzvos*, or b) that the intent is the *Chesed* in the *Gimmel Rishonos* of *Atik Kaddisha*. In my opinion, neither explanation is possible: a) The hidden taste is *Chochmah Stima’ah*, as explained in many places, including the aforementioned *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres.”* And in *Chochmah Stima’ah* is enclothed the *Gevurah* of *Atik Yomin* specifically—the **opposite** of what you mean in the *maamar* beginning *“VaYechulu.”* b) The *Admur HaZakein* explains that the *Gevuros* of *Atik Yomin* referred to there are the level of “flashes of fire,” which is the matter of enthusiasm, etc., and the *Chasadim* are like waters descending from a high place, etc. He connects and introduces this topic with what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 44, in the *Hagah*, regarding the sweetening of the *Gevuros* with the *Chasadim* through the inclusion of the *Middos*, etc. From all this, it is proven that it is speaking of *Middos* and not *Mochin*.

To me, there is no difficulty to begin with. For if you follow your own logic, why must you raise a difficulty from the *maamar* beginning *“VaYechulu”*? It would have been better to bring it from the *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”* itself, where he writes that the essence of the level of *Pnimiyus* and the essence of the will is in the essence of the *Gulgolta*, and this is the root of the *mitzvos*. The difficulty is that the essence of the *Gulgolta* is the *Keter* of *Arich Anpin*, which is lower than the *Chesed* of *Atik Yomin*, since it is what expands and enclothes itself within it to illuminate and vivify it (*Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Arich Anpin*, Chapter 287).

Therefore, it seems to me that the *Admur HaZakein* comes to explain the superiority of the will of the *mitzvos* over the will of the creation of the worlds in **all the levels** through which these wills are drawn down. That is, from *Arich Anpin*—which is the revelation of the will—and higher. He specifies that in *Arich Anpin* it is *Gulgolta* and *Chochmah Stima’ah* (in the *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”*); in *Atik* it is *Chochmah* and *Gevurah* (in the *maamar* beginning *“VaYechulu”*); higher than that—the *Sovev* and the *Kav*; higher than that—the *Shiur Komah* itself and what is above it; in His essence—the light that pertains to the other and what is above it (*maamar* beginning *“Esah”* 5672). See also regarding all this the *maamar* beginning *“HaShamayim Kis’i”* at the end of the *hemshech* of 5666.

**Note:** Regarding your precision in the aforementioned *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”* about “the essence of the *Gulgolta*,” it may be that he comes to exclude the hair of the *Gulgolta*, according to what is written in the *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”* (5667); see also the *Hosafos* to *Torah Or*, beginning of *Parshas Tetzaveh*.

In the *maamar* beginning *“BiYom HaShemini Atzeres”* (5667), he explains that the *Levnusa*—meaning the essence of the *Gulgolta*—is the essential *Ayin* of *Keter*, for there shines the level of *Netzach* and *Hod* of *Atik* (as in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Arich Anpin*, Chapter 5; *Mevo Shearim*, *Shaar 3*, Part 2, Chapter 7; *Maamarei Chazal*, *Maseches Arich*, Chapter 4). This requires study, **for in the entire** stature of *Arich Anpin* shine levels from *Atik*, as written in *Etz Chaim* there, Chapter 7, and elsewhere.

Perhaps it can be said, according to what is explained in many places, that the *Netzach*, *Hod*, and *Yesod* specifically have their root in *Keter* (*Likkutei Torah*, *Biur* on *Tza’u U’Re’u*, section 3, and in the *maamar* beginning *“Kol Dodi”* 5668, that this is from the *Pnimiyus* of the *Keter*). It seems more likely to me that, as is gathered from the *hemshech* of 5666, an essential drawing down can only be through *Ohr Chozer*. And *Ohr Chozer* in the enclothement of *Atik* that is in *Arich Anpin* is specifically through the illumination of *Netzach* and *Hod* that are in the *Gulgolta*, as written in *Etz Chaim*, *Mevo Shearim*, and elsewhere. However, the hair of the *Gulgolta* was also created through the *Kruma D’Avira*, unlike the *Levnusa*.

6) What you wrote in the *Siddur* regarding the order of the Shabbos meal, that there is no difference in the light of the second and third meal—he concludes there that in the second meal it illuminates above and not below, unlike the third meal. He writes similarly in the *hemshech* of 5666 (for example, in the *maamar* beginning *“Esah”* near the end). In general, it is highly questionable whether these matters are the same. Time does not permit a proper study of this now.

7) You raise a difficulty from what is written in the *Siddur* in the order of the third meal: “For the *Pnimiyus* of *Abba* is the *Pnimiyus* of *Atik*, the level of *Pnimiyus* is the level of pleasure and the simple will that shines from the essence of the simple pleasure and *Atik Kaddisha*, the will of *Atika*,” which implies to you that this is specifically the *Gimmel Rishonos* of *Atika* itself.

I do not understand that implication at all, especially since it says it is the level of pleasure **that shines** from the essence of pleasure, and it does not say that it *is* the essence of pleasure. Refer to the *maamar* beginning *“VaYetze-VaYishlach”* that I cited in my previous letter, and to the *maamar* beginning *“HaShamayim Kis’i”* (end of the *hemshech* of 5666) that the *Pnimiyus* of *Abba* is the *Pnimiyus* of *Atik*, meaning the simple pleasure that is specifically felt, and it is drawn down through the Torah, which is in the level of taste and *Chochmah*, unlike the essential pleasure itself which is drawn down through the *mitzvos*. Regarding what is mentioned in the *Siddur* there, “*Keter* within *Keter*,” refer to the order of the second meal, *maamar* beginning *“BeHadin Yoma,”* where he explains it as the *Gulgolta* of *Arich Anpin*, and *Gulgolta* in general includes the hair as well.

Surely you will not be offended by my comments; “And love is in its end.”

With wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 288

288

B”H, 28 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, Torah scholar, etc., the Tamim,
R. A. [Hecht]—may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your inquiry:

1) Regarding what you write, that the Rambam says, "I believe in the coming of Moshiach, etc., every day that he will come."

Actually, I have not found this in the Rambam, neither in the Commentary on the Mishnah (Perek Chelek) nor in the Yad (Hilchos Teshuvah, ch. 3, halacha 6; ch. 9, halacha 2; and the end of Hilchos Melachim). Rather, this is the wording found in the Siddurim.

2) Regarding what you heard explained about the above—that "every day" means he waits for him to come eventually, even though it is impossible for him to come today, such as on Shabbos or Yom Tov, according to our Sages (Eruvin 43b): This question regarding the contradiction between the text of "Ani Maamin" and the aforementioned statement of our Sages has been asked of me before, and I answered as above. However, it still requires study, for if so, it should have said, "Every day I will wait for him to come," so that there would be no doubt as to the intent of the words.

To sharpen the point, one could say: Since the fact that Ben Dovid does not come on Shabbos or Yom Tov is a matter of doubt and not a certainty (Rambam, Hilchos Nezirus, ch. 4, halacha 11), the text of "Ani Maamin" was formulated in such a way that it fits regardless of how the doubt regarding Ben Dovid’s arrival on Shabbos or Yom Tov is resolved.

Or, in a slightly different way: There are several halachic doubts that Eliyahu will resolve, even though "it is not in heaven," as is known that this is the acronym *Teiku* (Shelah, Chelek Toras Shebe'al Peh, Klal, letter Tav; and this is based on Zohar Vol. III, 28a. See also Aruch HaShalem under that entry). If so, when one stands on Shabbos or Yom Tov, it is possible that Eliyahu has already come to the Beis Din HaGadol on the eve of Shabbos or Yom Tov, or before that, and resolved the doubt leniently. If so, the Beis Din could come today.

3) Seemingly, it is difficult to accept the opinion of those who say that Ben Dovid does not come on Shabbos or Yom Tov due to the prohibition of *techumin* above ten *tefachim* (see the commentaries on the Yad there). For while this may apply to Eliyahu, who is found above, it is not so for Ben Dovid, who is found below (see Sanhedrin 98a). Especially in light of what is written in the Yad at the end of Hilchos Melachim: that if a king arises from the House of Dovid who studies Torah, etc., and compels all of Israel to follow it, etc., and fights the wars of Hashem, etc., and succeeds, etc., he is definitely Moshiach. This implies that Moshiach’s victory will be some time **after** he is revealed. The statement that he does not come on Shabbos or Yom Tov refers to when he is victorious, and as the Gemara says, once he comes, all are servants to Israel. If so, it has nothing to do with being above ten *tefachim*.

Rather, one must say that the arrival of Ben Dovid must be to all of Israel (see Iyun Yaakov on the aforementioned passage in Eruvin) or to the Beis Din HaGadol, who are the representatives of all of Israel. Now, the Beis Din HaGadol is destined to return first to Teveria and afterwards to the Beis HaMikdash (Rambam, Hilchos Sanhedrin, ch. 14, halacha 12). The war of Gog and Magog and the victory will be on the mountains of Israel (Yechezkel 38-39) or around Jerusalem (Zechariah 14). It is impossible for him to come to Teveria or to all of Israel except by traveling above ten *tefachim*, or by postponing it to a weekday, if *techumin* applies even above ten *tefachim*.

4) All of the above applies specifically to Moshiach Ben Dovid, but not to Moshiach Ben Yosef, who does not need to be revealed to all of Israel at once (see Iyun Yaakov there). Therefore, it can be said that the text of "Ani Maamin," which says "Moshiach" generally, refers to the beginning of the Geulah, which includes Moshiach Ben Yosef as well, and he can come even on Shabbos and Yom Tov according to all opinions, as mentioned above.

5) It is simply clear that the intent of "Ani Maamin" is the belief in the Geulah, waiting for its beginning every day. Also, the arrival of Eliyahu, who heralds that Moshiach will be revealed tomorrow or the day after, is also called the arrival of Moshiach. If so, one can say the text every single day, and this is well understood.

With wishes for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**

Just now, Rabbi Quint told me that there is a custom not to say "Ani Maamin" on Shabbos because of the aforementioned difficulty.

With blessings for a *ksiva v'chasima tova* and regards to all those who seek our welfare,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 290

B"H, 25 Elul, 5707

291

27 Elul, 5707

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, etc.,
Rabbi M. [Ashkenazi], may he live,

Peace and blessing!

It is with joy and great gratitude that I can inform you that the books *Torah Ohr* on the *Shemos* volume, *Shaarei Teshuvah*, and *Derech Chaim* have been received. We also received today 1,143 [dollars], from which we are delivering the amount for the *maamad* [support fund], in accordance with your letter to Rabbi D.B. Haskind, may he live. Surely you will do everything in your power to increase the aforementioned sum, both regarding the *maamad* and regarding the *melach* [fund for the Rebbe's household], for the necessity of this is beyond measure.

The magnitude of your merit in bringing the aforementioned to fruition is beyond words. I only wish to inform you that your merit was channeled into auspicious days, as the books were received and I delivered them into the hands of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, during the days of 13–18 Elul (the jubilee year of the wedding of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, for long and good years).

Enclosed is a *maamar* delivered today by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and you will surely confirm its receipt.

I will conclude with what I wrote to someone regarding the *inyana d'yoma* [the theme of the day]:

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, said at the *farbrengen* of 18 Elul that the early Chassidim explained that "Chai Elul" (the 18th of Elul) gives *chayus* (vitality) to the *avodah* of "I am to my beloved and my beloved is to me" (the acronym for Elul).

This can be explained as follows: Both the living and that which is not living possess all 248 limbs. However, the living being possesses a *neshamah* in addition, and through this, the body grows from smallness to greatness and moves from one place to another.

Our Sages have said (Tanya, Chapter 38) that the *kavanah* of the *mitzvos*—to cleave to Him, may He be blessed—is like the *neshamah* to the body of the *mitzvos*. This comes about through one’s birthing or revealing within himself the love and fear of Hashem, which is achieved through the study of the inner dimension of Torah in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular, as is explained in many places.

Now, through the *kavanah* to cleave to Him, may He be blessed, one achieves the greatest growth and the most possible movement—which is, in fact, the only true movement—as is known regarding the concept of "those who walk and those who stand." This occurs when the created being, who is limited, cleaves to the Creator, who is infinite and beyond limitation, as it is written: "And you who **cleave** to Hashem your G-d are all **alive** today."

This is the meaning of the saying that Chai Elul—the birthday and revelation of the Baal Shem Tov and his teachings, and the birth of the Alter Rebbe—gives vitality to the *avodah* of "I am to my beloved and my beloved is to me," whereby the created beings cleave to the Creator.

In a deeper sense, it can be said: Even in a limb that is not alive, there is flesh, sinews, and bones. In terms of the levels of *avodah*, this corresponds to the *avodah* of the mind (bones), the *avodah* of the heart (flesh), and their connection (sinews), as explained in *Likkutei Torah*, *Parshas Pinchas*, in the *maamar* beginning "Tzav," regarding the second [offering of] "My bread." Yet, all of this does not in itself constitute true *chayus*, which comes only through the prerequisite *avodah* of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), and specifically the *kabbalas ol* of Rosh Hashanah. See the *maamar* for this year’s Rosh Hashanah regarding the concepts of specific *chayus*, general *chayus*, "to give life," and "living in essence."

Concluding with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 292

[Late 5707?]

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said on the 13th of Elul of this year:

*Mochin* is for the sake of something; *mochin* is for the sake of *avodah* in practice. One must be a simple person.

It can be said that this is specifically relevant to Rosh Hashanah, for on Rosh Hashanah it must be, "You are standing today (Rosh Hashanah) all of you—your heads, your tribes, your elders, and your officers, every man of Israel... from the hewer of your wood to the drawer of your water," to be united as one, as explained in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of *Parshas Nitzavim*. Therefore, the *mitzvah* of the day is *tekiah*—a *kol pashut* (simple sound), specifically without the articulation of letters. Furthermore, even in this, the *tekiah* itself is not the essence of the *mitzvah*—for that, one would at least need to be an expert—but rather the *shemiah* (hearing), which in terms of *avodah* is the matter of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke of Heaven), as it is written, "Behold, to obey is better than a sacrifice." Moreover, this *kabbalas ol* is simple and general, not particular, as is known that this is the difference between the *kabbalas ol* of Rosh Hashanah and that of the rest of the year, as explained in the *maamar* entitled *Shofar Shel Rosh Hashanah 5702* and elsewhere.

With blessings for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 293

[Late 5707]

To the esteemed and exalted Dr. A. Hillman, may he live:

Shalom u’vrachah!

I spent several months in Europe, and during that time, many matters accumulated here in addition to my regular avodah. This caused a significant delay in responding to the letters I received. Furthermore, I was compelled to prioritize those letters that pertained to the practical work of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch, Machne Israel, or Kehot. I ask for your forgiveness for not having written until now.

Regarding your comments:

1) You ask: In the phrase "In anger, remember mercy... the binding... the innocence, remember," these correspond to Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. If so, what is the meaning of the addition, "In anger, remember love"?

This can be explained in two ways: 
a) In terms of Kabbalah, we are mentioning the totality of the Sefiros, as required by the context of the Chesed within them. "Mercy" (Rachem) has the gematria of Avraham, as is explained in many places—the right line. "The binding" (Akedah) is the left line, as it was bound and subdued by the right line; this is the concept of the binding of Yitzchak by Avraham, as explained in Likutei Torah by the Arizal at the end of Parshas Vayeira and elsewhere. "Innocence" (Temimus) refers to Yaakov, the middle line, who is called "innocent" (tam) because of the good he acquired (see the beginning of Parshas Toldos). "Love" (Ahavah) is the Sefirah of Malchus, which completes the Sefiros. This corresponds to the verse, "Then I will remember My covenant with Yaakov... and I will remember the land... when they are in the land of their enemies (in anger), I will not despise them, etc." 
b) Based on the above and closer to the simple meaning: We are praying that even in anger, Hashem should remember the Avos, the merit of the entire Jewish people, and the love with which He loved them. This is based on what is written in Zohar I, 196b, that this refers to Knesses Yisrael (and the matter is one, as is known regarding the connection between Knesses Yisrael and the Sefirah of Malchus).

2) You ask: In the prayer and Kiddush, why do we repeat the phrase "this holy festival" (Yom Tov Mikra Kodesh) twice?

It can be explained that the first mention describes the greatness of the matter—that we have been given a festival, a holy convocation, the time of our freedom. The second mention explains the reason for the "holy convocation," which is a remembrance of the Exodus from Egypt, and the second "holy convocation" is drawn **downward**.

3) Regarding what you wrote in the collection, that before "Ma Nishtana" it is the custom of the Rebbe’s house for even one who does not have a father to say, "Father, I want to ask you..."—I have not heard a reason or a source for this.

What seems to me is that it is because "one who honors him in his lifetime honors him in his death," as the halacha is ruled in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 240 (and see also Zohar III, end of Parshas Bechukosai, and the places cited in Nitzutzei Zohar there).

## 294

294

Beginning of the year 5708

To the honorable...

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the coming year, I send my blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for you, your family, and for all good things.

The primary sale period for the *Tzemach Tzedek* [sefarim] that we entrusted to others has concluded, and I have instructed that the six volumes be sent to you as you requested, as they are not sold in individual parts.

You are surely aware that for several months I was in Europe, and naturally, the *avodah* increased, in addition to the work of preparing for print what was published this past summer.

But now, I return once again to what we have been discussing for a long time: a copy of a *michtav* from *kavod kedushas adoneinu* regarding *Lashon HaKodesh* in particular, and an overview of the *avodah* during these years, in which you participated and can therefore testify to and describe. I know full well that you will answer that you are busy and will delay it again, but in light of the fact that it has been about a year and a half since we began discussing this, I hope that perhaps you will nevertheless carve out some time and do the aforementioned soon, *u’v’agala di’dan*.

And to conclude with a note on a relevant topic: In *Likutei Torah*, *seder d'chah* "Atem Nitzavim," it concludes, "For the *shofar* of *Rosh Hashanah* of a mountain goat is straight, etc., and the more straight it is, the better, etc." Now, this is the opposite of the *psak din* that the *shofar* for *Rosh Hashanah* must be from a ram (see also *Likutei Torah*, *d'chah* "Yom Tov Shel Rosh Hashanah," ch. 3, where he explains the matter of the ram's *shofar* specifically) and bent, for the more bent it is, the better. However, according to most *poskim*, it is *b'dieved* valid if straight, while according to the *Rambam*, it is *b'dieved* invalid. One should also note the *Shelah*, end of *Maseches Rosh Hashanah*, regarding the *be'ur* on the path of *mussar*.

Perhaps there is a way to resolve this, but this is not the place, as I have come here only to point it out.

## Ratzah

B.H., The seventh month shall be turned into joy,

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav R. Sh. Y.
May he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

You are surely aware that I spent several months in Europe. Upon my return, I found a number of matters that had accumulated during that time, in addition to the regular work, and specifically the burden of preparing for print what was published last summer. All of this caused a significant delay in responding to the letters addressed to me (those that do not pertain directly to the practical work of the Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch and Kehot). I ask for your utmost forgiveness.

First and foremost, I hereby express my blessing for a *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*, for you and for all that is yours, with all that is good in body and soul.

And now, I will address the comments in your letter:

1) You comment on what I wrote in *Likutei Haggadah*, p. 5, "The Levites recite the Hallel," that this is not so simple, because according to Rashi (Pesachim 64a, Sukkah 54b), the Israelites recited the Hallel.

Now, what I wrote is the language of the *Seder Korban Pesach* of the Yaavetz, and I did not add anything of my own, but merely cited the source in the Tosefta.

Regarding the substance of the matter: The Rambam has already ruled (*Hilchos Korban Pesach*, ch. 1, halacha 11) that the Levites recite the Hallel, and as of now, I have not found a *posek* who disagrees **explicitly** with this opinion (and regarding Rashi’s opinion, see below). It is well known that Rashi is an expositor and not a *posek*, and in his commentaries, he is accustomed to explaining things closer to the literal meaning, even if the *halacha* is not so (see *Yad Malachi*, *Klalei Rashi HaMekurim*, and elsewhere).

Furthermore: The fact that you brought Rashi’s opinion seems to be a result of following the language of the Tosafos in Sukkah there in a superficial manner, as well as the opinion of the *Minchas Chinuch*, mitzvah 364. But if you were to say that Rashi comes to state and innovate in his commentary that the Israelites also recited the Hallel, there are several difficulties with this: a) Why did he not explain in "Tiku" (they blew) who the ones blowing were? b) He should have said "it applies to all," and the word "all" is superfluous. c) And this is the main point: This opinion is the opposite of what is written in the Tosefta, as stated in Tosafos in Sukkah there. And even if you were to say that since there is no wine here, the Israelites are also **permitted** to sing this, similar to what is written in the *Minchas Chinuch* there, it is still a matter of *tzarich iyun* what **compelled** Rashi to disagree with the Tosefta, and where is the source for this?

Now, we are obligated to resolve the words of the Rishonim, even if it appears to us that they are in contradiction to an explicit statement of our Sages. However, this applies **when it is clear** that this is the opinion of the Rishon, whereas when there is doubt in the matter, the opposite is true.

In the present case, since the contradiction to this opinion from the Tosefta is **clear**, it appears to me that Rashi never intended this opinion. Rashi’s intent is simple: In the Mishnah (Pesachim there), it explains the entire order of the *Korban Pesach* **until the completion** of the first group, and it concludes, "As the procedure of the first group, so was the procedure of the second and third; they recited the Hallel if they finished, etc." In a superficial study, it implies that it is speaking only of the second and third groups, for if the first group also recited the Hallel, it should have been taught in the order of the first group in its place. Therefore, Rashi explains that it **"applies to all** the groups." And this is **consistent** with what Rashi is **concerned** to explain in Sukkah there, that "**every** group recites," for there is no practical difference in the *sugya* there whether the Levites recite or the Israelites also recite, as is understood—(and the reason it did not teach "they recite the Hallel" in the order of the first group is because there were many matters, as Rabbi Yehudah disagrees)—and Rashi is speaking only of the **time** of the recitation of the Hallel, which is also during the time of the offering of the first group, **and regarding this**, the Mishnah is also speaking. But he does not come to explain who the one reciting is, just as he did not explain who the one blowing was, because **the Mishnah itself** does not deal with this. Through this, all the aforementioned precision and more are resolved.

And also in Tosafos Sukkah (54a, top), it can be said that he only came to **explain** the language of Rashi, so that we would not err and say that all the **members** of the group recited, and the Tosafos did not bring this in the language of a question or refutation. This is not like the interpretation of the *Minchas Chinuch* on the words of the Rav (the Bartenura).

2) You raise a difficulty in your letter regarding what I wrote in *Likutei Haggadah*, p. 7, "that it is proven in the Mishnah and in the Yerushalmi that even during the time of the Beis Hamikdash they would take two cooked dishes," and you write regarding this, "that there is no such implication in the Mishnah and in the Yerushalmi; it is impossible that there should be such an implication, it is **simple** that they were instituted after the destruction."

Now: a) It is very difficult for me that you would consider me so mistaken, that I would write—and in print—**"it is proven"** in a place where "it is impossible that there should even be an implication, and it is simple" the opposite, especially when I also cited the source for my words. b) I would not have believed that you would write the above without first looking, at least in a cursory manner, at the Mishnah and the Yerushalmi **in their place**.

The language of the Mishnah in the Bavli **in its place** (Pesachim 114a) is: "They brought before him matzah, lettuce, charoses, **and two cooked dishes... and in the Mikdash** they would bring before him the body of the Pesach." And the language of the Yerushalmi in its place (Pesachim, ch. 10, end of halacha 3) is: **"And in the provinces** they require two cooked dishes, one as a remembrance, etc."

The publication of the collection has been halted for the time being due to the burden of preparing for print the *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—*maamarei d'chassidus*.

To conclude with a matter of Rosh Hashanah: I found in the library of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, his book *HaMoadim B'Halacha*, and I saw there, in passing, that he brings several discussions regarding the fact that we do not blow [the Shofar] on a Yom Tov of Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos, as a decree lest one carry it. It is a pity that he seemingly overlooked the surprising innovation of our Rebbe HaZaken (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 588:4), that the reason we do not blow is because of "weekday activities" (*uvdin d'chol*), see there. And based on this, one can resolve the lengthiness of the Rambam’s language in *Hilchos Shofar*, ch. 2, halacha 6.

With the blessing of *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 297

B"H, 7th of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Temimim, etc., may they live:

Peace and blessing!

During these days, I wish to express my blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chatimah tovah* for you and all that is yours.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning *pnimiyus Abba* and *pnimiyus Atik*: when you examine the places in *Hemshech 5666* that are marked in my note (in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*, p. 6), you will see that the goal is to reach the essence of the simple *taanug* which is higher than *pnimiyus Atik*—which is *pnimiyus Abba*. And one arrives at this through the performance of the *mitzvah* (or by being precise in matters of *chochmah*).

Now, regarding knowing which *mitzvah* one should be particularly careful with—this is not a matter of intellectual grasp (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 7), and consequently, it is easy to err due to the enticements of the *yetzer*. For, as is understood, the *yetzer* strives all the more to mislead one in this. Therefore, one of the best pieces of advice is to follow the path and *avodah* that one’s Rebbe points out to him with his finger. At that point, one should not come with arguments and requests as to whether the Rebbe might change his decision; and certainly, one should not look to the right or to the left to see if he might find some other matter to occupy himself with.

For example: My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe *shlita*, charged you, as I recall, with the *avodah* of *Melach* and *Machaneh* in your city (and perhaps also in your country). If so, it is simple that you should not seek out or occupy yourself with investigations into what the *avodah* of others consists of, nor should you chase after matters for yourself that you do not know if they belong to you or not—at least until you have fully fulfilled the role incumbent upon you, which was pointed out to you with the finger, saying: This is **your** path that leads to the House of G-d, and in this you will succeed.

After a few years of this, it is impossible to deceive others, or even yourself, because the deeds will prove the situation as it is: "I have brought such-and-such a number of boys and girls closer to a proper education; so-and-so began to put on *tefillin* through my efforts; in such-and-such a number of homes, they began to study and read proper books instead of improper ones; so-and-so and so-and-so began to study *Toras HaChassidus*; I have distributed such-and-such a number of proper books, and especially of *Toras HaChassidus*, etc., etc."

Now, if there is a deficit in the count, even though there are certainly reasons for it—especially the reason of the fear of a human being, who is a master of his own choice, and therefore he is righteous and innocent—nevertheless, the light is missing. But if one is not deterred and does his part, and the count matches, then through this gate all of his *Torah* and *mitzvos* ascend, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* there.

With wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 290

B"H, 7th of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, 5708

To the esteemed Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing and man of many accomplishments,
Moreinu HaRav Avraham Aharon,
May he live, HaKohen

Peace and Blessing!

During these days, I wish to extend my wishes for a *chasimah v'gmar chatimah tovah* to you and your entire household.

Regarding the theme of these days: The Rambam writes (*Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* 7:7), "And why do we not establish the calendar such that these days [Rosh Hashanah] fall on *Aleph, Dalet, Vav*... we establish a day of determination and a day of postponement." He does not explain "what sin did *Aleph, Dalet, Vav* commit that they should not be [days of Rosh Hashanah]... and what did the other days merit," as the Raavad questions in his *Hasagos* there.

It can be suggested that the first day of Rosh Hashanah, which is Rosh Chodesh Tishrei, is a *dina kashya* (harsh judgment). Therefore, it is postponed from falling on *Aleph* (the first day of the seven days of creation, which is the *sefirah* of *Chesed*) and on *Dalet* (the fourth day, which is the *sefirah* of *Netzach*, also from the right line). And since it is impossible to have two consecutive days of postponement, the only day remaining for the third postponement is *Vav*. It seems more likely to me that *Vav* is postponed because the *Yesod* of the day of *Vav* is the sweetening of the *Gevuros*, as hinted in the words of our Sages (*Pesachim* 54a): "Why was 'it is good' not said on the second day of the week? Because the fire of Gehinnom was created on it... He returned and included it **on the sixth**." See the gloss of the Mahari Algazi there.

With this, we can further understand a nuance: since the Rambam surely had a reason for the postponement of *Aleph, Dalet, Vav* specifically, as the Raavad noted, why did he not explain it?

If the reason is as stated above, it is understood, and in accordance with what is explained in *Sefer HaSichos* (Summer 5700, p. 41) in the name of the Baal Shem Tov, that the Rambam was a *mekubal* (see my note there regarding this), but he was careful not to reveal it, even by way of allusion, because it was dangerous to do so in his time.

With blessings for a *gmar chatimah tovah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Cover them with loose earth—*bitul*. And then one perceives the *ki bayom hazeh yechaper* (for on this day He shall provide atonement)."

Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, Erev Sukkos, 5708

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man of many accomplishments,
Rabbi A. A. [Yales]
Cohen

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter from the day after Yom Kippur, and since time does not permit an extensive reply, I will be brief:

1) Regarding what you wrote in your letter—that the fact that the first day of Rosh Hashanah is *dina kashya* (harsh judgment) is not in the category of *middos* (attributes), such as the seven days of *binyan* (construction)—I was astonished. How can one say such a thing when the Gemara, Zohar, *Pri Etz Chaim*, *sefarim* of *mussar*, etc., are full of the fact that Rosh Hashanah and the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* are days of judgment, that He sits on the throne of judgment, and the world is judged, etc., etc.

In *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Rosh Hashanah*, chapters 1-2: "And on the first day of Rosh Hashanah, the *nissirah* (sawing/separation) occurs from the head of *Ze’er Anpin* down to his *Tiferes* inclusive, and because it receives all these *nissiros* on this day, it is therefore *dina kashya*... The intent of the *nissirah*... is to give the *dinim* (judgments) that are in *Ze’er Anpin* to it [the *Nukvah*]... the *dinim* of the masculine are strong in the head, and therefore the first day is called *dina kashya*." And there are many other places with this phrasing.

2) Regarding the proof you brought from the fact that Rosh Hashanah is the *binyan* (construction) of *Malchus*—on the contrary, this is proof for the opposite, as it is known that the *binyan* of *Malchus* comes from the *Gevuros*, except that their root is from a higher source.

3) You brought proof from the fact that on the day of *dina kashya*, the ascent is in the *pnimiyus* (internal aspect), and on the day of *dina rafya* (lenient judgment), it is in the *chitzoniyus* (external aspect). Apparently, your proof is based on the assumption that *din* is simply *Gevurah*, but in fact, the opposite is the case.

However, the language of *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Rosh Hashanah*, chapter 4, is: "The matter is that on the first day, the worlds are not yet able to be included, **only** the *pnimiyus* **alone**, and therefore it is *dina kashya*. But on the second day, then **all the worlds** are sweetened... first one must include the *pnimiyus*, and afterwards, on the second day, **the worlds** are also included."

4) You bring proof from the fact that on Rosh Hashanah, *Malchus* is drawn from its source from above to above, and then a new light is drawn down that has never existed before, etc.

It is true that this is so, but it is not because of this that Rosh Hashanah is *dina kashya*. On the contrary, as mentioned above, this is accomplished through the *tekios*, which sweeten the *dinim*. (And this is also accomplished specifically through the *Gevuros* of the name *Elokim*. See *Likutei Torah*, *d.h. Sos Asis*, end of chapter 4. And there is judgment regarding this, as is known in the interpretation of "judgment for the G-d of Yaakov," except that "judgment is mercy," **because through the *tekios*** He sits on the throne of mercy).

5) You challenge my words regarding the fact that the first Rosh Hashanah—the day Adam HaRishon was created—was on a Friday (*Vav*). Even without what I wrote, this needs to be resolved, for surely the rule of "not *Adu* Rosh" (Rosh Hashanah cannot fall on Alef, Dalet, or Vav) has a reason in the *nistar* (hidden Torah), like all other matters of the Torah. If so, how did the first Rosh Hashanah happen to fall on a Friday?

What seems to me is that although even on the first Rosh Hashanah it is said that it is *dina kashya* (*Pri Etz Chaim*, ibid.), it is still not comparable to the *dina kashya* of Rosh Hashanah from that point onward: a) In the creation of Adam HaRishon, meaning before the sin, the state of the worlds and the *Sefiros* was higher than how they are now (*Likutei Torah* to the Arizal, end of *Parshas Bereishis*, and *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaShabbos*, chapter 23), and consequently, the *dinim* were not as harsh. b) Another proof that the *dinim* were not as harsh then is that all matters were done because "He desires kindness," whereas now there is *din* and *mishpat*, and the matter depends on *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below). (And therefore they say it is only a **remembrance** of the first day. *Likutei Torah*, *d.h. V'hayah Bayom HaHu Yitka*, end of chapter 1). Since, in any case, there were *dinim* even on the first Rosh Hashanah, it did not fall on *Alef* or *Dalet*, which are from the line of the right. But since they were not harsh (and perhaps to indicate the difference between this Rosh Hashanah and those that followed), it fell on *Vav*, which is not from the line of the right but leans toward it.

And there is a third point: The reason it does not fall on *Vav* now, according to what I wrote in my first letter, is because the second day is included in it in "very good." But the inclusion of the second day in "very good" was only accomplished by and after the creation of man, in accordance with the literal meaning of the verse, and therefore this reason does not apply to the first Rosh Hashanah.

6) You wrote to resolve the words of the Rambam in *Kiddush HaChodesh* (7:7) based on what is written in the *Tashbetz*, that the reason of "the vegetables and the dead" is not sufficient to push off the holidays, but it is enough to establish the days of postponement for *Adu*.

I did not at all argue in my letter that the Rambam did not use the reason of the Gemara. For although the *Tashbetz* is not before me, the above is explained in the commentary of the *Rosh* on Rosh Hashanah and in the commentary of the *Yad* **on the spot** (and the *Binah L'Itim* by Rabbi Ginzburg resolves the words of the Rambam similarly, even though he did not mention the *Tashbetz*). What I wrote was only a transcription of the *Ravad's* critique, that the Rambam begins "Why do we not establish... on *Adu*," and in the end, he does not explain "what is the sin of *Adu*... and what is the merit of *Gahaz*." And regarding this, one cannot argue that he relied on the fact that the reasons are explicit in the Gemara, because that is the **opposite** of the Rambam's way in every place—to bring **specifically** what is explicit in the Gemara, as is known in the rules of the Rambam.

Furthermore, if so, "this author did not act in the manner of the Sages... he began with questions and difficulties and left the matter as a difficulty" (language of the *Hasagos*, *Teshuvah* chapter 5). This is not the case according to what I wrote, that the reason is that the Rambam did not want to reveal even by way of allusion from the wisdom of Kabbalah; then the above is resolved.

And with this, one can also resolve the *Ravad's* critique in *Hilchos Teshuvah* mentioned above, because there, too, the Rambam was silent for this reason.

And while I am speaking of the rule of "not *Adu* Rosh," I will note that according to the opinion of Rav Hai Gaon, brought in the commentary of the *Rosh* (Shabbos 115a; and see also Sukkah 43b), it is a *Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai*! (And see the commentary of the *Yad* there in the commentary of the *Rosh* on Rosh Hashanah in *She'iltos*, *Parshas Vayakhel*). The explanation of this rule according to the *Sod* (secret) is in the *Hagahos HaRamaz*, end of *Mevo HaShemesh*—Jerusalem edition—section 174.

7) You wrote to note that in the Gemara, the phrase "Great is *teshuvah*" appears eleven times: eight in the revealed [Talmud] and two in the hidden [Zohar]. I am in doubt as to your intent, because in *Yoma* (86a and there) alone, according to the version of the *Ein Yaakov*, it appears ten times **and not nine**.

And to note what is difficult: at the end of the *sefer Reishis Chochmah*, all the statements of "Great is..." in the Gemara regarding *teshuvah* are collected, and he brings only four—and this is also copied in *Midrash Talpiyot*—(and one of them is not in the Gemara: "that it brings the distant ones near").

8) Regarding the term "ten days **between**," which includes the boundaries, I saw in the book *Shiurei Torah* by Rabbi Naeh (a book unique in its kind, and worthy of attention), page 210 (from the statement of our Sages, Rosh Hashanah 6b, "There is nothing between *Atzeres* and *Atzeres* and nothing between Rosh Hashanah and Rosh Hashanah except four days," which includes one of the boundaries).

With blessings for a *chag sameach* and all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 202

B"H, 1st Day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished, the Temimim, Moreinu Harav Sh. [Sholom] Shuv,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your inquiry regarding the recitation of Selichos during Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, I am transcribing here from my notes from Tishrei 5691 in Riga, and Tishrei 5708 in Brooklyn:

Tishrei 5691:

**Customs:** After Rosh Hashanah, one does not recite Selichos.

**Rosh Hashanah Sicha:** The Ruzhiner would go to Tashlich not on Rosh Hashanah, but on the 13 Attributes (the days of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah).

While I was in the United States—in New York—last year, I went to Tashlich a few days before Rosh Hashanah, on Motzaei Rosh Hashanah, and on the 13 Attributes.

The Tzemach Tzedek would recite the 13 Attributes. The Rabbanit (wife of the Rebbe Rashab) would also recite them, and there would be a special minyan for her, because the Rebbe Rashab would not come to the minyan to recite them (if he recited them in private—it was not stated clearly. But it seems "between the lines" that even in private he did not recite Selichos after Rosh Hashanah).

**From the Sichos of Tishrei, 5708:** The wife of the Rebbe Rashab, her mother-in-law (the wife of the Tzemach Tzedek), and also the wife of the Mitteler Rebbe would recite Selichos during Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, but the men would not.

My grandfather (the Rebbe Rashab) related to my father (the Rebbe Rayatz) that once, seeing that his mother was going to Selichos—during Aseres Yemei Teshuvah—while his father (the Tzemach Tzedek) was sitting and learning, he asked him about this. The Tzemach Tzedek replied: "There is a time when one must speak, and there is a time when one must act."

In response to my question regarding the instruction to recite Selichos on Tzom Gedaliah, the Rebbe Rayatz replied: "Tzom Gedaliah is, after all, one of the four fasts."

With regards and blessings,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Due to the holiday, I have not signed my name.

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 382. Collected in Yagdil Torah (N.Y.), Issue 2, p. 7, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

With wishes for all the best,
