## 44

B"H, 24 Tishrei, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav M. Sh. HaKohen,

Greetings and blessings!

I had certainly expected that, as in every year, you would come here for the days of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah, so that we could meet and converse. Apparently, various circumstances have hindered you, and you were unable to realize this trip.

It is a pity, for as our Sages of blessed memory state (Rosh Hashanah 16b), a person is obligated to appear before his Rebbe on the festival. See the *Kesef Mishneh* in Rambam, *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, chapter 5, halachah 7.

Now, although nowadays people are lenient regarding the aforementioned, and several reasons have been offered for this, there is yet another dimension to this matter.

This is based on the well-known question regarding what we say in our prayers: "And we are unable to ascend, appear, and bow down before You." Seemingly, "to ascend and appear" is impossible because of the hand [of the nations that prevents us], etc., but "bowing down" is something that can be done in any place before Him, may He be blessed, as we say, "And we kneel and bow down," etc. Why, then, is the Beis Hamikdash specifically required for this?

The answer to this is that there are two levels of bowing down: 1) An external bowing, where one bows with his **body**, or a higher level of external bowing, where through actual deed—which depends on his **body**—he will not rebel against the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. 2) An internal bowing, which is the state of nullifying one’s **will** before the will of the Holy One, blessed be He, such that he has no other will or desire at all. This is the bowing of the **soul**. This bowing was something that the Jewish people would receive through the "appearing" on the festivals in the Beis Hamikdash. And since the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, even though we cannot bow down [there], the holiness of this illumination has spread—at least to a small degree—into the *mikdash me'at*, the shul and the beis medrash, specifically during the time of *davening* (see *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Berachah, the first *maamar* beginning "Mizmor Shir," chapter 2, at length).

Now, we see tangibly that to reach the level of "nullifying your will, your intellect, and all the powers of your soul" without assistance is very difficult. For when one recognizes his own worth, he will not find a sufficient reason to nullify his own will entirely. On the contrary, if he reaches the recognition and resolution that he must nullify his own will, then a person who arrives at such a resolution is already a *yerei shamayim* of a significant level. If so, it is then difficult to understand why he should not rely on the resolutions of his own intellect and will. The advised counsel is that he should seek help from a person whom he acknowledges stands on a level higher than his own, and who has no ulterior motives, *chas v'shalom*, in these matters. For then, he will surely listen to his directive regarding how he should conduct himself in the ways of *avodas Hashem*. The auspicious time for this is during the three festivals, analogous to how it was during the time when the Beis Hamikdash existed. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this be fulfilled through the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, at least to the extent that can be conveyed in writing, until you are able to see him face-to-face.

I sign with best wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 205

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent man, who conducts his affairs with integrity,
Rabbi Y. H. HaKohen, may he live,

I had anticipated that we would see each other here during Sukkos (as was your custom, to come to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, for those days) and wish each other a *pesikta tava* for a good and joyous year. Unfortunately, you did not come this year.

I hope that all is well with you and your family, may they live, in good health.

Among the virtues of the Kohanim and their *avodah*—which exist even after the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash—is *nesi'as kapayim* during *davening*, as our *batei knesiyos* are indeed called *mikdash me'at*.

One of the things that *aliyah leregel* to the Beis HaMikdash used to accomplish for a Yid, as Chassidus explains, is that he would *hishtachaveh* (prostrate himself)—and not only externally, with the body, but also with his *neshamah*. That is to say, he would *batel* all the *kochos* of his *neshamah*—*ratzon*, *sechel*, and *midos*—to the *Ribono shel Olam*. Consequently, it is understood that a *beis kneses* where this *hishtachaus penimis* is carried out most effectively is more of a *mikdash me'at*, closer to the virtue of the Beis HaMikdash.

A Chossid finds this when he *davens* in the *beis medrash* of his Rebbe, for every Chossid is, more or less, *batel* to his Rebbe. And a Chossid who is a Kohen performing *nesi'as kapayim* in the *beis medrash* of his Rebbe is, in comparison to *nesi'as kapayim* in an ordinary *beis medrash*, closer to *nesi'as kapayim* in the Beis HaMikdash (which was incomparably greater than *nesi'as kapayim* in the provinces; see *Mishnah Sotah 37b*).

As you know, every year on Simchas Torah morning, according to the order of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the *pesukim* of **Atah Hareisa** are sold for the benefit of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. This year, since you were not here, I was initially in doubt as to what to do: a) whether to purchase a *pasuk* for you, and b) if so, for what amount, especially since you had not written regarding this.

However, subsequently, taking into account that: a) according to the language of the Alter Rebbe (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, ch. 16), "It has not been hidden from me the distress of the times, that livelihood has diminished... yet despite this, they do not act well... by closing their hand which had always been open to give with a full hand and a generous eye"; b) *tzedakah* is not merely a loan to Hashem... and He will repay him twofold in this world; c) one must be concerned... when his peers are counted for a *mitzvah* and he is not counted with them; d) as I once heard from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, "one should not show a path toward diminishing"; e) *zachin l'adam shelo bifanav* (one may act for the benefit of another in his absence)—it remained with me that I, **on my part**, must calculate and decide that **just as in previous years**, you are purchasing a *pasuk* for the same amount (*chai* times *chai* dollars).

The *pesukim* of "Atah Hareisa" on Simchas Torah morning, which were purchased for those who were not here, were recited by the Rebbe, my father-in-law.

With blessings for all the best for you and your entire family, may they live,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad HaPoel

In a separate package, our latest publications have been sent to you; please confirm that you have received them.

In response to your letters (and it is strange that you do not write which address I should use to write to you):

3) I will be able to inform you of the prices for the other seforim once you inform me of the printing and binding costs.

4) Rabbi Gorodetzky told me that he has already sent you one thousand *tarmchan* as you requested. I have arranged with him that he will provide more, as you will inform us. You should also take the proceeds from the aforementioned sales to cover the printing and binding expenses.

5) I am sure you have already begun printing the *Shulchan Aruch*; please expedite this and strive to ensure that both the printing and the binding are of the highest possible quality. I am awaiting clarification here regarding some details for the title page, and then I will send it to you.

6) You will surely find *Shaar HaEmunah* and *Shaar HaYichud* among *anash* in your camp or in Paris.

7) I am writing the response of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, to your personal question below*.

With wishes for all the best,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 208

8 Cheshvan, 5708

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and wise, etc., Moreinu Harav R. Sh. Y.
May he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the 18th of Cheshvan.

**Regarding the Recitation of Hallel during the Slaughtering of the Pesach Offering**

1) Before I comment on what I understood from your letter, I wish to emphasize once again what I already wrote in my previous letter—perhaps without the necessary emphasis—and that is: Regarding this matter, we find it explicitly stated in the Tosefta *ad loc*, and likewise in Tosafos and the Rambam, that the Leviim are the ones who recite the Hallel. Now, there is a desire to **innovate** a dispute and a view that Rashi disagrees with the aforementioned and holds that all of Israel recited the Hallel. Regarding this, I wrote that the basis for saying that Rashi disagrees is something I have found, for the time being, only in the **wording** of Rashi in Pesachim and Sukkah, and the wording of Tosafos in Sukkah; this basis does not at all compel or suffice to **innovate a dispute** and a strange opinion.

Furthermore, in that very wording of Rashi, it is more reasonable to say that **this is not** Rashi’s intent, as I have already written.

Now, you write in your letter that in Rashi on Pesachim, it is correct to say that Rashi did not intend to explain that the Israelites also recited the Hallel, but in Rashi on Sukkah, it is difficult to say so. Consider this: According to this, in Pesachim—which is the place where this law is discussed—Rashi did not set out to explain the aforementioned, yet in Sukkah, where the Mishnah is brought only to inform us of the **number** of blasts sounded during the slaughtering of the Pesach, for which it is **only** necessary to know that **three** groups recited the Hallel three times, Rashi would explain the law of whether the Israelites recite it!—and I have already written that the language of Tosafos in Sukkah can also be resolved. Even if you say it is a forced resolution, it is far more forced to say that Rashi, by way of allusion (and in his commentary **not in its proper place**, in Sukkah, as per your words), disagrees with the explicit Tosefta *ad loc*, without citing a source.

You further write that there is a "Talmudic statement that is almost explicit that the Israelites recited [it],"—but surely, one must perforce resolve this statement according to the view of Tosafos and the Rambam, and if so, the same applies to Rashi.

Regarding the essence of your proof from the Sages (Pesachim 95b and 117b): "Is it possible that the Israelites slaughter their Pesach offerings and take their lulavim and not recite Hallel?"—it is proven that "this is not an *avodah* of the offering but a special law, and the Israelites are the ones who recite it, just as with the lulav." Your proof seems to be twofold: a) Since it is not an *avodah*, it does not pertain to the Leviim. b) Just as the Israelites recited it with the lulav, so too must it be with the Pesach.

One may say: a) Since this is a law **pertaining to the offering**, the law of Leviim applies here—(and note the reason Rashi gives on 95b, s.v. *Efshar*—that since it is a matter of a mitzvah, it requires Hallel. It seems his intent is that **in addition** to the **joy** of the matter, there is a mitzvah here, and the mitzvah is the **offering of the sacrifice**. This requires further study). b) As to who recites it: It may be said that it is stated for separate cases: with the lulav, everyone recites it, and with the Pesach—the Leviim. This **corresponds** to the nature of the mitzvah, for the taking of the lulav is a mitzvah performed with one’s body, which everyone performs, and therefore everyone must recite the Hallel; whereas **in the slaughtering** of the Pesach, only one person slaughters (Kiddushin 41b) as an agent, and therefore the recitation of the Hallel is also performed by the Leviim, who are "given, given" from the Children of Israel. (And one should examine what is written in the book *Maaseh Nissim* by R. A. Maimon, Chapter 1, cited in the commentary on *Sefer HaMitzvos* by R. Saadia Gaon, by Rabbi Perla, *Mitzvos Aseh* 59-60). It is obvious that I do not wish to link this to the dispute of whether the Kohanim are agents of the Merciful One, etc.

A note in passing: According to the aforementioned opinion that "is it possible that the Israelites slaughter, etc."—then one who did not happen to have a lulav until after the prayer must recite Hallel again!

The responsa *Tzafnas Paneach* Vol. II and the book *Chukas HaPesach* are not at hand.

And note the description of the order of the Pesach offering brought in *Seder HaDoros* (year 3775), which writes that the Kohanim recited the Hallel. And in the version of this account in *Sefer Yaavetz*, it says that the owner of the offering also recited it. The book *Shevet Yehudah*, from which the aforementioned was copied, is not at hand for comparison.

**Regarding Two Cooked Dishes on the Seder Night**

You are upset with me for suspecting that you did not examine the Mishnah and the Yerushalmi, but what can I do when your first letter states: "**It is simple** that it was instituted **after the destruction**... and in the Yerushalmi there is **no** indication that even **on the Seder night** they took two cooked dishes, **and it is impossible** that there should be such an indication." And in the second letter, you yourself write: "From there (the Yerushalmi) it is implied that on the Seder night... they brought two cooked dishes." Furthermore, in the second letter, I did not know how to argue regarding such a thing, because after discussing in the letter that the Yerushalmi brings the *baraita* "It was taught: and in the provinces they require two cooked dishes," you conclude, "And it appears that this is what they added in the Yerushalmi to the Mishnah, for the Mishnah deals only with the present time, and therefore they said 'it was taught' that even in the provinces, etc."

At the same time, the *baraita* in the Yerushalmi is understood simply by one who examines the Mishnah there, for in the Yerushalmi’s version of the Mishnah, the custom that one must bring two cooked dishes is not mentioned, and therefore the *baraita* informs us of this. Thus, there is no place for this *baraita* in the Bavli. Therefore, it is impossible to say that the intent of the *baraita* is to say that **even** in the provinces, and not only in the present time, they would bring two cooked dishes, for we have not yet heard of the custom of two cooked dishes at all.

- And see Tosafos s.v. *Teirum* in Bechoros 22b, and other disputes between the Bavli and Yerushalmi regarding the versions of the Mishnah.

And if one wishes to bring some proof from the *baraita* regarding the time the Mishnah was stated, on the contrary, it implies that the Mishnah—and likewise the *baraita*—was stated in the time of the Temple, since it says "and in the provinces"—and did not add: "and in the present time in every place." It is not a conclusive proof, for the present time comes by way of an *a fortiori* argument from the provinces in the time of the Temple, and it did not need to be specified. It is simple.

Regarding the essence of the matter: a) It is simple that outside of Jerusalem they would not bring the Pesach offering itself. If so, what is written in the Mishnah, "In the Temple they would bring, etc.," speaks only of Jerusalem and the time of the Temple. b) It is simple that after the destruction, in every place **and on the Seder night** outside of Jerusalem, they would bring two cooked dishes, as I wrote regarding the Yerushalmi, and no one is found to disagree with this in the Bavli.

However, my intention is to say that the Mishnah, which is taught **without qualification**, explains the law for all times, all places, and all people, and what is written in the Mishnah that they bring two cooked dishes is a law for **all** times and **all** places, except for what is explained in the latter part: "and in the Temple they would bring, etc." But you say: No, the Mishnah speaks of the law of Jerusalem in the time of the Temple and the law of every place in the present time, and skips the law of outside Jerusalem in Eretz Yisrael and in all the Diaspora (where the **majority** of the nation was) in the time of the Temple, even though their law is equal to the present time!

I will now come to your difficulties with my explanation:

a) "Is it possible that the Mishnah would speak of the exception and the secondary (the sick and the Diaspora) and afterwards say 'and in the Temple, etc.'?"

I do not understand, for according to my explanation, on the contrary, the first part of the Mishnah speaks of all times, all places, and all people, except for the pure and healthy who were found in Jerusalem in the time of the Temple and were counted for the Pesach offering (Indeed, it is still a matter of study whether those found **in Jerusalem** for whom it is impossible to bring the Pesach offering itself must bring a remembrance. But from the simple language, it is implied that they bring before him one of these two: two cooked dishes or the Pesach offering).

- And seemingly, even if you say that the Mishnah was stated in the time of the Temple (even though it does not appear so to me), there is no difficulty, for the majority of the nation was in the Diaspora. See Shekalim, end of chapter 3.

b) "Where do we find that Jerusalem **alone** is called the Temple?"

It is in Shekalim 1:3: "On the 15th of the month, tables [and Rashi—Megillah 29b—explains: tables of the **money changers**] etc., in these **they sat in the Temple**." And see in the Yerushalmi Pesachim, end of chapter 5, that the "sitting" in the Mishnah means actual sitting, and it is not an impediment. If so, it is impossible that it was in the actual Temple, but rather on the Temple Mount and in Jerusalem.

And in the Bavli (Sotah 40b), it is also mentioned that it is " **profane** like the rest of the Temple Mount" (Rashi there). And that which is in Kelim (1:8) is only a rabbinic decree. The same applies to our case. (And it has not escaped me what the Rav Ovadiah of Bartenura and others wrote in Shekalim there. And it must be said that they interpret that even the Temple Mount—the camp of the Leviim—is included in the "Temple" according to Rashi! Or they interpret "sitting" as sitting on the tables and not on the money changers, contrary to Rashi. And I am not responsible for reconciling the words of all the commentators into one opinion). And it is likewise in the Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah, Rosh Hashanah, beginning of chapter 4: "Jerusalem as a whole **is called** the Temple."

His intent is as it sounds, that Jerusalem **is called** the Temple, not that the law of Jerusalem is like the law of the Holy Temple. (And note also the *Tiferes Yisrael* at the beginning of chapter 4 of Rosh Hashanah).

And as for your suggestion that the dispute between Rashi and the Rambam in Rosh Hashanah (beginning of chapter 4) regarding the definition of "Temple" is relevant here—this had long occurred to me, because of the difficulties the commentators raised regarding both views, for they only disagreed where the Mishnah itself did not explain its own words. Therefore, the Mishnahs in Maaser Sheni 3:4, Eruvin end of chapter 10, etc., have no relevance to this dispute. And through this, several other difficulties are removed.

The same applies to our Mishnah, for the Tanna himself explains his words: "In the Temple they would bring, etc.," meaning in the Temple, **where it is possible**, they would bring the Pesach offering itself. "In these they sat in the Temple," in a place where it is possible to sit, and thereby the meaning of the word "in the Temple" is explained.

- Regarding what you wrote in your letter that "the Pesach offerings were eaten only in the entire city and not in the Temple," it is a matter of study whether there is a prohibition against eating Pesach offerings in the Temple. And what you wrote, that they **went out** and roasted their Pesach offerings, is because of the majority of the people who ate the Pesach offering in their homes. But it is also permitted to eat in the Temple, since it is a sacrifice and not profane. Only in the *Heichal* is a special verse needed, for the *Heichal* is not a place of eating at all, were it not for the verse that "in the Holy of Holies you shall eat it," for a person does not eat in the place of his master—Zevachim 63a. And it is a matter of study whether for one eating in the *Azarah* they would bring only the Pesach offering itself or also lettuce, etc., and there are opinions to say that we arrive at the dispute of Rashi and Tosafos (Menachos 21b and elsewhere), or that everyone agrees they bring it, or that everyone agrees they do not bring it. And then it is well understood why, according to the Yerushalmi’s version of our Mishnah, it does not say "and in the Temple they would bring **even** the Pesach offering itself"—and this is not the place to elaborate.

**Regarding the Blowing of the Shofar on Rosh Hashanah that Falls on Shabbos**

You write that you do not see in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe that he holds that we do not blow then because of "weekday activities" (*uvdin d'chol*). But the words of the Alter Rebbe there (*Tikkun* 588:4): "On Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos, we do not blow the shofar, even though the blowing... is forbidden on the holiday... because of 'weekday activities,' and why **do we not override** such a minor prohibition... as we **override** it on **every** Rosh Hashanah that falls on a weekday, etc."

And the surprise is that he explains that we do not blow on Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos because of "weekday activities," and the decree of Rabbah comes to strengthen this *shevus* so that it should not be overridden. Unlike the view of Tosafos (Sukkah 43a and beginning of chapter 4 of Rosh Hashanah), which, according to the *Magen Avraham* and *Machatzis HaShekel*, also holds that we do not blow because there are two *shevusim*, it can be explained that the main point is the decree of Rabbah. And this is like the surface meaning of the **language of the Shas and the Poskim**.

Hoping you will not be upset by my comments, and with wishes for all the best.

**M. Schneerson**

I have heard that, from time to time, you publish in a newspaper in Eretz Yisrael critical articles about books being published. In light of this, since there are few among the G-d-fearing Children of Israel who have the talent for writing and also knowledge of the teachings of Chassidus and its *sichos*—and especially those of Chabad—and in recent times a movement is noticeable among various circles to know the essence of this Torah, and the main thing, *vas arum chassidus iz*, it would, in my opinion, be correct if you dedicated, at least a portion of your articles, to writing about the books of "Otzar HaChassidim"—those that have already been published and are now being published.

## 319

319

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5708
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R. B. Z.
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters:

Surely you have already received the committee’s reply that they may print temporary receipts, with instructions that a formal receipt will be issued later by the committee’s office, without specifying an address.

Several printing materials have been sent to you as you requested, including, via airmail, the biography of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in English, which corresponds to what you asked for. I trust you will confirm receipt of the aforementioned.

In general, there is no need to be overly stringent or to sift through thirteen sieves before speaking about the matter of *Nifneh*—especially considering that in recent years, it has been emphasized more than ever that he is the leader of **all** of Israel, and the communal work is, for the most part, in matters that are relevant to **every** soul, and sometimes even more so to those who are distant from the observance of Torah and mitzvos.

However, on the other hand, one should not speak about this with just anyone, and it goes without saying that one must be wary of those who might later boast, "I have enriched Avram."

There are two points regarding this: 1) It must be done in a manner of **respect** (and all the more so regarding a *talmid chacham*, whom our Sages (Kesuvos 105b) compared specifically to the offering of *Bikkurim*, and not to *Terumah* or the like. And you understand.) on the part of the giver; this is not, G-d forbid, a matter of a *meshulach* (fundraiser). The explanation must be that since not everyone is able to take a direct part in the holy work of the Rebbe—which is, in truth, the obligation of every Jew—by giving *Nifneh*, they: a) remove this burden from him so that this distraction does not interfere with his work. b) And this is the main point: through this, they take some part in his holy work, and because of this, the giving must be in a different manner and in a different amount. There must be an interest in drawing the giver and his family closer, if at all possible, to the general matters of the Rebbe and the customs of Israel, whether through conversation, **with warmth**, or through printed materials (memoirs, sichos, etc.).

Regarding your interest in the state of education, etc., in the places where you are located: this is **one** of the goals of such a mission of yours, but you must not forget the **primary** goal of your trip.

Whatever is already in your hands can be sent—without waiting for additions—to R. Moshe Gourarie, may he live, in Tel Aviv. It is possible that they will soon finish writing the Torah scroll for the reception of the *Penim* (private petitions), and it is appropriate that those who wish to participate in the writing should hasten to do so.

Please be so kind as to urge R. Binyaminson and R. A. Cohen to respond regarding what they were asked by the *Malach* (the committee) concerning what is being done regarding distribution.

I sign with regards to all those who seek your welfare and with best wishes.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Surely you will utilize—*oysnutzen*—the auspicious days: the 20th of Kislev, the 10th, and the 19th of Kislev for the benefit of your mission.

## 310

22 Cheshvan, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with Tzedakah and Chessed, etc., Rabbi Menachem HaKohen Chaikin.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter some time ago. Please forgive the delay in my response, which was due to an overwhelming number of preoccupations.

The books you requested have been sent to you in two packages. A portion of the sichos and maamarim are being covered by the Keren HaMitzvos fund, as you indicated they are for the benefit of the many. Please be kind enough to confirm receipt of the packages.

Regarding your question concerning what is written in the Moreh Nevuchim (Part II, Chapter 42), that the entire episode of Bilaam on the road and the words of the donkey occurred within a prophetic vision, and your question as to what compelled him to move the words of the donkey away from their literal meaning:

The reason is explicitly stated in the commentary of the Ralbag at the beginning of Parshas Balak, which reads: "There are very difficult questions in this narrative... How is it possible for the donkey to see the angel of Hashem, when it is known that one who is not a prophet does not see [an angel], as is written there at the end of Daniel, and the men who were with him did not see [it]... Why did the angel not appear to [Bilaam] first with his sword drawn, which would have achieved the intended purpose... For what benefit was it necessary to create a miracle where the donkey spoke? It is clear that the Holy One, blessed be He, does not perform miracles without necessity... However, the opinion of our Sages is that this matter occurred literally, and therefore they said that the mouth of the donkey was one of the things created at twilight [on the eve of the first Shabbos]."

He then explains what appears to us according to the principles... and from study, etc.—and he explains it as written in the Moreh Nevuchim.

Now, in Maseches Avos it is proven that the matter is literal. One can answer the aforementioned difficulties as follows:

1) How is it possible for a donkey to see the angel, when this is impossible for anyone but a prophet, as is proven in Daniel?

This is not a difficulty according to what is written in the Ramban (Bereishis 18:2), cited in the commentary of the Abarbanel in the Moreh Nevuchim there, that one does not need to be a prophet to see an angel. Alternatively, one can explain it according to the Ramban (Bamidbar 22:33), that the donkey sensed the angel or saw it without understanding the nature of the matter, but turned aside because of the drawn sword, as is the nature of animals.

Even though Bilaam did not sense or see the drawn sword, one can explain this based on what is known (see Tanya, Chapter 23) that the *mazikin* (harmful spirits) are hidden from the eyes of human beings, because since they possess intellect, they would become confused and it would harm them, which is not the case with animals. See also Berachos (6a): "If the eye were given permission to **see**—merely that—no creature could survive..." (And what is explained there regarding the *Goy* Katzen is not the literal meaning of this statement).

See also the Midrash Talpiyos, under the entry *Aton Bilaam*, for an additional reason.

2) Why did the angel not appear to Bilaam first, which would have achieved the intended purpose?

This is not a difficulty according to what is explained in the Zohar (Balak 166b and onwards), that Bilaam’s knowledge was through the donkey, and through his actions with it, he wanted and was able to draw a curse upon Yisrael. Therefore, it was necessary to first negate these sorceries and witchcrafts of his. It should also be noted from our Sages (Berachos 7a) that if not for the anger of the Holy One during all those days, Bilaam would have been able to carry out his plot, which proves that the mere sight of the angel would not have been sufficient.

3) For what benefit was the miracle of the donkey’s speech?

This can be explained according to the above: that through the donkey he sought to curse Yisrael, and it was a "miracle within a miracle" that specifically through it and its argument with him, the nullification of his intent began (similar to what our Sages say—Mechilta, Shemos 15, cited in Yalkut Shimoni—regarding the miracle at Marah, the healing of Hezekiah, and the waters of Yericho. See also Yalkut Shimoni, Remez 765: The ministers of Moav began to wonder, for they saw a miracle the likes of which had never existed in the world).

In Zohar Chadash (209b): "What was achieved... by these words [of the donkey]? Rabbi Yehuda said: The nobles mocked him... and through those words of the donkey, his honor was stripped away. Rabbi Chiya said... and through the words of the donkey he knew that his power was broken... and we learn that there is no power in animals for an 'other spirit' to rest upon them..." (And this is difficult to reconcile with the Tanchuma, cited in Yalkut Shimoni, Remez 765: "He closed the mouth of the animal, for if it had spoken, they would not have been able to withstand it," and it draws an *a fortiori* argument from the debate between the donkey and Bilaam). See also Zohar Chadash 201b.

With anticipation for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

It is understood that I am prepared to answer in the future as well, according to what appears to me, regarding what you ask of me, provided that you do not take offense at the delay in my response due to my preoccupations.

7 Kislev, 5708

Mr. M. S. Slonim
22 Mikveh Israel St., Tel Aviv

Greetings and blessings,

I have seen and borrowed for some time from the library of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, your book *Toldos Mishpachas HaRav MiLiadi*. You have performed a great and useful service with this compilation. However, it seems that several sources were not available to you, particularly those found in manuscript or those related through family tradition. Based on your note at the beginning of the book and in the introduction, and in order to correct matters that are not precise, I wish to offer the following notes, organized by page number:

Page 5, Generation 1: 1874 (in the errata list 1774) — should be 1773.

Page 5: He was 1823 — see page 45 of your book.

Page 5: In the year 1789 — according to the sicha of 19 Kislev 5693, sections 6-8, it is implied that he was born in 1787-1788 and passed away in 1876. There is another version that he was born after the passing of R. Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl and was named after him (letter of 17 Teves 5699).

Page 8: Egypt, the Four Holy Lands — perhaps the intent is that they are permitted to send a *meshulach*; if so, it should have been explained, as it is obscure to the vast majority.

Page 21: The entire page requires correction based on what was printed in the memoirs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, in the sicha of Chai Elul 5705. For example: Due to a movement for freedom from religion and mitzvos that began to spread before the *Haskalah* movement, the grandfather of R. Boruch and his father migrated from Posen. R. Boruch was born in Vitebsk. The Alter Rebbe — in the vicinity of Liozna. R. Yissachar Ber was a *Maggid*, not a Rav.

Page 23: That our Rebbe came to Vilna **before** he was in Mezritch — is disproven. See *HaTamim*, Vol. 2, p. 50, that he was in Vilna in secret during the years 1773-1776, in addition to the time he was there openly with R. Menachem Mendel of Horodok.

Page 24: In the year 1773 they offered him the leadership — disproven, in accordance with the Alter Rebbe’s relationship with R. Avraham HaMalach and R. Menachem Mendel of Horodok. See *HaTamim*, Vol. 2, p. 49 and onwards for the details of the matter.

Page 25: Add that in the year 1794, the Alter Rebbe’s *Hilchos Talmud Torah* was printed.

Page 25: *Adchumah* (Intermediate days of the festival) — this is incorrect, as he was arrested on *Isru Chag* of Simchas Torah (Sicha of 19 Kislev 5693, section 7; *Megillas 19 Kislev*, and elsewhere). Likewise, in the year 1800, he was not arrested on *Adchumah*, as written in your book (see *HaRav MiLiadi*, end of ch. 12; *Mishnas Yoel*, p. 71). This should also be corrected in *Hayom Yom*.

Page 26: Close — should be **more** than ten.

Page 26: The Rebbe wanted to remove, etc., and decided to travel — the Alter Rebbe traveled to assist the villagers (see the Alter Rebbe’s letter regarding this journey, printed in *Ginzei Nistaros*, part *Ohr HaMeir*, 14).

Page 26: Where is it written, etc. — this is a question the Alter Rebbe could not have asked, as the recitation of *U’Shamru* is found in the *Siddur* of the Arizal, in *Magen Avraham*, and elsewhere.

Page 29: Prayed to his sons — a mistake, as the Mitteler Rebbe was in Kremenchug, R. Chaim Avraham was ill (letter of the Mitteler Rebbe in *Sefer HaMichtavim* — manuscript — p. 62), and R. Moshe did not travel with them (ibid.).

Page 31: The passage "Also in these days" and the passage "Through this" are not at all in the style of the Alter Rebbe. I am puzzled as to where they were taken from.

Page 33: a) According to Talmudic foundations?!

Page 33: On the basis of the Ari?!

Page 33: d) *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* was omitted.

Page 33: h) *Bad Kodesh*. The letter of request is to the Mitteler Rebbe (see my preface in the *Otzar HaChassidim* edition of *Bad Kodesh*). The commentary on *Megillas Rus* is by R. Avraham of Stretin. This should also be corrected in *Hayom Yom*.

*HaShif* according to Kabbalah — the intent is likely the *Haggadah Sod Kedoshim* (Warsaw 1886). It is not according to Kabbalah (even though it is written on the title page that the **commentaries** — meaning the *maamarim* of Chassidus printed there — are built upon the foundations of Kabbalah). What appears there from the Alter Rebbe are a few *maamarim* of Chassidus from the *Siddur*, *Likutei Torah*, etc.

Page 46: d) According to Kabbalah **and with the addition** of *D.Ch.* (Divrei Chassidus)! — it is according to the teachings of Chassidus. *Derech Chaim* is the third part of this book.

Page 46: e) *Shaar HaPurim* was omitted.

Page 46: h) *HaMilim* should be *HaMilot* (from the second edition).

Page 46: i) *Maamar HaHisbonenus* — is *Shaar HaYichud* (up to the end of chapter 30).

Page 46: j) Additions to *T.Ch.* — likely should be *Toras Chaim*.

Page 46: k) *Kuntres*, etc. — likely refers to the **second** part of *Shaar HaTeshuvah VeHaTefillah* which was already mentioned.

Page 46: 12 — Add: Born Tammuz 1779.

Page 46: 1814 *HaIgeres HaKedosha* — should be *Igeres HaKodesh*.

Page 46: They say he was her husband, etc. — the father of the Tzemach Tzedek was then in Liozna, and the messenger was R. Yaakov of Smilian (Sicha of 20 Kislev 5693, section 11).

Page 52: a) See above in the note to page 5.

Page 57: In 1825 — likely copied from *Hayom Yom*, and should be 1827. This entire passage should be **placed** as a continuation of the previous passage.

Page 58: Against spying — likely should be Riga.

Page 62: *Ko* — should be *Koach*.

Page 65: z) Approximately should be: Born 2 Iyar 1834.

Page 66: In 1853 Elul — should be Cheshvan. This entire page needs to be changed and filled in according to *Sefer HaToldos — Admur Maharash* (Brooklyn 5707).

Page 83: 140 — should be Mrs. Sterna.

Page 83: 141 — Add: His wife, Mrs. Yocheved of the Schonberg family.

Page 84: 1 — Add: His wife in his first marriage, Malka, daughter of his brother, the Chassid R. Avraham (141).

Page 87: 158 — Correct according to *Sefer HaToldos*, pp. 22-23.

Page 85: Daughter 1868 — should be 1865.

Page 86: At the event of 1878 — should be 1875.

Page 87: In 1899 — the word "Zionist" was omitted (perhaps intentionally).

Page 87: His books — Add: *Chinuch LaNaar* (his first will), *Kuntres Eitz HaChaim*, *Kuntres HaAvodah*, *Toras Shalom* (all published in Brooklyn by the *Otzar HaChassidim* editorial board).

Page 106: After 282 — Add: b) Malka. In her first marriage, wife of her uncle, R. Nachum Schneersohn (1). In her second marriage — wife of R. Pinchas Zanis.

Page 106: c) R. Ben Zion Schneersohn. His wife, Cilia.

Page 107: In the margin of the page it should be: Sons and daughters of 156, 160 (according to the aforementioned *Sefer HaToldos*).

With blessings,

## 312

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5708

To the distinguished and elevated, G-d-fearing, the Rav, our teacher R. Avraham Yehuda Licht,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your book, *Toras HaChinuch*, reached me in due time, and I thank you for it.

I would like to offer a few comments on your aforementioned book, beginning with a general observation: it is a pity that while writing this book, you did not utilize the vast material pertaining to this subject found in the seforim of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im of Chabad Chassidim. Even the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, which you mention a few times, is absent in places in your book where it would have enlightened the reader.

Here are the points I noted as I went through the book, without the proper study due to a lack of time:

**Introduction:** See the *Maamar* on the principles of *chinuch* and guidance (printed in the *Kuntres Chai Elul* 5703 by the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita).

**Page 14, footnote:** See the Rambam’s *Peirush HaMishnayos*, beginning of *Perek Chelek*.

**Page 15, Bava Metzia 118b:** Seemingly, this does not belong in this work.

**Page 16, footnote:** See the Alter Rebbe’s *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 3, in the *Kuntres Acharon*.

**Page 19, second footnote:** "And the fact that it does not count 'educating him in mitzvos' here is because this is included in 'teaching him Torah,' etc." — This is not understood. Furthermore, teaching him Torah is a Torah obligation, while the mitzvah of *chinuch*—according to the majority of *poskim*—is Rabbinic.

**Page 24, Kiddushin 30:** See the aforementioned *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, beginning of Chapter 2.

**Page 27:** See the Mitteler Rebbe’s introduction to the Alter Rebbe’s *Shulchan Aruch*. There are countless other sources, which are cited in the book *Mekoros L’Toldos HaChinuch* by Asaf.

**Page 31, skipping sections:** See the letter of the Tzemach Tzedek on this matter (printed in *Beis Rebbe*, Vol. 3, and in its entirety in the *Kuntres HaTzemach Tzedek V’Tnuas HaHaskalah*).

**Page 41, Megillah and Sotah:** Seemingly, these do not belong in a book of this nature.

**Chapter 11 (which is Chapter 10):** The **subject** is not clarified in your book. In any case, it should have been included in the preceding chapter or the one before that.

**Chapter 17, Berachos, Sanhedrin, Vayikra Rabbah, Kesuvos:** Not relevant here.

**Chapter 29, footnote 2:** Same as above.

With best wishes,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

**Letter of the Tzemach Tzedek:** In his *Igros Kodesh*, Letter 12.

## 563

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Moreinu HaRav Y.
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter (which was undated)—as you requested, I have instructed that a special package be sent to you containing all that has been published recently. Since it is unknown up to what point you have received the publications in order, please consult the list of our publications at the end of *Sefer HaKitzurim* and inform us if you would like us to send more, and how many copies of each.

I will take this opportunity to urge you, again and again, regarding the great necessity of organizing the distribution of our publications in your country (both in *Chassidus* and in English. The latter is most necessary, for through this there is an opening and a hope to push back against the literature written in English that is contrary to Torah and tradition). See the *maamar* of Yom Kippur of this year regarding how all advice is good for reaching the ultimate goal. *V'd'l* (and a word to the wise is sufficient). I am confident that there is no need for elaboration for one such as yourself, so I will be brief.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of the three *kelipos* and how they are differentiated, I am enclosing what I wrote to someone else regarding this question. Incidentally, this will clarify what seemingly requires study in *Tanya*, as will be explained further on...

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was brought yesterday from the *Beis Din*.
Enclosed is a letter regarding the time of the *Siyum HaTorah*.

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 114

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5708

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., the Tamim, Moreinu Harav R. Y. Dubov, Shochet u-Bodek,

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is a Kuntres that was brought from the Beis Din yesterday. I have also sent copies to his colleagues, the Shochet u-Bodek, Moreinu Harav R. A. S. and Moreinu Harav R. Sh., may they live. I am certain they will merit the public through it in an appropriate manner, and the merit of the public depends upon them.

I fear that you may be upset with me for not having replied to your previous letters. But what can I do, when the burdens increase from day to day? Please know that your letters are kept by me, and I do not despair of answering them one by one over time, as I am able. However, certainly—and even for you—there is a priority for printed works, since they reach your honor as well as others, which is not the case with letters. I will now address in this letter what you noted regarding what I wrote in Kovetz Lubavitch:

1) Your honor questions what I explained there (Chapter 5) regarding the fact that for the Ohr Makif of Atzilus to rest, there must be an *atar shalim* (a complete place) in Beriah—arguing that Beriah is distinct and distant from Atzilus, and only an "offspring" light is drawn down, etc.

To my mind, this is not a difficulty, for the Ohr Makif must be drawn down into Beriah and even further below, down to this physical world (see Tanya, Chapter 46, and elsewhere). Therefore, there must be an *atar shalim* there.

2) You note that, seemingly, the performance of the mitzvah of Tefillin—which is also in Atzilus—would be more appropriate to be an *atar shalim* for the Ohr Makif of Atzilus. But even to warn [you], I wrote in the Kovetz there that, in my opinion, "It is understood that this perfection, through which it is possible for this Ohr Makif to rest, must have some connection to it, since it is specifically from that [level] that it is possible for the Ohr Makif to rest... and this is what was previously [mentioned]... drawing down the **Makif** light of the world of Beriah." See there. One can find many examples of this regarding Ohr Makif (just as a *ma'ad* that possesses limits draws down the *ma'ad* that is beyond limits from above). This is certainly true regarding Ohr Pnimi, where the vessel must be in the likeness of the light.

3) Your honor suggests that this is along the lines of the *hishtalshelus* (chaining) of the *kesarim* (crowns) one from another. In my opinion, the concept of the *hishtalshelus* of the *kesarim* is more inclusive. The aforementioned point—that the one drawing down must be akin to that which is being drawn down—applies also to Ohr Pnimi; on the contrary, its **essence** is in Ohr Pnimi, which is limited and becomes enclothed. The *hishtalshelus* of the *kesarim* means that the *keser* of a lower *partzuf* is, in many respects, higher than the Ohr Pnimi of the *partzuf* above it. Furthermore, it is written in the *maamar* "Shuva" (5673) that this *hishtalshelus* is not gradual, but rather that the essence of the being is drawn down, and they are one essence. This is not the place to elaborate.

4) You wonder why I brought an example for *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) resting in an *atar shalim* from what the Rambam writes regarding prophecy, rather than from what is written in Tanya, etc., on this subject. There are two reasons for this: a) The intent of the Kovetz is to draw those who are currently distant from the study of Chassidus closer to it, and to show them that even the *nigleh* (revealed) Torah **necessitates** and hints at the concepts of the hidden Torah. Therefore, I brought the Rambam. b) In the language of the *Yad*—"they direct their minds," "they seek," etc.—one can also interpret the details that were explained in the Kovetz, as I wrote there.

Nevertheless, in note 3 there, I referenced Chassidus—to the primary *maamar*, in my opinion—in Likkutei Torah that discusses these matters.

- See also in Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek, in the *maamar* "B'chaf-hei b'Kislev" (beginning of section 12), where, after elaborating on the distinction between *saba* (elder) and *saba d'savin* (elder of elders), he writes that it is possible to find a root for this in the Torah itself, and he brings [proofs] from the Mishnah and the Rambam.

I conclude with a wish for Chanukah, in Hallel—the revelation of the hidden light that shines with additional light and greater clarity (Shaarei Orah, *maamar* "B'chaf-hei b'Kislev," beginning of chapter 43).

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 315

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav R' S. [Nemtzov], Shochet and Bodek, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Yud-Tes Kislev, which was brought yesterday from the Beis Din. It has also been sent to his colleagues, Moreinu Harav R' Sh. and Moreinu Harav R' Y., may they live, Shochet and Bodek. Surely they will merit the many through it in an appropriate manner, and the merit of the many depends upon them.

In these days between Yud-Tes Kislev and Chanukah, one can say: "The Greeks defiled all the oils in the Sanctuary." The explanation of this is that external wisdoms gained the upper hand. As is known, this refers to the sect of the Hellenists who existed among the Jewish people at that time. Regarding the avodah within the human soul: the intellect of the nefesh habahamis—the human intellect within him—becomes so dominant that it defiles the power of Chabad in the soul. This means that it becomes impossible to grasp or feel any Divine matter or concept, even while, when discussing a physical matter, he is able to contemplate, understand, and grasp it well. But ultimately, one finds "one cruse of oil sealed with the seal of the Kohen Gadol," and from it, one illuminates the Menorah, which is "the candle of Hashem, the soul of man."

Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: after such a great descent, where all the oils in his soul have been defiled, what or who can lift him up from this deep pit? Regarding this, our Sages of blessed memory related that the hand of the Kohen Gadol is involved. The concept of the Kohen Gadol is as stated in the Rambam, Hilchos Kelei HaMikdash, Chapter 5, Halacha 7: "His splendor and his honor are that he sits in the Sanctuary all day... and his home is in Jerusalem—the place of complete awe—and he does not move from there." In every individual, the Kohen Gadol is the point of Yiddishkeit within him, the yechidah of the soul, which is not subject to the "other side" (sitra achra), and therefore it is always in a state of perfection. It is only possible that it may be in a state of "sleep" before one is brought to a test of faith, as is written in Tanya, Chapter 19.

Now, to awaken it from its sleep—even before one is brought to a test—is through one’s hiskashrus to the Kohen Gadol in the general sense, who is the "head of the thousands of Israel," who sits all day in the Sanctuary and never moves from the perfection of awe. He gives to each of those who are connected to him a cruse of oil, from which one can illuminate the candle of his soul, even though the oils were initially defiled. However, one must designate these days not only for hoda'ah—the power of faith and gratitude alone—but there must also be Hallel (Shabbos 21b), which is the grasp and understanding of Elokus: "Know the G-d of your father." This is the essence of the Chassidus of Chabad, for which the day of Yud-Tes Kislev is the Rosh Hashanah. The revelation of the light of the inner dimension of our Torah is drawn down, and it must shine within the inner dimension of our souls.

With best wishes,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 16

20 Kislev, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav R. Sh. Rein, Shochet u’Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for 19 Kislev, which was brought yesterday from the Beis Din. We have also sent it to his colleagues, Moreinu Harav R. Y. and Moreinu Harav R. A. S., Shluchim and Shochet u’Bodek. Surely they will merit the public through it—including those who are currently distant—for the merit of the public depends upon them.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said in one of his sichos that the "bringing close of the distant" must be done in a way that elevates them to him, rather than him descending (from his level of Torah, mitzvos, and tefillah) to them.

This can be understood in connection with the days of Chanukah that are approaching. For although the essence of the miracle was the victory in battle, the miracle is nonetheless attributed primarily to the oil (as explained in Torah Or and Shaarei Orah, in the discourse for the 25th of Kislev).

We find that oil possesses contradictory qualities: 1) It is produced specifically through crushing and beating (Shemos Rabbah, beginning of Parshas Tetzaveh; see also Menachos 88a), which signifies humility. 2) It permeates everything*—which signifies the act of bringing close to everything. Conversely: 3) It does not mix with other liquids (Shemos Rabbah, ibid.), which signifies separation (see also Imrei Binah, Shaar Krias Shema, chapters 54–56). 4) It rises above all other liquids (Shemos Rabbah, ibid.), which signifies transcendence.

Such must be the order of avodah when the time comes to illuminate even the **courtyard and the public domain**, and even until "the foot of the Tarmodai ceases" (which is an acronym for *moredes*—rebellious; see the discourse *Tanu Rabbanan* 5643, and elsewhere): 1) The beginning of his avodah must be *kavei esh*, and "let my soul be as dust to all." 2) Afterward, "love your fellow." If he sees that his fellow is not yet "oil" (his body does not rise and become consumed by the light of his soul, which is the "candle of Hashem"), he must permeate him. 3) He himself does not descend or mix through this; on the contrary, he rises higher and higher through this avodah. 4) Until, ultimately, he is in a state of transcendence—for in and of himself he is nothing, but through his avodah he is an emissary of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. And who can compare to Him? For an emissary of a person is like the person himself, as our Sages of blessed memory said (Bava Basra 75b), "In the future, the tzaddikim will be called by the name of the Holy One, blessed be He."

Signing with wishes for all the best.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

Regarding what is written there concerning "and there are those who are brief" (1:1), "and what is the remedy" (2:1), and "a person should not be" (2:7) — the comparison does not hold up well.

220

B.H., 16 Teves, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, etc., Rabbi D. Bravman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters—although you have surely already received replies to some of them via Rabbi Sh.M. [Kalmanson], may he live:

1) Regarding the Shulchan Aruch: You have surely already received from Rabbi B.G. [Gorodetzky] the draft of the introduction and the instructions for printing the title page. It should read: "Third Heichal, Second Shaar." The additions from the Tzemach Tzedek must be omitted. I also sent via the aforementioned a photograph of the Alter Rebbe’s own handwriting regarding the laws of *re'iah* (lung examination) to be printed therein. The paper and binding (in three volumes) must be of the highest quality. I do not have a copy of the introduction remaining with me, and I request that you send me a copy of it. He should print the title page and introduction last (in terms of time, not placement, of course), as there may yet be some changes to them.

2) All the *Shaarei* of the Mitteler Rebbe are included in "Fourth Heichal, First Shaar," as are *Shaar HaOrah*, *Shaar HaEmunah*, and *Shaar HaYichud*. In the introduction to *Atarah*, it should of course read 5707, not 5708.

Furthermore, we have received: **two** *Tanya*s and **one** *Shaarei Orah* that Rabbi B.G. brought when he traveled here, and nothing more! You must hasten to send here at least 500 copies of *Sefer HaMaamarim* Vol. 1 and 500 *Tanya*s.

The price for *Sefer HaMaamarim* or *Sefer HaSichos* is sixty cents (in Paris, 75) each. *Pokei'ach Ivrim* is 15 (in Paris, 20).

You may offer a commission from this to the sellers or buyers of up to thirty percent.

8) I heard that some other *sichos* were printed and have already been sold (at a profit). Please be kind enough to send us four or five copies for our library. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to connect with those who handled the aforementioned regarding the sale and distribution of what you are printing, as they are apparently experienced in this. I rely on your judgment.

9) I believe I already wrote that you should also print *Torah Or*, *Likutei Torah*, and also the *Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek, 500 copies each—as well as *Shaar HaEmunah* and *Shaar HaYichud*. Please inform me if you have them and from which edition. Also, if possible, let me know approximately how much the expenses will be for each.

10) The booklet for *Tanya* has not yet been published due to being overwhelmed with work. I will send the other items that have been published as you requested; please let me know how long the transit takes. Please confirm receipt of the letter sent under separate cover.

Awaiting a detailed response regarding the above, and wishing you all the best.

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 222

222

B"H, 22 Teves, 5708

R. L. Meckler, may he live

Peace and Blessing!

I have heard that you have returned from your trip to Europe, and I hope that it was successful in every respect.

It gives me pleasure to send you a copy of **Sefer HaZichronos** by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. If you would like to receive additional copies, we will gladly send them to you.

A few words regarding the significance of the **Zichronos**.

In Torah, every detail is of great importance; even the order of the Torah teaches us much.

Torah is *Lashon Hora’ah* (a language of instruction)—meaning, the Torah is not a storybook, but a book that teaches.

The order of the Torah is that Sefer Bereishis comes first, and only afterwards Shemos, Vayikra, and so on. The basis for this is not merely that this was the chronological progression of the events described—a sufficient reason for a history book, but not for a book that serves as a guide for life.

Rather, it is also—and perhaps primarily—because this is how the path of learning a *seder hachayim* (order of life) must be for an individual, for a collective, and for an entire nation.

The beginning of such learning is not the explanation of *mitzvos asei* and *mitzvos lo saasei*, but the narration and presentation of a living example of individuals, or entire generations—parents, relatives, or simply people who lived the desired *seder hachayim*. They have, so to speak, "blazed the trail," demonstrating clearly how one must live life, how one can overcome the various obstacles that arise, and that this—and only this—is the correct path in life.

And only afterwards come the directives: "Come, do," "Return, and do not do"—as a conclusion and almost a self-evident result of the previously recounted life stories.

In this vein, this is the primary significance of the **Zichronos**.

The main purpose is not intended to be—however important that may be—the recounting of the life path of this person or that person, so that one might know the history of those generations or personalities.

The **main** purpose is to show us a living example of how a Yid—a Rav, a scholar, a merchant, a craftsman, a pauper—each of them, in his own respect, a great Yid—lived through their lives.

And this should point out to us the correct path in our own times, and also make it easier to overcome the difficulties that are associated with walking in such a path.

I conclude by once again expressing a heartfelt *yasher koach* for your great contribution to this important publication.

With respect and regards,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 323

B"H, Hilula of the Alter Rebbe, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' A. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter was received. It is, of course, appropriate that during these times there should be frequent letters informing us of your well-being, to your brother-in-law and family, etc., and consequently, it will reach us as well.

It is surprising that throughout this entire time, neither you nor your brother-in-law, R' M. G. shlita, have informed me regarding your decision concerning the publication of our Rebbeim’s *seforim*. Perhaps the general situation has caused this. It is possible that now, specifically, is the time to take such a matter upon yourselves.

The *seforim* you ordered have been sent, and I am sure you will confirm their receipt as soon as they arrive.

The *Siyum HaTorah* has not yet been performed.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, and I am certain you will share its merit with the many.

To conclude with a topic of the day:

Our Sages have said (Megillah 13a), "Tevet is the month in which the body derives pleasure from the body." It is known that Esther represents *Knesses Yisrael*, and the *Midrash* states (cited in the *maamar* beginning "B'layla Hahu," *Torah Or*) that Achashverosh refers to the *Ribono shel Olam*.

If so, it can be explained that "the body"—a term commonly used by our Sages in phrases such as *gufi Torah* (the bodies/essentials of Torah) and *gufa*, meaning the core and essence (see *Likutei Torah* on *Gimmel Parshiyos* at the beginning)—refers to *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof* blessed be He, who, as it were, derives pleasure from "the body," which is the essential point within each individual, the *yechidah* in the *nefesh*. This occurs through the physical body, *avodah* within the body and with the body, just as it will be revealed in the future that the *neshamah* will receive from the body.

The Baal Shem Tov revealed—as in his interpretation of the verse "When you see the donkey..." (cited in *Hayom Yom*, p. 23)—that it must be in the manner of "deriving pleasure." The Alter Rebbe deepened this in the teachings of Chassidus to infuse vitality into everything (*Maaneh* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Hayom Yom*, 24 Tevet), so that even the "dead" part of the body—the *Chabad*, the cold brain that is not moved (see Rashi in *Megillah* there: "because of the cold")—should be transformed to be moved by *Elokus* (see *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*, beginning of Chapter 4).

With best wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

28 Teves, 5708

To the honorable, learned, and distinguished Rabbi Menachem Mendel, may he live, Shochet u’Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, regarding what you wrote:

(1) In *Shemos Rabbah* (end of Chapter 1 and Chapter 17:3), it states: "To the lintel—that Avraham is the greatest of the converts, and just as the lintel is high, so too was he the greatest of the Patriarchs. And to the two doorposts—in the merit of Yitzchak and Yaakov."

You pointed out that this contradicts what is explained in many places: that Avraham is the right line, Yitzchak is the left line, and Yaakov is the middle line that connects them.

I am hereby transcribing what the Tzemach Tzedek wrote in his *Maamar* entitled *Mezuzah MiYamin* (printed in *Ohr HaTorah*, page 328a), and through this, the aforementioned will be understood. The following is the text of the Tzemach Tzedek there, Section 1: "In *Rabbah*, Chapter 17, it says: 'To the lintel—in the merit of Avraham; and to the two doorposts—in the merit of Yitzchak and Yaakov.' The Ramaz, in *Zohar Chadash*, Chapter 1, explains that the lintel and the two doorposts are the *Chochma, Binah,* and *Da’as* within *Malchus*, which are drawn from the *Tiferes, Netzach,* and *Hod* of *Ze’er Anpin*, etc. According to this, it would be appropriate to say that the two doorposts are Avraham and Yitzchak, who are the two lines, etc., and the lintel is the middle line, *Tiferes*, the aspect of Yaakov, etc. However, it is possible to explain it in the manner that Avraham is called 'the greatest man among the giants,' etc.—meaning *Arich Anpin*, which is called *Atik Yomin* (the Ancient of Days). Similarly, Avraham is a 'grandfather' (*saba*) to Yaakov, who is *Ze’er Anpin*. And Yitzchak, his father, is *Abba* (Father), just as they say to Yitzchak, 'For you are our father.' Also, in the *Maamar* on *Vayeshev*, etc., it explains that 'the dwelling of his father' refers to *Chochma Ila’ah*, which is called his father. And even though Yitzchak is *Din* (Judgment), *Chochma* is considered *Din* relative to *Keter*. Therefore, Avraham is called the lintel, which is *Keter*, and Yitzchak and Yaakov, who are *Abba* and *Ze’er Anpin*, are the two doorposts." End of quote relevant to our subject.

It is found, therefore, that regarding the Patriarchs—and likewise in the *Remez* (allusion) concerning them, the lintel and the two doorposts—one must understand their distinction from the perspective of two aspects: 

A. **Length:** The order of the generations, where one is above the other. In this case, the lintel, by virtue of being high and above the doorposts, alludes to Avraham in his aspect of being higher than Yitzchak, and Yitzchak higher than Yaakov—meaning *Arich Anpin*, *Chochma*, and *Ze’er Anpin*. (It may be said that even among the doorposts, the right doorpost—which according to this aspect refers to Yitzchak—precedes the left one in time as well, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages regarding the mitzvah of *mezuzah* (*Yoma* 11b): "The right foot is lifted **first**.") 

B. **Width:** The three lines. In this case, the lintel refers to Yaakov, as mentioned above.

Regarding what is written in *Magen Avos*, *Maamar* *Mezuzah MiYamin*, end of Section 3, that he "rides two horses" and combines the two aforementioned aspects together—it is possible that he was brief in his language, or more accurately, that some words were omitted. And "by the mouth of two or three witnesses shall a matter be established": 

1) The aforementioned *Maamar* of the Tzemach Tzedek, upon which the *Maamar* in *Magen Avos* **is based**. See there. 
2) In the Tzemach Tzedek’s *Sefer Shemos* (in the collection of manuscripts of the Rebbe Rayatz), on the verse *Shemos* 12:22, subsection 4, it states: "When the time of the Exodus arrived, it was said, 'Leaping over the mountains'—these are the Patriarchs, the three lines, etc. Right and left, and the lintel that is above them, this is the root of the middle line, etc., the 'central bolt,' etc. In the *Midrash*, Chapter *Bo*, etc., 'The lintel is Avraham,' etc., the greatest of the Patriarchs. And this is from the perspective of their root in the *Chesed, Gevurah,* and *Tiferes* of *Atik*, because the *Chesed* of *Atik* is enclothed in the *Gulgolta* of *Arich Anpin*—the *Keter* within the *Keter* is the lintel, etc., and this is the aspect of Avraham. And Yitzchak is the *Gevuros* of *Atik* enclothed in the *Mocha Stima’ah* (the Hidden Brain), and Yaakov is the *Tiferes* of *Atik*, the aspect of the 'membrane of air' (*kruma d’avira*)." 
3) What is written in *Sefer Maharid* (by the grandson of the Tzemach Tzedek) in the first chapter of *Krias Shema* on the verse "And you shall write them," which states: "In *Rabbah*, Chapter *Bo*, they said, 'To the lintel—in the merit of Avraham,' etc., and they are the *Chochma, Binah,* and *Da’as* within *Malchus*, which are drawn from the *Tiferes, Netzach,* and *Hod* of *Ze’er Anpin*. And Avraham and Yitzchak are the two lines, 'Chesed for Avraham' and 'Pachad (Fear) for Yitzchak,' etc., and the lintel is the middle line, *Tiferes*, the aspect of Yaakov. And as for why Moshe Rabbeinu reversed the order and said, 'And you shall reach the lintel and the two doorposts,' it is stated in *Rabbah*, Chapter *Shemos*: 'The lintel is Avraham, the aspect of *Keter*, and Yitzchak is *Abba*, *Chochma*, because *Chochma* is called *Din* relative to *Keter*, and Yaakov is *Ze’er Anpin*, *Tiferes'." End of quote relevant to our subject.

And in this manner, it must also be in *Magen Avos*.

(2) You ask for the explanation of the concept of the "twelve diagonal boundaries" above, for their application in the *avodah* of the human soul is explained in *Magen Avos*, Part 4, *Maamar* *Yavo Zeh*.

It is not clearly explained what your intent is in writing "the concept above." It seems to be a continuation of what is written in the aforementioned *drush* regarding the explanation of *Chesed* and *Gevurah*—that this is when the world's conduct is from the attribute of *Chesed* alone or *Gevurah* alone. And the question is: If so, what are the "twelve diagonal boundaries" in this?

This is understood based on what is explained regarding the concept of the "six thousand years that the world exists," which correspond to the six days of Creation, where each one pertains to one attribute. In the first millennium, the attribute of *Chesed* shone (of *Ze’er Anpin*, which is a vessel for the *Chesed* of *Arich Anpin*, as explained in the *Maamar* *VeChol HaAm Ro’im*, end of Section 5). Therefore, they were sustained by the *Chesed* of the Holy One, Blessed be He, even though they were provoking Him. In the second millennium, *Gevurah*—and therefore there was the Flood, total destruction, etc. In the third millennium, *Tiferes*—and therefore there was the Exodus and the Giving of the Torah, the "third light." The fourth millennium, *Netzach*, a branch of *Chesed*—and therefore there were the two Holy Temples, even though there was the opposition of idolatry, as it is said, "Against My anger and against My wrath," etc. In the fifth millennium, *Hod*, the conclusion of the left line—"all the day" (*d’vah*), the letters of *Hod*—entirely decrees and persecutions, G-d forbid. (But regarding this, they will say, "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me," etc., and it is not like the Flood in the second millennium). In the sixth millennium, *Yesod*, the connection and the completion of the attributes, for then the Redemption will be, and were it not for our sins, etc., it would have already come, as per the words of our Sages (*Sanhedrin* 97b).

Now, all of this is when the conduct is from each attribute individually. But when it is conducted from the "twelve diagonal boundaries," meaning when the attribute is blended with the attribute of the opposite line, the conduct is also blended, as is understood.

See also in the Tzemach Tzedek’s *Sefer HaMitzvos*, the mitzvah of the prohibition of the *gid hanasheh* (sciatic nerve), for an explanation of the attributes **above**. And in *Sefer Ohr HaTorah*, *Maamar* *Vayomer Lo Yehonasan* and its explanations, from which it seems the aforementioned *Maamar* *Yavo Zeh* was taken, except that in *Ohr HaTorah* it is more expansive and explanatory.

With wishes for all that is good.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

I am surprised that you are writing to me at a different address. If you wish for my letters to reach me in a timely manner, please be kind enough to send them to the address of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch or Kehot.

Surely you are aware of the several books on the teachings of Chassidus that have been published recently by Kehot.
