***

Regarding a matter of Chassidus: In the enclosed maamar, it is brought in Chapter 7 regarding the good character traits that are **in the nature** of Bnei Yisrael, whether they stem from the nefesh ha'elokis (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 12) or from the nefesh habehamis (Tanya, end of Chapter 1). For some time now, I have heard people posing a contradiction (*raminu*) between these two. To my mind: In the Tanya, we are taught that Bnei Yisrael possess good character traits **in the nature of the nefesh habehamis** (without avodah).

In Iggeres HaKodesh, we are taught that the nefesh ha'elokis **in its nature** has chessed prevailing over gevurah. Both are true, and both are necessary for us, as is understood.

2) In Yevamos (79a; cited in Rambam, Hilchos Issurei Biah 19:17; mentioned in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 11), three signs of Bnei Yisrael are listed. In the Tanya, the trait of "bashfulness" is omitted (in Iggeres HaKodesh it is understood, for shame stems from yirah and not from chessed — Nedarim 20a). However, it is understood according to our Sages (Beitzah 25b; Nedarim ibid., see there in Chiddushei Aggados) that the sign of shame is not like the others, as it is created specifically through Matan Torah. From this, one can see how precise even the omissions in the Tanya are.

## 327

15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos, 5708

To the honorable Rabbi, the brilliant scholar, the expert in Torah, the man of action and energy who seeks the good of his people, etc., Rabbi A. Silver, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

You are surely aware, at least in general terms, of the work of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, founded by and under the presidency of the Rebbe, may he live. Given the various facets of its work, I am certain that it is unnecessary to elaborate to a man of your stature regarding the importance of this work and its established standing. It is a matter dear to you, and you will surely not refrain from assisting in the appropriate manner.

Some time ago, our friend, the Rabbi and Chossid, R' Shlomo Aharon Kazarnovsky, may he live, visited one of the long-standing supporters of the Merkos’s activities in Cincinnati. This gentleman had expressed interest in our work when he was in New York about two years ago.

While in Cincinnati, Rabbi Kazarnovsky observed among his acquaintances an awakening to assist the work of the Merkos. The lack of funds for its regular operations, in addition to the heavy debts in which it is mired, weighs heavily upon the continuation of its most necessary and vital work in the field of education—and all the more so regarding the expansion of this work as is required.

It would have been proper and correct for him to consult with you and hear your advice and opinion before beginning any activity. However, the difficulty was that you were not at home at the time. Fearing that the enthusiasm might cool—and knowing that "what is delayed is lost"—he felt compelled to begin doing what he could to organize a circle of those interested in and helpful to the work of the Merkos in general, and the printing department in particular.

What was done then was merely a beginning, a form of planting. Before we tell our friend Rabbi Kazarnovsky to continue in this great mitzvah he has begun, we are turning to you with a double and triple request: to inform us of your opinion in general, and specifically regarding the appropriate time and manner to proceed. In particular, we seek your esteemed assistance through your tremendous influence to increase the number of supporters for the work of the Merkos—a matter that concerns the literal spiritual survival of thousands of Jewish boys and girls.

It is unnecessary to remark upon that which is "beyond doubt to any complete person, and is open and known to the people," that the Merkos is a non-partisan institution, and is not connected or affiliated with any yeshiva whatsoever.

To conclude with a matter of the day: Today is 15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos. According to the Rambam (beginning of Hilchos Maaser Sheni), it is implied that this date is Torah-ordained, unlike the view of Rashi on the Rif in Masechta Rosh Hashanah. Although from the text of the Torah we only know that it is after the Rosh Hashanah for years (Tosafos, s.v. *U’peiros*, Rosh Hashanah 10a), it is possible to explain this timing in two ways: either it is among the other measurements that are *Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai* according to the overwhelming majority of authorities, or the Torah entrusted the Sages to establish the time for Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos, and through their establishment, it becomes Torah-ordained.

We find similar concepts, according to various opinions, regarding trading in forbidden items, the afflictions of Yom Kippur, work on Chol Hamoed, the prohibition of "do not walk in their statutes," and the treatment of a bechor.

The practical difference between these two approaches is that according to the latter, if there were a Great Beis Din, etc., they could change the date of Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos to another time.

Since the Mishnah equates all four Rosh Hashanahs, it seemingly implies the first approach. However, since the Gemara discusses the establishment of this Rosh Hashanah based on **logical reasoning**—stating that we follow the majority of years—which implies that it is providing a reason rather than a sign, it appears more likely that it is the second approach. That is, the Torah entrusted the Sages to set the time for Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos so that the fruits of the new year will ripen, for nature aligns with the Torah* (as the Sages say in Yerushalmi, Kesubos 1:2, regarding the verse "He who completes for me"). I have come only to offer a thought.

One could elaborate on the subject, for man is (at times, only) "the tree of the field," and the Sages, through the power of Torah, can establish and effect within him a time for the fruits (these are the mitzvos) of a new year to ripen ("renew your deeds"), provided that this is after the Rosh Hashanah for man, as man is man. But this is not the place to elaborate.

With respect and esteem, and wishing you the best of everything.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 228

16 Shevat, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi A. A. Axelrod

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter:

Regarding what you wrote concerning Tanya, Chapter 20, that letters are "born" when one begins to think about how to bring his desire from potential into action (and similarly in *Boneh Yerushalayim*, Siman 132):

You note that the revelation in the heart from the mind, as well as the knowledge in the mind, are certainly also impossible without letters; if so, the letters already exist prior to the thought.

However, what the Tanya comes to explain in these chapters is the matter of unity after the world was created, just as it was before the world was created. The worlds in general are divided into two: *Olam HaTzomtzum* and *Olam HaTziumtzum*, whose formation comes from the letters of thought and the letters of speech, as explained in many places (most notably in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, Chapter 11). Regarding this, it explains that the letters of thought and speech above, even after they have emerged into action, are unified in the ultimate sense, just as they were before they emerged into action.

Now, the worlds—even before they were created—exist in their source and root, far above, up to the level that was "conceived in potential," except that they are not there in the state of "existence" and "being" as they are in their source. From this, we can understand the intent regarding the letters: that above the level of thought, they do not exist in a state of "being" and "separation." For only the intellect, the *middah*, etc., are felt, not the letters. For one who is thinking, the intellect feels the love, etc., but not the letters. (See *Likutei Torah*, *Biur BeChukotai*, beginning of Chapter 2; *Biurei HaZohar* at the beginning, and elsewhere).

The order of this process is: Through his connection (*da'as*) to the knowledge of *Elokus*, for example, the desire to know is revealed within him. Through this, an intellectual grasp is revealed from the power of the *maskil* (the intellective faculty) through the examination and survey of the intellect (*chochmah*). Afterward, through his connection to the subject, he delves into the understanding of this intellect (*pnei binah*), and consequently, the love and fear of Hashem are born within him. He then begins to think and contemplate how to quench his thirst through *Torah* and *mitzvos* in thought, speech, and action—and at that point, it is **inevitable** that letters are born. See further on this in the *maamar* "Lulav VeAravah" 5659, and also the *maamar* "Ein Omdin" (*Hemshech* 5666).

It is understood that (in a revealed sense) one can skip parts of this order. For example, someone who suddenly weeps during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, which is explained (in the name of the Arizal, cited in *Nitzotzei Torah* on *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 584) to be because he is being judged at that moment above, even though he is completely unaware of this in his revealed faculties. This can cause him to immediately begin reciting *Tehillim* or the like, or he is suddenly struck by thoughts of *teshuvah* and begins to confess his sins in speech. In such a case, the letters of speech have indeed become a garment for the illumination from the essence of his *neshamah* without intermediaries.

However, aside from the fact that this "skipping" of the order occurs only on rare occasions, the aforementioned illumination still passes—at least in a hidden way and as a transitional path—through the intermediate levels. See *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, Chapter 8: "And in every thought in the world, some *middah* is clothed, etc."

It is understood that there is no contradiction to this from the explanation of the concept of *Rosh Chodesh*, where *Malchus* receives from *Chochmah* and *Binah* **and not from Ze'er Anpin**, which is like speech within intellect and reason. For even then, there must be within him **love** for intellectual matters, or **fear** that his study might veer into a crooked path in the understanding of the intellect, and the like. See also *Or HaTorah* (p. 52), the end of the explanation of "And it shall be from new moon to new moon," and in the section regarding the verse "To make known to the sons of man," regarding the *middos* within the intellect from which the letters in the thought are born.

With blessings for all good,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 329

25 Shevat, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R. D. shlita,

In response to your letter of the 2nd of Shevat (I have passed on the enclosed letter for the Rebbe shlita to his secretariat, as I do not wish to take responsibility for those matters).

1) Once again, I request that you expedite the printing and shipping as much as possible.

2) You may also send them in the name of Machne Israel and Kehot. For the time being, only five packages of Tanya have been received, and among them, several copies have pages that are blank or missing.

Surely the Torah Or has the additions at the end, and the Likutei Torah also has the table of corrections at the end. 10) If you intend to travel, how will you arrange the matter of the printing so that all the above comes to fruition? Aside from the money and effort invested in this, it would be a chillul Hashem, chas v'shalom, after the publicity surrounding the matter, and a source of great distress, chas v'shalom, to the Rebbe shlita, etc., etc.

Awaiting your reply at your earliest convenience, and wishing you all the best,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Enclosed is a letter for R. Sh. Z. Kalmanson; please be kind enough to deliver it to him.

## 330

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., the *Tamim* R' Yehuda Chitrik, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letters were received, and enclosed is a detailed letter regarding the conditions and methods of *hafatzah* (dissemination). Certainly, like all matters of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, this too will be successful.

Regarding your concluding remark (concerning what I wrote about "permeating" one's fellow) — "What is one to do if he is locked in his room; how can one draw him out from his shell?" — my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, has already written in his letters (in the name of the Rebbe Rashab): "When one sets up a lantern, those who desire the light — *lichtigkeit* — gather to it," end quote.

One can explain the precision of the phrase "those who desire (*ha-chefetz*) the light," for the word *chefetz* denotes the inwardness of the will, unlike the word *rotzeh* (see *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach*, *siddur ha-maamar* "Tovah Ha-aretz"). The inward will of every member of *Bnei Yisrael* is complete toward Hashem and His Torah, and Torah is **light**, as is known from the proof regarding a *get* (divorce document) given under duress being valid, and per what is written in the Rambam, *Hilchos Geirushin*, end of Chapter 2.

As for what you further wrote, that perhaps the oil does not shine even within itself because it is murky — even murky oil permeates and shines, though the light is not as bright. But that it emerges from the category of darkness is **obvious**, and it is still considered the kindling of a lamp, as is proven in the *Shas*, the *poskim*, and in tangible reality. In general, what is the point of [dissemination] if it does not bring benefit in *Torah*, *avodah*, or *gemilus chasadim*? And if it prevents them, it is a forbidden thing.

Every person in his place is an emissary of Divine Providence, and if he only begins the action of fulfilling his mission, he will surely succeed. It is also good for him, both in *ruchniyus* and in *gashmiyus*.

Wishing you success and all the best.

**M. Schneerson**

## 331

B"H, 2nd day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., Rabbi Y. Altayn, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

1) Regarding R. N. K., may he live, I have written to him.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning Tanya, Chapter 2: "And even now, in the son, the nourishment and vitality of the fingernails are drawn from the brain in the head"—it seems **simple** that the intention is the brain in the son’s head, not the father’s. This is how it is in reality, and as is also written later in the analogy: for the nourishment and vitality of the *nefesh, ruach, neshamah* of the *am ha’aretz* (the analogy for the fingernails of the firstborn of Israel) is from the *nefesh, ruach, neshamah* of the leaders of the Jewish people of their generation (the analogy for his brain and head).

**Note:** In the analogy: the *nefesh, ruach, neshamah* of the *am ha’aretz*, through clinging to a *talmid chacham*, are unified in their primary essence with the *Shechinah* itself.

If so, in the analogy, the son’s fingernails should, through their nourishment from the brain in the son’s head, be unified with the drop of the father’s brain. Perhaps it can be said that in truth **this is so**, because the brain in the son’s head—which is also made from the "whiteness" (Gemara, ibid.), i.e., the drop of the father’s brain—does not turn into a different essence; it remains and is always clothed within it with the essence of the drop of the father’s brain. The fingernails, in their nourishment from the brain, are consequently connected through this also to that which is clothed within it, which is of the essence of the drop of the father’s brain. Or, it could be said that this is where the analogy **differs** from the thing being represented, and this is also what is explained, that the son becomes an essence **in his own right**, separate from his father—and therefore he is not obligated in *mesiras nefesh*—unlike the soul. See *Likutei Torah*, *d.h. Shir HaMaalos MiMaamakim*, end of Chapter 1.

3) In Tanya, Chapter 3: Why does he write the term **"koach"** (potential/power) regarding *Chochmah*, but not regarding *Binah*?

There are two interpretations of the term *koach*: (a) When we speak of the *kochot* of the soul, which means the "limbs" of the soul. See Tanya, Chapter 51, regarding the 613 *kochot* of the soul. In this sense, there is no distinction between *Chochmah, Binah, Da’as*, etc., as one can say *koach* for all of them: *koach* of *Chochmah*, *koach* of *Binah*, etc. (b) *Koach* (potential) and *po’al* (actual). The distinction is that when a thing is still in its general, hidden state (or even just in capacity), we say it is in *koach* (in a broader sense, this is also said regarding ability; see *d.h. Ki Menaseh*, which was just discussed in sections 5-6). When it emerges from (capacity or) concealment into revelation and the details are specified, it is "emerging from *koach* to *po’al*." This is the distinction between *Chochmah* and *Binah*, which is why they are called "father" and "mother," as is written in many places. See later in Chapter 18, *Iggeres HaKodesh* sections 6, 15, 29, and elsewhere.

4) What is the difference between *Tiferes*—beauty—and *Hod*—beauty? And what connection is there between the beauty of *Hod* and the concept of "counseling kidneys"?

In the vast majority of *Chassidus* discourses I have seen, they interpret *Hod* as being from the root *hoda’ah* (acknowledgment/gratitude), not from the root *hod v’hadar* (splendor and majesty), and only in a few places is the latter interpretation brought—among them *Iggeres HaKodesh* section 15, where both interpretations are cited.

From there, the difference between the praise of *Tiferes* and the praise of *Hod* is understood: *Tiferes* is a beauty that is understood and grasped by the intellect (one sees that there is a mixture of various colors, attributes, and the like), whereas *Hod* is when one understands that there is some aspect of beauty here, but one does not understand what that beauty is, because it is entirely above one’s level and comprehension.

I have not yet found that the attribute of *Hod* is used with the term *Tiferes* and *yofi* (beauty), because seemingly, beauty is only relevant where there is a synthesis of colors and attributes. See *Iggeres HaKodesh* there, *Derech Mitzvosecha* Chapter 3, and elsewhere.

This itself is also a form of beauty: a matter that is most profound, yet it is revealed to the recipient (even though the recipient does not understand it even after it is revealed to him). It is understood that in such a manner, a more internal aspect of the *mashpia* (the one who influences) can be revealed, since the matter is not clothed in the recipient’s understanding. But because the matter is most internal, it can only be revealed from the **lowest** level within it. The essence of this beauty is that the matter is arranged in such a way that even a **very low** recipient can receive it ("counseling kidneys"), even though he does not grasp it (unlike *Tiferes*). Sometimes he does not even have any connection to the matter at all, to the point that it does not even arouse in him the attribute of *hoda’ah*, only that he acknowledges that he *should* acknowledge (*Hod sheb’Hod*). An example of this: a villager who has no understanding at all of the essence of the king, but sees that his village head, whose greatness the villager does grasp, bows to a royal minister. Consequently, **acknowledgment** of the minister is aroused in the villager, because he is a wondrous person in his eyes, since the village head bows before him. And then, when he sees the royal minister bowing before the king, the greatness of the king is revealed **in the acknowledgment within the acknowledgment** of the villager.

See the *Lag B'Omer* discourses (in the *Siddur* and elsewhere) regarding *Hod sheb’Hod*, upon which the above is based. And in the *Tzemach Tzedek’s* commentary on *Tehillim*, Chapter 104, 1, section 7, he writes: "There is the essence of *Chochmah*, which is the intellect contemplating on its own and not revealing it... and there is when he explains the intellect to another... this is what is called *Hod*. Unlike when he is not influencing, where there is no aspect of *Hod* in the intellect, like the sun when it does not shine... If so, according to this, the aspect of *Netzach* and *Hod* does not mean... the language of *hoda’ah*... even though this aspect is also called *Hod*, the primary meaning of the word *Hod* is the radiance, which is that which they illuminate, etc." End quote, as it pertains to our subject. There is much to elaborate on this.

With wishes for all good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

If so, there are two differences: 1) In *Tiferes*, one grasps the beauty with the intellect; in *Hod*, one does not. 2) And it seems to me that this is the essence: In *Tiferes*, beauty is an intrinsic matter. In *Hod*, it is due to external circumstances—in this *mashpia*, it is a most internal matter which, to this recipient, is a most exalted matter. It is **relative** beauty, not beauty for everyone.

## Stage

7 Adar I, 5708

To the esteemed philanthropist, the G-d-fearing man who loves Torah and pursues charity, the distinguished communal leader, Mr. Tzvi Eliezer, may he live, son of R. Avraham Avir HaLevi Kraushar.

Greetings and Blessings!

I take this opportunity to thank you heartily in the name of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch for your worthy undertaking and assistance in publishing the series of encyclopedic volumes known as *Sdei Chemed* by R. Chaim Chizkiya Medini, of blessed memory.

At the same time, we confirm receipt of your generous contribution—the first installment toward this undertaking. An official receipt is enclosed.

This encyclopedic work, which the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, chose to grant you the merit of participating in—a merit that brings merit to the many—is a highly important encyclopedia. It contains the *piskei dinim* for the conduct of a Jew, both as an individual and as a collective, according to the *Acharonim* and the *Acharonei Acharonim*.

Even before the last war, this work had already gone out of print, and it was reprinted in Poland in 5699-5700. However, along with the millions of *kedoshim* who perished at the hands of the murderers, may their names be blotted out, this work was also destroyed. Thus, the necessity to revive and reprint this rare treasure is very great.

Precisely now, we are reading the *sedros* that speak of the building of the *Mishkan*, which later gave way to the *Beis HaMikdash*. The enemies of Israel destroyed our *Beis HaMikdash*, but they only had power over the wood and stones—over the physical, material things; over the spiritual holiness, the enemies had no control.

The same is true regarding the millions of Jewish lives that were lost *al kiddush Hashem* and the holy *seforim* that were destroyed. Only the bodies and the paper were destroyed, but the *neshamos* and the spirit of the *seforim* are eternal.

Yet, a *neshamah* without a *guf* is not the ultimate purpose of the world, just as a *guf* without a *neshamah* cannot exist. By educating a new generation in the spirit of our *kedoshim* and *tehorim*, and by reprinting and disseminating the spirit of these holy *seforim*, we reconnect the eternal spirituality into physical *gufim* and *levushim*.

Therefore, the great merit you have acquired by enabling us to print and distribute this important encyclopedic work is beyond measure.

Equally immeasurable is the merit for the *neshamos* of the *kedoshim*, the parents of your esteemed wife, Mrs. Sashe, may she live—the *kedoshim* R. Elazar son of R. Neta and Mrs. Ita daughter of Michel, who sacrificed their lives *al kiddush Hashem*.

May the merit of this endeavor stand by you and your wife, both in material and spiritual matters. May your travels be successful, and may the blessings that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, gave you be fulfilled.

With blessings for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Preserving the desired form and the tradition of our ancestors requires special effort on the part of every member of the household; the command and instruction of the head of the household alone is not sufficient at all.

Our Sages of blessed memory stated (Shemos Rabbah, ch. 28:2) that at the Giving of the Torah, the address had to be to the women first and then to the men, and only then is the Torah sustained. The instruction for all generations is understood.

I sign in anticipation of hearing good news from you, and wishing you all the best.

## 335

B"H, Purim Katan, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with public needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Menachem Mendel, may he live and be well, Shochet and Bodek.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding your observation concerning Rashi’s commentary (Sanhedrin 17a, s.v. *Mi*), where he explains that Eldad and Medad did not refrain from going to the Tent out of humility, but rather out of fear that they would not be chosen—which seems to contradict his commentary on the Torah (Bamidbar 11:27).

1) Rashi’s commentary on the Torah cites the opinion of the Sifrei, which aligns with the view of Rabbi Shimon in the Gemara. They **disagree** with the Tanna Kamma, whose words Rashi explains in the aforementioned *s.v. Mi*. See the supplement to Rashi printed in the Ein Yaakov on Sanhedrin there, which proves this point. (See also Yalkut Shimoni in the corresponding location for another opinion, that there was no lottery at all, but rather they took six from each tribe and four from the tribe of Levi, and they are listed by name).

2) How does Rashi know to interpret the words of the Tanna Kamma in this way? This interpretation is necessary, because the Tanna Kamma states that they remained in the lottery, meaning Eldad and Medad did not participate in the lottery at all and did not go to take the slips. If so, if you were to say it was because they said, "We are not worthy of such greatness"—yet the judgment of the lottery is from Hashem—they should have been confident that they would be chosen. Why, then, would they not participate in the lottery? Therefore, one must say that, on the contrary, they remained behind because they believed they would be chosen. This is clear.

3) How does the Tanna Kamma know to interpret the intention of Eldad and Medad as not being out of humility, but rather the opposite?

One could say that he is uncomfortable with the idea that they were chosen for the status of Elder and yet remained in the camp out of humility; for since they had already been designated **from Above** for prophecy, they should not have refrained from it.

Based on this, the dispute between the Tanna Kamma and Rabbi Shimon is akin to the dispute in Berachos (7a, bottom) regarding whether Moshe was punished for hiding his face or whether he was rewarded for it.

Alternatively, one could say that even according to the one who says Moshe acted correctly, that is specifically because there it was a vision of the Divine Presence, which is impossible for any other prophet (except for Moshe; see there in the Chiddushei Aggados of the Maharsha). But regarding Eldad and Medad, where it was an emanation of the spirit from Moshe onto the seventy elders, everyone agrees they should not have refrained from accepting this prophecy if they had already been chosen for it from **Heaven**. This is the reasoning of the Tanna Kamma. Rabbi Shimon holds that these seventy elders were also expected to judge, teach, and exercise authority over Israel, and therefore they excused themselves. (In the Responsa *Lachmei Torah*, section 16, it is noted that according to the Zohar, these seventy elders were not in the position of the elders at the end of Parshas Mishpatim to judge, but **only** for the resting of the Shechinah). There is much more to elaborate on this, but this is not the place.

With best wishes for all that is good.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 337

B"H, 21 Adar Rishon, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [individual], may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 14th of this month.

1) Regarding the work in [the institution], you write four reasons for not engaging in the work there, despite the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita: that the elder Chassidim told you the intention is that it depends on their own will; that you lack vitality in it; that the work is no longer so necessary because it is not developing; and that others are also not involved in the aforementioned. You ask for my opinion on this.

I have just seen a copy of the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, to you... and I see no room for doubt regarding what work he has imposed upon you, and he blesses you that you should succeed in it.

As for your lack of vitality in it, it is well known what is written in many places in Chassidus that a *tzivuy* (command) and *mitzvah* are related to the term *tzavta* (connection) and *hiskashrus*—that one becomes connected through the fulfillment of the command to the Commander. When it is possible for a particular soul to connect to its collective soul through this, there is no greater drawing down of vitality than this. Even if, for the time being, it is not felt in the powers of the *nefesh habehamis*, this does not change the matter; see the *maamar* "Ki Menaseh," section 7.

Regarding the fact that [the work] is not developing and that others are also not involved in it, this is precisely the matter under discussion: the fact that some of the committee members (and, in general, anyone who is in a position to assist in this) refrain or are negligent in their duty causes a delay in the development of proper education based on the foundation of Torah and *mitzvos*, and it also weakens the hands of others. This is especially true if you are counted among the camp of the *Temimim*, whose actions are meant to be candles that illuminate. If one's candle is not burning for the time being, one thereby prevents the illumination of many other candles that could have been lit during this time. See *Kuntres HaAvodah*, end of page 43, *Kuntres U’Maayan*, page 22, and elsewhere; there is no need to elaborate further...

With wishes for all the best.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

...Regarding what was heard about the arrest... I will conclude with the words of our Sages (Taanis 29b, cited by later authorities as *halacha l’maaseh*): A Jew who has a legal case against a non-Jew... should try to find himself in Adar, for his *mazal* is strong. And in Sotah (12b), one opinion holds that Moshe was born in Adar Rishon. It is known in *Chassidus* that the *mazal* of a Jew is the *Ayin* (*Likutei Torah*, beginning of *Parshas Haazinu*, and elsewhere).

Waiting to hear good news from you,

**M. Schneerson**

If Rabbi D. is forced to leave, who is the most suitable person to handle the printing there, naturally from among those who are there or in the vicinity?

## Perhaps

B"H, 10 Adar Sheni, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished... may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

When it was printed in the *maamar* for *Tishrei* 5708 that a lack of knowledge does not change the reality of a matter—and this was reinforced with an analogy—I had a question: in worldly matters, this is obvious, so what is it coming to teach us? However, when I observed the ways of people, especially in places where the temptations of the *sitra achra* hold sway, I saw that this form of self-justification is extremely common. A person says that because **he** is diverting his attention from a certain matter, or because he is not speaking about it, this very fact removes the matter from the order of the day.

But we are dealing with *Asiyah*, which is on a higher level. It seems that the approach of... now is that if they pass over in silence that which they are obligated to do, or that which they even promised to do... this removes the matter from the agenda! And here, they have opened a door for the well-known craftsman, who today tells him thus, etc.

Enclosed is the *maamar* for Purim, to be used to bring merit to the many.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***Perhaps***

From a photocopy of the letter.

## 342

B"H, 11 Adar II, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, etc.,
Moreinu Harav A.A., may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

a) Regarding the holes for the tzitzis in the tallis katan—I have already told you that in the tallis katan of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, they are in this configuration:

(A diagram appears here in the book)

b) Regarding your observation on Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, Chapter 6, concerning the statement there that from the interinclusion of the middos with one another Above, it is evident that "He and His attributes are One," and therefore they are interincluded—and you raised the difficulty that we also find the interinclusion of middos with one another in a human being:

Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah is transcribed almost in its entirety in the Hemshech Mayim Rabim 5636, with slight variations and in a different order, and the aforementioned point is in Chapter 11 there. It can be explained that the interinclusion of the middos and their unification with one another is possible in two ways:

1) Because of their weakness (due to the influence of the mochin and the like), they make room for the opposite middah as well. This category includes the middos of Tikkun, which are "soft like a reed"—the revealed middos in a person who possesses intellect.

2) Even while they are in their full strength, through the illumination of a much higher power, they are nullified from their own existence, and consequently, opposite middos can exist together. This category includes middos as they are in Akudim, the middos that are in the essence of the soul.

All of this is explained at length in Toras Chayim, Bereishis—the second discourse. See also Sefer Bad Kodesh, Chapter 4.

Now, these two ways are found both Above and in a human being. However, the general distinction between Above and below is that Above, the interinclusion of the middos is due to the illumination of the supernal light, the Ohr Ein Sof, which is in Chochma (see Toras Chayim there, Chapter 34), because there is no "weakness" Above. What is called the "soft" middos of Tikkun is only in comparison to the middos of Tohu, and this is the explanation of what is written in Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah there. Below, in the revealed middos, it is due to the actual weakness that the mochin exert upon the middos.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Purim that was just published, and surely you will merit the many through it.

With the blessing of a happy and joyous Purim,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 343

11 Adar Rishon, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Tz. [Lieberman], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure, as I have heard of your activities to strengthen the Torah and its mitzvos, particularly in the field of education.

You are surely expanding the scope of your work from time to time, as is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh* (Epistle 13) that the revelation of the supernal light is constantly increasing; if so, it is understood that the *is'harusah d'lesata* (the arousal from below), or at the very least the *keli* (vessel) below, must also be constantly expanding. And although "the generations have been refined" (in the sense of *temimus*), it is known that "according to the effort is the reward."

In brief response to your comments:

1) Regarding the father of the Alter Rebbe: He supported himself through the labor of his hands. He did not accept any position as a Rav, Maggid, or the like, but rather occupied himself with gardening, as is written in *Sefer HaZichronos*, etc. It appears that he did not even travel on missions from the Baal Shem Tov, or if he did, it was only on rare occasions. Therefore, there is no difficulty in the fact that in those days, when they were precise in writing titles, they did not title him "the great Gaon" or the like. Especially—and this is the clear point—he would actively flee from any publicity, as written in *Sefer HaZichronos*. And a person’s will is his honor.

2) Regarding your question as to what constitutes the preparation for the first *yechidus*: It is not explicitly stated, but in my opinion, it is clear once one understands the concept of *yechidus*. The Rebbe, my father-in-law, explained (transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, p. 86) that it includes three points: clarifying the status of the person entering, establishing the manner of his *avodah*, and *hiskashrus* through *mesiras nefesh*—see there. Now, all of this must not be merely lip service, but in absolute truth. One must be a *keli* prepared to receive as mentioned above, and a *keli* worthy (*pardeent*) to receive as mentioned above. The more one increases the level he has attained through his own efforts, the greater will be what he receives in *yechidus* (and perhaps also what is given to him in *yechidus*. For it appears that aside from isolated cases where they gave in *yechidus* that which was completely out of proportion to the *keli* of the person entering—for example, one might say R’ Yekusiel Liepler—the usual way is that it is given not in proportion to the *recipient* [himself], but rather on the order of the distinction between a *makif* (encompassing light) of a garment and a house). And how difficult it is for an intellectual person to act on his own to surrender and give himself over in a way that is not according to intellect, for there is no "reason" for *mesiras nefesh* in the intellect for specific instructions, or for a person of strong will to reach the level of "nullify your will" and not merely "do His will," etc. And the greater one is in this, the more difficult the preparation is for him.

3) Regarding the fact that one of your acquaintances hand-copied the *Tanya*, and you suggest that perhaps there is a concept in *Tanya*—the Written Torah of *Chassidus*—similar to the *mitzvah* to write a *Sefer Torah*, even if it is not exactly the same:

What appears to me is that in matters of *avodah*, there are matters of intellect and matters of *segulah* (spiritual efficacy).

For example: breaking a bad trait by being diligent in the opposite trait, or refining the power of desire by using it only for good—all of this is according to logical reasoning (*ta'am v'da'as*). "Charity elevates"—that one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over—is a matter of *segulah*. It is understood that not all people, and not all times within the same person, are equal; what is sometimes only a matter of *segulah* in one’s state can, in another state, become a matter of intellect.

Now, in matters of *avodah* that are according to intellect, it is the obligation of everyone to seek out advice and paths, according to what is explained in the books of our Rebbes, both regarding one’s own *avodah* and regarding "love your neighbor as yourself." This is not the case with matters of *segulah*; what was said was said, and even regarding that, one must clarify whether it was an instruction for a specific time or for all time. But one does not derive general laws from a novelty.

Regarding the aforementioned hand-copied *Tanya*: In general, this is a matter of *segulah*. There is a person who will make such a strong impression on his soul that the "loss of time" from studying *Tanya* (etc.) is outweighed by the reward of the holiness of the thing being fixed in his soul. But for the vast majority, a servant who can be a diamond-cutter and chooses **for himself**—as opposed to following an instruction—to give his time to simple tasks, this is not the path at all. And this is simple.

The two stories of our Sages are well-known regarding the two extremes: Rabbi Akiva, when he occupied himself with a *meis mitzvah* (an unattended corpse), which takes precedence over everything, but he interrupted his study with a Torah scholar because of it—he was told, "For every step, etc." (*Kesuvos* 17a). And on the other hand, when Rabbi Zeira was tired, he occupied himself by sitting at the entrance of the *beis medrash* to stand up for Torah scholars (*Berachos* 28a).

Enclosed is the *Kuntres Purim* that has just been published. It is to merit the public with it.

We will also send you some of our other publications as you requested. Please be kind enough to acknowledge receipt.

With blessings for a happy Purim and a good heart, and with regards to all those who seek your welfare.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 444

B"H, 11 Adar II, 5708

To Mr. Alexander HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In honor of the Yom Tov of Purim, I am writing to you on behalf of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch and in my own name to wish you a joyous Purim.

I am enclosing the maamar that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, may he live, released for Purim, as well as copies of my letters to our friends Mr. Stulman and Mr. Lesser, may they live.

The Gemara (Bava Basra 9a) states, "Greater is the one who causes [others] to do [a mitzvah] than the one who does it himself." This means that as great as the merits are of those who support with their money, even greater are the merits of the one who brought them close and led them to perform these good deeds.

And every time we think about the important assistance that our friends have provided to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch through your help, and we feel gratitude toward them, our gratitude toward you—as the one who caused this, who brought them closer to Yiddishkeit in general and to the work of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch in particular—is far greater.

I hope that you will continue your good work and see to it to influence our good friends to make even greater efforts to help carry out the program of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which is constantly expanding and **must** continually expand. Already today, the minimal requirements of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch are far greater than the maximal requirements were a few years ago.

With heartfelt greetings and best wishes for a Purim of joy and goodness of heart to you and all yours, may they live.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## Shemah

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' M. may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was informed by his brother, R' Y. may he live, that a daughter was born to him, and subsequently that her name in Israel was called Rachel. I hereby send my thanks that my suggestion was accepted, and my blessings that you may raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with abundance in both physical and spiritual matters.

To conclude with a word of Torah, for it is a matter of significance: It is written in *Yonas Eilem*, Chapter 8, that *Vayehi Ohr* (And there was light) has the same gematria as *Rachel*. This can be explained based on what is written in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* beginning *Vatosif Esther*, that *Knesses Yisrael* is called by the name of the level of *Rachel* when she is in a state of revelation. This is true for every individual among the Jewish people—that their desire should be to achieve *bitul* and to be included in His light, may He be blessed, and this is [accomplished] through revelation and *hispaalus*.

Now, among the Jewish people, every matter must be achieved through *avodah* and the superiority of light coming specifically from darkness, as is well known. With this, we can understand the words of our Sages in *Bereishis Rabbah*, Chapter 3, [that] "And there was light" corresponds to the Book of *Shemos*, in which the Jewish people emerged from darkness to light—and there is no need to elaborate further here.

With blessings of Mazal Tov and wishes for a happy and joyous Purim,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a receipt for 18 shekel in the name of Rachel bas Rivkah Hecht, which was donated to tzedakah on her behalf.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres* for Purim; may you share its merit with the public.

## Shmo

13 Adar Sheni, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., R’ Y.A. Orenstein, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I trust that my telegram to Kolel Chabad and the Worldwide Tehillim Society, requesting prayers for the health of Mordechai Yaakov ben Baila, was received in time. They will surely do so. Please have the relatives give 36 shekels to the Kolel and 36 shekels to the Tehillim Society through R’ M.G. The receipts should be sent to me, but they should be written in the name of Mr. Farber, each for thirty-six (twice Chai) dollars.

I ask your forgiveness for not having replied to your letter until now; it is only due to the many pressures that have surrounded me. I take this opportunity to express my thanks for your copying into your letter two points regarding the interpretation of the passage "And He saw his suffering" and the passage "He will send upon them the fury of His anger," etc.

Regarding your question on the *sefer Shaar HaSukkos*, in the *maamar* beginning "To understand the statement of the Zohar, Parshas Emor," where it is written there: "But metals and stone—their flat pieces are tamei, etc., and flat pieces of wooden vessels are tahor, etc." Yet, it is explicit in the Gemara (*Shabbos* 58a) that stone vessels cannot contract tumah.

There are several ways to explain this, some of which are forced; choose whichever you prefer:

1) The *sefer* there lists all the categories that cannot contract tumah, noting that there is a distinction between flat pieces and vessels, whereas for things that can contract tumah, there is no distinction between a flat piece and a vessel. Stone falls into the latter category, because in the case of things that can contract tumah, there is no distinction between a flat piece and a vessel—namely, in the tumah of *golel v’dofek* (see *Tosafos* s.v. *ad*, *Kesuvos* 4b).

2) Seemingly, it appears to me that the tumah of *golel v’dofek* is a matter of wooden construction (*Chullin* 129a), which is why one may use them for *sechach* for things that are tamei via *golel v’dofek*, such as boards used as a cover for a chest. According to this, one could say that the *siddur* (the *maamar*) first explains the law of **vegetation** (*tzomeiach*), that as long as it is growing, it cannot contract tumah at all. Afterward, it explains two types of **inanimate matter** (*domem*), where there is a distinction between a vessel and a flat piece, and where there is no distinction between them. For the **foundational principle** of this *drush* is the connection between the concepts of "vessel" and "tumah." The second category includes metals and stone, **in both of which** the tumah is not dependent on the definition of a "vessel" (for metals, even a flat piece can contract tumah; for stone, even a vessel cannot). The first category includes wooden vessels. However, one should not act like a peddler and list everything; therefore, it only brings the **beginning** of the Mishnah regarding these laws, and hints at the rest with the word **"etc."** Just as the word **"etc."** appearing after the words "flat pieces of wooden vessels are tahor" hints at the law that their receptacles are tamei, so too the first word **"etc."** hints at the laws—that certainly, receptacles of stone vessels are tahor, and certainly their flat pieces are as well.

3) Since the analogy above in that *sefer* mentions only metals and wood, it is most likely that in the parable, too, only metals and wood should be mentioned, and the word "stone" is a scribal error. Either it should be removed entirely, or it was displaced from the line **preceding it**, where it should say: "It is found in the world of Asiyah that vegetation, such as trees and produce (and inanimate matter), and stone are not vessels that can contract tumah at all."

Please be kind enough to confirm receipt of this letter.

With blessings for a happy and joyous Purim, and regards to all those who seek my welfare,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 347

B"H, 18 Adar II, 5708

To the distinguished scholar, esteemed for his good deeds, active in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi N. Mindel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

**1. Regarding the count of the Rabbinic mitzvos.** The question divides into three: a) What is the number of Rabbinic mitzvos? b) Which of the Sages' enactments are included in this count? c) Why were these specific enactments included in the count and not others? I will address them one by one.

a) **The number of Rabbinic mitzvos.** The Shelah writes (Parshas Yisro, Chelek Torah Ohr, at the beginning): "The Ten Commandments contain 620 letters, corresponding to the *Keser Torah*. 613 letters correspond to the 613 mitzvos, and the seven extra letters are the **seven** Rabbinic mitzvos, **as the early authorities have written**," end quote. Similarly, the following count **seven** Rabbinic mitzvos: *Sefer HaChinuch* (at the end of the indices), *Megaleh Amukos* (Ofan 55), *Maorei Ohr* (Os Zayin, subsection 13), Admur HaZaken (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 27 and elsewhere), the Gra (in *Sefer Beis Yitzchak*, in his name), *Heichal HaBracha* on the Torah (at the end), *Mitzvos HaShem* (on the mitzvos, at the end), and others.

The only exception is R. D. Nieto in *Sefer Kuzari Sheni* (Vikuach 3, 1), who counts **ten** Rabbinic mitzvos.

b) **Which enactments are included in the count of Rabbinic mitzvos.** Netilas yadayim, Eiruvin, Berachos, Shabbos (candles), Megillah, Chanukah, Hallel. These are listed in *Sefer HaChinuch*, *Megaleh Amukos*, *Heichal HaBracha*, the aforementioned *Mitzvos HaShem*, and others.

c) **What is the reason that specifically these enactments were counted.** They were not included in the count as mitzvos **in their own right**, but rather those enactments that have no basis in the Torah, and regarding which the Sages ordained that a blessing be recited (*Mitzvos HaShem*).

**Note:** The *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* (at the end of the section on positive commandments) and *Shaarei Kedushah* by R. Chaim Vital (Part 1, Gate 4) count other enactments as Rabbinic mitzvos and omit some of the above, but neither of them states how many Rabbinic mitzvos there are in total. Therefore, it can be said that they do not disagree with all the aforementioned sources that count **seven** Rabbinic mitzvos; rather, they differ on which enactments should be included in the count and which should be omitted. Just as we find a dispute regarding the count of the Torah-level mitzvos—where everyone agrees that their number is 613, yet there are differing opinions as to what is counted and what is omitted—and this is not the place to elaborate.

**2. Whether the terms *chochma*, *binah*, and *daas* are found in the Tanach.** In *Shemos* (31:2), it appears as *chochma*, *tevunah*, and *daas*.

The expression *chochma binah* in construct form: See *Devarim* 4:6; *Yeshayahu* 29:14; *Mishlei* 4:5-7, 7:4, 16:16, 23:23; *Iyov* 28:12, 28:20, 38:36, 39:17.

The expressions *chochma binah daas* in construct form: *Yeshayahu* 11:2; *Mishlei* 3:5-7, 8:12-14, 9:10, 30:2-3.

**3. What is the difference between *binah* and *tevunah*.** Regarding the levels of the intellect, *binah* denotes a higher level of intellect, or in the language of the *Zohar* (Vol. 3, 291a), *binah ilah* (higher *binah*) is superior to *tevunah*. That is, even though *binah* is when the intellect has already arrived at explanation and comprehension in detail and the understanding of one thing from another (unlike *chochma*, which denotes the flash of the intellect and the beginning of its revelation in the brain (*Tanya*, chapters 3 and 18)), nevertheless, the essence of it is still the intellectual analysis and logical explanations. When, after the analysis, one arrives at practical conclusions, and these become the essence—the focus of one's engagement—while the intellectual explanation becomes secondary and hidden, then the term *tevunah* applies to it (see there in the *Zohar*, and in the commentaries on *Mishlei* 2:3, where both terms, *binah* and *tevunah*, are cited together, and elsewhere).

Of course, these distinctions between *binah* and *tevunah*, or *chochma* and *binah*, apply in the Scriptures or in the words of our Sages when they are **precise** about these details. However, in places where these distinctions have no practical implication for the matter being discussed, they use one of these terms that is most relevant to that specific statement, even though the intent includes the other levels of the intellect as well. And this is not the place to elaborate with proofs.

**4. Regarding Rashi’s commentary (*Shemos* 32:4) that the *Erev Rav* made the calf, and therefore they said, "These are your gods, O Israel," and did not say, "These are our gods, O Israel." If so, how is the expression "Shema Yisrael" to be interpreted?**

Rashi’s precision lies in the fact that they said "your gods" and not "our gods," and regarding this he explains that the speaker could not include himself among those to whom he was speaking. But in "Shema Yisrael," the verse concludes afterward, "Hashem Elokeinu," etc.

Furthermore, when the head of the people speaks to the people, it is customary to use a style where he does not include himself with them. But in the incident of the calf, the call "These are your gods, O Israel" was also made by the people, and therefore it is explained that this was done by a separate segment of the Jewish people—the *Erev Rav*.

The call "To your tents, O Israel" (*Melachim I* 12:16) is not relevant here, because there, every individual has his own tent, as is understood.

With wishes for success and blessing, that your speeches may be words that come from the heart and enter the hearts of the listeners, to increase their knowledge of Hashem and to strengthen them in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. Best regards to the entire group, may they live.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

However, he does lead for Mincha on Erev Shabbos or Erev Rosh Chodesh. The Half-Kaddish and Barechu of Friday night do not pertain to the mourner, and the same applies to Kel Adon and Aleinu.

c) You mention a story from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, regarding Admur Maharash and the Rav of Belz (from the Riga sichos). Perhaps you could provide me with the details of the sichos from that holiday that you remember?

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Pesach, which was just published. I am certain you will share its merit with the public.

Wishing you, your household, and all those dear to you a kosher and joyous holiday, and may we merit the true and complete Redemption immediately.

The essential work of the *Melach* is to expand kosher education and push aside the *treif* education through kosher *melamdim*, textbooks, and reading material in the holy tongue, and the planting of *yiras shamayim* in parents and teachers through learning in general and the study of *Chassidus* in particular, etc., etc. Now, it is possible to penetrate circles that have never before offered such an opportune time to engage with them and who would be willing to listen. Yet, because of the "sin of the tree," etc., there are obstacles, and it seems there is not enough money even to begin the work. This requires effort to find the means and to demonstrate that the obstacle does not exist in the world (and as the distinction between a *nisayon* and a *birur*), and after that, what room is there for his response...

I will conclude with blessings for a kosher and joyous *Chag HaPesach* and with the hope to hear good news from you.

## 454

454

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Tzvi, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Your letters confirming receipt of the *kuntreisim* for Purim and the 2nd of Nissan have been received. Enclosed is the *kuntres* for *Chag HaPesach*, and I trust you will merit to share it with the public (including those who are currently in the "public domain," as per the response to *Mashiach*—specifically when "your springs spread outward").

Surely you have comments regarding my letter from 11 Adar Rishon, and I will be pleased if you [share them] in this regard, in accordance with the words of our Sages (Bava Metzia 84a) regarding Resh Lakish, who would raise [twenty-four] difficulties whenever he heard a teaching, etc.

Give my regards to the entire group. With blessings for a kosher and joyous *Chag HaPesach*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***454***

From the secretariat's copy.

**Rabbi Tzvi:** Lieberman. Another letter to him—see above, 443.

## Year

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5708

To the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 23 Adar Sheini, and in response:

1) The continuation of the *Rosh Hashanah* [maamar] of this year concludes in the *maamar* of *Parshas Noach*.

2) The *Hayom Yom* has been sent to you as you requested. Since this is an exception to the rule, you will surely make an effort to share its merit with the many.

3) Whatever funds you have on hand for printing matters and for the *Sefer Torah* should be turned over to the office of the *Rav* [Rabbi] B.G., and they will notify us here, and we will receive the equivalent. After the holiday of *Pesach*, the *Sefer Torah* committee will announce which letters have fallen to [the donors'] lot.

4) Enclosed is a *Kuntres* for the holiday of *Pesach*, to be shared for the merit of the many.

While studying it, I looked for an explanation of the *maamar* [beginning with the words] "When the *Sitra Achra* is subdued, it is removed..." and I found it in *Torah Or*, as noted in the footnote. It occurred to me that perhaps one could say that this is also the explanation for the custom of those who transcribe *maamarim* of *Chassidus* to conclude with the word *Salik* ("concluded"). They are hinting that at the conclusion of the *maamar*—that is, the matters that are within the realm of understanding and comprehension—*Salik* ("ascends") the light that is drawn down, the *Ohr Makif* and *Sovev*, the exalted and transcendent, the verification of *Chochmah* that comes after understanding, and the *avodah* of *Kabbalas Ol* that follows the *avodah* that is according to *Ta'am V'Da'as*. There is much to elaborate on this.

Wishing you a *Pesach* that is kosher and joyous for all.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Sent via one of the *mashpi'im* to give one of them to each of the *batei medrash* of *Anash*, and thanks for the trouble.

## 557

B"H, 14 Nissan, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' H. H., may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

1) I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 18 Adar II. In the meantime, you surely have received my letter from 26 Adar II, along with the enclosed *Kuntres* for 2 Nissan and the letter to R' Sh. Z.

2) From Weinberg, the funds from here have been received.

3) Enclosed is a *Kuntres* for *Chag HaPesach* which has just been published; may you merit to share it with the public.

4) I have received news that one of our friends has succeeded in arranging for the Vaad HaYeshivos of Chicago to grant the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva five hundred [dollars] from here, in addition to the previous amount.

5) You are surely aware that Rabbi Sorotzkin received one hundred thousand dollars here from the Joint [Distribution Committee] immediately upon his arrival for the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, and this is aside from what he has been collecting all along from institutions and other places.

6) I wish to express my blessings for the Bar Mitzvah of your son, the *avreich* Eliyahu Dovid, may he live, which falls on 16 Nissan, the day of the *Ketziras HaOmer*.

One may explain this based on the well-known concept that the harvesting of the *Omer* of barley—which is animal fodder—is "when the sickle is first applied to the standing grain" (*be'hachel chermesh bakamah*), referring to the stature of the *nefesh habehamis*. Now, the Tzadukim, who follow their own intellect, argue that a person is incapable of this *avodah* unless it is "on the morrow after the Shabbos"—immediately following the Shabbos, when his world is in a state of ascent and there is no room for the waste of "your Shabbos" (*shabbososeichem*). [They argue that this] does not apply when he is previously occupied with matters of *ochel nefesh* (food for the soul), where there is a concern for waste. This is as ruled in *Shulchan Aruch*, *Siman* 529, that one must be standing over it so that he does not sin, especially according to the opinion that carrying from a private domain to a public domain is permitted [on Yom Tov], even for unnecessary matters.

However, this is not the way of the Children of Israel, who accept the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven. Rather, whether it is in proximity to Shabbos or not, and whether his body is so refined that he can ascend to Heaven as he is, or whether he is "ruddy" (i.e., of a lower nature) and possesses no life of his own at all—he performs his *avodah* through this, by establishing the yoke of *teshuvah* and the yoke of Torah. For even the Torah, "your wisdom and your understanding," is rooted in the fear of Heaven and the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven.

I must be brief due to the holiness of the day.

May it be the will of Hashem that you see much *nachas* and pleasure from this son and from the rest of your household, may they live, in all matters, with abundance.

Concluding with blessings for a happy and kosher *Chag HaPesach*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 258

B"H, 14 Nissan, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [scholar], R' Naftali Gluskin, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 22nd of Adar. Regarding the present matter, I am enclosing the *Kuntres* for *L'Chag HaPesach* which was published yesterday. Even though it will be received after the *Yom Tov*, you will surely endeavor to share its contents with the public—whether through the *maamar* or the *sicha*—each person according to their capacity (as the *Hakdamas HaTanya* states, based on the *Zohar*). However, in all of them, the "master of the house" must be known.

It could be said that this is the point of contention with Pharaoh, who said, "Go now, you men, and serve Hashem." But our approach, which Moshe charted for us—and which is the *hitpashtuta* (extension) in every generation, and especially in the generation of the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, as stated in *Tikkunei Zohar* (Tikkun 69)—is that "with our youth and with our elders we shall go, with our sons and with our daughters." And it is specifically through this that "it is a festival of Hashem for us."

With wishes for a kosher and joyous *Chag HaPesach*, and with regards to all those who seek your welfare.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 359

The main point of my letter: The *Piskei Dinim* needs to be enlarged slightly, so that it matches the size of the *Tzemach Tzedek* in our editions—that is, the pages should be 25.5 cm by 16.5 cm. The binding should be 26.5 cm by 17.5 cm.

If it is no longer possible to enlarge the pages, perhaps at the very least you can enlarge the binding as mentioned above. Bind it in two volumes.

The *Re'em* grid pattern must be the same as the one on the *Tzemach Tzedek* in our editions, which is the same as the one I added to *Derech Mitzvosecha*.
