## 360

27 Nissan, 5708

To the *avreich*, the learned and G-d-fearing, etc., R’ Sh. *sheyichyeh*,

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your question on what is written in the *maamar* "Vayareach Hashem" 5708, section 30, that the configuration of created beings—"whether they are round spheres or square and horned, this is not specified in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*"—given that our Sages have stated (Yerushalmi, end of Maseches Maaseros; Nedarim 3:2; Shevuos 3:8; Tosefta, end of Maaseros) that there is no "square" from the six days of Creation—[in the *maamar* "VehaChochmah Ta'oz" 5663, it is written: "whether round or horned or triangular"*].

First, we must clarify whether this rule is universally accepted and in all respects:

1) The Bavli and Yerushalmi—in Shevuos (29a and there), regarding a false oath... "If I did not see a snake like the beam of an oil press, let me be *taraf*." The Gemara challenges this: "All of them are *taraf* [i.e., doomed/torn], even if it is [merely] a back [i.e., a snake's back]." It would have been more appropriate to say "like the **square** beam of an oil press," as is stated in the Yerushalmi there, and then there would be no room *ab initio* for the challenge "all of them are *taraf*..." (and see what is written in *Shirei Korban* on the Yerushalmi in Nedarim there). However, if you say that the Bavli does not hold by the rule that there is no "square" from the six days of Creation, then it is understandable. It also explains, **simply**, the difference in the texts of the Bavli and the Yerushalmi. Yet, this still requires study, as according to many commentators, *taraf* means square (see *Aruch*, entry *taraf*; and *Aruch HaShalem* there).

2) Rabbi Shimon ben Gamliel and the *Tanna Kamma*. In the Tosefta at the end of Maaseros, it seems, on the face of it, that the *Tanna Kamma* disagrees with Rabbi Shimon ben Gamliel, who states the aforementioned rule, and this is not like the *sugya* in the Yerushalmi there. As mentioned above, this is somewhat forced, for if so, the two *Shas* texts—or Rabbi Shimon ben Gamliel and the *Tanna Kamma*—disagree on the reality of the matter.

3) There is no "square" from the six days of Creation in living creatures, but there is "square" in foodstuffs—this is the conclusion of the Yerushalmi from the *beraisa* there.

4) Even in living creatures—only a square on all sides with all its surfaces smooth does not exist from the six days of Creation, but there is a square that is round on one side, or at least one of its surfaces is not smooth (Yerushalmi there).

5) According to the interpretation of the *Noda B'Yehuda* (*Even HaEzer*, 1st edition, sec. 21; 2nd edition, sec. 31) that the rule "a woman does not conceive from one act of intercourse" means that this is the vast majority of cases, but there are exceptions—the same may be said regarding the rule that there is no "square" from the six days of Creation.

6) Generally, "square" means its length is equal to its width (though this is difficult in *Zevachim* 62a), but in a borrowed sense, a long rectangle is also called "square." It is possible that this is what was intended in the *maamar*. Based on the above, there is no difficulty with what is written in the aforementioned *maamar* "Vayareach."

It should be noted:

a) Based on what is written in section 7, there is no difficulty with the well-known fact that a crystal of salt is cubic and all its surfaces are smooth.

b) Based on what is written in section 4, one can understand what is written in the *Mechilta* at the beginning of *Parshas Beshalach* (cited in *Yalkut Shimoni* there), which states: "And they returned and camped before Pi HaChiroth. What were these *Chiroth*? They were not sloped, but rather mound-like..." See the entire length of the passage, which seemingly is not understood at all. What is it teaching us, and why does it elaborate in its style: "They were not... but rather..."? It should have said: "These *Chiroth* were mound-like..."

It can be explained that it wants to clarify that the encampment before Pi HaChiroth **compelled** one to say "they are entangled," as it is written there, "There is no 'entangled' except for 'confused'." It proceeds to specify: They were not sloped (for then there is no proof, as they are confused, because when the Egyptians caught up to them, the *Bnei Yisrael* could have climbed them on **all** sides and escaped), but rather mound-like (like a wall). They were not *terutos* (open on at least **one** side—see Yerushalmi, beginning of *Maseches Shabbos*, and *Aruch*, entry *tartot*—to escape), but rather surrounded. They were not round (for with two round objects, such as round pillars and the like, adjacent to one another, one who wishes to pass between them only needs to demolish the part of the circle at the **narrowest** point), but rather square (and if so, they are touching, and one must demolish the entire length of their thickness).

They were not "made by man" (which it is simple that another man could destroy), but "made by Heaven." (And if you ask: How is it possible that they were "made by Heaven," for there is no "square" from the six days of Creation? Therefore, it concludes:) "And they have eyes that are open," and if so, their surface is not smooth. This resolves **the entire** length of the language in the *Mechilta* and also its **style** and **order**.

- Regarding what is written "they were not made by man, etc.": 1) It explains their status, that Pi HaChiroth was not prohibited even according to the one who says it was *avodah zarah*, because "the mountains are not their gods" (*Avodah Zarah* 45a)*. 2) It resolves **simply** why the Holy One, Blessed be He, told them to camp before Pi HaChiroth, even though one cannot say "keep for me [a place] near *avodah zarah*" (*Sanhedrin* 63b), and even if it is a rabbinic prohibition, a matter that the Torah explicitly permitted, the Sages do not prohibit, as is known (and noted in *Yad Malachi*, rule 290).

See also *Daas Zaken Mibaalei HaTosafos* on *Shemos* 14:2.

c) The expression "from the six days of Creation" can be interpreted: 1) A creation by the hands of Heaven, even if it came **after** the six days of Creation, such as the *tachash* and the mouth of the earth; but from the actions of Adam HaRishon on the **sixth** day, it is possible that there was also a square. 2) **Everything** that existed during the six days of Creation, whether made by Heaven or made by man. But it is possible for there to be a **creation afterwards** that is square. This requires further study.

d) In *Chassidus* and Kabbalah: In *Avodas HaLevi* (Part II, p. 73b), he cites *Sefer Limudei Atzilus* that the first *Tzimtzum* is in the mystery of a square, and he explains it. In *Ma'orei Or*, letter 6: Every square thing is in the *Nukvah*... The earth is square. In *Biurei HaZohar* to *Zohar Chadash* 180a. In the *maamar* "Vayehi Binsoa" 290, and in the *maamar* "HaOseh Sukkaso" 270, is an explanation of the concept of a circle and a square. In the section *Drush Brachas HaZimun* is an explanation of the concept of the six days of Creation. And more.

***

It was noted some time ago regarding what is recounted in *Sefer Toras Shalom* that the Alter Rebbe innovated a method of salvation for R’ P., the author of *HaHafla'ah*: "Since the Rambam rules that a *goses* (dying person) is considered as dead, if he were a *goses* and then recovered, the verdict would have already been fulfilled. The *Chavraya* (the group) and the Maggid at their head agreed to the ruling of the Rambam, and so it was"—and I wrote there (p. 332) that I did not find this in the Rambam, and on the contrary—therefore it seems to me that it should say Rashi (*Kiddushin* 78b, end of side), and such is also the opinion of the *Rif* and the *Bach* in *Even HaEzer*, subsection 21.

One might say that what is written in *Toras Shalom* does not refer to the dispute among the *poskim* as to whether a *goses* can perform an action, but rather to his status as an entity unto himself. If so, it is explicit in the words of the Rambam (*Erchin* 1:13) who writes: "A *goses* has no... value, since most *gosesim* are destined for death, he is as one dead." If so, there is no need to correct the premise.

But this cannot be said:

1) The entire style of the story is that the Alter Rebbe searched and found an opinion that contains some innovation, and then there had to be the agreement of the Maggid and the *Chavraya* on the opinion of this *posek* that the *halacha* follows his words—(see there, p. 96)—and only because of this was R’ P. saved.

If you say that the intention is to the law of *Erchin* mentioned above—this is a standard *Mishnah* and is agreed upon everywhere; why would we need to mention the Rambam or another *posek* and require the decision of the Maggid, etc.!

2) Even without the style of the story, the very fact proves that this cannot be said, for a verdict of death was passed on R’ P. in the Heavenly Court, and the Maggid sought advice on how to save him. Now, one who is going to be executed according to Torah law has no status and is as one dead, because the Torah kills him (as in the language of the *Peirush HaMishnayos* to *Erchin* 1:3)—and it can be said that he is **even more** than a *goses*, for only the **majority** of *gosesim* are destined for death, whereas one sentenced to death is certainly dead **in potential**. If so, what would be added by him becoming ill and becoming a *goses*, for ultimately he is also not dead **in actuality** according to **this** opinion*. *It is astonishing.*

And if you say that this comes as a punishment and suffering of atonement, then it has no connection to a *goses*, who can exist even without suffering. It should have said that he would become blind and then regain his sight, for he is considered as dead (*Nedarim* 64b) **according to the opinion****.

And one cannot distinguish and say that specifically one going to be executed according to human law is considered as dead because there is no possibility of reversal, whereas one sentenced in the Heavenly Court, where *teshuvah* is effective, the King—the King of the World—reverses His word (see there in *Peirush HaMishnayos*)—for if *teshuvah* were effective to nullify the verdict of R’ P., then why did he need to become ill and a *goses*? He should have been saved through *teshuvah*. This is difficult.

***

He also elaborated in his first letter to reconcile the language of the Rambam in various places, even if one were to say that he holds like the opinion of Rashi that a *goses* is as one dead, and even though the surface of his language does not seem so, and the *Hagahos Maimoniyos* and others wrote that the Rambam holds that he is considered as living. But through this, it might be possible to reconcile what is written in the *Lechem Mishneh* by way of **possibility** in order to **resolve a difficulty** and **precision** in the words of the Rambam.

Now, I do not know what compels him to enter into all this forced reasoning. The gates of answers are not locked. And even if he were correct in everything he wrote in his letter, even then, in my humble opinion, one must correct *Toras Shalom*. Consider this:

The Alter Rebbe could have supported his advice and ruling on what Rashi and the *Rif* (and the *Bach*, who is one of the later **poskim**) write **explicitly**, and instead he brought the Rambam, and relied on this—that through several forced interpretations and the rejection of the interpretation of the *Hagahos Maimoniyos* and others, it could be said that **even** the Rambam holds like Rashi. There is no greater astonishment than this.

Signing with wishes for the best, and with the merit of his parents, may they live,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

361

a) The cases are not comparable, for the Torah entrusted all the laws of valuations and monetary assessments to the earthly Beis Din. Therefore, it can be said that **by definition**, they are also included in the rule that a judge has only what is visible to the eyes, and not what is in the heart or hidden. As explained (in *Responsa Noda B’Yehuda*, Orach Chaim, 1st ed., 36; *Responsa Chaim Sha’al*, Vol. 2, 62; *Pesach HaSha’ar* to *Responsa Tuv Ta’am V’Da’as*, 2nd ed., Laws of Treifos; see also Rambam, Laws of Idol Worship, ch. 4, law 6. Regarding what is written in *Responsa Shem Shimon* by R. Shimon Pollak, 1st ed., Choshen Mishpat, 2, interpreting the Gemara *Bava Basra* 159a, that Moshe is disqualified from testifying for his father-in-law, and *Shabbos* 118b, "I know **myself** that I am not a Kohen," and the *Maharsha* in *Zevachim* 101a regarding why Pinchas did not see the tzaraas of Miriam, which is due to the concept of *gilgulei neshamos*—this requires further study), this applies to *teshuvah*, which is ineffective against the punishments of a Beis Din. This is not the case in the matter at hand, which pertains **only** to the Heavenly Beis Din. And if so, in the manner in which his obligation came about, it is self-evident that his exemption can also come about.

It should be noted that there is an intermediate state between the two categories mentioned above: matters where the ruling is in the **revealed** Torah, but the punishment is a specific punishment by the **Hand of Heaven**. In this case, *teshuvah* that is in the heart and matters that are hidden are effective (*Makkos* 13b; see also *Tosafos* to *Kesuvos* 30a, *Rosh* to *Sotah* ch. 3, and this is not the place to elaborate).

b) This requires further study from *Devarim* 31:28 (based on *Tosafos* to *Avodah Zarah* 17a) and the *Pesikta* brought in *Yalkut Shimoni*, Remez 191: "And he called to Michael and Gavriel, etc., through an **elder** and through **witnesses**."

c) Regarding the matter of "It is not in heaven," see the discussion in *Shem HaGedolim* by the Chida, Vol. 1, letter *yud*, 224; *Sdei Chemed*, Klalim, letter *aleph*, subsections 94, 101, 112; *Responsa Chasam Sofer*, Vol. 6, 98; Chida’s commentary to *Avos* 6:6; the introduction of *Keses HaSofer* to *Responsa Min HaShamayim*; and elsewhere. Note also *Beis HaLevi* on Parshas Vayishlach.

d) The distinction is simple: according to the opinion that disagrees with Rashi, a *goses* (dying person) is only considered dead **in potential**, for his actions are still actions, and even if his judgment was passed in Beis Din, he is still only dead in potential. Thus, the state of a *goses* does not **add** anything to the state of one who has been judged in Beis Din. This is not the case according to Rashi. In other words: the explanation of the dispute between Rashi and those who disagree with him regarding the law of a *goses* is whether a *goses* is dead only in potential or also in actuality (at least regarding most of his laws), whereas one who has been judged in Beis Din is, according to all opinions, only dead in potential.

It is forced to say that according to the first opinion, one must say *goses*, because it adds that he becomes dead in potential even from the perspective of the body.

For ultimately, since death in potential is insufficient, death of the body in potential is also insufficient.

e) It is possible that the *Or Sameach* intends in his language (and I have not seen the original text) a person to whom the commandment "Do not murder" does not apply. With this, the difficulty raised against the *Or Sameach* is resolved.

f) I have already told you orally that there are two questions here: 1) **From where do we know** that through the verdict of the Beis Din itself, one becomes a "dead man" (*gavra katila*), 2) How is it possible **to explain** this. In response to the second question: the logic is simple. We are discussing someone who has been judged: have his **laws and statutes** according to the **Torah** changed? Therefore, it is irrelevant that no physical act has been performed, since a change has occurred (even if it is not visible) according to the **ruling of the Torah**, and consequently, this changes his **legal status** according to the **Torah**.

g) *Klapai laya* (To the contrary). If, for example, even in the present time, when these events occurred only on very rare occasions, they did not wish to nullify [the laws of the four deaths], then certainly it would not have been understood at all if they had nullified the law of *malkos* (lashes).

Regarding his difficulty as to [why] it is not explicitly stated that the law of *malkos* was not nullified, it can be explained in several ways, among them: a) When our Sages taught that the law of the four deaths was not nullified, they were still discussing the Beis Din’s law of *malkos*. And afterwards, there is no need to inform us, for it comes by way of *kal v’chomer* (an *a fortiori* argument), as mentioned above. b) The punishment of *malkos* is the concept of "lest your brother be degraded" (*Makkos* 22b and there). If so, there is no novelty in informing us that the punishment of *malkos* was not nullified, for "lest your brother be degraded" is a daily occurrence. This is not the case with the four deaths, where we have not seen their fulfillment in the manner described in Tractate *Sanhedrin*. Therefore, it informs us that one who falls from a roof, etc., is in the place of stoning, etc.

h) I wonder if this reason can be stated, for according to this opinion, one who stones someone who is liable for strangulation is also exempt, and vice versa. And how does he fulfill his law in this? And if we distinguish that he fulfills at least a common detail that exists in all four deaths, and that in this is the commandment of "Do not murder," then in *malkos* as well, one could say the same.

## 362

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. [Minkovitz] shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Nisan:

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Lag B’Omer, which has just arrived from the binder. It is intended for you to use to bring merit to the public, as per your letter. I am certain you will inform me of the study schedule and the manner in which you intend to bring merit to the public through the aforementioned, and it will surely bring nachas ruach to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita.

I do not know who is at the head of every group regarding matters such as these, but I rely on the assumption that matters concerning my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, will not lead to any unpleasantness, and when I send the Kuntres to him, everything will surely be arranged as it ought to be.

I hope you still remember when we were together in the year 5687 at the farbrengen—held without publicity in the hallway in Malachovka—your argument and discussion regarding the subject of the Parah Adumah.

May it be the will of Hashem that we feel in our hearts and in our physical flesh what is written in the Lag B’Omer sicha within the Kuntres: that whether one is on the wheel or, Heaven forbid, beneath it, one should not be agitated, and that we are wealthy—the members of the community of Chassidim in particular—with eternal wealth.

With regards to his entire group,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Several copies of the other Kuntresim have been sent to the office for general sale.

364

365

16 Iyar, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., Moreinu Harav Yitzchak Dubov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a *kuntres* for Lag B’Omer; may you merit to share it with the public.

I hope that in the near future our *shluchim*, the *avreichim* Rabbi Poizner and Rabbi Baumgarten, will visit your country and your community. It is surely unnecessary to ask you to assist them to the best of your ability in fulfilling the goals of their *shlichus*. I only mention it to urge you to prioritize providing them with substantive assistance, both from your own part and from all those whom you are able to influence in this matter.

Regarding the questions in your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Acharei:

1) You mention what is written in the *Haggadah* with *Likutei Minhagim v’Taamim* (p. 35) — that the place for *dinim* is in the *Shulchan Aruch* and not in the *Siddur* — and you raise a difficulty: the Alter Rebbe wrote several *dinim* in his *Siddur*.

I concluded there, "And only the *minhagim* of the *Seder* are being taught." For the *halachos* in the *Siddur* are of two types: a) Complete *kuntresim* that the Alter Rebbe composed to include in the *Siddur* **as a distinct unit**. These are *psak din* in extreme brevity regarding common matters that are equal for every person, and they must be accessible even when the *Shulchan Aruch* is not on one’s table at that moment. These are called a **Seder** (as written in *Shaar HaKollel*, Ch. 1, Sec. 4) or **Halachos**. It is possible that *Hilchos Birchas Kohanim* is also included in this category. b) Individual **minhagim** (not *dinim*) pertaining to the recitation of a specific *tefillah* or *brachah* (see *Shaar HaKollel* that **all** *Hilchos Krias Shema* should be printed at the beginning of the *sefer* together).

In the *Haggadah*, the Alter Rebbe did not write a *kuntres*; rather, he brought the *minhagim* necessary to know at the time of the act. My writing in the *Likutim* is based on this.

2) I copied in *Hayom Yom* (p. 45) that *Bedikas Chometz* is after *Tzais HaKochavim* — **without qualification**. You raise a difficulty that in the *Shulchan Aruch* there are distinctions regarding this.

As written in the introduction to *Hayom Yom*, I did not bring *dinim* there, but rather the *minhagim* of the Chassidim, which are based on the *minhagim* of the *Nesi'im* or their instructions. The accepted *minhag* is as stated — **always** after *Tzais HaKochavim*.

There are several reasons for this. The one that seems most clear to me is that **according to my system**, there is also a reason here: it is our *minhag* to extend the time spent on *Bedikas Chometz* **significantly** — I did not copy this into *Hayom Yom* because I have not heard a specific measurement for it. See *Sdei Chemed*, *Ma’areches Chometz U’Matzah*, Sec. 6, Subsection 16, where he cites from *Magen HaElef* to *Hilchos Pesach*, Sec. 12, that there is a discussion regarding the words of the Alter Rebbe in the aforementioned *Kuntres Acharon* to *Orach Chaim* 431.

3) In *Tanya*, end of Chapter 28, it is written that the *inyan* of the prostrations during the *Shemoneh Esrei* is to accept the yoke of Heaven after having previously accepted it through the speech of *Krias Shema*, in order to accept it now in action. You raise a difficulty: in *Berachos* (21a), our Sages said that *tefillah* does not contain the yoke of Heaven.

One can explain this: in every *mitzvah*, there are primary elements and secondary elements. In the *mitzvah* of *tefillah* specifically, the primary element is speech (see *Tanya*, Ch. 31). Secondary to it is thought (see *Kuntres Acharon* there, s.v. *Lehavin Mah Shekasuv B’Shaar HaYichud*). The action within it is merely a secondary element of a secondary element. Therefore, our Sages said that it—the speech, which is its essence—does not contain the yoke of Heaven. This is even better understood in that the *Shas* is speaking in the context of the *takanas Ezra*, and his *takanah* was specifically regarding matters of speech, as our Sages said there (20b), "as we find at Sinai" (see *Tosfos* there). With this, the **simplicity** of the *Shas’s* question (in *Sukkah* 26b), "Shall we say that Rabbi Yehuda holds that a *baal keri* is forbidden to don *tefillin*?" is also resolved.

If so, the prostration of *Shemoneh Esrei*, whose *inyan* is the yoke of Heaven, has no connection at all to the *takanas Ezra*.

The inner reason why the *takanas Ezra* applies only to matters of speech can be explained according to our Sages that the holiness of the tongue and the holiness of the reproductive organ correspond to one another (discussed at length in *Reishis Chochmah*, *Shaar HaKedushah*, Ch. 11 and 17; *Shelah*, *Shaar HaOsios*, letter *Shin*, and elsewhere).

With blessings for all the best,

**M. Schneerson**

## 366

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5708

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Rabbi R. Sh. [Krinsky], Shochet and Bodek,

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to introduce to you the bearer of this letter, the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Chossid, a man of exemplary character, R. M. HaKohen, whom I have known for many years. I have a twofold request: to assist him to the best of your ability in obtaining the document he requires, in accordance with the agreement of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, and as he will explain to you personally. It goes without saying that there is no concern here of any impropriety regarding compensation.

This can be understood in light of what is written in *Likutei Torah* on this week’s parsha, in the *maamar* titled *Beshovri Lachem*, that words of rebuke are, in truth, nothing but blessings. The verse states, "And they shall stumble one upon another," and our Sages explain (Shevuos 39a) that this refers to "one because of the sin of his brother," for all of Israel are responsible for one another. The blessing in this is that one person can be of benefit to another, since they are intertwined and connected to one another. One does this willingly, for all of Israel are "responsible" (*areivin*) and pleasant (*ne'imim*) to one another. This is in addition to the three interpretations of our Sages' statement that "all of Israel are responsible for one another" which are brought in Chassidic discourse—especially since the reward for this is very great, as our Sages say in *Vayikra Rabbah* regarding the parsha of last week, that it is greater than what the householder himself does for that same matter.

Hoping to hear good news from you regarding the above, and sending regards to all those with you,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 367

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5708

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' D. [Bravman]—may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

1) For *Torah Ohr*, the first title page should have the layout as in the edition from which we are printing: at the top, "Sifrei Otzar HaChassidim Lubavitch"; below that, a dividing line in the middle; and in two lines, "Kovetz Shalsheles HaOhr," with "Heichal Shlishi" on the right and "Shaar Shlishi" on the left. Following this, "Sefer Torah Ohr" on *Parshas Vayakhel*, then a dividing line, then "Fourth Edition," then the Kehot seal, then "Published by... N.Y." (as was done on the title page of the *Shulchan Aruch*).

Regarding the introduction, the second title page should have "Sifrei..." and "Shlishi" as above for the first title page. Following this, "Sefer..." at the end of the book, then a dividing line, then "Fourth Edition," then the Kehot seal, then "Published by... N.Y." as above for the first title page.

Regarding the rest of the book from that point on, it should be as in the book from which you are printing. For the title page of the *Hosafos* section: "Sifrei..." and "Shlishi" as above, "Hosafos l'Sefer Torah Ohr" of the Rebbe, may his soul be in Eden, then the dividing line, then "Third Edition," then the Kehot seal, then "Published by... N.Y." as above, with the rest of the page left blank. At the end of the book, the list of corrections enclosed herewith should be included.

2) For *Likutei Torah*, the first title page should be exactly as described above for *Torah Ohr*, except that instead of "Heichal Shlishi," it should read "Heichal **Revi'i**," and it should state "Seventh Edition."

Regarding the introduction, do the same.

For the second title page, everything should be as described above, except that instead of "Printed for the fifth time," it should read "Printed for the seventh time." This should also be the case for the title pages of the volumes of *Bamidbar*, *Devarim*, and *Shir HaShirim*. At the end of all the parts, the enclosed notes should be included.

3) R' N. Nemannov has 450 *shekalim* [earmarked] for the printing. He will instruct R' N.N. as to whom to give them. Beyond this, 300 *shekalim* have already been paid to one of his creditors there, and there will be more as needed, for which I take responsibility.

4) What is the status of the *Siddur*, *Shulchan Aruch*, *Etz Chaim*, and our books, Volume 1? Surely there are no obstacles regarding the introductions. If they were printed, aside from the spiritual benefit, it would be possible to sell them in the regions and settle part of the debts. This is a matter of great urgency for those involved in this.

5) In my opinion, you should bring in someone else whose primary focus would be distribution, and I would like to suggest R' M. Teitelbaum.

6) The *Kuntres* for Lag B'Omer was surely received on time, along with the letter enclosed with it...

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 370

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5708

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Menachem Mendel, may he live, Shochet u'Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your question regarding what is written in the commentary of the Rosh on Tamid (31b), that there is an opinion that the baking of the Lechem HaPanim overrides Shabbos, and you ask who is the author of this view.

The dispute regarding this is in Menachos (95b). See what is written in Tosafos (s.v. *Ella d'tavra*): "He who taught this (that the baking of the Lechem HaPanim is inside) did not teach that (that the baking does not override Shabbos)."

According to this interpretation, there are three opinions on the matter: 1) That even the baking does not override Shabbos (and this is the view of the anonymous Mishnah, which follows the dispute there, 100b). 2) That the baking overrides Shabbos, but not the kneading and shaping. (These two opinions are cited anonymously in the Mishnah). 3) That the entire process of the Lechem HaPanim overrides Shabbos, which is the opinion of Rabbi Yehuda there.

However, according to the Rambam (Hilchos Temidin U'Musafin, ch. 5:7, 10), who rules that the baking of the Lechem HaPanim is inside and does not override Shabbos, one could say that there is no dispute among the Tannaim on this matter, and everyone agrees that the baking does not override Shabbos, as per the anonymous Mishnah there (see *Lechem Mishneh* on the Rambam there, and *Tosafos Yom Tov* on Menachos, ch. 11:2). But this is not the opinion of Tosafos, as mentioned above. This is also the case in the commentary of the Radak (Shmuel I, 21), who writes that according to Rabbi Yehuda, the baking overrides Shabbos. See the Radak and the Yalkut Shimoni there, that this was the point of contention between Doeg and Dovid* (regarding the version in the Yerushalmi, Sanhedrin ch. 10:2, it requires further study).

Now, on the face of it, this is difficult to understand. For according to the one who holds that the baking of the Lechem HaPanim overrides Shabbos, the baking must be done **specifically** on Shabbos, for otherwise it would be disqualified by remaining overnight (*linah*). And according to the dissenting opinion, the baking must be done **specifically** before Shabbos. If so, how could they have been in doubt regarding this law, when it was a practical matter that occurred every single week from the days of Moshe Rabbeinu? This is a question raised in various places (Yerushalmi, Pesachim 6:1; see *Yesod HaMishnah* by R. Margaliot).

One could say that there was always a dispute regarding this, and in every generation, they would rule according to the Sanhedrin of that time (as our Sages said, Rosh Hashanah 25** — "You have only the judge who is in your days"). Doeg was the head of the Beis Din, as Rashi explains on the verse (Shmuel I, 14), "the mightiest of the shepherds." And regarding Dovid, the Halacha was in accordance with him in every place (Sanhedrin 93b). Therefore, when both of them were in Nov **at the same time**, the question was raised once again as to whether the baking of the Lechem HaPanim overrides Shabbos or not.

- Regarding why this dispute is not counted among those that arose before Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel (Yerushalmi, Chagigah 2:2), it is because each time this law was **decided** by the majority, unlike the law of *semichah* (leaning on the sacrifice), which **remained** a subject of dispute. And this is clear. But this is not the place to elaborate.

On this occasion, I will express my confidence that just as you yourself were inspired to print one **(special)** book from the works of our holy Rebbes, so too, without a doubt, you will have a "good eye" regarding others, to arouse and urge your acquaintances and those you know so that they, too, will print from the works of our Rebbes at their own expense, to bring merit to the public. The greatness of the merit of those who act and perform in such matters certainly requires no explanation. I have written this only to urge and encourage you in this campaign as much as possible. If you will exert yourself and occupy yourself with this as is fitting, your efforts will surely bear fruit, and you will succeed in finding donors who are suitable and worthy of this great merit.

Looking forward to hearing good news from you regarding the above in actual practice, and wishing you the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 371

B"H, 7 Tammuz 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' A. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding your inquiry as to whether it is customary to eat matzah on Pesach Sheni:

In addition to what I told you orally—that our custom, which is based on the custom of the Beis Chayeinu shlita, is to eat matzah at the meal on the 14th of Iyar—I have now found in printed seforim, in the sefer *Likutei Meir* (by R' M. Bennet of Tschorda, Hungary), second edition, regarding the matters of Pesach Sheni, quoting from *Likutei Maharich* Vol. 3, that it is the custom of *anshei maaseh* to eat matzah on the 14th of Iyar. It requires study, however, as the eating of the Pesach Sheni offering is on the night of the 15th of Iyar. In the sefer *Zichron Yehuda*, it is written that the author of *Imrei Esh* and his father-in-law, R' Dovid Deutsch, were accustomed to eating matzah and also a boiled egg on the night of the 15th of Iyar.

In the sefer *Darchei Chaim V'Shalom* (by R' M. Gold of Munkatch), section 631-632, he brings that the Munkatch custom was to eat matzah and maror at the meal on the 14th of Iyar. Even though the eating of the Pesach Sheni offering was on the night of the 15th, the offering itself took place during the day, and the main thing is the beginning; and on the night of the 15th, they were also particular to eat matzah.

With best wishes,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## Hour

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5708

To the illustrious Torah scholar and Chassid, G-d-fearing and diligent in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi M. Ashkenazi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for *Chag HaGeulah* which has just been published, and may you merit to share it with the many.

You have surely already received the letter from R' Ch. M. A..

It is highly appropriate and correct that you utilize the time between 12 Tammuz and 18 Elul, in particular, to increase efforts regarding the *maamad* among all those who are connected to it (and to be precise with the language of our Sages: "all who are accustomed to it, and not [only] you"). Likewise, exert yourself in finding assistance for the *Melach* (through membership dues, donations for printing, and the like). The great necessity of this cannot be overstated, and you will surely do everything in your power regarding this.

Concluding with regards to all those who seek your welfare, and with blessings for *Chag HaGeulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***Hour***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 24, p. 419, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 380

380

B”H, 15 Tammuz, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R’ Ch. H. Havlin, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letters from 5 Nissan and 17 Sivan. In the interim, you surely received my letter from 14 Nissan, along with the *kuntres* for *Lag B’Omer*. In response to your letters:

...It has become clear that the beginning of the *maamar* by R’ Sh. Glitzenstein regarding the Mitteler Rebbe was printed in *Yahadus* in Kislev 5708. It is a pity that a reader might be misled by certain points, among them the notion that the Alter Rebbe was concerned only with the moral state of his Chassidim, at a time when he dedicated a significant portion of his time, energy, and strength to improving their economic situation. Furthermore, he even traveled personally across the country to collect funds for work in this field (as is known regarding the Alter Rebbe’s response to R’ B. of Mezhibuzh, and the *takanos* regarding *hasagas gevul*, etc., etc.). The suggestion for Jews to engage in agricultural work began with the proposal of the Mitteler Rebbe, which is cited in the aforementioned *maamar*, even though the proposal itself mentions that there were already colonies in "Steppet." Furthermore, immediately after his marriage and throughout his leadership, the Alter Rebbe also strove to disseminate agricultural work among those who listened to his voice (the colonies in White Russia; this is recounted at length in the booklet regarding the public activities of the Alter Rebbe, which is now being prepared for print).

The order for military conscription was issued in the year of the Mitteler Rebbe’s passing, which is **many** years [after] the proposal he published, and not as the superficial reading of the *maamar* would imply.

3) Please be so kind as to give R’ P. Z. Mendelson five pounds from the funds in your possession belonging to *Melach*.

4) Enclosed is a *kuntres* and a letter for 12 Tammuz. The *kuntres* was sent via regular mail.

5) Please be so kind as to inform me of the details regarding our relative, Pinchas Landau, and his family.

6) Please be so kind as to convey to R’ Ch. A. Naeh, may he live, in response to his question via Rabbi Telushkin, that I cannot guarantee that his *hagahos* will arrive here before the printing of the *Shulchan Aruch* is completed, as I do not know how long they will be in transit. However, I do not understand where the responsibility lies, since, after all, he desires to print them, and if so, he is surely obligated to prepare them for print; there is nothing here other than that he should expedite this as much as possible. If he sends the *hagahos* to me, it would be best if there were **two** copies, as the *Shulchan Aruch* is not being printed here itself, and it is appropriate that one copy remain with me and the other I will send to the *Beis Din*...

I will conclude with wishes for all the best and peace in every detail, and regards to the entire group.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 380

19 Tammuz, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, etc., Rabbi Sh. [Krinsky], Shochet and Bodek,

Peace and blessing!

Your son-in-law, the distinguished scholar, etc., Rabbi Y. Goodman, conveyed your questions to me. In response:

1) You mentioned the Chazal cited by the Ramban in his commentary on the Torah (Bereishis 2:9): "Three spoke the truth and perished from the world: the serpent, the spies, and Doeg the Edomite."

It seems the source is in *Pirkei Rabbenu HaKadosh*, Chapter 3, item 47. However, the Ramban’s version differs from ours, as in the edition I have seen (at the end of *Kol Bo*, in *Otzar HaMidrashim* by Eisenstein), the text reads: "Three who spoke the truth and perished from this world and the World to Come: the spies, Doeg, and the sons of Rimmon the Beerothite."

I would note: a) This Chazal is also cited by the Alter Rebbe in his letter from 3 Nissan 5711 (printed in *Beis Rebbe*, Chapter 20), but it is impossible to clarify his version, as he only lists the one relevant to his subject, which is Doeg. b) One should not raise a difficulty against this Chazal from what is stated in *Bereishis Rabbah* (Chapter 19) that the serpent spoke a lie, for both are true: he was banished from the world because he spoke the truth, but in order for his incitement to be accepted by Chava, he also spoke words of falsehood. See also *Torah Ohr* and *Torah Or HaChassidim* on the discourse beginning "And the serpent was cunning."

2) You were troubled by the fact that in many letters you have seen, the day of the week is not mentioned, only the day of the month, even though according to the Ramban (*Shemos* 20:8), Yisrael count all days for the sake of Shabbos—"the first day of Shabbos," "the second day of Shabbos"—because this is part of the mitzvah we were commanded (regarding Shabbos) to remember it constantly every day.

To my mind, this is not difficult: a) Even according to the Ramban, it is obvious that this is not a matter whose mitzvah applies all day long, like Torah study; rather, by mentioning it once, one has fulfilled the obligation, just as we say in the *Shir Shel Yom*, "Today is the first day of Shabbos," etc. b) In my humble opinion, it is clear that the Ramban’s intent is not to obligate us to count every day for the sake of Shabbos, but rather that if one happens to count the days of the week, one should count them for the sake of Shabbos, similar to the mitzvah of *ma'akeh* (a parapet), etc. What he meant by "constantly" is not that it must be done every day, but that it is not limited to Shabbos or Erev Shabbos alone. This also resolves why the counts in Tanach are not for the days of the week (*Rosh Hashanah* 3a). c) It seems that even initially, people do not follow the Ramban’s view, for in any case, he did not forbid counting the days of the week in other ways when not for the sake of Shabbos, and I have never seen people being careful to avoid saying or writing "Sunday," "Monday," etc.

We are currently joined by the shluchim, the esteemed scholars, Rabbi A. and Rabbi N. Gurary, who have surely told you about the sichos of the Rebbe regarding the great value and necessity of these travels. I have no doubt that despite your preoccupations, you will assist and endeavor to ensure that the aforementioned visit to your camp and its surroundings will bring the desired benefit in its entirety, in all its details and sub-details, in body and soul. I write this only to encourage you further.

Signed with wishes for all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

*Postscript:* I have since found the Chazal, "Three spoke the truth," etc., in *Machzor Vitry*, in the manuscript fragment printed at the end of *Menoras HaMaor* by R. Yitzchak Aboab (Part 4, p. 568). It reads: "Three who confessed the truth and passed from this world and the World to Come: Doeg the Edomite, the sons of Rimmon the Beerothite, and the spies. Rabbi Meir says: also the son of the man who was an Amalekite."

The notes there refer to *Avos D'Rabbi Nosson*, Version B, Chapter 45; *Pirkei Rabbenu HaKadosh*, Schechter edition (in *Three Books*), 27a; and *Otzar HaAggados*, Horowitz edition, item 133.

## 583

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished Dr. A. Hillman, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 7 Iyar (which was sent via regular mail), and I was pleased to learn that you and your family, may they live, are well.

In the meantime, my letter from before Pesach must have reached you, in which I also informed you regarding the receipt of the *Sinai* monthly journal for Adar 5707, and I thank you for it.

Regarding the comments on your letter and its sections:

a. Regarding what you wrote—that in the Bavli the expression *chazi* is common, while in the Yerushalmi it is *chami*—see the *Archei Midrash* to *Bechor* and the *Aruch HaShalem* at the end of the entry *Cham* (3). See there for several examples. However, in my humble opinion, there is more here than just this distinction, for *chazi* is a contraction of *machazeh echzeh* (I shall see a vision). It is also worth noting what is written in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Matos*, in the *maamar* beginning *Einei Kol* (ch. 1).

b. That *Haggadah* is named after "And you shall tell (*ve'higadta*) your son"—I noted in the *Haggadah* with the *Likutim* that this is stated in the *Abudarham* and elsewhere.

If you argue that the term *Haggadah* refers to the *Midrash* of the *Shema*, then this would only encompass the section of our *Haggadah* from *Avadim Hayinu* until *Vene'emar Lefanav Halleluyah*. Seemingly, this is not the implication in the *Shas* and the *Rishonim*.

c. That the signs of the *Seder* are in rhyme. It seems that this supports our version, **Rachtzah**. Seemingly, on the contrary, this supports the version *Rachatz*, because then *Barech* and *Nirtzah* also rhyme:

Kadesh, Rachatz, Maror, Korech
Karpas, Yachatz, Shulchan Orech
Maggid, Rachtzah, Tzafun, Barech
Motzi, Matzah, Hallel, Nirtzah.

d. The verses of the Wise and the Simple are in the singular, but the one speaking about the Wicked is in the plural.

Perhaps it can be suggested that the reason is that the category of "Wicked" includes types who differ in their knowledge: the Wise, the Simple, and even the one who does not know how to ask, for the common denominator among them is wickedness. Consequently, the phrasing of their question is also identical: "What is this service to you?"

—And we have seen tangibly that those who argue most strongly, "What is this service to you?" are precisely those who do not even know how to ask. —

(Although, seemingly, if so, "one wicked" should have come last. But this can be resolved.)

Rabbi Hodakov, may he live, pointed out to me that the reason for the aforementioned distinction can be explained by the fact that when wicked people speak or ask, it is in a state of confused order and disarray (based on Rashi, *Devarim* 1:22), and each one is separated and divided from his fellow (based on Rashi, *Bereishis* 46:27).

***

In the margin of your letter, you ask regarding what I copied from the *Levush*—that on a *Yom Tov* we do not say "**with love**, a holy convocation," because the acceptance of the *Yom Tov* mitzvos was only through [Hashem] forcing the mountain over them—for if so: 1) How is it that we say "And You gave us, Hashem our G-d, **with love**..." even on *Yom Tov*?

The distinction, in my humble opinion, is simple: the first "**with love**" relates upward, to the word "And You gave," meaning that You, **Hashem, gave** with love. The second "with love" relates downward, meaning that the *Bnei Yisrael* recite the holy convocation with their own love.

2) How does the statement of our Sages, "He forced the mountain over them... from here there is a great protest against the Torah" (*Shabbos* 88a), reconcile with the statement "we will do and we will hear" (and they accepted His kingdom **willingly**—this refers to the time of the Splitting of the Sea, not to the acceptance of the yoke of Torah and mitzvos)?

The inner meaning of this is as follows: The possibility of not accepting the Torah and mitzvos exists only as long as one does not recognize—with complete recognition in intellect, emotion, and tangible reality—that they are the only true good, and their absence is the ultimate evil. The closer one comes to this recognition, the more the possibility of not accepting the Torah and mitzvos diminishes.

Now, at the time of the Giving of the Torah, only fifty days had passed since the Exodus from Egypt, which had been the "nakedness of the land" in terms of corrupted character traits, etc., as is known. There had not yet been enough time for *Bnei Yisrael* to arrive at such a recognition—that they were at the opposite extreme from their previous state. Rather, **from Above**, He "forced upon them" this recognition by causing the light of the recognition of Truth to shine upon them to such an extent that they saw tangibly that the Torah and mitzvos are the ultimate good (even in physical terms), and that without them, their lives are not lives (even in physical terms). Therefore, they said with all their heart and soul, "We will do and we will hear." But since they did not arrive at this recognition on their own and gradually, but rather by way of a gift and a flash from Above, after the Giving of the Torah, nothing remained of this except an impression in a hidden state. Therefore, from that point on, there is a "protest against the Torah," because in the state in which they must fulfill the Torah and mitzvos in practice, it is a great and difficult *avodah*.

In short: At the Giving of the Torah, all of *Bnei Yisrael* were in a state of **gift from Above**, similar or identical to a prophet at the time of prophecy (see *Zohar Chadash* 94a; *Moreh Nevuchim* Part II, ch. 32 and Abarbanel there; *Avodas HaKodesh* Part IV, ch. 29; *Ikkarim* 3:11; and others, and this is not the place to elaborate), who sees visions of G-dliness; it is understood that they said "we will do and we will hear" with a willing heart and desire.

But once the prophecy departs, one cannot demand that they carry out everything they accepted upon themselves **at the time** of the prophecy.

See *Torah Or*, *Megillas Esther*, the *maamar* beginning *Chayav Inish* (the second *drush*), ch. 4.

Wishing you and your family, may they live, all the best.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 384

B”H, 3 Menachem Av, 5708

To the honorable Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and upright, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Moshe Shapira, may he live,
Atlantic City,

Peace and Blessing!

Our friend, the excellent educator Rabbi Yaakov Hecht, may he live—one of the activists in chinuch and director of the department for the protection and expansion of kosher chinuch at the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch—is planning to visit your camp to work and act for the benefit of the SHL"H program (**Sh**iurei **L**imud **H**adas — "Wednesday Hour").

The work of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch in general, and this department in particular—through which approximately ten thousand Jewish boys and girls, may they be well, from the public schools receive religious instruction free of charge—is surely known to your honor, may he live. This work, which, thank G-d, has grown and expanded greatly, requires significant resources, and the strained financial situation compels him to come to your camp to raise tangible assistance so that this great and unique institution in the field of kosher chinuch does not collapse, G-d forbid.

Therefore, I have come to request that your honor, may he live, receive Rabbi Hecht, may he live, with a friendly face and extend a helping hand to him in accordance with the extent of your influence. And although I imagine the magnitude of your many preoccupations due to your communal work, I am confident that your heart is sensitive to the great value of this educational work and that you will not refrain from being a brother-helper in this great and lofty mitzvah, which touches the souls of thousands of Jewish boys and girls. My thanks are extended to you in advance.

## 387

20 Menachem Av, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak Fogelman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your inquiry regarding what was stated in the maamar (in the *D'h* "Ten who sit," 5728) that *El* is the first of the thirteen attributes of mercy—you ask: How can this be, when the opinion of the Tosafos (Rosh Hashanah 17b), and the gloss there, is that the first *Havayah* or the second *Havayah* is the first attribute?

There are four opinions regarding the beginning of the count of the thirteen attributes (mentioned in *Korban Netanel* at the end of the first chapter of Rosh Hashanah, and see also R’ Bachya, Parshas Tisa):

1. The first *Havayah* (Pesikta Rabbasi, Shocher Tov 93, the sages of France cited in Abudraham in the commentary on the Ne’ilah of Taanis—and it appears these are the *Rabbenu Tam* in the Tosafos there, the Ibn Ezra on the Torah, the Rosh, and others).

2. The second *Havayah* (R’ N.G. in the gloss to the Tosafos there, a Gaon cited by the Ibn Ezra there—and according to the introduction of the Ibn Ezra to his commentary, this is R’ Saadia Gaon. This is also somewhat implied by the commentary of **Echad** in *Sefer HaLikutim* of the Arizal, Parshas Ki Tisa).

3. *El* (Zohar Vol. III 131b; *Etz Chaim*, Shaar Arich Anpin, ch. 11; *Peri Etz Chaim*, Shaar HaSelichos, ch. 4; *Shaar HaKavanos*, Drushei Vayaavor, Drush 3 and onwards; *Mishnas Chassidim*, Maseches She’eris HaAtzilus, ch. 10 and onwards; and others.

Regarding what is written in *Derech Emes* to Zohar Vol. I 20a, subsection 4, supporting the first opinion—it requires study. Were I not afraid, I would say it is not from R’ Chaim Vital, as it contradicts what is explained in all the writings of the Arizal as mentioned above. It has already been written that several notes from the book *Imrei Binah* were mixed in by the error of the printers into the book *Derech Emes*).

4. *Rachum* (*Sefer Chassidim*, siman 250; Maharal of Prague in *Nesivos Olam*, Nesiv HaTeshuvah, ch. 6.

Regarding what is written there, bringing proof for his words from the aforementioned Zohar and the Gemara—I have not been able to understand it, for on the contrary, it proves the opinion of the Arizal).

The accepted decision in matters of the secrets of Torah is according to the Kabbalists*. Especially since they also saw the words of the Tosafos and R’ N.G., etc., and yet they decided as stated above. The Azulai already wrote in his commentary to *Sefer Chassidim* there, and I quote: "Our Rabbis and the Tosafos in the first chapter of Rosh Hashanah strove to count the thirteen attributes because in their days the holy Zohar had not yet been revealed. But there, and in the writings of our Rabbi the Arizal, they revealed to us their count and their secret." End quote*.

According to the *nigleh* (the revealed dimension of Torah), one could say it depends on the version of the text in the Gemara. For the version of the Rif and the Rosh is that the teaching of R’ Yehuda there—that a covenant is forged for the thirteen attributes, etc.—comes immediately after the teaching regarding *Havayah, Havayah*. Therefore, it is **possible** to say that this is the beginning of the thirteen attributes—and the connection between the Rosh and the Baalei Tosafos (of whom Rabbenu Tam was a leader) is well known, as is the connection between the Rif and the Geonim.

However, according to the version in the Gemara that has spread and been accepted by us, where the Gemara precedes the teaching of the covenant of the thirteen attributes with the words *El Rachum*, etc. (and see also the version of the *Ein Yaakov*), this is **decisive** proof that the beginning of the count is *El*—as the Maharal wrote there, and this proof is cited in *Etz Yosef*** (and in *Dikdukei Soferim* they did not note this textual variation!).

Now, the Rosh there asks: If it is not according to the opinion of Rabbenu Tam, why did the custom spread that the congregation, when reciting the thirteen attributes aloud, begins with the words *Havayah, Havayah*?

The answer is understood according to what is written in the writings of the Arizal there: that these two *Havayah* names are the source of all the thirteen attributes.

This is understood according to *Chassidus*, based on what is written in *Likutei Torah*, *D’h* "And it shall be on that day a shofar shall be blown," ch. 4, and in *Torah Or*, Parshas Mikeitz, at the end of the explanation for *D’h* "For You are my lamp" (and based on this, one can answer the Pesikta and the words of *Shocher Tov* **simply** according to the opinion of the Arizal). Or, in plain words: The congregation says, "(You are) *Havayah, Havayah* (we ask that You be) *El Rachum*, etc."

As for the further question of the Rosh there, that "keeping kindness for thousands" should be one attribute—this is already answered in the Tosafos there.

With thanks for acknowledging receipt of this letter, and with wishes for all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

*See Likutei Amarim, p. 17, regarding the two names of Havayah. In the book Kisvei Kodesh, a maamar of the Baal Shem Tov is brought regarding the aforementioned maamar, and it is printed in Sefer HaBaal Shem Tov in its place.*

***387***

*Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 4, p. 1348, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.*

*)* **After some time.** In *Bnei Yissaschar*, Maamar Elul 2, 3: In the book *Doresh L’Tzion*, he brings proof for the opinion of the Zohar and the writings of the Arizal that the thirteen attributes begin with *El Rachum*, from the words of our Sages regarding the difference between the time of the Beis HaMikdash and when there is no Beis HaMikdash. If it began with the Name, then in the Beis HaMikdash it would be called as it is written, and thus there would be a distinction.

**) This is also stated in *Bnei Yissaschar* there, and he explains through this a precision in the language of Rashi, "these" (halalu).

## 388

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Chaim Hillel, may he live,
Havlin

Greetings and blessings!

My letter from last week (the main point of which was that for the time being, nothing should be done regarding R' Sheina) surely arrived. You have also surely received in the meantime the *kuntres* for Chag HaGeulah.

I trust the *yahrtzeit* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was observed as it should be. Please be so kind as to distribute from our funds, on my behalf, three pounds each to Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, the Kollel Chabad, and the Chevras Tehillim HaOlamis. I will reimburse you once you inform me.

To conclude with *pitpatei d'oraisa* regarding what I explained during the *farbrengen* on the day of the *yahrtzeit*—the insights that occurred to me regarding the Mishnah in *Keilim* (26:1)—based on *Chassidus*, I will present them here in brief:

"There are three types of shields": *Mitzvos* are crowns, etc., and there are three categories among them, meaning in the manner of their fulfillment:

The "bent shield" (*taris hakafuf*): One who fulfills them because he wants the *mitzvos* to protect him from every trouble. Furthermore, he "lies upon it" in battle—he is in the midst of the battle with the *yetzer* and yet he lies down—his head and his feet are on the same level. His *avodah* is not from the *mochin*—standing—nor from intellectual *dov-v'ra*—sitting, where the head is lowered to the feet. Rather, it is from natural *dov-v'ra* or merely from *ahavas hashem* that also includes *yirah*.

Therefore, although this is the beginning of *avodah* (Rambam, end of *Hilchos Teshuvah*), since for the time being "he serves himself" and not because of the "good taste" in spirituality, there is nothing to prevent him from becoming a "scoundrel with the permission of the Torah." Consequently, he can become *tamei*—even with *tumas midras*—meaning not only sinning due to his nature, but also becoming coarsened and sunken in materiality, even without the heat of desire (a "dead limb").

(See *Ohr HaTorah*, 246b). This is *midah k'neged midah*; just as his *avodah* is without *chayus*—*chivhei*—or *mochin*, he is in a state of lying or sitting, and thus he falls into the state of a "dead limb."

The second type is the "shield that one plays with in the *kunfon*" (*taris shemischakin bo b'kunfon*): This relates neither to lying nor sitting, because his fulfillment of *mitzvos* is through the *avodah* of *mochin*—standing—(and not through the lowering of the *midos*), through contemplation of the goodness of *Elokus*. However, he is still in the midst of battle, and it is possible that his "fellow" (see the notes of the Rebbe, of blessed memory, printed in *Torah Or*, 130a, on "Love your fellow as yourself") will strike him and cause him to fall from his level. But this occurs only through the battle of the heat of desire. Therefore, although there is no place for the *tumah* of a "dead limb," he can be *tamei* with other *tumas*, and he will certainly be *tamei* with *tumas meis*, which is the matter of "the serpent's instigation."

The third type is the "shield of the Arabs" (*tziyatz ha'arviyin*): For him, the *mitzvos* are not "vessels of service" at all. For he is an "Arab"—in holiness—he bows down to the dust, "my soul is like dust," *bitul*. Therefore, the shield is very small, as the *Ra'av* explains, for he has no existence for himself at all, but exists only to cause *nachas ruach* and joy Above. The *taanug* of the Master is his own *taanug*. Consequently, he is not even found in battle, for he is nothing but the "emissary," and there is no battle possible against him, for "they shall melt like wax." Thus, he is pure of everything.

With wishes for all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 390

B"H, Friday, 1 Elul, 5708

To the *avreich*, the *nosei v'nosei*, the *ish yirei Elokim*, the *Tamim* Yehuda Leib, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter. The questions you raise are not "clumsy questions" (*klotz-kashyos*), as you describe them in your letter; on the contrary, they touch upon fundamental matters. It is only because people are accustomed to them that they do not pay attention to their content. The very fact that they are "used" so frequently causes one to **imagine** that they are fully understood, even though, upon reflection, it appears that most of them are difficult to grasp and comprehend.

This is the case in every branch of wisdom and science: the part that requires the most study and depth is the part that encompasses the first principles and foundations of that discipline.

Questions of this nature are difficult to explain in a letter, especially when there is no time to elaborate, but I will write them in brief.

**Question:** Why is the world of Atzilus called "the world hidden from all living," the world of Beriah — "the world of the Throne," the world of Yetzirah — "the world of the angels," and the world of Asiyah — "the world of the spheres"?

**Answer:** Every thing created with intellect and wisdom has an intent and purpose. Consequently, it is understood that both the whole of the thing and its details must be in such a manner that the purpose is fulfilled.

Now, the purpose of the creation of the worlds, as our Sages of blessed memory have made known, is for the revelation of His Kingship, blessed be He (*Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, ch. 1), as is also hinted at in the verse (Yeshayahu 43:7): "Everything that is called by My name, and **for My glory** I have created it, I have formed it, and I have also made it," as expounded in *Avos* (end of ch. 6).

Just as in general, all matters below have a root above, so too, in particular, from the "Kingship of the Heavens" (*malkusa d'rakia*) was the "kingship of the earth" (*malkusa d'ara*) drawn down. Therefore, just as it is possible to understand the "Kingship of the Heavens" from the conduct of the "kingship of the earth"—as is related in the words of our Sages (*Berachos* 58a)—so too is it the case in the opposite direction: in order to understand even a tiny fraction of the "Kingship of the Heavens," one must study, **according to the instructions of our Sages**, the "kingship of the earth."

Because of this, the language common in the *Midrashim* regarding the Holy One, blessed be He, is understood: "A parable of a king, etc." Even more so in *Eichah Rabbah* at its beginning: "The Holy One, blessed be He, said to the ministering angels: 'What is the way of a king of flesh and blood? ... So do I do, etc.'"

Our Sages have taught us many details from a king of flesh and blood and the manner of kingship below: The king’s officials must be in a state of great separation from the king—"separated, foreign, and distant," in the language of the *Tanya* (loc. cit., see there). As it is written in the *Rambam* (*Melachim*, ch. 2): "They place upon him awe and fear... and he shall not stand before a person, and he shall not speak softly, and he shall not call a person by anything other than his name, etc." Yet, despite all this, they accept him as king over them because they recognize his greatness—at least to some degree. Furthermore, the king (who is worthy of being a king) does not have his **entire** essence defined by the fact that he is a king; he is a man of stature in his own right. It is only that his connection with the people is through the fact that he is called "king" over them and leads them. The order of leadership is as follows:

The qualities of the king in his own right—the people have **no** connection to this (and this is the hint of our Sages: "They do not see him when he is naked"). The qualities of the king as he is king over a people, and he envisions **in his soul and wisdom** the needs of the people and their lacks—the people do not yet **see** these. Afterward, the king goes out to his palace and sits on his throne of kingship (*Rambam*, ibid.). Based on the decision of his wisdom **within** his soul, he commands the ministers regarding the modes of governing the state, and sometimes he even announces the reason for them. It is understood that in the inner chamber, where the king sits on his throne, those present cannot forget the king, and they have no need at all for proofs that a king exists.

However, the will of the king is that the people in the far reaches of his state should conduct themselves according to his instruction. Therefore, messengers go out with the king’s decrees in their hands (and the reason for the decree is not [provided] at all) to inform all the inhabitants of the state.

And all these things are, to distinguish with an *aleph* [i.e., to differentiate with] infinite distinctions, [the same as] above:

The king **in his own right** — the matters before the *Tzimtzum*.

When it is drawn down below and he envisions **within his wisdom** the people — the world of Atzilus. It is called a "world" because he has already envisioned in his wisdom the needs of the **people**, but it is hidden from the eye of all living, as mentioned above, that the people do not see this.

He goes out to his palace, etc. — the world of Beriah, where, similar to a king sitting on his throne, the created beings are in a state of *bitul*. This is *alma d'itkasiya* (the hidden world), as mentioned above.

Below this — angels, messengers going out, the world of Yetzirah — (and through a **garment** they are revealed also in the world of Asiyah) — with decrees in their hands: kosher, invalid, innocent, guilty, etc.

Until it reaches even the far reaches of the state, to the lowest world — the world of the spheres, which are comprised of soul and body, and from them emerged all the creations in the lowly world.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to Redemption,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 391

2 Elul, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished communal leader, a man of many accomplishments, the generous R’ Moshe Tzvi Wexler, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Our representatives, the distinguished *avreichim*, the esteemed and distinguished, etc., Rabbis Shalom Chaskind and Shimon Aharon Simpson, may they live, brought us good tidings of you and your warm interest in the work of **"Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch."**

We were particularly pleased to hear that you have promised to assist the work of the Merkaz by arranging a "tea" in your home. In this way, you will not only be one who causes others to do, but you will also be a doer yourself, and it is unnecessary to elaborate on how great the *zechus* of this *mitzvah* is. We hope you will inform us in good time when the planned gathering will take place at your home.

Elul, the final month of the year, is a preparation for Rosh Hashanah, when we all come to beseech the Ribono shel Olam for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for health, *parnassah*, and all the best in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

There are two allusions for this month of Elul: 1) *Ani L’dodi V’dodi Li* (I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me), and 2) *Ish L’re’ehu U’matanos La’evyonim* (A man to his friend and gifts to the poor), both of which form the acronym *Elul*.

These two allusions indicate how the preparation of Elul must be: First and foremost, there must be "Ani L’dodi"—every Jew must return to the Ribono shel Olam with a feeling of *teshuvah*. Then, this feeling must be transformed into concrete actions, and this is what the second allusion points to—*ish l’re’ehu u’matanos la’evyonim*.

In general, a person comes into contact with other people who are more or less in the same status and situation as himself. Such people are considered to be on the level of "*re’ehu*"—equal peers. However, there are people who stand on a lower level than he does—in the category of "*evyonim*" (poor) relative to him. This applies, naturally, both in a spiritual and a material sense. The complete *avodah* is when a Jew fulfills both: both *l’re’ehu* and *la’evyonim*. The one who causes others to act, and who himself acts, whose eye is good regarding the affairs of others, fulfills both in their entirety—especially when it concerns help for the work of **Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch**.

With feelings of gratitude and blessings for the year,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

## 392

B"H, 10 Elul, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Moshe Zev, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter, along with the enclosed contribution from R' Dalfon, may he live, has reached us, and it is certainly nothing more than a beginning and a prelude.

My response was delayed due to my preoccupation with publishing the *Kitzurei HaTzemach Tzedek* and his glosses on *Tanya*, along with several additions, which I hope will be released from the press in the coming week.

The sefer *Zecher Yehuda* and the sefer *Tzeror HaChaim* are not in my possession...

To conclude with a *dvar Torah*, I was inspired by the aforementioned printed sefer, which cites a *maamar* of the Baal Shem Tov that even the angel Michael would give all his *avodah* for one *tzitzah* (fringe) of the four *tzitzis* of a Yid. Regarding the precision of why he specifically chose the *mitzvah* of *tzitzis*, and why one *tzitzah* rather than one thread: It can be explained according to what is written (*Zohar Chadash* 3, 216a) that the angel Michael is from the *Merkavah* of *Reishis Chochmah*—all of the *Merkavah* is *Gemara*. Now, it is stated in *Tikkunei Zohar* (Tikkun 10) that anyone who wears *tzitzis* is as if he has established the Throne. Therefore, he says that even though *tzitzis* is only "as if," etc., nevertheless, he would give the *avodah* of the *Merkavah* itself for this. And that is why he specified one *tzitzah* of the four, for all of this—and only this—is relevant to Michael, as is understood. In my notes in the printed version, I also addressed this from the perspective of *Nigleh*.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* and regards to your family,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

393

B"H, 10 Elul, 5708
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your question on what is written in the *maamar* "Bereishis 5702," Chapter 2, that the *keilim* of the *Sefiros* of *Atzilus* are [considered] *Beriah*—this is, *chas v'shalom*, not like the *Beriah* of *Biya* (Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah). Rather, relative to the simplicity and *dveikus* of the *Oros* of *Atzilus*, the *dveikus* of the *keilim*, which is a noticeable *dveikus*, is called *Beriah*.

[You ask] about what is written in many places, that the *dveikus* of the *keilim* is a *dveikus* that is not noticeable.

The intention in the *maamar* "Bereishis" is to explain that even though in *Atzilus*, "He, His life, and His vessels"—which are the *keilim*—are one, a *dveikus* and not a [mere] connection, nevertheless the *keilim* are called *Beriah* because the manner of their *dveikus* is noticeable; it is a *dveikus* that has been formed. That is to say, there were two things here, and **afterward** they became one—which is not the case with the *Oros*.

This is similar to the distinction regarding the *dveikus* of *haskalah* and *hasagah* in the *maamar* "Ve'atah Yigdal" 5700. See also the *maamar* "VeHar Sinai" from *Dahash* 5701.

As for what is explained elsewhere, that the *dveikus* of the *keilim* is a *dveikus* that is not noticeable, the intention is that in the *keilim* themselves, by their very nature, the *dveikus* to their source is not noticeable or felt **within their own feeling**, because the general nature of *keilim* is concealment.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 395

B”H, 18 Elul, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R’ Sh.M. [Klemenson]—may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter informing me of the successful arrival of the group of Shochetim—may they live and be well—to Dublin. As per your request, I am enclosing the Kuntres for Chai Elul, which arrived yesterday afternoon from the bookbinder. May it be a merit to benefit the many and to bring even those who are currently distant closer to Torah and mitzvos in general, and to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe in particular.

And if it has fallen to their lot to come for a time to the **"outside" (chutz)**, they will surely utilize this to fulfill through themselves the mission of "Your springs shall spread outward" (yufutzu maynotecha) that pertains to this "outside."

They have surely heard the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live and be well: "A Shochet is not a slaughterer (skataboyetz); he is a man with a knife in his hand," etc.

Regarding these days, from Rosh Hashanah to "Rosh Hashanah"—meaning Yom Kippur, which is also called Rosh Hashanah, as stated in Tosafos (Nedarim 23b; see also Sefer Chassidim, sec. 256, and Likkutei Torah, beginning of the maamar *Vehaya Bayom Hahu Yitaka* and the maamar *Yechayenu Miyomayim*)—there are many deep allusions within them. One of them is:

"All the living" (kol hachai)—for Yisroel are called "living"—should take to heart that Hashem commanded us to observe and celebrate Rosh Hashanah not on the first day of the work of Creation, when the heavens and the earth and all their hosts were created (Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 1), nor on the seventh day of creation, the day Hashem chose to sanctify above all other days. Rather, Hashem commanded us to observe Rosh Hashanah specifically on the day G-d created man—a creature who, immediately upon his creation, declared and proclaimed to all created beings: "Hashem is King, He has donned majesty," etc., "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bend the knee before Hashem our Maker," as recounted by our Sages (Pirkei D’Rabbi Eliezer, ch. 11; Zohar I, 221b). Through this proclamation, Adam HaRishon drew this into them and elevated them to the level of recognizing "Hashem is King, He has donned majesty," etc.

This is also akin to the concept of shechitah (though the aforementioned action is performed in a different manner), for "there is no 'slaughtered' (v'shachat) except 'drawn' (v'mashach)" (Chullin 30b)—he transfers it entirely to another place. This is done by taking its soul (see Shabbos 75a), its vitality, or its "inner fire" (zayn koch) from the place where it was until now.

And then it can be transformed into the blood and flesh of man—*Adamah L’Elyon* (resembling the Supernal), *Adam HaElyon*. Time does not permit me to elaborate further.

Concluding with wishes for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for you and the entire group—may they live and be well—with revealed good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, 18 Elul, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav A.A., may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

The matter has been facilitated, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, has authorized the publication of a Kuntres for 18 Elul, printed in memory of his late uncle. Enclosed is one copy. In a few days, there will also be a number of copies bound more elegantly, and we will then send them to the family of the deceased. Please be so kind as to inform me whether to send them directly to them or via your honor.

Regarding what you explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, in the discourse *Dovid Zemirot* (concerning what is written there, "Torah is [something], and Ohr Ein Sof is as naught"), that this is because Ohr Ein Sof animates the worlds—this does not seem correct to me **in this context**. For in that Iggeres HaKodesh, he explains this superiority of Torah because it is unified with Ohr Ein Sof, and therefore it is "something." Yet, in that very same place, he writes that in relation to Ein Sof, it is "as naught," and Ein Sof is higher than Ohr Ein Sof. Furthermore, the Ohr Ein Sof, which is the cause of the Torah’s superiority, must be higher than the superiority of the effect—namely, the Torah.

Concluding with blessings for all good things for you and your entire family, may they live,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Your letter from 18 Elul has just been received. I will endeavor with [Name], may he live, regarding the thousand, and in any event, I remember my guarantee; you need not be concerned about this at all.
